10
Introduction
In the beginning of the creation itself, God has provided mankind with knowledge of the Vedas. This 
knowledge is like an elaborate user manual which contains everything that one needs to know about 
facts, philosophies, sciences, duties and consequences of actions, in order to live a happy and meaningful 
life and attain the ultimate goal of mokṣha. The sages started propagating this knowledge via oral 
traditions. However, in the beginning itself, they noticed that the masses found this knowledge to be 
overwhelming and that because of the lack of its proper understanding, some convoluted practices had 
started taking hold in the society. There was a need for a more concise and easier to understand text 
that summarized the Vedic wisdom. Maharṣhi Manu took the initiative and produced this treatise called 
Manusmṛiti. The name itself means “as understood and remembered by Manu”. Several other such 
treatise were created by other sages over a period of time, but Manusmṛiti withstanding the test of time 
is the most famous and universally accepted.
Over the period of time, almost in all of the scriptures except the Vedas, other scholars sometimes with 
good intention and sometimes to push an agenda, added their own opinion and inserted shlokas here 
and there. The more famous the book, the greater were the number of insertions, sometimes increasing 
the size of the text manifold. The works like Maharṣhi Vaalmeeki’s Raamaayaṇa, Maharṣhi Vyaasa’s 
Mahaabhaarata and Maharṣhi Manu’s Manusmṛiti, being one of the most famous, were on the receiving 
end of these extensions and convolutions, due to which the size of the Mahaabhaarata increased about 
ten fold, Raamaayaṇa about four fold and Manusmṛiti about two fold. Thanks to the path breaking 
research of scholars like Swami Jagadeeshwaraananda and Dr. Surendra Kumar etc. these extensions 
and convolutions have been systematically identified. Their extensive efforts identify the extensions 
based on certain criteria including, differences in style of the formation of the shloka, contradiction of
the Vedas, contradiction of something that the author had said at some other place, no correlation with 
the current topic, unnecessary duplication of some idea already conveyed etc. Many of these shlokas 
appear to be conforming to the Vedic wisdom, but are classified as extensions merely for the reason that 
they are either out of context or redundant. 
Lately Manusmṛiti has also been under a lot of controversy wherein some politicians have tried to 
discredit it and blame it for the discriminations that have taken hold in our society in the last few hundred 
years. This is primarily due to their inability to understand the concept of dharma, their political agenda 
and also due to the extension and the convolution that were not originally part of the Manusmṛiti. 
In this translation, after referring to the research by Dr. Surendra Kumar, I have segregated the shlokas 
into two sections. The first section contains only the shlokas that are deemed to be written by Maharṣhi 
Manu. The second section contains the shlokas which are considered as extensions i.e. added by others. 
The translation in english are based on my understanding of the Manusmṛiti. In both of the sections, the 
reference number of the shloka from the current versions of traditional Manusmṛiti has been provided
at the end of the translation of each of the shloka, e.g. 1:12 implies that it is the twelfth shloka of the 
first chapter.

I have tried to keep the translations simple. In order to facilitate reading in a flow, the shlokas have been 
moved to footnotes in the Original Manusmṛiti section. Since a flow is not expected in the extension
section, a traditional approach of providing translations after the text of the shloka has been used.
I hope this translation will help everyone develop the love and respect for the Manusmṛiti that it truly 
deserves.
Sañjay Mohan Mittal
March 4th, 2023

Transliteration guide for Romanizing various phonetics
Devanagari script has 17 main vowels, 36 consonants and 30 biconsonantal conjuncts. It 
is very difficult to transliterate all of these original sounds just using 26 letters from roman 
alphabet. Following guideline has been used for transliteration in our compilations.
Vowels स्वर
The long vowel sound is represented by double occurrence of a roman vowel
अ a आ aa इ i ई ee उ u ऊ oo ऋ ṛi ॠ ṛee लृlṛi लॄlṛee ए e ऐ ai ओ o
औ au अंaṅ, añ, aṇ, an, am अँan
̐ ᳬ◌ंṁ ꣳ m̈ अ: aḥ ऽ ’ १ 1 ३ 3
• The vowel “अ aं ṅ, añ, aṇ, an, am” which is represented in Devanagari by a dot over a 
letter, changes its sound based on the sound immediately following it. It defaults to 
“m” but can also be “ṅ, ñ, ṇ or n” if the following sound is guttural, palatal, retroflex 
or dental respectively. 
• The Vowel “अँan
̐” is not pronounced separately. It represents nasalization of the base 
sound it is transforming. The nasal sound changes depending on the base sound. 
However, we are representing it with only one symbol due to lack of enough symbols 
in roman script. 
• The avagraha “ऽ ’ ” is not pronounced. It represents the loss of a vowel during 
conjugation or is used for separating vowels which if combined would result in 
different chhanda for a mantra.
• Suffix of numeral 1 to a vowel means that the vowel should be sung using more than 
1 musical note.
• plut - Suffix of numeral 3 to a vowel represents extension of the vowel.
Consonantsव्यञ्जन
Devanagari has provision for several nasal sounds, retroflex consonants and dual 
consonants. Please refer to following table for transliteration of the consonants.

Conjugation with the consonant “र्r”: When “र्r” appears before a consonant, it is 
represented by a curve on top of the succeeding consonant e.g. र+्क = कर् rka. When “र्r”
appears after a consonant, it is represented by a slanting line or a hat symbol below the 
preceding consonant e.g. प+् र = प्र pra and ड्+र = ड्र ḍra.
Devanaagaree also has a provision of conjugation of three or more consonants. They are 
not being discussed over here just for the sake of brevity.
In order to maintain the original pronunciations of the shlokas, complex words have not 
been broken down while transliterating. However immediately after each shlokas a 
breakdown of the root words call pada paaṭha has been provided. In case the pada 
paaṭha also has some composite words termed as samaasa, the inherent root words have 
been separated by a hyphen.

मनुस्मृित अध्याय १ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 1
15
Chapter 1
Sages visit Maharṣhi Manu
(maharṣhayaḥ) Many sages (abhigamya) visited (manum) Maharṣhi Manu, who was 
(aaseenam) sitting quietly, contemplating on some subject (ekaagram) with a focused 
mind. After (pratipoojya) paying their respects to him (yathaa) as per (nyaayam) the 
norms, they (abruvan) spoke these words. 1:1
In this context the word ekaagram doesn’t refer to the state of samaadhi. It would 
normally be inappropriate for someone to disturb another person who is in samaadhi.
The text starts in a passive voice suggesting that either one of his disciples (most likely 
Bhṛigu) scribed Maharṣhi Manu’s lectures and events around them or Maharṣhi Manu 
wrote about himself as a third person, which is not uncommon even in the modern times.
(bhagavan) Reverend! You (arhasi) are capable of (vaktum) explaining to (naḥ) us the 
different (dharmaan) duties assigned to different individuals from (sarva) all of 
(varṇaanaam) the classes in the society, (cha) and (antara)(prabhavaaṇaam) different 
stages of life as well, (yathaavat) as is and (anupoorvashaḥ) in a proper order. 1:2
The classes within the society i.e. the braahmaṇa (scholars), kṣhatriya (warriors), vaishya
(farmers and merchants) and shoodra (servants) are based on the duties assigned to 
individuals and are not based on their birth in a particular family. Parents are the first 
teachers of the children and hence it becomes likely that children normally follow the 
duties and hence the class of their parents. However, everyone has an equal right to

मनुस्मृित अध्याय १ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 1
16
education and the class of an individual could be changed by his/her teachers during the 
education, based on the individual's capabilities and the level of his/her intelligence.
The different stages in one’s life are brahmacharya (student), gṛihastha (householder), 
vaanaprastha (preparation for detachment) and sannyaasa (ascetic). The brahmacharya
stage is a preparation for the gṛihastha stage and the vaanaprastha stage is a preparation 
for the sannyaasa stage.
The word “dharma” translated above as duties, has a much broader meaning. Dharma is 
the basis for the functioning of this World in an orderly and proper manner. Each and 
every verse of the Vedas points towards Dharma. For individuals, it can also be viewed as 
the righteous conduct that takes one away from sins and fosters belief, trust and loyalty.
It is also the proper utilization of all resources natural and artificial, for the wholesome 
good of the society and the universe. Dharma protects those who uphold it.
(prabho) O Learned! (hi) Because (tvam) you are (ekaḥ) the only one (arthavit) who 
knows (kaarya)(tattva) the intricacies of (asya) these (vidhaanasya) rules of conduct 
(sarvasya) for all humans, as laid out in the Vedas that contain (aprameyasya)
immeasurable wisdom of the Supreme Soul, who is (svayam)(bhuvaḥ) not created by 
anyone and (achintyasya) is beyond comprehension by thoughts. 1:3
After hearing (tathaa) those (pṛiṣhṭaḥ) questions (samyak) properly asked (taiḥ) by 
those (mahaatmabhiḥ) great souls, (saḥ) Maharṣhi Manu, (amitaujaaḥ) the possessor of 
never ending brilliance, (archya) welcomed (sarvaan) all of (taan) those (maharṣheen)
sages and (pratyuvaacha) replied, “(shrooyataam) Please listen to (iti) this.” 1:4
 
1:3 त्वमेको  स्य सवर्स्य िवधानस्य स्वयम्भ

मनुस्मृित अध्याय १ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 1
17
Creation of the Universe
Maharṣhi Manu starts his discourse with an explanation of the origins of the Universe. 
Someone may think that he is going completely off the topic touched upon by the sages
in their question. However, the purpose of the creation of this Universe leads into the 
purpose of life and hence the duties of the mortal beings. It is easier to understand and 
retain any knowledge when it is layered on top of the foundation of the basic concepts 
themselves. 
The following chart is based on Kapil Muni’s Saaṅkhya Shaastra. It ties in with Maharṣhi 
Manu’s description of the various elements that are formed during the process of 
creation.
 
सः । तैः । प ः ृ । तथा । सम्यक्। अिमतौजाः । महात्मिभः ॥
प्रत्यवाचु । अच्यर्। तान्। सवार्न्। महष न्। श्रयताम ू ्। इित ॥
4. sa taiḥ pṛiṣhṭastathaa samyagamitaujaa mahaatmabhiḥ,
pratyuvaachaarchya taansarvaanmaharṣheeñchhrooyataamiti. saḥ taiḥ pṛiṣhṭaḥ tathaa samyak amitaujaaḥ mahaatmabhiḥ,
pratyuvaacha archya taan sarvaan maharṣheen shrooyataam iti.
मनुस्मृित अध्याय १ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 1
18
Before the creation of the Universe, (idam) there (aaseet) existed matter in its basic 
subatomic state in (tamobhootam) complete darkness, where (aprajñaatam) nothing 
worth knowing, (alakṣhaṇam) with any kind of tangible attributes existed. There was 
(avijñeyam) nothing to know about or (apratarkyam) to debate about; (iva) as if, 
(sarvataḥ) all over, everything was (prasuptam) dormant. 1:5
(tataḥ) Then (bhagavaan) the Supreme Soul who is (avyaktaḥ) devoid of any physical 
characteristics, (svayambhooḥ) is capable of the creation by himself, (tamonudaḥ) is the 
 
1:5 आसीिददंतमोभ
ू
तमप्र ातमल णम्
। अप्रतक्यर्मिव ेयंप्रस
ु
 िमव सवर्तः ॥५॥
आसीत्। इदम्। तमोभतमू ्। अप्र ातम्। अल णम्॥ अप्रतक्यर्म्। अिव ेयम्। प्रस मु ्। इव । सवर्तः ॥
5. aaseedidan tamobhootamaprajñaatamalakṣhaṇam,
apratarkyamavijñeyam prasuptamiva sarvataḥ. aaseet idam tamobhootam aprajñaatam alakṣhaṇam,
apratarkyam avijñeyam prasuptam iva sarvataḥ.
मनुस्मृित अध्याय १ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 1
19
inspirer of the activity in the dormant matter and (vṛittaujaaḥ) is the creator of 
(mahaabhootaadi) the elements that were subsequently used to form everything in this 
universe, (praaduraaseet) showed his might by systematically and deliberately bringing 
(idam) this universe to (vyañjayan) a tangible state. 1:6
The word “praaduraaseet” can also be interpreted as “showed himself”. However this 
verse also claims the God as “avyaktaḥ” i.e. without any perceptible qualities. Hence the 
phrase “showed himself” is metaphorical and is pointing towards God making his 
presence felt through his creation.
The 7th - 13th shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu and were most 
likely inserted by someone else later.
(cha) And this process starts with a transitional state that (udbabarha) originates (eva)
from (aatmanaḥ) the basic matter possessing the three qualities satva, rajas and tamas
in equal proportions (cha) and (manaḥ) contains the combined intellect of the entire 
universe that is yet to be formed. (aatmakam) This state is called mahat, which is (sat)
tangible as well as (asat) intangible because it has not yet manifested into a final 
product i.e. the universe and its contents. The mahat then gains (ahaṅkaaram) self 
awareness (api) and creates (manasaḥ) the subtle mind element that has (eeshvaram)
the capability of (abhimantaaram) experiencing existence. 1:14

mahaabhootaadi vṛittaujaaḥ praaduraaseet tamonudaḥ.

14. udbabarhaatmanashchaiva manaḥ sadasadaatmakam,
manasashchaapyahaṅkaaramabhimantaarameeshvaram. udbabarha aatmanaḥ cha eva manaḥ sat-asat-aatmakam,
मनुस्मृित अध्याय १ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 1
20
These concepts can be correlated to modern scientific terms. The primary subatomic 
particles i.e. electrons, protons and neutrons represent the three qualities satva, rajas
and tamas. During the destruction of the prior creation, God had separated them and as 
a result they were in a dormant state. At the beginning of new creation, God mixed them 
up and created a dough called mahat, wherein these subatomic particle eagerly find their 
match and subsequently form the atoms which show the first signs of self awareness i.e. 
ahaṅkaara. These atoms then combine to form some basic molecules which are the five 
tanmaatraa. These basic atomic and molecular structures then react to form other 
complex molecular structures represented by the sixteen vikṛiti.
(cha) And from this (mahaantam) great substance possessing self awareness, several 
other elements, including (aatmaanam) the subtle mind (cha) and (pañcha) five 
(indriyaaṇi) senses (graheetṛiṇi) for the perceptions (viṣhayaaṇaam) of different subject 
matters, are created (shanaiḥ) gradually in an orderly fashion, each inheriting (sarvaaṇi)
all of (triguṇaani) the three qualities in different proportions. 1:15
(ṣhaṇṇaam) Six (avayavaan) ingredients, i.e. self-awareness and five perceptions, which 
are, the sound, the beauty, the touch, the taste and the smell, were used in 
(teṣhaam)(tu) the substances discussed in prior shloka. From (sanniveshya) a mix 
(aatmamaatraasu) in different proportions of these (amitaujasaam) highly powerful 
and (sookṣhmaan) subtle ingredients, (sarva) all of (bhootaani) the five major elements, 
i.e. the sky, the fire, the air, the water and the earth, are (api) also (nirmame) formed. 
These major elements make up everything in this entire universe. 1:16
 
manasaḥ cha api ahaṅkaaram abhimantaaram eeshvaram.

mahaantam eva cha aatmaanam sarvaaṇi triguṇaani cha,
viṣhayaaṇaam graheetṛiṇi shanaiḥ pañcha-indriyaaṇi cha.

मनुस्मृित अध्याय १ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 1

The 17th shloka is not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
All of these subtle and powerful elements, each (saha) with (karmabhiḥ) a definite 
purpose and function, the five (mahaanti) major (bhootaani) elements i.e. the sky, the 
fire, the air, the water and the earth (cha) and the eleven (sookṣhmaiḥ) subtle 
(avayavaiḥ) elements including senses, actions and (manaḥ) the mind, (tadaa) after 
their creation of together formed the subtle and physical bodies that (aavishanti) are 
occupied and (sarva)(bhoota)(kṛit) utilized by (avyayam) the indestructible souls. 1:18
(idam) This (vyayam) spendable universe (sambhavati) is primarily created 
(saptaanaam) from the seven (avyayaat) indestructible*, (sookṣhmaabhyaḥ) subtle and
(mahaujasaam) extremely powerful elements that (moortimaatraabhyaḥ) are the basis 
of creation of other intermediate elements that form everything in this universe. (tu)
Hence (teṣhaam) these seven elements i.e. mahat, ahaṅkaara and the five tanmaatraa, 
(puruṣhaaṇaam) are part of every tangible thing. *These seven elements are 
indestructible only during the creation and sustenance phase of this universe. They do 
revert back into the basic matter in the destruction phase. 1:19
 
तेषाम्। तु। अवयवान्। स मान ू ्।षण्णाम्। अिप । अिमतौजसाम्॥
सिन्नवेश्य । आत्ममात्रासु। सवर्भतािन ू । िनमर्मे॥
16. teṣhaan tvavayavaansookṣhmaan ṣhaṇṇaamapyamitaujasaam,
sanniveshyaatmamaatraasu sarvabhootaani nirmame.
teṣhaam tu avayavaan sookṣhmaan ṣhaṇṇaam api amitaujasaam,
sanniveshya aatmamaatraasu sarva-bhootaani nirmame.

The 27th shloka has been repositioned after the 19th shloka as it fits better in the context 
and flow at that place.
(tu) These are the (dashaardhaanaam) half of ten i.e. five (aṇvyaḥ) subtle (maatraaḥ)
elements (yaaḥ) that are (smṛitaaḥ) said to be (vinaashinyaḥ) destructible. Created 
(saardham) with a mixture (taabhiḥ) of them, (sarvam) everything in (idam)this universe 
(sambhavati) has come into existence (anupoorvashaḥ) in the order of complexity. 1:27
(smṛitaḥ) It is said that (yaavat ithaḥ) whatever are (guṇaḥ) the qualities of (yaḥ)(yaḥ)
the ingredients, (eṣhaam) they are (taavat) also inherent in (saḥ)(saḥ) the product. The 
(guṇam) qualities of these tanmaatraa are also apparent in the mahaabhoota; which
when (aadya) listed in the proper order, (paraḥ)(paraḥ) the later ones (tu) also 
(avaapnoti) inherit (eṣhaam) the qualities (aadyasya) of the prior ingredients (cha) as 
well. The sky inherits the vibration from sound, the air inherits touch as well as 
vibration, the fire inherits beauty, touch and vibration, the water inherits taste, 
vibration, touch and beauty and the earth inherits smell, vibration, touch, beauty and 
taste. 1:20
 
तेषाम्। इदम्। तु। स ानाम्। प षाणाम ु ्। महौजसाम्॥

19. teṣhaamidan tu saptaanaam puruṣhaaṇaam mahaujasaam,

teṣhaam idam tu saptaanaam puruṣhaaṇaam mahaujasaam,
sookṣhmaabhyaḥ moortimaatraabhyaḥ sambhavati avyayaat vyayam.

(cha) And (saḥ) he, (prabhuḥ) the God, (asṛijat) created, (devaanaam) the divine forces 
of nature and heavenly bodies (karmaatmanaam) who continue to work incessantly, 
(praaṇinaam) the living beings, (gaṇam) a group of (saadhyaanaam) accomplished 
scholars (cha) and (yajñam) all of the periodic activities of this universe powered by 
(sookṣhmam) the subtle (cha) and (sanaatanam) ancient elements (eva) as well. 1:22
Revelation of the Vedas
(tu) For (siddhi) fulfilling (artham) the purpose of (yajña) the creation of this universe i.e. 
to provide an opportunity for the souls to attain nirvaaṇa, God (dudoha) established in 
the minds of the extraordinary sages named (agni) Agni, (vaayu) Vaayu and (ravibhyaḥ)
Ravi the (sanaatanam) eternal (brahma) wisdom of the vedas containing (trayam)
three* (lakṣhaṇam) types of knowledge i.e. (ṛig) of the facts, (yajuḥ) of the duties and 
(saama) of devotion. *The three types of knowledge doesn’t mean that Maharṣhi Manu 
is acknowledging only three of the Vedas. The Vedas are four in number and each of 
them contains all of the three types of knowledge. 1:23

21st shloka has been repositioned after 23rd shloka.
(saḥ) He, the God, (aadau) at the time of creation (eva)(tu) itself, (vedashabdebhyaḥ)
through the words of the Vedas, has conveyed (pṛithak)(pṛithak) separate (naamaani)
names, (karmaaṇi) capabilities (cha) and duties / utilizations (sarveṣhaam) of everything 
living or otherwise. He has (cha) also (nirmame) created (pṛithak) different (sansthaaḥ)
classifications for things, animals and humans, including the four sub-division of 
humans based on their capabilities. 1:21
The 24th - 25th shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
(artham) To foster (viveka) a deeper understanding (karmaṇaam) of the actions, God 
(vyavechayat) divided them into the categories of (dharma) the righteous (cha) and 
(adharma) the immoral (cha) and then (ayojayat) provided the knowledge of their 
consequences (dvandvaiḥ) in the form of the conflict between (sukha) happiness and 
(duḥkhaadibhiḥ) sorrows to (imaaḥ) these (prajaaḥ) beings. 1:26

मनुस्मृित अध्याय १ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 1

Similarity with prior creations
(yasmin) Whatever (karmaṇi) actions (nyayuṅkta) were assigned, by (saḥ) (prabhuḥ)
God, (yam)(tu) to any class of beings (prathamam) in prior creations, (sṛijyamaanaḥ)
upon their creation, (saḥ) they (punaḥ) again and (punaḥ) again (bheje) engage (tat) in 
the same actions (svayam)(eva) themselves. 1:28
(hinsra) Violent, (ahinsre) non-violent, (mṛidu) docile, (kroore) fierce, (dharma)
righteous, (adharma) unrighteous, (ṛita) forthright, (anṛite) deceitful, (yat) whatever 
temperaments (saḥ) God (adadhaat) assigned (yasya) for that class of beings (sarge) in 
the beginning, (tasya) they (svayam) automatically (aavishat) acquired (tat) that 
temperament. 1:29

dvandvaiḥ ayojayat cha imaaḥ sukha-duḥkhaadibhiḥ prajaaḥ.

(yathaa) As (ṛitavaḥ) the seasons (svayam)(eva) automatically (abhipadyante) show 
(ṛituliṅgaani) the signs of (ṛituparyaye) the change in a season, (tathaa) similarly 
(dehinaḥ) the living beings too engage in (karmaaṇi) actions (svaani)(svaani) assigned to 
them. 1:30
Four classes of the humans
(tu) (artham) For (vivṛiddhi) the prosperity and maintenance of order(lokaanaam) in the 
society, he (niravartayat) created the classes of (braahmaṇam) the scholars, 
(kṣhatriyam) the warriors, (vaishyam) the farmers / merchants (cha) and (shoodram) the 
servants as the (mukha) mouth, (baahoo) arms, (uroo) stomach / thighs and (paadataḥ)
feet of the society respectively. 1:31

whatever are (kramayogam) the procedures of their (janmani) birth, (abhidhaasyaami)

(pashavaḥ) The domesticated animals (cha) and (mṛigaaḥ)the wild animals (eva) as well, 
(vyaalaaḥ) the violent animals (ubhayatodataḥ) with rows of teeth on both of the jaws, 
(rakṣhaansi) the demons, (pishaachaaḥ) the uncouth (cha) and (manuṣhyaaḥ) the 
cultured humans, all (jaraayujaaḥ) are born from placenta. 1:43
(pakṣhiṇaḥ) The birds, (sarpaaḥ) the snakes, (nakraaḥ) the alligators, (matsyaaḥ) the 
fishes (cha) and (kachchhapaaḥ) the turtles (cha) and many (yaani) other (evam) similar 
(prakaaraaṇi) types of animals, both (sthalajaani) terrestrial (cha) and (audakaani)
aquatic, (aṇḍajaaḥ) are born from eggs. 1:44

The (dañsha) stinging (mashakam) mosquitos, (yookaa) the lice, (makṣhika) the flies, 
(matkuṇam) the bedbugs (cha) and (yat) whatever (anyat) other creatures (kiñchit) that 
(eedṛisham) are similar, are (upajaayante) born (ooṣhmaṇaḥ) from heat, dampness (cha)
and (svedajam) sweat. 1:45
(sthaavaraaḥ) The immobile trees and plants including (sarve) everything that 
(prarohiṇaḥ) rises from (beeja) a seed or (kaaṇḍa) a graft, (udbhijjaaḥ) are born from the 
soil. The ones that grow (bahu) a lot of (puṣhpa) flowers and (phala) fruits (upagaaḥ)
closer to the earth and those whose (phala) fruits (paakaantaaḥ) ripen to produce food 
and grains are called (oṣhadhyaḥ) nutritional and medicinal plants. 1:46
(ye) Those that (phalavantaḥ) grow fruits (apuṣhpaaḥ) without flowers; (te) they 
(smṛitaaḥ) are called (vanaspatayaḥ) vanaspati. Those (tu) with (ubhayataḥ) both

yaani cha evam prakaaraaṇi sthalajaani audakaani cha.

(puṣhpiṇaḥ) flowers (cha) and (phalinaḥ) fruits (eva) as well (smṛitaaḥ) are called

the same roots and (tathaa) similarly (jaatayaḥ) different kinds of (tṛiṇa) grass (eva) as 
well, (prataanaaḥ) the creepers that spread on the land (cha) and those that (vallyaḥ)
spread by climbing on supports (eva) as well, whether (ruhaaṇi) sprouting from (beeja)
a seed or from (kaaṇḍa) a graft, all of them fall under the category called sthaavara. 1:48

in (tamasaa) the darkness of ignorance in (bahu) many (roopeṇa) ways, many souls are 
assigned to the life of these trees and plants. (ete) They (bhavanti) have 
(antaḥ)(sañjñaaḥ) consciousness and (samanvitaaḥ) experience (sukha) happiness and 
(duḥkha) sorrows as well. 1:49

The 50th - 51st shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
God’s desire to create and destroy this universe.
(yadaa) When (saḥ) he, (devaḥ)the God, (jaagarti) awakensi.e. desires to create, (tadaa)
then the matter (cheṣhṭate) develops activity to form (idam) this (jagat) universe and 
(yadaa) when he, (shaantaatmaa)the placid soul, (svapiti)sleepsi.e. desires to destruct, 
(tadaa)then (sarvam)the whole universe (nimeelati) destructs and becomes inactive.1:52
When (tasmin) he (susthe) stops and (svapiti) starts the destruction phase, (tu) then 
(karmaatmaanaḥ) the souls designated to perform actions (shareeriṇaḥ) through their 
bodies (nivartante) are also relieved (svakarmebhyaḥ) from their respective duties (cha)
and even (manaḥ) the subtle bodies attached to these souls destruct and 
(glaanim)(ṛichchhati) merge back into the original elements. 1:53
 
49. tamasaa bahuroopeṇa veṣhṭitaaḥ karmahetunaa,
antaḥsañjñaa bhavantyete sukhaduḥkhasamanvitaaḥ. tamasaa bahu-roopeṇa veṣhṭitaaḥ karma-hetunaa,
antaḥ-sañjñaaḥ bhavanti ete sukha-duḥkha-samanvitaaḥ.

मनुस्मृित अध्याय १ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 1
31
(yadaa) When (tasmin) the (mahaatmani) great soul (praleeyante) has destroyed 
(yugapat) everything, (tadaa) then (ayam) that (sarva)(bhoota) all pervading (aatmaa)
soul (nirvṛitaḥ) having relieved himself, is considered (tu) as (sukham) blissfully (svapiti)
sleeping from the perspective of the unliberated souls. Though he is still active from the 
perspective of the liberated souls. 1:54
The 55th - 56th shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
(cha) And (evam) like this, (saḥ) he , (avyayaḥ) the indestructible, through his (jaagrat)
wakeful and (svapnaabhyaam) sleeping stages respectively (sañjeevayati) creates and 
maintains (ajasram) till eternity, (idam) this (sarvam) entire universe (charaacharam)
which is filled with mobile and immobile creatures (cha) and then (pramaapayati)
dissolves it back to the original state of the sub-atomic matter. 1:57
The 58th - 63th shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
The measurements of time
The time taken for (dasha) ten (cha) and (aṣhṭau) eight i.e. eighteen (nimeṣhaaḥ) blinks 
of the eye defines the measurement of (kaaṣhṭhaa) a Kaaṣhṭhaa; (triñshattu) thirty of 
(taaḥ) these make up one (kalaa) Kalaa; (triñshat) thirty (kalaa) Kalaa make up one

मनुस्मृित अध्याय १ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 1
32
(muhoortaḥ) Muhoorta (cha) and (taavataḥ)(tu) the same count i.e. thirty of Muhoorta
(syaat) become (ahoraatram) one day and night. 1:64
1 Muhoorta = 24x60/30 = 48 minutes; 1 Kalaa = 48/30 = 1.6 minutes or 96 seconds;
1 Kaaṣhṭhaa = 1.6*60/30 = 3.2 seconds; 1 Nimeṣhaa = 3.2/18 = 0.17̇ seconds.
(sooryaḥ) The Sun (vibhajate) creates the division of (aho) the day and (raatre) the night 
for all beings including (maanuṣha) humans and (daivike) for the forces of nature as well. 
(raatriḥ) During the night (bhootaanaam) the beings (svapnaaya) sleep and 
(cheṣhṭaayai) tend to perform (karmaṇaam) actions during (ahaḥ) the day. 1:65
The 66th shloka is not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
One (daive) divine (raatryahanee) day and night together are equivalent to (varṣham)
one human year, (tatra) which (punaḥ) again (pravibhaagaḥ) is divided into (tayoḥ) two
based on the direction of the movement of the sun after the solstices*, (udagayanam)
the northward movement of the sun becomes the divine (ahaḥ) day and 
(dakṣhiṇaayanam) the southward movement of the sun (syaat) becomes the divine 
(raatriḥ) night. Accordingly the measure of one divine year would be 360 divine day and

nights i.e. 360 human (earth) years. *Alternatively, it can also be viewed as the Sun’s 
movement in the north and in the south of the equator. 1:67
Metaphorically, in the 67th shloka, the divine time frame can also be viewed as the time 
frame for elevated souls called maharṣhi. They work so diligently and efficiently that 
they accomplish in a day what would take normal humans a year to accomplish.
(yat) Whatever are (pramaaṇam) the measures of (braahmasya) God's (ahasya) day (tu)
and (kṣhapaa) night (tu) and of (ekaikashaḥ) each and every other (yugaanaam) major 
division of time, now (nibodhata) listen (samaasataḥ) briefly about (tat) them 
(kramashaḥ) in the proper order. 1:68
(aahuḥ) It is said that (chatvaari) four (sahasraaṇi) thousand (varṣhaaṇaam) divine years 
together make (tat) the (kṛitam) Satya (yugam) Yuga era and (yaavat) the same number 
of i.e. four (shatee) hundred years is (sandhyaa) the leading period (tasya) of that era 
(cha) and (tathaa)(vidhaḥ) another four hundred years is (sandhyaañshaḥ) the trailing 
period. 1:69

And in regards (itareṣhu)to the other (triṣhu)three eras i.e. Tretaa Yuga, Dvaapara Yuga
and Kali Yuga, their measures can be respectively obtained (apaayena) by reducing the 
count by (eka) one (sahasraaṇi) thousand in the main (cha) and one (shataani) hundred 
(sasandhyeṣhu) in the leading (cha) and (sasandhyaañsheṣhu) in the trailing periods from 
the prior period in the same order. 1:70
1:71 (parisaṅkhyaatam) The measures of (etat) the (chatur) four (yugam) eras (yat) that 
were discussed (aadau) prior (eva) as well, together sum to (dvaadasha) twelve 
(saahasram) thousands divine years. Together (etat) they are (uchyate) said to 
constitute one (devaanaam) divine (yugam) era. 1:71

मनुस्मृित अध्याय १ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 1
35
(jñeyam) Know (sahasram) one thousand (daivikaanaam) divine (yugaanaam) eras 
(pari)(saṅkhyayaa) as equivalent (tu) to (braahmam) God’s (ekam) one (ahaḥ) day (cha)
and (taavateem) so as his (raatrim) night (eva) as well. 1:72
Era Divine Years Earth
Leading Phase Main Phase Trailing Phase Total Years
Satya Yuga 400 4,000 400 4,800 1,728,000
Tretaa Yuga 300 3,000 300 3,600 1,296,000
Dvaapara Yuga 200 2,000 200 2,400 864,000
Kali Yuga 100 1,000 100 1,200 432,000
Total 12,000 4,320,000
God’s one day is equal to 4,320,000,000 earth years and so is his night.
The people who (viduḥ) understand (tat) that the time frame of (braahmam) God’s one 
(puṇyam) pious (ahaḥ) day is as long as the time taken for the completion of 
(sahasraantam) one thousand divine (yuga) eras (cha) and (taavateem)(eva) so is his 
(raatrim) night, (te) they are (vai) indeed (janaaḥ) the ones who (vidaḥ) possess the 
knowledge (ahoraatra) of the creation and destruction of this universe. 1:73

मनुस्मृित अध्याय १ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 1
36
Creation of the basic elements
Maharṣhi Manu resumes the discussion on the elements that form the universe.
(saḥ) He, the God, (prasuptaḥ) after being inactive, (ante) at the completion (tasya) of 
this (aharnishasya) cycle of destruction, again (prati)(budhyate) becomes active (cha)
and (prati)(buddhaḥ) engages in creation from the matter that (aatmakam) exists (sat)
in sub-atomic state and (asat) not in any kind of elements and (sṛijati) creates the basic 
element called (manaḥ) mahat. 1:74
(sisṛikṣhayaa) With a desire to create further, from (manaḥ) mahat he (sṛiṣhṭim) creates 
(vikurute) another element named ahaṅkaara and then (chodyamaanam) inspired 
(tasmaat) from the elements of ahaṅkaara, and with combination of further derivative 
named (shabdam) shabda tanmaatraa, (aakaasham) the sky element (jaayate) is born 
(tasya) whose primary (guṇam) quality (viduḥ) is known to be the sound vibrations. 1:75
(tu) And (vikurvaaṇaat) from the combination of some derivatives (aakaashat) of the 
sky element and the (sparsha) sparsha tanmaatraa, (shuchiḥ) the pure and (balavaan)
strong, (vahaḥ) the carrier of (sarva) all (gandha) scents, (vaayuḥ) the air element

(jaayate) is born and (saḥ) that is (vai) definitely (mataḥ) known to possess (guṇaḥ) the 
quality of the touch. 1:76
And then (vikurvaaṇaat) from the combination of some derivatives (vaayoḥ) of the air 
element and the (roopa) roopa tanmaatraa (api) as well, (virochiṣhṇuḥ) the bright and

(cha) And (vikurvaaṇaat) from the combination of some derivatives (jyotiṣhaḥ) of the 
fire element and the (rasa) rasa tanmaatraa, (aapaḥ) the water element possessing 
(guṇaaḥ) the quality of taste (smṛitaaḥ) is known to be born and (adbhyaḥ) from the 
combination of some derivatives of the water elements and the (gandha) gandha 
tanmaatraa, (bhoomiḥ) the earth possessing (guṇaa) the quality of smell is born. And 
(iti) this is how the creation of (eṣhaa) this (sṛiṣhṭiḥ) universe (aaditaḥ) began. 1:78

मनुस्मृित अध्याय १ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 1
38
The Manvantara time frame
(daivikam) The divine (yugam) era (yat) that is (praak) mentioned in the prior shlokas as 
(dvaadasha) twelve (saahasram) thousands (uditam) divine years long, (ekasaptati)
seventy one (guṇam) times i.e. that many of (tat) them together constitute another 
measure of time (iha) that is (uchyate) called (manvantaram) Manvantara. 1:79
(parameṣhṭhee) That greatest soul, (punaḥ) again and (punaḥ) again (kurute) performs 
(etat) these cycles of (sargaḥ) the creation (cha) and (saṅhaaraḥ) the destruction (eva)
as well of the universe, the cycles that last for (asaṅkhyaani) numerous (manvantaraaṇi)
Manvantara, (iva) as if he is just (kreeḍan) playing. 1:80
A Summary of various time frames
Time Frame Description
God’s Day From the beginning of the creation to its end. 4,320,000,000 earth years.

मनुस्मृित अध्याय १ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 1
39
Time Frame Description
God’s Night
From the start of destruction to the start of new creation. 4,320,000,000 
earth years.
Manvantara 14 Manvantara with 306,720,000 earth years each. 
The remaining time is equally distributed between the Manvantaras as 
the transition period of 1,728,000 earth years each. There are fifteen 
such transition periods, one each in the beginning and at the end of the 
creation and thirteen between the Manvantaras.
Each Manvantra is named after a Manu, who are:
1. Svayambhu Manu
2. Svarochiṣha Manu
3. Uttama Manu
4. Tapasa/Tamasa Manu
5. Raivata Manu
6. Chakṣhuṣha Manu
7. Vaivasvata Manu (current)
8. Savarṇee Manu
9. Dakṣha Savarṇee Manu
10. Brahma Savarṇee Manu
11. Dharma Savarṇee Manu
12. Rudra Savarṇee Manu
13. Rauchya or Deva Savarṇee Manu
14. Indra Savarṇee Manu
Chaturyugee Combined measure of four eras totalling 4,320,000 earth years. 71 
Chaturyugee together make up one Manvantara. The four eras are:
Satya Yuga - lasting for 1,728,000 earth years
Tretaa Yuga - lasting for 1,296,000 earth years
Dvaapara Yuga - lasting for 864,000 earth years
Kali Yuga - lasting for 432,000 earth years
Divine Year 360 earth years
Samvatsara Earth Year - 360 earth days or 1 Divine day and night
Ayana
(Divine day 
and night)
2 Ayana 180 earth days each, providing the direction / hemisphere of 
Sun’s movement.
Uttaraayana – Sun in the northern hemisphere or northward movement 
of the sun.
Dakṣhiṇaayana – Sun in the southern hemisphere or southward 
movement of the sun.
मनुस्मृित अध्याय १ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 1
40
Time Frame Description
Ṛitu 6 Seasons - the time frames vary based on the geographic location of the 
place. Vasant Ṛitu (Spring), Grishma Ṛitu (Summer), Varsha Ṛitu 
(Monsoon), Sharad Ṛitu (Autumn), Hemant Ṛitu (Pre-Winter) and Shishir 
Ṛitu (Winter)
Maasa One earth month. Normally 30 earth days long. Consists of two phases of 
the moon.
Pakṣha One phase of the moon, either waxing or waning. Normally 15 earth days 
long.
Earth Day One day and night equivalent to 24 modern hours.
Muhoorta One-thirtieth fraction of the day, equivalent to 48 modern minutes.
Kalaa One-thirtieth fraction of the Muhoorta, equivalent to 1.6 modern 
minutes.
Kaaṣhṭhaa One-thirtieth fraction of the Kalaa, equivalent to 3.2 modern seconds.
Nimeṣhaa One blink of the human eye. One-eighteenth fraction of the Kaaṣhṭhaa, 
equivalent to 0.17̇ modern seconds.
The 81st - 86th shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
Duties of the four classes of humans
(guptyartham) (tu) For the protection, prosperity and the maintenance of order in (asya)
this (sarvasya) entire (sargasya) creation, (saḥ) he, (mahaadyutiḥ) the ultimate source 
of light, (akalpayat) designed and created the rules for different classes which are 
assigned (pṛithak) different (karmaaṇi) duties akin to various parts of the body
(jaanaam) known for their particular functions i.e. (mukha) the mouth for speech, 
(baahoo) the arms for protection, (uroo) the stomach and thighs for sustenance and 
(pad) the feet for carrying and serving. 1:87

मनुस्मृित अध्याय १ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 1
41
For the performance of duties like (adhyayanam)studying and (adhyaapanam)teaching, 
(yajanam) performing yajña and (yaajanam) helping others in the performance of yajña
and (tathaa) similarly (daanam) making donations for worthy causes (cha) and 
(pratigrahaḥ) taking donations (eva) as well, (braahmaṇaanaam) the class of 
Braahmaṇa (akalpayat) was designed. 1:88
The attributes and duties (kṣhatriyasya) of the Kṣhatriya class (samaasataḥ) are briefly 
described as (rakṣhaṇam) the protection (prajaanaam) of the masses, (daanam) the 
performance of charity, (ijyaa) the performance of yajña (cha) and (adhyayanam)
studying (eva) as well, (cha) while (aprasaktiḥ) remaining detached (viṣhayeṣhu) from 
the worldly pleasures. 1:89
The attributes and duties (vaishyasya) of the Vaishya class are (rakṣhaṇam) protection 
and rearing (pashoonaam) animals, (daanam) charity, (ijyaa) performing yajña, (cha)
and (adhyayanam) studying the scriptures (eva) as well, (vaṇikpatham) trading,
(kuseedam) lending money on interest (cha) and engaging (kṛiṣhim) in agriculture (eva)
as well. 1:90

(prabhuḥ) God (samaadishat) has decreed (ekam) one and (eva)(hi) only one (karma)

The importance of the code of conduct
(aachaaraḥ) The details of the righteous conduct (uktaḥ) as detailed (shruti) in the Vedas 
(cha) and (smaartaḥ) the subsequent literature (eva) as well, (paramaḥ) are the ultimate 
guide (dharmaḥ) to dharma. Hence (asmin) the (dvijaḥ) noble souls who seek (nityam)
everlasting (aatmavaan) inner strength should (sadaa) always (syaat) be (yuktaḥ)
engaged in a conduct conforming (tasmaat) to these rules. 1:108

(vipraḥ) The scholar who (vichyutaḥ) aberrates (aachaaraat) from this conduct (na) does 
not (ashnute) attain (phalam) the fruit of happiness and bliss mentioned in (veda) the 
Vedas. (tu) And the one who (sañyuktaḥ) is fully engaged (aachaareṇa) in this conduct 
(bhavet) gets (sampoorṇa) all of (phala) the benefits (bhaag) assigned to oneself. 1:109
(dṛiṣhṭvaa) After watching (evam) this (aachaarataḥ) conduct resulting (gatim) in 
attainment (dharmasya) of dharma, (munayaḥ) the sages (jagṛihuḥ) accepted this 
(aachaaram) conduct as (param) the ultimate (moolam) root (sarvasya) of all (tapasaḥ)
of the fortitude. 1:110

Dr. Surendra Kumar is of the opinion that in order to maintain the continuity of the subject 
being discussed, the first chapter does not end here and the first twenty five shlokas from 
the second chapter should be included in the first chapter.

मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2
44
Chapter 2
(nibodhata) Listen about and follow (tam) that (dharmaḥ) conduct (yaḥ) which
(abhyanujñaataḥ) is worth establishing (hṛidayena) in the mind, heart and soul and 
which (sevitaḥ) is displayed (nityam) persistently (sadbhiḥ) by the benevolent 
(vidvadbhiḥ) scholars who (adveṣharaagibhiḥ) are devoid of all vices including jealousy, 
favoritism etc. 2:1
Importance of desire
(na) Neither (kaamaatmataa) excessive attachment to desires (na)(cha) nor 
(akaamataa) an absolute lack of desire (eva) as well (asti) is (prashastaa) commendable 
(iha) in this World, (hi) because (vedaadhigamaḥ) seeking Vedic wisdom (cha) and 
(karmayogaḥ) engagement in (vaidikaḥ) Vedic duties is (kaamyaḥ) highly desirable. 2:2
(kaamaḥ) Every desire (moolaḥ) originates from (saṅkalpa) a thought or the realization 
that something is yet to be obtained. All of (yajñaaḥ) the yajña and actions 
(sambhavaaḥ) can be accomplished (vai) only with (saṅkalpa) a mental determination. 
(smṛitaaḥ) As per the Vedas and other scriptures (sarve) all of (vrataani) the adherence
to a righteous code of conduct and fulfillment of one’s (dharmaaḥ) duties towards self 
 
2:1 िवद्विद्भः सेिवतः सिद्भिनर्त्यमद्वेषरािगिभः ।
 दयेनाभ्यनु
 ातो यो धमर्स्तंिनबोधत ॥१॥
िवद्विद्भः । सेिवतः । सिद्भः । िनत्यम्। अद्वेषरािगिभः ॥  दयेन । अभ्यन ातः ु । यः । धमर्ः । तम्। िनबोधत ॥
1. vidvadbhiḥ sevitaḥ sadbhirnityamadveṣharaagibhiḥ,
hṛidayenaabhyanujñaato yo dharmastan nibodhata.
vidvadbhiḥ sevitaḥ sadbhiḥ nityam adveṣharaagibhiḥ,
hṛidayena abhyanujñaataḥ yaḥ dharmaḥ tam nibodhata.
2:2कामात्मता न प्रशस्ता न चैवेहास्त्यकामता ।
काम्यो िह वेदािधगमः कमर्योग  वैिदकः ॥२॥
कामात्मता । न। प्रशस्ता । न। च । एव । इह। अिस्त । अकामता ॥
काम्यः । िह। वेदािधगमः । कमर्योगः । च । वैिदकः ॥
2. kaamaatmataa na prashastaa na chaivehaastyakaamataa,
kaamyo hi vedaadhigamaḥ karmayogashcha vaidikaḥ. kaamaatmataa na prashastaa na cha eva iha asti akaamataa,
kaamyaḥ hi vedaadhigamaḥ karmayogaḥ cha vaidikaḥ.
मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2

(cha) and (yama) towards the society as well (jaaḥ) stem from (saṅkalpa) mental 
determination. 2:3
(yat)(yat) Whatever (kiñchit)types of actions (kurute) are performed by anyone (tat)(tat)
they are all (cheṣhṭitam) initiated (kaamasya) by a desire (hi) because, (iha) in this World,
(kaachit) any (kriyaa) action (akaamasya) without a desire has (na) never (karhichit) ever 
(dṛishyate) been witnessed. 2:4
Whosoever (vartamaanaḥ) is currently (samyak) wholeheartedly engaged (teṣhu) in 
these benevolent conducts, he/she (gachchhati) attains (amara)(lokataam) nirvaaṇa 
(cha) and is also (samashnute) bestowed with fulfillment of (sarvaan) all (eva)(kaamaan)
desires (yathaa) for which the deeds (saṅkalpitaan) were initiated. 2:5

5. teṣhu samyagvartamaano gachchhatyamaralokataam,
मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2
46
The four roots of dharma
(moolam) The roots (dharma) of the righteous conduct stem from (akhilaḥ) the all 
encompassing (vedaḥ) Vedic wisdom, (smṛiti)(sheele) the other scriptures authored by 
those who are compassionate (cha) and (vidaam) have mastered this knowledge, the 
examples set by (tat) them in their own (aachaaraḥ) conduct (cha) and the engagements 
(saadhoonaam) by the benevolent for bringing (tuṣhṭiḥ) contentment and bliss 
(aatmanaḥ) to their souls (eva) as well. For an action performed for contentment of the 
soul, to qualify as righteous, that action has to be benevolent. 2:6
The 7th shloka is not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
Benefits of following dharma
(vidvaan) A scholarly person (tu) after (nikhilam) completely (sam)(avekṣhya) examining 
(sarvam) all of (idam) these facts with his/her (jñaana) knowledge based (chakṣhuṣhaa)
discriminating intellect and using (shruti) the Vedas as (praamaaṇyataḥ) the final rubric, 
should determine his/her (sva) own (dharme) duties and proper conducts and 
(nivisheta) get invested in them (vai) accordingly. 2:8
 
yathaa saṅkalpitaañshchaiva sarvaankaamaansamashnute.
teṣhu samyak vartamaanaḥ gachchhati amara-lokataam,
yathaa saṅkalpitaan cha eva sarvaan kaamaan samashnute.

8. sarvan tu samavekṣhyedan nikhilañ jñaanachakṣhuṣhaa,
मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2
47
(hi) Because, (maanavaḥ) the humans who (anutiṣhṭhan) follow this (dharmam) code of 
righteous conduct as (uditam) propounded in (shruti) the Vedas and (smṛiti) the 
subsequent scriptures, (avaapnoti) attains (keertim) fame (iha) in this World (cha) and 
the place of (anuttamam) unparalleled (sukham) bliss and happiness (pretya) upon 
death. 2:9
Vedas are not the subject matter of a debate
(vijñeyaḥ) Know the wisdom handed down by (shrutiḥ) oral tradition (tu) as (vedaḥ) the 
Veda and the subsequent (shaastram)treatise on (dharma) dharma by sages (tu) as their 
(smṛitiḥ) understanding of it. (te) These (dharmaḥ) codes of conduct are universally 
applicable in (sarva) all of (artheṣhu) the situations and (ameemaansye) are not 
debatable based on the personal opinions of the unscholarly (hi) because they 
(nirbabhau) have evolved (taabhyaam) from these two types of scriptures (vai) only. 2:10
 
shrutipraamaaṇyato vidvaansvadharme nivisheta vai.
sarvam tu sam-avekṣhya idam nikhilam jñaana-chakṣhuṣhaa,
shruti-praamaaṇyataḥ vidvaan sva-dharme nivisheta vai.

10. shrutistu vedo vijñeyo dharmashaastran tu vai smṛitiḥ,
te sarvaartheṣhvameemaansye taabhyaan dharmo hi nirbabhau.
shrutiḥ tu vedaḥ vijñeyaḥ dharma-shaastram tu vai smṛitiḥ,
te sarva-artheṣhu ameemaansye taabhyaam dharmaḥ hi nirbabhau.
मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2
48
(yaḥ) Those (dvijaḥ) twice born who (aashrayaat) with the help of (hetu)(shaastra)
sophistry (avamanyeta) try to discredit (te) these two (moole) sources of dharma, (saḥ)
they (bahiṣhkaaryaḥ) should be ostracized (saadhubhiḥ) by the benevolent because 
(nindakaḥ) whosoever criticizes (veda) the Vedas is (naastikaḥ) a non-believer. 2:11
(vedaḥ) The Vedas, (smṛitiḥ) subsequent scriptures, following (sadaachaaraḥ) the 
conduct of the benevolent (cha) and the inspiration from (svasya) one’s own 
(priyam)(aatmanaḥ) conscience, (etat) these (chatur) four (vidham) types are (praahuḥ)
said to be (saakṣhaat) the true (lakṣhaṇam) attributes of the origins (dharmasya) of the 
righteous conduct. 2:12
Those who are (asaktaanaam) unattached (kaameṣhu) to the desires of (artha) wealth 
etc., are the ones who (vidheeyate) possess (jñaanam) the true knowledge of (dharma)
the dharma. For those (jijñaa)(samaanaanaam) who seek the knowledge of (dharmam)
the dharma, (shrutiḥ) the Veda is (paramam) the ultimate (pramaaṇam) reference. 2:13

2:13अथर्कामेष्वस ानांधमर् ानंिवधीयते।
धम िज ासमानानांप्रमाणंपरमंश्र
ु
ितः ॥१३॥
मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2
49
(yatra) When (shruti) the Vedas say (dvaidham) two different things about something 
(tatra)(tu) then (ubhau) both of them (syaat) are considered to be (dharmau) dharma.
(ubhau) Both of (tau) them (uktau) are (smṛitau) accepted as (samyak) valid (dharmau)
duties (maneeṣhibhiḥ) by the knowledgeable scholars who are in control of their mind,
(hi) because the Vedas are devoid of any contradictions. 2:14
For example, it is said that the yajña should be performed (udite) at the time of the 
sunrise (cha) and (anudite) at the time of the sunset (tathaa) and (eva) even when those 
(samaya) times (adhyuṣhite) have passed. It means that (yajñaḥ) yajña could be and 
should (vartate) be performed (sarvathaa) at all times; (iti)(iyam)this is what (vaideekee)
the Vedas (shrutiḥ) are implying. 2:15
The 16th shloka is not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.

dharmam jijñaa-samaanaanaam pramaaṇam paramam shrutiḥ.

15. udite’nudite chaiva samayaadhyuṣhite tathaa,

मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2
50
Nation called Aaryaavarta
(deva) The divine (nadyoḥ) rivers from (sarasvatee) the Sindhu in the west and 
(dṛiṣhadvatyoḥ) the Brahmaputra in the east facilitate the noble conduct of the scholars; 
on the land (antaram) between (yat) these rivers (desham) a nation has been (nirmitam)
built (deva) by the divinities, and (tam) that nation inhabited by scholars (prachakṣhate)
is known as (brahmaavartam) Brahmaavarta. 2:17
(tasmin) In that (deshe) nation (yaḥ) whatever (aachaaraḥ) code of conduct has been 
(paaramparya) traditionally (kramaagataḥ) passed down through the lineage of sages 
(varṇaanaam) for all four classes and (saantaraalaanaam) for all four stages of life as 
well, (saḥ) that (uchyate) is said to be the code of (sadaachaaraḥ) righteous conduct. 2:18
The 19th shloka is not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
(sarva) Without any discrimination, for (svam)(svam) their (shikṣheran) studies, 
upliftment and (charitram) character building, (maanavaaḥ) people (pṛithivyaam) from 
all over the earth would come to (etat) this (desha) nation (sakaashaat) to seek the 
company of (agrajanmanaḥ)the best scholars (prasootasya) born here and to learn from 
them. 2:20
 
2:17 सरस्वती षद्वत्योद वनद्योयर्दन्तरम्
। तंदेविनिमर्तंदेशंब्र ावत प्रच ते॥१७॥
सरस्वती षद्वत्योः । देवनद्योः । यत्। अन्तरम्॥ तम्। देविनिमर्तम्। देशम्। ब्र ावतर्म्। प्रच ते॥
17. sarasvateedṛiṣhadvatyordevanadyoryadantaram,
tan devanirmitan desham brahmaavartam prachakṣhate.
sarasvatee-dṛiṣhadvatyoḥ deva-nadyoḥ yat antaram,
tam deva-nirmitam desham brahmaavartam prachakṣhate.
2:18 तिस्मन्देशेय आचारः पारम्पयर्क्रमागतः ।
वणार्नांसान्तरालानांस सदाचार उच्यते॥१८॥
तिस्मन्। देशे। यः । आचारः । पारम्पयर्क्रमागतः ॥ वणार्नाम्। सान्तरालानाम्। सः । सदाचारः । उच्यते॥
18. tasmindeshe ya aachaaraḥ paaramparyakramaagataḥ,
varṇaanaan saantaraalaanaan sa sadaachaara uchyate.
tasmin deshe yaḥ aachaaraḥ paaramparyakramaagataḥ,
varṇaanaam saantaraalaanaam saḥ sadaachaaraḥ uchyate.
2:20 एतद्देशप्रसू
तस्य सकाशादग्रजन्मनः ।
मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2
51
(madhyam) In between (himavad) the Himalaya in the north (cha) and (vindhyayoḥ) the 
Vindhyaachala mountain ranges in the south (eva)(api) as well as (prayaagaat) from 
Prayaaga to the place (pratyak) in the west (yat) where (praak) the Sarasvatee river 
(vinashanaat) disappears into the sea, all of this area (prakeertitaḥ) is termed as 
(madhya) the middle (deshaḥ) region. 2:21
(aa)(samudraat) From the ocean shoreline (poorvaat) in the east (tu) to (aa)(samudraat)
the ocean shoreline (pashchimaat) in the west (eva) and also (antaram) between (tayoḥ)
those (giryoḥ) two mountain ranges, this land is (vai) indeed (budhaaḥ) called 
(aaryaavartam) Aaryaavarta (viduḥ) by the learned. 2:22
 
स्वंस्वंच रत्रंिश ेरन्पृ
िथव्यांसवर्मानवाः ॥२०॥
एतत्। देशप्रसतस्य ू । सकाशात्। अग्रजन्मनः ॥ स्वम्। स्वम्। च रत्रम्। िश ेरन्। पिथव्याम ृ ्। सवर्मानवाः ॥
20. etaddeshaprasootasya sakaashaadagrajanmanaḥ,
svan svañ charitrañ shikṣheranpṛithivyaan sarvamaanavaaḥ. etat desha-prasootasya sakaashaat agra-janmanaḥ,
svam svam charitram shikṣheran pṛithivyaam sarva-maanavaaḥ.
2:21 िहमविद्वन्ध्ययोमर्ध्यंयत्प्रािग्वनशनादिप ।
प्रत्यगेव प्रयागाच्च मध्यदेशः प्रक ितर्तः ॥२१॥
िहमविद्वन्ध्ययोः । मध्यम्। यत्। प्राक्। िवनशनात्। अिप ॥ प्रत्यक्।एव । प्रयागात्। च । मध्यदेशः । प्रक ितर्तः ॥

मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2
52
(tu) And in this land (yatra) where (svabhaavataḥ) by default (kṛiṣhṇasaaraḥ) blackbuck
(mṛigaḥ) deers (charati) roam in abundance, (jñeyaḥ) know (saḥ) this (deshaḥ) nation 
(yajñiyaḥ) as the one fit for performance of yajña. (tu) And (ataḥ)(paraḥ) beyond the 
boundaries of this nation, (deshaḥ) the land of people with (mlechchha) lower levels of 
desires and impure languages begins. 2:23
The 24th shloka is not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
(eṣhaa) This is (yoniḥ) the source (dharmasya) of the dharma. I have (samaasena) briefly 
(prakeertitaa) described (sambhavaḥ) the origin and the creation (asya) of this 
(sarvasya) entire universe, for (vaḥ) your benefit. (cha) And now (nibodhata) listen about
(dharmaan) the duties of (varṇa) various classes mentioned before. 2:25
Various sacraments for humans
(dvijanmanaam) The twice-born should (kaaryaḥ) perform all of the sixteen 
(sanskaaraḥ) sacraments, (niṣhekaadiḥ) from conception to (shareera) cremations, 
carried out properly (puṇyaiḥ) with the pious (karmabhiḥ) yajña (cha) and the chanting 
of the associated (vaidikaiḥ) Vedic mantras. These should be done for (paavanaḥ) the

53
purification of the mind, body and soul, during (iha) this lifetime (cha) as well as (pretya)
the next life cycles as well. 2:26
Maharṣhi Manu is not against performing the sacraments for the Shoodra. He talks about 
the sacraments for the Shoodra later.
Various sacraments performed (homaiḥ) along with a yajña, (dvijaanaam) by the twice 
born, (gaarbhaiḥ) the ones performed in the prenatal stage, (jaata)(karma) the ones 
performed within a few months after the birth, (chaula) the ones performed in the early 
childhood and (mauñjee)(nibandhanaiḥ) the ones performed when the child is ready to 
start the studies, all of them (apamṛijyate) help with the removal of (enaḥ) vices and 
impurities, those that are (baijikam) hereditary (cha) and those acquired (gaarbhikam)
during pregnancy and early childhood as well, due to mistakes committed by parents 
and other family members. 2:27
(svaadhyaayena) By diligent and persistent self study of the scriptures containing the 
knowledge about getting over the three types of sorrows, (vrataiḥ) by maintaining 
discipline, determination and fortitude, (homaiḥ) by making offerings into the fire twice 
a day during the student phase of life, (traividyena) by learning and teaching the three 
types of knowledge contained in the vedas, (ijyayaa) by performing the fortnightly,

seasonal and yearly yajña, (sutaiḥ) by instilling proper values in children,

Sacrament at the time of the birth
(vidheeyate) A rule has been made for the performance of (karma) a sacrament (jaata)
for the newborn immediately after the birth of (punsaḥ) a child. It starts (praak) before
(naabhi) the umbilical cord (vardhanaat) is cut. During this process using (hiraṇya) a 
golden stick, (asya) the child is (cha) also (praashanam) given a taste of (madhu) a mix 
of honey and (sarpiṣhaam) clarified butter, (mantravat) while Vedic mantras are 
chanted. 2:29
Naming of the newborn
(tu) Then after the birth, (dashamyaam) on the tenth day (vaa) or (dvaadashyaam) the 
twelfth day (vaa) or (puṇye) any convenient (tithau) day and (muhoorte) time

(nakṣhatre) associated with any star (vaa) or (guṇaanvite) when the weather is

(braahmaṇasya) The Braahmaṇa’s child’s name (syaat) should reflect (maṅgalyam)
auspiciousness, (kṣhatriyasya) the kṣhatriya’s child’s name should represent 
(balaanvitam) physical strength and valor, (vaishyasya) the vaishya’s child’s name 
should represent (sañyuktam) association with (dhana) wealth (tu) and (shoodrasya) the 
shoodra’s child’s name should represent (jugupsitam) helpfulness. 2:31
The name given to a child (syaat) should also represent the function he/she is expected 
to perform. The name of a child expected to become (braahmaṇasya) a Braahmaṇa
should (sharmavat) convey scholarly bliss, (raajñaḥ) a kṣhatriya (samanvitam) an 
association with (rakṣhaa) protection, (vaishyasya) a vaishya (sañyuktam) integration 
with (puṣhṭi) prosperity and (shoodrasya) a shoodra (sañyuktam) an association with 
(preṣhya) service. 2:32

मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2
56
It may seem inappropriate to many that a child is given a varṇa specific name, when the 
true varṇa of the child is yet to be determined. The name given at the birth is a symbol 
of the expectations of the family. In most cases the child would learn from the parents 
and continue the legacy of their varṇa. However, later if the student is deemed to be in 
another varṇa by the guru then his/her name would be changed by the guru 
accordingly.
The The names given (streeṇaam) to a female child should be (sukhodyam) easy to 
pronounce, with (vispaṣhṭa) an unambiguous (artham) meaning, (antam) ending in 
(deergha) a long (varṇa) vowels, (akrooram) soft, (manoharam) pleasing and 
(abhidhaanavat) representing (maṅgalyam) auspiciousness and (aasheervaada)
blessings. 2:33
Taking the newborn out of home and feeding him/her grains for the first time
(chaturthe) In the fourth (maasi) month after birth (shishoḥ) the child (kartavyam)
should be taken (niṣhkramaṇam) out (gṛihaat) of the home and to a temple. And 
(ṣhaṣhṭhe) in the sixth (maasi) month after birth, the child should be (praashanam) fed 
(anna) grains for the first time. (vaa) Alternatively these sacraments can also be done 
(yat) whenever it is (iṣhṭam) convenient and (maṅgalam) favorable (kule) for the 
family.2:34

य म ु ्। शद्रस्य ू । प्रेष्यसं

sharmavat braahmaṇasya syaat raajñaḥ rakṣhaa-samanvitam,
vaishyasya puṣhṭi-sañyuktam shoodrasya preṣhya-sañyuktam.

Tonsuring of the newborn’s head
(chodanaat) As decreed by (shruti) the Vedas, (sarveṣhaam) all of (dvijaateenaam) the 
twice born (dharmataḥ) following the proper procedure should (eva) as well 
(kartavyam) perform (chooḍaa)(karma) the tonsuring of the head of the child either 
(prathame) in the first (abde) year (vaa) or (tṛiteeye) in the third year after the birth. 2:35
Starting the formal education
(tu) Then (upanaayanam)sacrament for starting the formal education (kurveeta)should 
be performed as per this timeline; (aṣhṭame) during the eighth (abde) year (garbha)
after birth (braahmaṇasya) for the Braahmaṇa, (ekaadashe) during the eleventh year 
(garbhaat) after birth (raajñaḥ) for the Kṣhatriya and (dvaadashe) during the twelfth 
year (garbhaat) after birth (vishaḥ) for the Vaishya. 2:36

36. garbhaaṣhṭame’bde kurveeta braahmaṇasyopanaayanam,
मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2
58
Maharṣhi Manu has not decreed against the performance of the tonsuring of the head 
and the starting of the formal education sacraments for the Shoodra. They can 
optionally perform it as well. In fact Maharṣhi Manu doesn’t believe in the assignment 
of the class by birth. A child of Shoodra who shows the ability to learn can and should 
be promoted by the guru accordingly.
In case the child shows extraordinary brilliance in the early childhood and shows a 
desire to learn faster, then his/her sacrament for starting the formal education can be 
(kaaryam) performed earlier as per an accelerated timeline; (pañchame) during the fifth 
year after birth for the one who has (kaamasya) the desire of becoming 
(brahmavarchasa) an scholarly (viprasya) Braahmaṇa, (ṣhaṣhṭhe) during the sixth year 
after birth for the one who has (arthinaḥ) the desire of becoming (bala) a strong 
(raajñaḥ) Kṣhatriya and (aṣhṭame) during the eighth year after birth for the one who has 
(iha) the desire of becoming (arthinaḥ) a wealthy (vaishyasya) Vaishya. 2:37
In case of delays, performing (saavitree) the start of the formal education for those 
desirous (braahmaṇasya) of becoming a Braahmaṇa before they are (aa)(ṣhoḍashaat)
sixteen years old, for those (bandhoḥ) desirous of (kṣhatra) becoming a Kṣhatriya before 
they are (aa)(dvaaviñshaat) twenty two years old and for those desirous of becoming 
(vishaḥ) a Vaishya before they are (aa)(chaturviñshateḥ) twenty four years old, (na)
doesn’t (ativartate) violate the norms. 2:38
 
garbhaadekaadashe raajño garbhaattu dvaadashe vishaḥ. garbha-aṣhṭame abde kurveeta braahmaṇasya upanaayanam,
garbhaat ekaadashe raajñaḥ garbhaat tu dvaadashe vishaḥ.
2:37 ब्र वचर्सकामस्य काय िवप्रस्य पञ्चमे।
रा ो बलािथर्नः ष ेवैश्यस्येहािथर्नोऽ मे॥३७॥
ब्र वचर्सकामस्य । कायर्म्। िवप्रस्य । पञ्चमे॥ रा ः । बलािथर्नः ।ष े। वैश्यस्य । इह। अिथर्नः । अ मे॥
37. brahmavarchasakaamasya kaaryam viprasya pañchame,
raajño balaarthinaḥ ṣhaṣhṭhe vaishyasyehaarthino’ṣhṭame.
brahmavarchasa-kaamasya kaaryam viprasya pañchame,
raajñaḥ bala-arthinaḥ ṣhaṣhṭhe vaishyasya iha arthinaḥ aṣhṭame.

मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2
59
(ataḥ) When these time (oordhvam) limits have passed (api) and (asanskṛitaaḥ) the 
sacraments have not been (yathaa)(kaalam) timely performed, (ete) those individuals 
from (trayaḥ) all of three classes, (bhavanti) having (vraatyaaḥ) drifted away from 
righteous conduct are considered (patitaaḥ) fallen (saavitree) from grace, and 
(vigarhitaaḥ) are subject to criticism from (aarya) the other members of the society. 2:39
(vidhivat) As per the norm, (braahmaṇaḥ) the twice born should (hi) indeed (na) refrain 
from any kind of (aacharet) engagement, (karhichit) either (braahmaan) for the purpose 
of studies (cha) or (yaunaan) for establishing marital (sambandhaan)relationship, (saha)
with (etaiḥ) these (apootaiḥ) fallen individuals, (api) even (aapadi) in case of an 
emergency. 2:40

मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2
60
Clothes and mats for a student
As a mat to sit on, (brahmachaariṇaḥ) the students from the three classes can use 
(charmaaṇi) the skin of animals that have died naturally, (kaarṣhṇa) the blackbuck deer 
skin for the Braahmaṇa, (raurav) the golden deer skin for the Kṣhatriya and 
(avaastaani) the goat skin for the Vaishya. And they are allowed (vaseeran) to wear 
clothes made from (shaaṇa) the cotton for the Braahmaṇa, (kṣhauma) the silk for the 
Kṣhatriya (cha) and (aavikaani) the wool for the Vaishya (aanupoorvyeṇa)
respectively.2:41
The girdle for a student
(mekhalaa) The girdle (viprasya) for a Braahmaṇa’s waist should be (shlakṣhṇaa)
smooth and (kaaryaa) made by (samaa) putting together (trivṛit) three braids of 
(mauñjee) mauñjee grass fiber, (kṣhatriyasya) for the Kṣhatriya it should be made (jyaa)
from the bow string which in turn is made (maurvee) from the maurvee grass fiber (tu)
and (vaishyasya) for the Vaishya it should be made (shaṇataantavee) from the thread 
of sana. 2:42
(tu) In case (muñja) the mauñjee etc. grass fiber (alaabhe) is not available, then the fiber 
from (kusha) the kusha, (ashmantaka) ashmantaka and (balvajaiḥ) balvaja grass

The sacred thread for a student
(upaveetam) The sacred thread (viprasya) for the Braahmaṇa should be made 
(kaarpaasam) of the cotton thread, (raajñaḥ) for the Kṣhatriya (shaṇa) of the sana

(vṛitam) a knot (oordhva) on the top. 2:44

मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2
63
The student seeking donations
(pareetya) After (pradakṣhiṇam) circumambulating (agnim) the holy fire, a student 
should stand (pratigṛihya) holding (eepsitam) a desired (daṇḍam)staff in hand (cha) and 
(upasthaaya) facing (bhaaskaram) the sun, and then (charet) should (bhaikṣham) seek 
donations (yathaa) as per (vidhi) the norms. 2:48
(upaneetaḥ) After being vested with the sacred thread, while (charet) seeking 
(bhaikṣham) donations, (dvijottamaḥ) the Braahmaṇa should use (bhavat) the word 
“bhavat” (poorvam) in the beginning of the call for donation, (raajanyaḥ) the Kṣhatriya
should use (bhavat) the word “bhavat” (madhyam) in the middle of the call (tu) and 
(vaishyaḥ) the Vaishya should use (bhavat) the word “bhavat” (uttaram) at the end of 
the call; “bhavatee bhikṣham dadaatu”, “bhikṣham bhavatee dadaatu” and “bhikṣham 
dadaatu bhavatee” respectively. 2:49
A student should (prathamam) first (bhikṣheta) seek (bhikṣhaam) donations from 
his/her (maataram) mother, (svasaaram)sister (vaa) or (maatuḥ) mother’s (nijaam) real 
 
ṛijavaḥ te tu sarve syuḥ avraṇaaḥ saumya-darshanaaḥ,
anudvegakaraaḥ nṛeeṇaam satvachaḥ anagni-dooṣhitaaḥ.

(bhagineem) sister (cha) or (enam) those (yaa) who (na) would not (avamaanayet) turn

water. Maharṣhi Manu is advising that while eating the focus should be on the food and

(nityam) Each (cha) and every time, (poojayet) respect should be shown towards 
(ashanam) the food. (dṛiṣhṭvaa) The sight of food should induce (hṛiṣhyet) excitement

(hi) When (ashanam) the food (poojitam) is respected it (nityam) always (yachchhati)

shown while (tat) its (bhuktam) consumption, (tu) then it (naashayet) diminishes 
(ubhayam) both of (idam) these. 2:55

मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2
66
(uchchhiṣhṭam) The leftovers from one’s plate (na) should not be (dadyaat) offered to 
(kasyachit) anyone else. One (na) should not (adyaat) eat (eva) again (cha) and again 
(tathaa)(antaraa) between meals (cha) and (kuryaat) should (na) not (ati) (ashanam)
overeat (eva) as well. (cha) And after the meals one (na) should not (vrajet) go (kvachit)
anywhere (uchchhiṣhṭaḥ) without rinsing the mouth. 2:56
(ati) Excessive (bhojanam) eating diminishes (anaarogyam) health, (anaayuṣhyam)
longevity (cha) and (asvargyam) happiness. It is considered (apuṇyam) unrighteous and 
is (lokavidviṣhṭam) looked down upon in the society. (tasmaat) Hence, (tat) it is
(parivarjayet) always forbidden. 2:57

मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2
67
Sipping the Water
Using their right hand (nitya) each and every (kaalam) time, (vipraḥ) the educated 
(upaspṛishet) can sip water (braahmeṇa) from the Braahma (teerthena) Teertha, from 
(kaaya) the Kaaya Teertha (vaa) or from the (trai)(dashikaabhyaam) Traidashika
Teertha, but (na) never (kadaachana) ever (pitryeṇa) from the Pitṛi Teertha. 2.58
(braahmam) The Braahma (teertham) Teertha (prachakṣhate) is known as the valley 
near the wrist (moolasya)(tale) at the base of (aṅguṣhṭa)the thumb, (kaayam)the Kaaya 
Teertha is the valley on the side of the hand near (moole) the base of (aṅguli) the pinky

After finishing the meal, they should (poorvam) first (aachaamet) sip (apaḥ) the water 
(triḥ) thrice again (tataḥ) followed by (pramṛijyaat) rinsing (mukham) the mouth (dviḥ)

(aatmaanam) the heart (cha) and (shiraḥ) the head (adbhiḥ) with water. 2:60
The 61st – 62nd shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
Wearing the sacramental thread
When (dvijaḥ) a scholar wears the sacramental thread on his/her left shoulder and 
under the right arm (uddhṛite) by raising his/her (dakṣhiṇe) right (paaṇau) hand, he/she 
is (uchyate) said to be (upaveetee) Upaveetee; the one who wears it on the right 
shoulder by raising (savye) the left hand is said to be (praacheena)(aaveetee)

Praacheena Aaveetee; and the one who wears it (kaṇṭha) around the neck (sajjane) like

In case (mekhalaam) the girdle, (ajinam) a cloth, (daṇḍam) the staff, (upaveetam) the 
sacred thread or (kamaṇḍalum) the wooden bowl (vinaṣhṭaani) gets debilitated, it
should (praasya) be assigned (apsu) to a flowing water stream and then (mantravat)
along with the chants of associated Vedic mantras, (anyaani) another new replacement 
(gṛihṇeeta) should be assumed. 2:64
(vidheeyate) The rule is that (keshaantaḥ) the tonsuring of the head sacrament should 
be performed latest by the age of (ṣhoḍashe) sixteen (varṣhe) years (braahmaṇasya) for 
a Braahmaṇa, by the age of (dvaaviñshe) twenty two years (raajanyabandhoḥ) for a 
Kṣhatriya and (dvyadhike) additional two years(tataḥ) to it i.e. by the age of twenty four 
years (vaishyasya) for a Vaishya. 2:65

The 66th - 67th shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
I have (proktaḥ) elaborated on (eṣhaḥ) these (vidhiḥ) procedures of various (puṇyaḥ)
virtuous sacraments including (aupanaayanikaḥ) the start of the education, that 
(utpatti)(vyañjakaḥ) grow and transform (dvijaateenaam) the twice borns. Now 
(nibodhata) learn (karma)(yogam) about the duties of the scholars. 2:68
Start of the education
(upaneeya) After completion of the sacrament for the start of the education, (guruḥ) the 
teacher (shikṣhayet) should teach (shiṣhyam) the disciple (aaditaḥ) starting with various 
(aachaaram) codes of conduct related to (shaucham) hygiene (cha) and purification of 
the body, the mind, the soul and the environment including (kaaryam) the procedures 
for (agni) yajña (cha) and (sandhyopaasanam) meditation (eva) as well. 2:69
The 70th shloka is not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.

मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2
71
Paying respect to the teacher
(aarambhe) At the start of (brahma) the lesson (cha) and (avasaane) at its end as well, 
the student, with his/her (hastau) palms (saṅhatya) pressed together in (saḥ)(hi) what 
is (smṛitaḥ) called (brahma)(añjaliḥ) the namaste pose, should (sadaa) always pay 
respect to the teacher by first bowing to the teacher and then (graahyau) seeking and 
touching (guroḥ) the teacher’s (paadau) feet and should (adhyeyam) study diligently 
during the lesson. 2:71
(kaaryam) While (upa)(saṅgrahaṇam) seeking and touching (guroḥ) the teacher’s feet, 
(paaṇinaa) the hands of the student should (vyatyasta) be crossed, so that (savyena) the 
left hand (spraṣhṭavyaḥ) touches (savyaḥ) the left feet (cha) and (dakṣhiṇena) the right 
hand touches (dakṣhiṇaḥ) the right feet. 2:72
Discipline in the class
(tu) During the class (guruḥ) the teacher should (nitya)(kaalam) always (atandritaḥ)
remain focused and in command and (brooyaat) should say (adhyeṣhyamaaṇam) to the

मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2
72
students, “(bho) You should now (adheeṣhva) study (iti) this” (cha) and should say, “(iti)
it (astu) is time for (viraamaḥ) a break” (aaramet) at the end of the class. 2:73
God’s primary name and basic qualities
The chant of (brahmaṇaḥ) the God’s (praṇavam) primary name i.e. om should 
(sarvadaa) always (kuryaat) be performed both (aadau) at the start (cha) and (ante) at 
the end of the class. The lesson learned (anoṅ)(kṛitam) without the chant of om 
(poorvam) at the beginning, (sravati) leaks away from the memory (cha) and the one 
without the chant of om (purastaat) at the end, (visheeryati) does not take hold in one’s 
mind. 2:74
The 75th shloka is not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu. 
The three basic sounds of (akaaram) “A”, (ukaaram) “U” (cha) and (makaaram) “M” (api)
as well, represent the summary (trayaat) of the three types of (veda) knowledge 
contained in the four vedas provided by God, (prajaapatiḥ) the lord of masses; the 
knowledge which has been analyzed deeply by the sages, who, from it have (niraduhat)
extracted God’s three primary qualities as (bhooḥ) the basis and sustainer of all being,

ब्र णः । प्रणवम्। कुयार्त्। आदौ । अन्ते। च । सवर्दा ॥ स्रवित । अनोङ्कृतम्।पवर्मू ्। परस्तात ु ्। च । िवशीयर्ित॥
74. brahmaṇaḥ praṇavaṅ kuryaadaadaavante cha sarvadaa,
sravatyanoṅkṛitam poorvam purastaachcha visheeryati.
brahmaṇaḥ praṇavam kuryaat aadau ante cha sarvadaa,
sravati anoṅ-kṛitam poorvam purastaat cha visheeryati.
मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2
73
(bhuvaḥ) the destroyer of evil (cha) and (svaḥ) the creator of happiness. (iti) This is it 
(cha) and (iti) this summarizes it all. 2:76
Importance of the Gaayatree Mantra
(prajaapatiḥ) God (eva)(tu) indeed (parameṣhṭhee) in his absolute perfection 
(adooduhat) extracted and summarized the essence of each of (tribhyaḥ)the three types 
of knowledge, (vedebhyaḥ) contained in the vedas, (paadam)(paadam) respectively in 
each of the three limbs (asyaaḥ) of this (saavitryaaḥ) Saavitree (ṛichaḥ) verse (tat)(iti)
that is also popularly known as the Gaayatree mantra (Yajurveda 36:3). 2:77
(vipraḥ) The scholars (vedavit) of the Vedas who during their (sandhyayoḥ) morning as 
well as evening meditation, (japan) chant this mantra, along with (etat) this (akṣharam)
monosyllable “Om” (cha) and (etaam) these three (vyaahṛiti) basic qualities of God 
added (poorvikaam) prior to it, (yujyate) beget (puṇyena) the virtues and benefits of 
studying (veda) the Vedas. 2:78

मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2

The 79th - 87th shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
The eleven senses
(iva) As (yantaa) a charioteer controls (vaajinaam) the horses pulling the chariot, so 
should (vidvaan) a scholar (aatiṣhṭhet) make all kinds of (yatnam) efforts (sañyame) to 
control (indriyaaṇaam) the senses that keep on (vicharataam) chasing (viṣhayeṣhu) the 
pleasures that (apahaariṣhu) wreck the virtues. 2:88
(ekaadasha) The eleven (indriyaaṇi) senses (faculties of interaction) (yaani) which 
(poorve) the prior (maneeṣhiṇaḥ) wise men (aahuḥ) have mentioned, I (pravakṣhyaami)
shall now talk about (taani) them (yathaavat) as is, (samyak) comprehensively and 
(anupoorvashaḥ) in the same order. 2:89

89. ekaadashendriyaaṇyaahuryaani poorve maneeṣhiṇaḥ,
taani samyakpravakṣhyaami yathaavadanupoorvashaḥ. ekaadasha indriyaaṇi aahuḥ yaani poorve maneeṣhiṇaḥ,
taani samyak pravakṣhyaami yathaavat anupoorvashaḥ.
मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2
75
They are (smṛitaa)said to be (shrotram) the ears, (tvak) the skin, (chakṣhuṣhee) the eyes, 
(jihvaa) the tongue (cha) and (naasikaa) the nose (eva) as well is (pañchamee) the fifth;
(paayu) the rectum, (upastham) the reproductive organ, (hasta) the hands, (paadam)
the legs (cha) and (vaak) the mouth (speech) (eva) as well is the (dashamee) tenth. 2:90
(anupoorvashaḥ) In the same order, the first (pañcha) five (eṣhaam) of them, i.e. 
(shrotraadeeni) the ears etc, (prachakṣhate) are said to be (indriyaaṇi) the faculties of 
(buddhi) perception and the second set of (pañcha) five (eṣhaam) of them, i.e. 
(paayyavaadeeni) the rectum etc., are (indriyaaṇi) the faculties of (karma) action. 2:91
(jñeyam) Know (ekaadasham) the eleventh as (manaḥ) the mind, which (svaguṇena) by 
its own inherent qualities has (ubhaya) two (aatmakam) facets. It interact with both 
types of the faculties and once (yasmin) it (jite) has been controlled then faculties in 
(etau) both of (gaṇau) the sets of (pañchakau) five each, (bhavataḥ) become (jitau)
controlled as well. 2:92

मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2

Control of the senses
The living being (asañshayam) without a doubt, (prasaṅgena) due to the indulgence in 
the pleasures experienced (indriyaaṇaam) by the senses, (ṛichchhati) becomes attached 
(doṣham) to malice; and (tu) when one (sanniyamya) develops command over (taani)
these faculties (tataḥ) then he/she becomes (niyachchhati) vested (siddhim) with 
extraordinary powers (eva) for sure. 2:93
(kaamaḥ) The desires are (na) never (jaatu) ever (shaamyati) quenched (upabhogena)
by indulging (kaamaanaam) into the pleasures, (iva) as (kṛiṣhṇa)(vartmaa) the fire (eva)
only (bhooya)(varddhate) intensifies (abhi) further when (haviṣhaa) oil, wood and herbs 
are offered to it. 2:94
 
यिस्मिञ्जतेिजतावेतौ भवतः पञ्चकौ गणौ ॥९२॥
एकादशम्। मनः ।  ेयम्। स्वगणेनु ।उभयात्मकम्॥ यिस्मन्। िजते। िजतौ । एतौ । भवतः । पञ्चकौ । गणौ ॥
92. ekaadasham mano jñeyan svaguṇenobhayaatmakam,
yasmiñjite jitaavetau bhavataḥ pañchakau gaṇau.
ekaadasham manaḥ jñeyam svaguṇena ubhaya-aatmakam,
yasmin jite jitau etau bhavataḥ pañchakau gaṇau.

94. na jaatu kaamaḥ kaamaanaamupabhogena shaamyati,

na jaatu kaamaḥ kaamaanaam upabhogena shaamyati,
haviṣhaa kṛiṣhṇavartmaa iva bhooya eva abhi-varddhate.
मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2
77
Amongst someone (yaḥ) who (praapnuyaat) earns (sarvaan) all of (etaan) these sensory 
pleasures (cha) and someone (yaḥ) who (tyajet) gives (kevalaan) all of (etaan) them up, 
the one who (pari) completely (tyaagaḥ) detaches himself/herself (vishiṣhyate) is far 
superior than the one who (praapaṇaat) keeps on engaging (sarva) in all (kaamaanaam)
of the desires. 2:95
(tathaa) Even (asevayaa) keeping away from the appeasement of (etaani) these 
faculties who are always (prajuṣhṭaani) seeking (viṣhayeṣhu) pleasure, is (na) not 
(shakyante) enough (sanniyantum)to control them completely. (yathaa) This control can 
only be achieved by (nityashaḥ) persistently pursuing (jñaanena) the knowledge of the 
issues with these pleasures. 2:96
(vipra) A scholar who possesses (duṣhṭa) malignant (bhaavasya) tendencies, his/her 
other acts like (vedaaḥ) study of Vedas, (tyaagaḥ) non-indulgence, (yajñaaḥ)
performance of yajña, (niyamaaḥ) following the rules (cha) and (tapaansi) forbearance

मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2
78
etc. (na) do not (karhichit) ever (gachchhanti) enable him/her (siddhim) to achieve 
perfection. 2:97
(naraḥ) A human (yaḥ) who (shrutvaa) having heard, (spṛiṣhṭvaa) touched, (dṛiṣhṭvaa)
seen, (bhuktvaa) consumed (cha) or (ghraatvaa)smelled the favorable (na) does neither
(hṛiṣhyati) feel happiness (vaa) nor (glaayati) feels sorrow on the occurrence of contrary, 
(saḥ) he/she (vijñeyaḥ) has won over the senses and is said to be (jitendriyaḥ) in total 
control of them. 2:98
(yadi) Even (tu) if (ekam) one (indriyam) faculty out (sarveṣhaam) of all of these 
(indriyaaṇaam) faculties (kṣharati) falters and keeps on chasing the pleasures, (tena) it 
(kṣharati) depletes (asya) one’s (prajñaa) intellect (iva) as a small hole (dṛiteḥ) drains all 
of (udakam) the water (paatraat) from a pot. 2:99

2:99 इिन्द्रयाणांत
ु
सव षांयद्येकं  रतीिन्द्रयम्
।
मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2
79
By keeping all of (graamam) these (indriya) faculties (sañyamya) in check (cha) and 
(vashe) after achieving a complete control (manaḥ) of the mind, and (kṛitvaa) having
practiced (yogataḥ) yoga, one’s (tanum) body (akṣhiṇvan) does not develop any disease 
or weakness. (tathaa) By following this routine, one can attain (sarvaan) all of (arthaan)
the wealth and (sansaadhayet) resources. 2:100
Meditation
One (tiṣhṭhet) should sit (samyak) properly and (japan) chant (saavitreem) the 
Gaayatree mantra (sandhyaam) while meditating (poorvaam) in the morning 
(arka)(darshanaat) till the sun rises (tu) and similarly (samaaseenaḥ) sit (pashchimaam)
in the evening (vibhaavanaat) till the bright (ṛikṣha) stars are visible. 2:101
 
तेनास्य  रित प्र ा  तेः पात्रािदवोदकम्
॥९९॥
इिन्द्रयाणाम्। तु। सव षाम्। यिद ।एकम्।  रित । इिन्द्रयम्॥

101. poorvaan sandhyaañ japanstiṣhṭhetsaavitreemarkadarshanaat,
pashchimaan tu samaaseenaḥ samyagṛikṣhavibhaavanaat.
poorvaam sandhyaam japan tiṣhṭhet saavitreem arka-darshanaat,
मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2
80
(samaaseenaḥ) Properly (tiṣhṭhan) sitting and (japan) chanting (sandhyaam) while 
meditating (poorvaam) in the morning (hanti) removes tendencies (kṛitam) to engage in 
(malam) malicious and unworthy actions (divaa) during the day (tu) and its performance 
(pashchimaam) in the evening (vyapohati) removes (enaḥ) sinful thoughts (naisham)
during the night. 2:102
Effects of an action once performed can not be nullified. God being just, never forgives 
and awards appropriate rewards for each and every action. Hence it is implied in the 
prior shloka that these activities help us by curbing our tendencies of committing sins 
and not with the atonement of prior sins.
Importance of the daily worship
The one (yaḥ) who (na) does not (tiṣhṭhati)sit and (upaaste) meditate (poorvaam) in the 
morning (tu) or the one (yaḥ) who (na) does not sit and meditate (pashchimaam) in the 
evening, (saḥ) he/she (bahiṣhkaaryaḥ) should be ostracized (saadhubhiḥ) by the nobles 
(sarvasmaat) from all of (karmaṇaḥ) the performances (dvija) of the twice born. 2:103
 
pashchimaam tu samaaseenaḥ samyak ṛikṣha-vibhaavanaat.

poorvaam sandhyaam japan tiṣhṭhan naisham enaḥ vyapohati,
pashchimaam tu samaaseenaḥ malam hanti divaa-kṛitam.

81
One who (aasthitaḥ) has faith (naityakam) in the daily (vidhim) procedures of meditation 
(gatvaa) should go (araṇyam) to the nearby forests or a place of solitude and (niyataḥ)
after seeking a place (sameepe) near (apaam) a water body (samaahitaḥ) should 
meditate while chanting (saavitreem) the Gaayatree mantra and (adheeyeeta)
contemplating on its meaning (api) as well. 2:104
There (asti) is (na) no (anurodhaḥ) relaxation allowed (anadhyaaye) for not performing 
(naityake) the daily (veda) study of the vedas (upakaraṇe) along with other associated
scriptures, (svaadhyaaye) meditation (cha) and (homa) yajña (mantreṣhu) along with the 
chant of mantras (eva) as well. These activities are (hi) indeed mandatory. 2:105
No (anadhyaayaḥ) excuses (asti) exist for (na) not performing (naityake) the daily acts 
(hi) because (tat) they (smṛitam) are said to be (satram) a session (brahma) with God. 
These (vaṣhaṭ) acts when (kṛitam) performed (anadhyaaya) while one is incapacitated

due to illness etc. are considered special (aahuti)(hutam) offerings (brahma) to God and

As the clouds (abdam) rain happiness, (eṣhaḥ) these daily acts (kṣharati)shower (payaḥ)
milk, (dadhi) yogurt, (ghṛitam) butter and (madhu) honey on the one (yaḥ) who diligently

मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2
