Worthy student
One who is (putraḥ) a child of (aachaarya) a teacher, (shushrooṣhuḥ) is ready to serve, 
(jñaanadaḥ) is a master of a subject and can exchange knowledge, (dhaarmikaḥ) is 
righteous, (shuchiḥ) observes cleanliness and hygiene of body and mind, (aaptaḥ)
believes in facts, (shaktaḥ) is mentally and physically strong and is capable of learning, 
(arthadaḥ) can make monetary donations, (saadhuḥ) is benevolent or (svaḥ) maintains 
a similar ideology as the teacher himself/herself; anyone who meets any of these 
(dasha) ten criteria (adhyaapyaaḥ) should be taught (dharmataḥ) as per dharma. 2:109
How to ask and when to reply
(loke) In this World, (medhaavee) wise (na) should not (brooyaat) speak (kasyachit)
anything, (api)(hi) even when he/she (jaanan) knows the subject, when (na) not 
(apṛiṣhṭaḥ) asked (cha) or when (anyaayena) improperly (pṛichchhataḥ) asked and 
should maintain silent and (aacharet) behave (jaḍavat) like a stone. 2:110
 
108. agneendhanam bhaikṣhacharyaamadhaḥ shayyaaṅ gurorhitam,
aasamaavartanaatkuryaatkṛitopanayano dvijaḥ. agni-indhanam bhaikṣhacharyaam adhaḥ shayyaam guroḥ hitam,
aa-samaavartanaat kuryaat kṛita-upanayanaḥ dvijaḥ.

110. naapṛiṣhṭaḥ kasyachid brooyaanna chaanyaayena pṛichchhataḥ,
मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2
84
One (yaḥ) who (adharmeṇa) improperly and maliciously (pṛichchhati) asks (cha) and the 
one (yaḥ) who (adharmeṇa) improperly and maliciously (praaha) replies, (tayoḥ) both 
are subject to disrepute (anyataraḥ) worse than (praiti) death (vaa) and/or
(adhi)(gachchhati) beget (vidveṣham) jealousy and sorrows. 2:111
Who to teach and who not to
(yatra) Where the student (na) neither (syaataam) shows (dharma) righteousness 
and/or (arthau) ability to provide monetary assistance (vaa) nor (vidhaa) an attitude of 
(shushrooṣhaa) servitude (tat) towards the teacher (api) as well, (tatra) there should be 
(na) no (vaktavyaa) lectures or (vidyaa) knowledge given to him/her, because it is (iva)
similar to (shubham) sowing (beejam) seeds (ooṣhare) in an infertile land. 2:112
(vaadinaa) The preacher (brahma) of the Vedas (kaamam)should prefer (martavyam) to 
die (samam) along with his (vidyayaa) knowledge (eva) as well (hi) but (na) not (vapet)
 
jaanannapi hi medhaavee jaḍavalloka aacharet.
na apṛiṣhṭaḥ kasyachit brooyaat na cha anyaayena pṛichchhataḥ,
jaanan api hi medhaavee jaḍavat loke aacharet.

disburse (enaam) it (iriṇe) to an unworthy mind, (api) even (tu) in case of (ghoraayaam)
extreme (aapadi) emergency. 2:113
(vidyaa) Knowledge (etya) came near (braahmaṇam) the Braahmaṇa and (aaha) said, “I 
(asmi) am (te) your (shevadhiḥ) treasure. (rakṣha) Protect (maam) me. (maa) Never
(daaḥ) give (maam) me (asooyakaaya) to someone who would abuse or misuse me. 
(tathaa) That’s how (syaam) I shall become (veeryavattamaa) stronger.” 2:114
The 116th shloka is not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
“(tu) And the one (yam) whom you (vidyaat) consider (shuchim) pure and (niyata)
diligently focused (brahmachaariṇam) on righteous conduct (eva) as well, (broohi)
preach and teach (maam) myself (tasmai) to that (vipraaya) scholar, who will 
(apramaadine) carefully (nidhipaaya) protect myself as a treasure.” 2:115

मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2
86
Etiquettes in a classroom
(poorvam) Before the start of the class of (laukikam) practical knowledge (vaa)(api) or
(vaidikam) the knowledge contained in the scriptures (tathaa)(cha) and (adhyaatmikam)
the spiritual knowledge (eva) as well, students (abhivaadayet) should bow (tam) to the 
person (yataḥ) from whom (jñaanam) the knowledge (aadadeeta) is obtained. 2:117
The 118th shloka is not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
(shayyaasane) If a seat or bed (adhyaacharite) has been used (shreyasaa) by a superior, 
an elder or a teacher, then a student (na)should not (samaavishet)sit or rest on it; (cha)
and when the student (shayyaasanasthaḥ) is resting and a teacher, an elder or a 
superior shows up, the student should (prati)(utthaaya) get up (eva) and (abhivaadayet)
bow to (enam) him/her. 2:119

मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2
87
Etiquettes for Greetings
(aayati) On the arrival (sthavire) of superiors, an anxiety automatically manifests and 
(utkraamanti) shows in the form of (oordhvam) elevated (praaṇaaḥ) breath, (hi)
however as soon as (yoonaḥ) the inferior (prati)(utthaana) gets up and 
(abhivaadaabhyaam) bows to them (taan) the breath (prati)(padyate) becomes normal 
(punaḥ) again. 2:120
One who displays (sheelasya) humility, (abhivaadana) bows to (vṛiddha) elders and 
superior and goes (upa) near them (sevinaḥ) with an intention to serve them (nityam)
all the time, (tasya) his/her (aayuḥ) longevity, (vidyaa) knowledge, (yashaḥ) fame and 
(balam) strength, all (chatvaari) four of them (vardhante) continue to increase. 2:121
(abhivaadayan) While bowing (jyaayaansam) to the elders and superiors, (param) after 
(abhivaadaat) uttering the words signifying respect, (vipraḥ) a scholar (parikeertayet)
should introduce (svam) oneself with one’s (naama) name by saying (iti) this. “(aham) I 
(asmi) am the one (naamaa) named (asau) …”. 2:122
 
shayyaasanasthaḥ cha eva enam pratyutthaaya abhivaadayet.

मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2
88
The 123th shloka is not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
After mentioning (svasya) his/her (naamnaḥ) name, (ante) at the end (abhivaadane) of 
the greeting, the greeter (keertayet) should use (shabdam) the word (bhoḥ) “you” to 
address the elderly (hi) because (ṛiṣhibhiḥ)the sages (smṛitaḥ) have said this word (bhoḥ)
“you” to be (bhaavaḥ)(svaroopa) a representation (naamnaam) of the name (bhaavaḥ)
itself. Addressing the elders and the superiors by their names is considered 
inappropriate. 2:124
Replying (abhivaadane) to the greeting, (vipraḥ) the elder (vaachyaḥ)(iti) should say 
“(saumya) O humble! (aayuṣhmaan)(bhava) May you live long …” (cha) and then 
(vaachyaḥ) mention (asya) the greeter’s (naamnaḥ) name extending (ante) the last 
(akaaraḥ) vowel and (poorva) the preceding (akṣharaḥ) consonant (plutaḥ) three times.
The elders should show interest and enthusiasm while replying to the greetings. 2:125

(vipraḥ) The elder (yaḥ) who (na) does not on purpose or does not (vetti) know how to
(prati) reciprocate (abhivaadanam) with a greeting in response (abhivaadasya) to a 
greeting, (saḥ) he/she (na) should not (abhivaadyaḥ) be greeted (viduṣhaa) by the wise 
because (saḥ) he/she (tathaa)(eva) is the same (yathaa) as (shoodraḥ) an uneducated.
This shloka does not imply that a shoodra should not be greeted at all. It is also not 
applicable if the elder is ignoring someone as a punishment to one’s misdeeds. 2:126
(samaagamya) Upon meeting someone, after the greetings, one should be asked about 
something that is important to him/her. (pṛichchhet) Ask (braahmaṇam) the braahmaṇa 
if their (kushalam) bliss and study of scriptures are going well, (kṣhatra)(bandhum) the
kṣhatriya if their (anaamayam) strength is without any issues, (vaishyam) the vaishya if 
their (kṣhemam) prosperity and wealth is increasing (eva)(cha) and (shoodram) the
shoodra if they are maintaining good health, (aarogyam) free of any sickness. 2:127

akaaraḥ cha asya naamnaḥ ante vaachyaḥ poorva-akṣharaḥ plutaḥ.

127. braahmaṇaṅ kushalam pṛichchhet kṣhatrabandhumanaamayam,
मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2

(deekṣhitaḥ) When someone has been accepted for a specialized study or has 
graduated, (api) even when (yaḥ) he/she (bhavet) is (yaveeyaan) younger, (tu) then 
(dharmavit) someone well versed in dharma should treat him/her with respect and 
(abhi)(bhaaṣheta) greet (enam) him/her (bhavat) using (bho) a pronoun and (avaachyaḥ)
not by uttering his/her (naamnaa) name , (poorvakam) as explained earlier. 2:128
(stree) A lady (yaa) who is (para) someone else’s (patnee) wife (cha) or who (syaat) is 
(asambanghaa) not related (yonitaḥ) by kinship, should not be addressed by her name 
(tu) as well and (taam) she (brooyaat) should be addressed (iti) as (bhavati) “you”, 
(subhage) “grace” (evam)(cha) or (bhagini) “sister”. 2:129
The 130th - 135th shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.

129. parapatnee tu yaa stree syaadasambanghaa cha yonitaḥ,

मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2
91
Who deserves respect and courtesy
(vittam) Wealth, (bandhuḥ) number of friends, (vayaḥ) age, (karma) benevolent actions 
and (vidyaa) knowledge (bhavati) is (pañchamee) the fifth criterion; (etaani) these are 
the criteria that enable one to earn (maanya) respectable (sthaanaani) positions in the 
society, with (yat)(yat) one possessing (uttaram) the latter quality enjoying (gareeyaḥ)
more respect than the one with the prior in the same order. In the modern World 
however, we see a reversal in this order where wealth and political power are taking 
precedence over other qualities. 2:136
Within the upper (triṣhu) three (varṇeṣhu) classes, many are (bhooyaansi) better (cha)
and more (guṇavanti) qualified (pañchaanaam) at these five qualities compared to 
others. (yatra) Wherever there is a higher order or more of these qualities are present 
(saḥ) one (syuḥ) becomes (maanaarhaḥ) more respectable (atra) here. However, 
(shoodraḥ) a shoodra (dashameem) in the tenth decade of (gataḥ) age deserves more 
respect (api) as well. 2:137
As a courtesy, (panthaa) the right of way (deyaḥ) should be given to (chakriṇaḥ) one 
riding a vehicle, (dashameesthasya) one in the tenth decade of age i.e. an old person, 
(rogiṇaḥ) one who is sick, (bhaariṇaḥ) one who is carrying something heavy, (striyaaḥ) a

woman, (snaatakasya) a graduate scholar, (raajñaḥ) a king (cha) and (varasya) a

When all of (teṣhaam) them (samavetaanaam) are gathered at a place (tu) then 
(snaataka) the graduate scholar and (paarthivau) the king (maanyau) take precedence 
(cha) and (eva) even out of (raaja) the king and (snaatakayoḥ) the graduate scholar, 
(snaatakaḥ) the scholar (bhaak) deserves (maana) precedence over (nṛipa) the king i.e. 
the king should show respect to the graduate scholar. 2:139
Attributes of different types of teachers and priests
(dvijaḥ) The twice born (yaḥ) who (upaneeya) after investing (shiṣhyam) the disciples 
with the sacred thread, (tu)(adhyaapayet) teaches them (vedam) the Vedas (sakalpam)
along with the associated six branches (cha) and (sarahasyam) the deeply embedded 
messages in the upaniṣhad and the sub-branches i.e. the philosophies, (tam) he/she 
(prachakṣhate) is viewed as (aachaaryam) an aachaarya. 2:140

(tu) And one (yaḥ) who (artham) for his/her (vṛitti) sustenance (adhyaapayati) teaches 
(eka) a (desham) particular aspect (vedasya) of the Vedas (vaa) or some of (aṅgaani) the 
branches of (veda) the knowledge (punaḥ)(api) as well, (saḥ) he/she (uchyate) is said to 
be (upaadhyaayaḥ) an upaadhyaaya. 2:141
One (yaḥ) who (karoti) performs (karmaaṇi) all of the sacraments (niṣhekaadeeni) from 
conception onwards (yathaa) as per (vidhi) the procedures laid out in the scriptures 
(cha) and (sambhaavayati) sustains and nourishes the child (annena) with grains, (saḥ)
that (vipraḥ) scholar (uchyate) is said to be (guruḥ) a guru. Accordingly, the mother and 
the father or someone who is in charge of the all round development of the child 
including the spiritual aspect, is the guru. 2:142

A scholar (yaḥ) who is (aadheyam) the custodian of (agni) the fire and (yasya) who has 
been (vṛitaḥ) nominated to perform (makhaan) yajña on behalf (tasya) of the nominator
householder, (karoti) performs various offerings including (agniṣhṭom) offerings into the 
fire, (yajñaan) offerings of (paaka) the cooked food to poor, birds and animals and 
(aadikaan) other periodic offerings; (saḥ) he/she (uchyate) is said to be their (ṛitvik)
ṛitvik. 2:143
Comparison between mother, father and teacher
One (yaḥ) who (avitatham) consistently, persistently and (aavṛiṇoti) repeatedly gets 
(brahmaṇaa) the wisdom of the Vedas (ubhau) to both of (shravaṇau) the ears, (jñeyaḥ)
consider (saḥ) that person as (maataa) the mother and (pitaa) the father and (na) never 
(kadaachana) ever (druhyet) act maliciously (tam) towards him/her. 2:144
The 145th shloka is not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
Amongst the one who (utpaadaka) gives birth and the one who (brahmadaatroḥ) gives 
knowledge, (pitaa) the father (brahmadaḥ) giving knowledge (gareeyaan) is better, (hi)
because (viprasya) for the twice born, the second (janma) birth (brahma) into the

knowledge is the one that has (shaashvatam) lasting impact in (iha) this life (cha) and

(yat) When (maataa) the mother (cha) and (pitaa) the father (mithaḥ) together 
(kaamaat) under influence of desire, (utpaadayataḥ) reproduce (enam) this child, (yat)
which (abhi)(jaayate) is the birth (yonau) from the mother's womb, (taam) that birth 
(tasya) of the child (vidyaat) is considered (sambhootim) an ordinary birth and only the 
second birth into knowledge makes him/her extraordinary. The biological parents are 
the ordinary parents; the ones who teach are the real mothers and fathers. 2:147

(saa) that is (asya) the child’s (satyaa) true class and (saa) it (amaraa) universally 
accepted and is (ajaraa) unchangeable, unless he/she engages in improper conduct. 2:148
Stature of the teacher
One (yaḥ) who (upakaroti) obliges (yasya) someone (shrutasya) by teaching (bahu) a lot
(vaa) or (vaa) even a (alpam) a little bit, (tam) that person should (api) also be (vidyaat)
considered as (gurum) a guru (iha) in this World because of (tayaa) that (upakriyayaa)
favor of imparting (shruta) knowledge. Everyone should have multiple gurus. 2:149
The one who (kartaa) performs the ritual of the second (janmanaḥ) birth by initiating 
someone onto the path (braahmasya) of seeking knowledge (cha) and (shaasitaa)
teaches (dharmasya) the values and conducts of (sva) the assigned varṇa, that (vipraḥ)
scholar (dharmataḥ) by rule (bhavati) becomes equivalent to (pitaa) a parent (api) even 
if he/she is (baalaḥ) young and the student is (vṛiddhasya) older. 2:150

Story of a young teacher from the lineage of Sage Aṅgira
(kaviḥ) A foresighted scholarly (shishuḥ) child (aaṅgirasaḥ) from the lineage of Sage 
Aṅgira (adhyaapayaamaasa) taught (pitṛeen) the elders from his own clan and since he 
(parigṛihya) imparted (jñaanena) lessons to them, he once (ha)(uvaacha) addressed 
(taan) them (iti) as (putrakaaḥ) “Sons!”. 2:151
(aagatamanyavaḥ) Angered by that address, (te) those elders (apṛichchhanta) asked 
other (devaan) scholars about (tam) its (artham) appropriateness; (cha) and (sametya)
unanimously (devaaḥ) the scholars (oochuḥ) replied (etaan) to them, “that (shishuḥ)
child (uktavaan) has addressed (vaḥ) you (nyaayyam) as per norms.” 2:152

(ajñaḥ) “A ignorant person (bhavati) is considered as (baalaḥ) a child (vai) indeed and 
(mantradaḥ) the provider of knowledge (bhavati) is equivalent to (pitaa) a parent, (hi)
because scriptures (eva) as well (aahuḥ) say (iti) that (ajñam) an ignorant person 
behaves like (baalam) a child (tu) and (mantradam) a teacher (iti) as (pitaa) a 
parent.” 2:153
“(na) Neither (haayanaiḥ) by the number of years i.e. the age (na) nor (palitaiḥ) by the 
grayness of the hairs, (na) neither (vittena) by the amount of wealth (na) nor 
(bandhubhiḥ) by the number of supporters i.e. the political power, (dharmam) the 
norms (chakrire) given by (ṛiṣhayaḥ) the sages are that (yaḥ) whosoever amongst (naḥ)
us (anoochaanaḥ) is the most knowledgeable (saḥ) he/she is (mahaan) the 
greatest.” 2:154
“The one (jñaanataḥ) with greater knowledge (vipraaṇaam) amongst the braahmaṇa is 
considered (jyaiṣhṭhyam) the eldest, the one (veeryataḥ) with more strength 
(kṣhatriyaaṇaam) amongst the kṣhatriya, the one with more (dhaanya) grains and

(dhanataḥ) greater wealth (vaishyaanaam) amongst the vaishya (tu) and by the order of

“(tena) He/she (na) is not (bhavati) considered (vṛiddhaḥ) an elder (yena)(asya) whose

The uneducated or improperly educated is not a real Braahmaṇa
(yathaa) As (hastee) an elephant (mayaḥ) made out of (kaaṣhṭha) wood (cha) and
(yathaa) as (mṛigaḥ) a deer (mayaḥ) made out of (charma) leather, so is (vipraḥ) a 
braahmaṇa (yaḥ) who (anadheeyaanaḥ) has not been educated properly. All (trayaḥ)
three of (te) these are just (bibhrati) for the sake of (naama) name only i.e. without any 
real value. 2:157

vaishyaanaan dhaanyadhanataḥ shoodraaṇaameva janmataḥ. vipraaṇaam jñaanataḥ jyaiṣhṭhyam kṣhatriyaaṇaam tu veeryataḥ,
vaishyaanaam dhaanya-dhanataḥ shoodraaṇaam eva janmataḥ.

(yathaa) As (ṣhaṇḍhaḥ) an impotent person is (aphalaḥ) useless (streeṣhu) for women 
i.e. can’t produce children, (yathaa) as (gauḥ) a cow (aphalaa) can’t produce calves 
(gavi) with cows (cha) and (yathaa) as (daanam) a donation made (ajñe) to an ignorant 
(aphalam) is of no use, (tathaa) so is (vipraḥ) a braahmaṇa (aphalaḥ) useless (anṛichaḥ)
without the knowledge of the Vedas. 2:158
Propagation of the righteous conduct
Those (ichchhataa) desirous of (prayojyaa) propagating (dharmam) the righteous 
conduct should (kaaryam) keep other (bhootaanaam) human beings (anushaasanam)
under discipline (ahinsayaa) by remaining non-violent (cha) and by teaching and 
commanding in (madhuraa) a sweet and (shlakṣhṇaa) non-malignant (vaak) speech
(eva) as well. This is (shreyaḥ) the best approach (eva) indeed. Non-violence doesn’t 
mean absence of self defense or lack of the punishments awarded as per the law. 2:159

yaḥ cha vipraḥ anadheeyaanaḥ trayaḥ te naama bibhrati.

(yasya) Whose (vaaṅ) speech and (manasee) mind (sarvadaa) always remain (shuddhe)
pure (cha) and under (samyak) proper (gupte) control, (saḥ) he/she (vai) indeed 
(avaapnoti) realizes (sarvam) all of (phalam) the rewards (upagatam) described 
(vedaanta) in the Vedic scriptures. 2:160
(api) Even (aartaḥ) when suffering, one (na) should not (syaat) cause (tudaḥ) pain to 
someone else’s (arun) heart. One (na)should not harbor jealousy, hate, anger or (dheeḥ)
intentions of (karma) causing (droha) harm (para) to others. And any kind of (vaachaa)
words (yayaa) that (udvijate) can cause aggravation for others, one (na) should not let 
(taam) such (alokyaam) undesirable words (ut)(eerayet) escape (asya) one’s mouth. 2:161
The desire of fame or praise
(braahmaṇaḥ) A braahmaṇa should (nityam) always (udvijeta) stay away (sammaanaat)
from praises, treating them (iva) similar (viṣhaat) to poison (cha) and treat 
 
vaak chaiva madhuraa shlakṣhṇaa prayojyaa dharmamichchhataa.
ahinsayaa eva bhootaanaam kaaryam shreyaḥ anushaasanam,
vaak cha eva madhuraa shlakṣhṇaa prayojyaa dharmam ichchhataa.

(avamaanasya) criticisms (iva) as (amṛitasya) the nectar of deathlessness, (aakaaṅkṣhet)
with a desire to (sarvadaa) forever stay with righteousness regardless of praises or 
criticisms. The criticisms should propel one towards corrective actions needed for 
achieving perfection. 2:162
(hi) Because one who (avamataḥ) is without any preference and has gotten rid of the 
desire for fame, he/she (shete) sleeps (sukham) peacefully (cha) and remains (sukham)
happy in one’s (prati)(buddhyate) wakeful state as well. He/she (charati) lives (sukham)
happily (asmin) in this (loke) world while the one who (avamantaa) is bothered by 
criticism (vinashyati) is destroyed by sorrow and worry. 2:163

(sañchinuyaat) should increase one’s (tapaḥ) fortitude (adhi)(gamikam) by learning 
(brahma) the Vedas. 2:164
(choditaiḥ) As directed by various (vidhi) the rules and procedures laid out in the 
scriptures, (dvijanmanaa) a twice born should observe (vividhaiḥ) different types of 
(vrataiḥ) abstinences (cha) and (visheṣhaiḥ) special (tapo) penances and should make 
efforts (adhi) to study and (gantavyaḥ) get to (kṛitsnaḥ) the entire (vedaḥ) vedic 
knowledge (sarahasyaḥ) along with its hidden and subtle messages. 2:165
(dvijottamaḥ) The best amongst the twice borns(sadaa)(eva) always (abhyasyet) engage 
in the study and practice of (vedam) the Vedas (tapsyan) while suffering from (tapaḥ)
penances, (hi) because (iha) in this world (abhyaasaḥ) the practice of (veda) the Vedas 
(uchyate) is said to be (param) the most rigorous (tapaḥ) penance (viprasya) for the 
scholars. 2:166

2:166 वेदमेव सदाऽभ्यस्ये पस्तप्स्यिन्द्वजो मः ।
वेदाभ्यासो िह िवप्रस्य तपः परिमहोच्यते॥१६६॥
वेदम्। एव । सदा । अभ्यस्येत्। तपः। तप्स्यन्। िद्वजो मः॥ वेदाभ्यासः। िह। िवप्रस्य । तपः। परम्। इह। उच्यते॥
मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2
104
(dvijaḥ) The twice born (yaḥ) who (api) while (sragvee) adorning a necklace i.e. in spite 
of being laden with the duties of the householder stage, (shaktitaḥ) makes special 
efforts (anu)(aham) everyday (adheete) to engage (svaadhyaayaḥ) in the self study of 
the Vedas, (saḥ) he/she (ha)(eva) indeed (tapyate) is bathed in (paramam) the ultimate 
(tapaḥ) penance (aa) till (nakhaagrebhyaḥ) the tip of one’s toenail. 2:167
(dvijaḥ) The twice born (yaḥ) who (anadheetya) does not study (vedam) the Vedas and 
(kurute) focuses one’s (shramam) efforts (anyatra) elsewhere i.e. on other scriptures 
only, (saḥ) he/she (eva) indeed (saanvayaḥ) along with his/her family*, (jeevan) during 
his/her lifetime, (aashu) quickly (gachchhati) attains (shoodratvam) lowly stature.
*When the head of the household digresses completely from the source of truth, the 
family follows in similar behaviors and attitudes. However, it doesn’t mean that the 
Vedas should not be taught to one born in the lower class. Vedas are for everyone and 
only when one does not study the Vedas or digresses from them, he/she attains a lowly 
stature; it is not by birth into a particular family. 2:168
 
166. vedameva sadaa’bhyasyettapastapsyandvijottamaḥ,
vedaabhyaaso hi viprasya tapaḥ paramihochyate.
vedam eva sadaa abhyasyet tapaḥ tapsyan dvijottamaḥ,
veda-abhyaasaḥ hi viprasya tapaḥ param iha uchyate.

मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2

The 169th - 174th shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
Disciplines of a student
(brahmachaaree) A student (vasan) should reside (gurau) with the Guru (artham) with a 
sole purpose of (vṛiddhi) elevating (aatmanaḥ) one’s (tapo) knowledge and fortitude. 
One should learn (sanniyamya) to control one’s (indriya)(graamam) senses (tu) and 
(seveta) practice (imaan) these (niyamaan) rules described henceforth. 2:175
(nityam) Everyday, without exception, after (shuchiḥ) purifying oneself (snaatvaa) with 
a proper bath, one (kuryaat) should work towards (tarpaṇam) pleasing (ṛiṣhi) the sages, 
(deva)the scholars and (pitṛi)the elders, (abhi)(archanam) meditate and thank (devataa)
the Supreme Soul (eva) as well (cha) and (eva) also (samid)(aadhaanam) make offerings 
in the fire. Sages, scholars and elders are pleased when they see one diligently taking 
responsibility, seeking knowledge and engaging in virtuous actions. 2:176
 
sa jeevanneva shoodratvamaashu gachchhati saanvayaḥ. yaḥ anadheetya dvijaḥ vedam anyatra kurute shramam,
saḥ jeevan eva shoodratvam aashu gachchhati saanvayaḥ.

मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2
106
A student (varjayet) is forbidden to consume (madhu) alcohol (cha) and (maansam)
meat, to use (gandham) fragrances and all ornaments including (maalyam) necklaces, 
to consume excessively (rasaan) flavored food, to seek proximity to (striyaḥ) a person 
of the opposite sex, to consume (sarvaaṇi) all (yaani) kinds of (shuktaani) excessively 
sour or spicy foods (cha) and to engage in any kind of (hinsanam) violence (praaṇinaam)
towards any living being (eva) as well. 2:177
A student is forbidden to use (abhyaṅgam) skin lotions (cha) and (akṣhṇoḥ) eye 
(añjanam) liners, (dhaaraṇam)to wear (upaanat)shoes and (chhatra) umbrellas, to have 
feelings of (kaamam) lust, (krodham) anger (cha) and (lobham) greed (cha) and to 
practice (narttanam) dance, (geeta) singing and (vaadanam) music for 
entertainment. 2:178
A student is forbidden to engage in (dyootam) gambling, (janavaadam) spreading 
rumors, (parivaadam) criticizing someone, (anṛitam) unnecessary (tathaa) and untrue 
speech, to (prekṣhaṇa) meet (cha) or (alambham) touch (streeṇaam) someone from the

Asking for endowment
A student (aaharet) should bring (udakumbham) water in a pot, (sumanasaḥ) flowers 
and fruits, (goshakṛit) cow dung fuel, (mṛittikaa) soil and (kushaan) grass fibers (yaavat)
as (arthaani) needed to fulfill the immediate needs (cha) and (charet) should 
(bhaikṣham) beg (ahaḥ)(ahaḥ) everyday for food and other needs. 2:182

(anu)(aham) Everyday, (brahmachaaree) a student should (prayataḥ) diligently and 
politely (aaharet) seek (bhaikṣham) endowment of things needed for sustenance
(gṛihebhyaḥ) from the households where the householders are (prashastaanaam)
mindful (svakarmasu) of their duties and (aheenaanaam) have not digressed 
(vedayajñaiḥ) from the daily yajña prescribed in the Vedas. 2:183
A student (na)should not (bhikṣheta) beg from one’s (guroḥ) teacher’s (kule) family, (na)
nor from one’s own (jñaati) family, (kula) relatives and (bandhuṣhu) friends. (tu)
However, when sustenance (alaabhe) is not available from (anya) other (gehaanaam)
households, then one (vivarjayet) can approach them (poorvam)(poorvam) in a reverse 
order i.e. friends, relatives, own family and at last the teacher’s family. 2:184
And when sustenance (asambhave) is not available from any of the households 
(poorvoktaanaam) mentioned before, keeping one’s (vaacham) speech (prayataḥ)

Student and yajña
A student should (dooraat) travel some distance to the forest (aahṛitya) to collect 
(samidhaḥ) firewoods and (vihaayasi) keep them in an open space (sannidadhyaat) for 
drying out. Then (taabhiḥ) using them one, (atandritaḥ) without any sign of laziness, 
(juhuyaat) should perform (agnim) yajña every (praataḥ) morning (cha) and (saayam)
evening. 2:186

Student teacher interaction
(nityam) Everyday, (choditaḥ) as directed (guruṇaa) by the teacher (vaa) or (eva) even 
when (aprachoditaḥ) not directed by the teacher, a student should (yatnam) diligently 
(kuryaat) engage (adhyayane) in studies (cha) and other activities (hiteṣhu) for the 
benefit (aachaaryasya) of the teacher. 2:191

In the presence of the teacher, a student (niyamya) should control his/her (shareeram)

(mukham) face. 2:192
A student (syaat) should (nityam) always keep his/her right (uddhṛitapaaṇiḥ) hand 
exposed out of the shawl (cha) and (susañyataḥ) controlling oneself should display 
(saadhu) courteous (aachaaraḥ) behavior. He/she (aaseeta) should sit (abhi)(mukham)
facing (guroḥ) the teacher only (san) after the teacher (iti)(uktaḥ) says (aasyataam) to 
sit. 2:193

(sannidhau) When with (guru) the guru, (sarvadaa) always consume (anna) food or wear

(sam)(bhaaṣhe) During a conversation or (prati) after (shravaṇa) hearing from the guru, 
one should (na) not (sam)(aacharet) reply (shayaanaḥ) while lying down, (na) neither
(aseenaḥ) while sitting (na) nor (bhuñjaanaḥ) while eating (cha) and (na) neither
(tiṣhṭhan) from a distance (na) nor with (mukhaḥ) the head (paraaṅ) turned the other 
way. 2:195

113
A student should (na) never (udaaharet) refer (asya) to the teacher (kevalam) only by 
his/her (naama) name without respectful prefixes and suffixes, (api) even in his/her 
(parokṣham) absence (cha) and should (na) never humorously (anu)(kurveeta) mimic 
(asya) the teacher’s style of (gati) walking, (bhaaṣhita) speaking or his/her (cheṣhṭitam)
typical actions (eva) as well. 2:199
(yatra) Wherever, (pareevaadaḥ) the faults (guroḥ) of the teacher (pravarttate) are 
being discussed (vaa) or he/she is being (nindaa) unfairly criticized (api) as well, (tatra)
there the student should either (pidhaatavyau) shut one’s (karṇau) ears i.e. not pay 
attention and engage in those discussions (vaa) or should leave (tataḥ) that place and 
(gantavyam) go (anyataḥ) elsewhere. 2:200
(enam) A student (na) should not (archayet) greet the teacher (doorasthaḥ) from afar, 
(na) neither disturb the teacher when he/she (kruddhaḥ) is angry, (na) nor when the

teacher (antike) is intimately (striyaaḥ) with their spouses (cha) and if the student 
(aasanasthaḥ) is riding (yaana) a vehicle then (enam) he/she (avaruhya) should alight 
from the vehicle and (eva) then (abhivaadayet) bow to the teacher. 2:202
A student (na) should not (aaseeta) sit (saha) with (guruṇaa) the teacher in situations 
(prativaate) when the air is flowing from the front of the student towards the teacher 
(cha) or (anuvaate) when it is flowing from the back of the student towards the teacher.
(cha) And the student should (eva)(api) also (na) not (keertayet) say (kiñchit) anything 
(guroḥ) to the teacher at places (asañshrave) where it is hard to hear properly. 2:203
A student (aaseeta) can sit (saardham) alongside (guruṇaa) the teacher while traveling 
(yaana) in a vehicle pulled by (go) ox, (ashva) horse or (uṣhṭra) camel etc., (cha) or on 
seats offered (kaṭeṣhu) on mats while visiting (praasaada) palaces or (srastareṣhu)
rooftops (cha) and (shilaa) on rock, (phalaka) wooden plank or (nauṣhu) in a boat. 2:204

मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2
115
If (guroḥ) the teacher's (gurau) teacher (sannihite) is present then he/she (aacharet)
should be treated with the same (vṛittim) respect (guruvat) as the teacher. (cha) And 
when other (guroon) teachers (svaan) of the student arrive then he (na) should not 
(abhivaadayet) bow to them (anisṛiṣhṭaḥ) without the explicit permission (guruṇaa) of 
the current teacher. 2:205
(nityaa) Always show (eva) similar (vṛittiḥ) respectful behavior, (etat) as mentioned in 
the prior shlokas, towards (guruṣhu) the teachers who impart various kinds of (vidyaa)
knowledge, towards the elders from (sva) one’s (yoniṣhu) clan (cha) and towards those 
(api) as well (upadishatsu) who advise (hitam) well (cha) and help one (pratiṣhedhatsu)
get away (adharmaan) from unrighteousness. 2:206
The 207th - 211th shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.

मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2
116
Avoid close physical interaction with opposite sexes
A student, who has (poorṇa) completed (viñshati) twenty (varṣheṇa) years of age and 
(vijaanataa) has acquired the knowledge of distinguishing between (guṇa) good and 
(doṣhau) bad (iha) in this World, (na)should not (abhivaadyaa) greet (guru)the teacher’s 
(yuvatiḥ) young (patnee) spouse (tu) by touching her/his (paadayoḥ) feet. 2:212
(iha) In this World, (eṣhaḥ) it is (svabhaavaḥ) natural that the interactions between 
(naareeṇaam) women and (naraaṇaam) men result in (dooṣhaṇam) undesirable 
conducts and (ataḥ) hence, (arthaan) due to this reason, (vipashchitaḥ) the wise (na) do 
not (pramaadyanti) engage in carefree interactions (pramadaasu) with the opposite 
sexes. 2:213
(loke) In this World, (pramadaaḥ) carefree individuals are (hi) indeed (alam) fully 
capable of scheming and (vasha) influencing (avidvaansam) the uneducated (vaa)(api)
as well as (vidvaansam) the scholars (punaḥ) alike (anugam) by utilizing their emotions 
of (kaama) lust and (krodha) anger etc. and cause their (utpatham) derailment (netum)
from righteousness. 2:214

One (bhavet) should (na) not (aasanaḥ) sit (vivikta) alone with a person of the opposite 
sex, even with (maatraa) mothers, (svasraa) sisters (vaa) or (duhitraa) daughters 
because (balavaan) the strong influence of (indriya) (graamaḥ) the sensual pleasures is 
capable of (karṣhati) pulling (api) even (vidvaansam) the scholars towards unethical 
conducts. 2:215
It is (kaamam) desirable (tu) that (yuvaa) the young students (vandanam)(kuryaat) greet 
(yuvateenaam) the young (patneenaam) spouses (guru) of the teacher (vidhivat) by 
properly (bhuvi) bowing from a little distance and by introducing them (bruvan) by 
speaking (iti) these words, “(aham) I am (asau) …”. 2:216

मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2
118
(anusmaran) In accordance (dharmam) with the rules of the conduct (sataam) for the 
responsibles, (anu)(aham) everyday one (kurveeta) should only (abhivaadanam) greet 
(guru) the teacher’s (daareṣhu) spouse from a little distance (cha) and (viproṣhya) only 
after coming back from a journey to distant land should one greet her (grahaṇam) by 
touching her (paada) feet. 2:217
Benefits of serving the teacher
(yathaa) As (naraḥ) a human persistently (khanan) digging (khanitreṇa) with a pickaxe 
(adhi) finally (gachchhati) gets to (vaari) a water source, (tathaa) so does a student who 
(shushrooṣhuḥ) consistently serves the teacher, (gachchhati) get (adhi) all of (vidyaam)
the knowledge (gataam) known to (guru) the teacher. 2:218
Limit of a student’s interaction with the society
A student (syaat) can optionally (muṇḍaḥ) shave his/her head, (vaa) or (jaṭilaḥ) keep all 
hairs as is, (vaa) or (athavaa) else (shikhaa)(jaṭaḥ) keep a crest and shave off the rest. 
During (enam) a student’s stay (graame) in a village, (kvachit) without a strong reason,

मनुस्मृित अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 2
119
(sooryaḥ) the sun (syaat) should (na) neither (abhi)(nimlochet) set (na) nor 
(abhi)(udiyaat) rise i.e. he/she should be in the hostel during the entire night time. 2:219
(chet) If (avijñaanaat) inadvertently (sooryaḥ) the sun (nimlochet) sets while (tam) the 
student is still in the village (vaa)(api) or due to circumstance, the student needs to 
(shayaanam) sleep in the village as well and (kaamachaarataḥ) carelessly sleeps over 
(abhi)(udiyaat) until the sunrise, then he/she should as a penance (upavaset) fast 
(dinam) the whole day and (japan) chant the Gaayatree mantra. 2:220
The student (yaḥ) who stays in a village (sooryeṇa)(abhi)(nirmuktaḥ) beyond sunset or 
(shayaanaḥ)sleeps over (abhi)(uditaḥ) after sunrise (cha) and then (akurvaaṇaḥ) doesn’t 
perform (praayashchittam) the penance described in the prior shloka, he/she (syaat) is 
(yuktaḥ) ridden with (mahataa) a great (enasaa) sin (hi) indeed. 2:221

ण्डो वा जिटलो वा स्यादथवा स्यािच्छखाजटः ।

Connecting with God
(nityam) Everyday, (ubhe) both (sandhye) at the dawn and at the dusk, a student should 
find (shuchau) a clean and quiet (deshe) place and (yathaa) as per (vidhi) the procedure, 
(aachamya) having sipped water, he/she should (prayataḥ) effortfully (samaahitaḥ) get 
focused (upaaseeta) on God (japan)(japyam) while chanting Om, Gaayatree mantra and 
any other suitable mantra. 2:222
Learn from everyone
(yadi) If someone (samaacharet) displays (kiñchit) some (shreyaḥ) extraordinary skills or 
behaviors then regardless of his/her (stree) gender (vaa) or (avarajaḥ) class, others 
should be willing to learn from this person and (aacharet) follow (sarvam) all of (tat)
those behaviors in their conduct as well, because (yatra) whatever actions (asya) their 
(manaḥ) minds (ramet) find joy in, they (yuktaḥ) acquire traits related to those 
actions. 2:223

praayashchittam akurvaaṇaḥ yuktaḥ syaat mahataa enasaa.

The 224th - 237th shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
(shraddadhaanaḥ) One having a strong desire to attain (shubhaam) the auspicious 
(vidyaam) knowledge, (aadadeeta) should be willing to learn (api) even (avaraat) from 
a person of lower stature. It is good practice to learn (api) even (antyaat) from a person 
of the lowest stature who is engaged in (param) commendable (dharmam) deeds and 
(api) also to marry (stree) someone (ratnam) extraordinary (duṣhkulaat) who belongs to
an infamous family. 2:238
One should be capable of (graahyam) extracting (amṛitam) the nectar (api) if it exists 
(viṣhaat) within poison i.e. not be judgemental and be willing to accept good things and 
values even when the source is dubious; one should accept (subhaaṣhitam) words of 
wisdom (api) even (baalaat) from someone much younger; one should be willing to 
emulate (sad) the good (vṛittam) habits of (api) even (amitraat) the enemies; and one 
should be willing to accept (kaañchanam) the gold (api) even when it is found 
(amedhyaat) in an unclean surrounding. 2:239
 
tatsarvamaacharedyukto yatra vaa’sya ramenmanaḥ. yadi stree yadi avarajaḥ shreyaḥ kiñchit sam-aacharet,
tat sarvam aacharet yuktaḥ yatra vaa asya ramet manaḥ.

(sarvataḥ) From anywhere and everywhere, whenever something extraordinary is 
available, (atho) including (striyaḥ) spouses, (ratnaani) jewels, (vidyaa) knowledge, 
(dharmaḥ) righteousness, (shaucham) cleanliness, (subhaaṣhitam) words of wisdom 
(cha) and (vividhaani) various (shilpaani) works of art and sculpture, it (samaadeyaani)
should be gladly accepted. 2:240
(kaale) In the times (aapat) of emergency i.e. when not available from a proper source, 
it is (vidheeyate) advisable (adhyayanam) to learn (abraahmaṇaat) from a person who 
is not a braahmaṇa. (cha) And (yaavat) till (adhyayanam) the education is going on this 
person should be (shushrooṣhaa)served and (anuvrajyaa) obeyed (guroḥ) as a guru. 2:241
(shiṣhyaḥ) A student (kaaṅkṣhan) desirous of learning (anuttamaam) at an extraordinary 
(gatim) speed (na) should not (vaasam)(vaset) stay (aatyantikam) long (gurau) with a 
 
amitraadapi sadvṛittamamedhyaadapi kaañchanam.
viṣhaat api amṛitam graahyam baalaat api subhaaṣhitam,
amitraat api sad-vṛittam amedhyaat api kaañchanam.

guru (abraahmaṇe) who is not a braahmaṇa (cha) or even (braahmaṇe) with a 
braahmaṇa (ananoochaane) who is not trained properly in the scriptures. 2:242
(yadi) If a student (rochayeta) likes (vaasam) to stay (aatyantikam) forever at (guroḥ) the 
guru’s (kule) place (tu) then he/she should (yuktaḥ) diligently (paricharet) serve (enam)
the guru (aa) until (shareera)(vimokṣhaṇaat) death. 2:243
The 244th shloka is not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
Gift for the teacher after graduation
(tu) Upon his/her (snaasyan) graduation, a student (dharmavit) well versed in righteous 
conducts, (aajñaptaḥ) after seeking (guruṇaa) the teacher’s permission, (aaharet)
should bring gifts (artham) for (guru) the teacher (shaktyaa) as permitted by his/her 
means and capabilities, however, (na)(kiñchit) no gifts (upakurveeta) should be given 
(guruve) to the guru (poorvam) before the graduation. 2:245

A student (aavahet) could bring the gift of (kṣhetram) land, (hiraṇyam) gold, (gaam)
cows, (ashvam) horses, (chhatra) umbrellas, (upaanaham) shoes, (aasanam) seat, 
(dhaanyam) grains, (shaakam) fruits (cha) and vegetables, (vaasaansi) clothes etc. 
(guruve) for the teacher as per his/her (preetim) preferences. 2:246
The 247th - 248th shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
Benefits of a disciplined student life
(vipraḥ) The twice born (yaḥ) who (evam) so (charati) follows the rules of conduct 
(brahmacharyam) for the the student life (aviplutaḥ) without fail, (saḥ) he/she 
(gachchhati) attains (uttama) high (sthaanam) stature (cha) and after death attains 
nirvaaṇa i.e. is (na) not (aajaayate) born (punaḥ) again (iha) in this world. 2:249

249. evañ charati yo vipro brahmacharyamaviplutaḥ,

मनुस्मृित अध्याय ३ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 3
125
Chapter 3
Duration of the student life
A student (vratam) with a resolve to study all (trai) three types of (vedikam) Vedic 
knowledge to the full extent, should reside (gurau) with the teacher and (charyam)
follow the rigors of the student life (triñshat) for thirty (ṣhaṭ) six (aabdikam) years or 
(ardhikam) for half of (tat) that i.e. eighteen years (vaa) or (paadikam) for a quarter of 
that i.e. nine years (vaa) or until the time he/she (grahaṇa) has satisfactorily completed 
(antikam) the desired curriculum (eva) as well. 3:1
A student, who (brahmacharyaḥ) has followed the rigors of the student life (avipluta)
without fail and has (yathaa)(kramam) systematically (adheetya) completed the study 
(vedaan) of the four vedas along with the associated scriptures (vaa) or any (vedau) two 
of the four (vaa) or just (vedam) one of them (api) as well, upon graduation should marry 
and (aavishet) enter (gṛihastha) the householder (aashramam) phase of life. 3:2

1. ṣhaṭtriñshadaabdikañ charyaṅ gurau traivedikam vratam,

tat ardhikam paadikam vaa grahaṇa-antikam eva vaa.

मनुस्मृित अध्याय ३ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 3
126
The process of graduation
A student who has (daayaharam) the inheritance (brahma) of knowledge from his/her 
(pituḥ) fatherly teacher and has become (prateetam) aware of (tam) his/her (dharmeṇa)
duties (sva) as per the class assigned to him/her, is (sragviṇam) garlanded and offered 
(talpe) a high (aaseenam) seat. Thereafter, he/she is (prathamam) first offered (gavaa)
sweets made from cow’s milk and then (arhayet) is bestowed with the honor of 
graduation and a permission to return back to his/her family. 3:3
Marriage follows graduation
(snaatvaa) Upon graduation, (anumataḥ) after obtaining the permission (guruṇaa) from 
the teacher, and his/her (samaavṛittaḥ) return to his/her family, (dvijaḥ) a graduate
should (yathaa) as per (vidhi) the norms (udvaheta) marry (bhaaryaam) a spouse who is 
(savarṇaam) from the same class as oneself and (anvitaam) displays the desirable
(lakṣhaṇa) traits. 3:4
Desirable and undesirable qualities of the spouse
Someone (yaa) who is (asapiṇḍaa) not from the same village/town (cha) and (yaa) who
(asagotraa) is not from the same lineage i.e. doesn’t have the same last name as 
(maatuḥ) the mother’s maiden name (cha) or (pituḥ) the father’s last name, (saa) that 
person is considered (prashastaa) the best (dvijaateenaam) amongst the twice borns

(maithune) for procreation and performance of other (daara) spousal (karmaṇi)
duties. 3:5
(api) Even if they are (mahaanti) very (samṛiddhaani) prosperous and possess large 
quantities of (go) cows, (aja) goats, (avi) sheeps, (dhana) wealth and (dhaanyataḥ)
grains, it is (pari)(varjayet) forbidden (stree)(sambandhe) to marry someone from the 
(dasha) ten (etaani) types of (kulaani) families mentioned in the following shloka. 3:6
The ten (kulaani) families to avoid are the ones that are engaged in (heena) lowly 
(kriyam) deeds against the recommendations of the scriptures, the ones that 
(niṣhpuruṣham) do not have good role models or are devoid of scholars, the ones that 
(nishchhandaḥ) do not study the Vedas, the ones that have (romasha) big bodily hairs,
and the ones that have genetic/chronic diseases like (arshasam) piles, (kṣhayee)
tuberculosis, (aamayaavee) gastric issues, (apasmaari) seizures, (shvitri) leukoderma 
(cha) or (kuṣhṭhi) leprosy. 3:7

(na) Do not (udvahet) marry (kanyaam) someone (kapilaam) whose skin has turned 
brown due to illness, (aṅgeem) whose body is (adhika) large or has extra organs, 
(rogiṇeem) who is chronically ill, (alomikaam) who is devoid of bodily hairs, who has 
(ati) excess of (lomaam) bodily hairs, (vaachaaṭaam) who speaks too much or 
(piṅgalaam) who has turned yellow due to sickness. 3:8
Inappropriate names
(na) Do not marry someone who (naamneem) is named after (ṛikṣha) a star, (vṛikṣha) a 
tree or (nadee) a river, or (naamikaam) their name represents (antya) an outcast or 
(parvata) a mountain, or who is (naamneem) named after (pakṣhee) a bird or (ahi) a 
snake, or their (naamikaam) name represents (preṣhya) slavery (cha) or (bheeṣhaṇa)
cruelty and ferocity. This is a temporary defect and can be fixed by changing the 
name. 3:9
 
हीनिक्रयम्। िनष्प षम ु ्। िनश्छन्दः । रोमशाशर्सम्॥  यीऽआमयावीऽअपस्मा रऽि ित्रऽकुि ऽकुलािन । च ॥

kṣhayyaamayaavyapasmaarishvitrikuṣhṭhikulaani cha.
heena-kriyam niṣhpuruṣham nishchhandaḥ romasha-arshasam,
kṣhayee-aamayaavee-apasmaari-shvitri-kuṣhṭhi-kulaani cha.

One (udvahet) should marry (striyam) a spouse whose (aṅgeem) body is (avyaṅga) free 
from any handicap, who has (saumya) a beautiful and civil (naamneem) name, who 
(gaamineem) walks elegantly like (hansa) a swan or (vaaraṇa) an elephant, who has 
(tanu) soft (loma) bodily hairs and (kesha) locks, small (dashanaam) teeth and 
proportionate and (mṛidu) pleasing (aṅgeem) bodily organs. 3:10
The 11th - 19th shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
Types of marriages
(imaan) These (aṣhṭau) eight types of (stree)(vivaahaan) marriages have long term (hita)
benefits or (ahitaan) harms (chaturṇaam) for all of the four (varṇaanaam) classes, (iha)
during this life (cha) and (pretya) in the after life (api) as well. (nibodhata) Listen and 
know about them (samaasena) summarily. 3:20
The eight types of marriages are, (braahmaḥ) the godly, (daivaḥ) the scholarly (tathaa)
and (aarṣhaḥ) the sagely (eva) as well in the highest category, (praajaapatyaḥ) one 
arranged by parents, (aasuraḥ) the discordant, (tathaa) and (gaandharvaḥ) the artistic
 
na ṛikṣha-vṛikṣha-nadee-naamneem na antya-parvata-naamikaam,
na pakṣhee-ahi-preṣhya-naamneem na cha bheeṣhaṇa-naamikaam.

(eva) as well in the middle category (cha) and, (raakṣhasaḥ) the demonic (cha) and 
(adhamaḥ) the worst amongst all, (aṣhṭamaḥ) the eighth one, (paishaachaḥ) the hateful
in the lowest category. 3:21
The 22nd - 26th shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
When the bride (svayam) herself, (aahooya) invites (sheelavate) a courteous scholar 
(shruti) of the Vedas (cha) and (archayitvaa) after having bowed to him (cha) and 
(aachchhaadya) having adorned him with good clothes, the responsibility of the
(kanyaayaaḥ) the bride’s love and care (daanam) is granted to him, (dharmaḥ) the rite 
(prakeertitaḥ) is known as (braahmaḥ) the godly marriage. The initiative of the bride, 
scholarliness of the groom and the simplicity of the ceremony are the key features of 
this kind of marriage. The permission of the elders, though implied, is not mandatory.
It is also called svayamvara i.e. personal choice of the bride. 3:27
When the parents (vitate) organize (yajñe) an elaborate yajña and invite several priests 
to preside over it and (tu) then (daanam) grant the responsibility of love and care of 
(sutaa) their daughter, (alaṅkṛitya) who has been adorned with jewelry, (ṛitvije) to one

of the priests, who (kurvate) displays (samyak) the best knowledge of (karma) the 
procedures of the yajña, (dharmam) the rite (prachakṣhate) is said to be (daivam) the 
scholarly marriage. The initiative of the parents and the elaborate yajña are the key 
features of this kind of marriage. The willingness of the bride is implied. 3:28
When the parents (dharmataḥ) righteously (aadaaya) accept (ekam) a pair of (go) a cow 
and (mithunam) an ox (vaa) or maximum (dve) two pairs as a gift (varaat) from the 
groom and then (vidhivat) properly (pradaanam) grant him (kanyaa) the responsibility 
of love and care of the bride, (saḥ) the (dharmaḥ) rite (uchyate) is said to be (aarṣhaḥ)
the sagely marriage. The simplicity of the ceremony is the key feature of this kind of 
marriage. The gift of a few cows is nominal and not expensive. The groom is expected 
to bring gifts for the bride’s family which is starkly opposite to the current tradition of 
dowry. The willingness of the bride is implied. 3:29
When the parents (anubhaaṣhya) announce (iti) these (vaachaa) words “(ubhau) Both 
of you now (saha) together (charataam) engage (dharmam) in the righteous conduct” 
(cha) and (abhyarchya) respectfully (pradaanam) grant the responsibility of love and 
care (kanyaa) of the bride, (vidhiḥ) the rite is (smṛitaḥ) known as (praajaapatyaḥ) the 
arranged marriage. The initiative and acceptance of the parents is the key feature of

this marriage. The willingness of the bride and the groom, though implied, is 
secondary. 3:30
When the groom, (shaktitaḥ) as per his financial capacity, (dattvaa) gives (draviṇam)
money (jñaatibhyaḥ) to the bride’s parents and relatives (cha) and (kanyaayai) to the 
bride (eva) as well and (svaachchhandyaat) out of their selfishness, the parents 
(pradaanam) grant the responsibility of love and care (kanyaa) of the bride to the 
groom, (dharma) the rite (uchyate) is said to be (aasuraḥ) the discordant marriage. The 
money given to buy the bride and the selfishness of her parents and relatives are the 
key features of this marriage. Vice versa, the groom can also be forced into marriage for
dowry. The willingness of the bride or the groom is not considered necessary. 3:31
When (ichchhayaa) with a mutual desire (cha) and (sambhavaḥ) due (kaama) to lust,
disregarding the social norms, (kanyaayaaḥ) the bride (cha) and (varasya) the groom, 
(anyonya)(sañyogaḥ) copulate, (tu) then (saḥ) this (maithunyaḥ) sexual union (vijñeyaḥ)
should be understood as a (gaandharvaḥ) artist marriage. The willingness of both the 
bride and the groom and their apathy towards the social norms are the key features of 
this union. Neither the permission of the parents or elders is sought nor any religious

rites are performed. This type of marriage is more prevalent in the artist community as

(hattvaa) After killing (cha) and (chhittvaa) wounding the bride’s relatives (cha) or 
(bhittvaa) after destroying their home, the (rudateem) crying and (kroshanteem)
bellowing (kanyaa) bride (haraṇam) is kidnapped (gṛihaat) from her home and 
(prasahya) forced into a marriage, this (vidhiḥ) procedure (uchyate) is said to be 
(raakṣhasaḥ) a demonic marriage. 3:33
(yatra) When one finds a woman (rahaḥ) alone, (suptaam)sleeping, (mattaam) drugged
(vaa) or (pramattaam) intoxicated and (upagachchhati) forces himself upon her, 
(vivaahaanaam) out of all marriages, (saḥ) this (aṣhṭamaḥ) eighth type is (paapiṣhṭhaḥ)
a sinful (cha) and (adhamaḥ) heinous act known as (paishaachaḥ) the hateful 
marriage. 3:34

The 35th - 38th shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
Children born from different types of marriages
(anupoorvashaḥ) In the given order, (putraaḥ) the children (jaayante) born (chaturṣhu)
out of the first four i.e. (braahmaadiṣhu) the godly to the arranged (vivaaheṣhu)
marriages maintain (brahma) God’s (varchasvinaḥ) blessings in their life and are (eva)
indeed (sammataaḥ) applauded (shiṣhṭa) by the cultured. 3:39
These children are (roopa) beautiful, strong and (upetaaḥ) are laden with (sattva)
virtuous (guṇa) qualities. They are (dhanavantaḥ) wealthy, (yashasvinaḥ) famous, 
(paryaapta)(bhogaaḥ) fulfilled with abundance, (dharmiṣhṭhaaḥ) righteous (cha) and 
(jeevanti) live for (shatam) one hundred (samaaḥ) years. 3:40

(tu) And (sutaaḥ) the children, (jaayante) born (shiṣhṭeṣhu) out of the remaining 
(itareṣhu) other (durvivaaheṣhu) outrageous marriages, are (nṛishansaa) cruel,
infamous, (anṛita)(vaadinaḥ) liars and have (dviṣhaḥ) ill feelings towards (brahma) God 
and (dharma) righteousness. 3:41
(prajaa) The children born (aninditaiḥ) out of impeccable (stree)(vivaahaiḥ) marriages 
(bhavati) become (anindyaa) uncriticizable and (nṛeeṇaam) the humans born (ninditaiḥ)
out of outrageous marriages become (ninditaa) infamous. (tasmaat) Hence, one 
(vivarjayet) is forbidden to engage in these (nindyaan) outrageous marriages. 3:42
The 43rd - 44th shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
Proper time for procreation
A couple (syaat) should (sadaa) always (abhigaamee) copulate only (ṛitukaala) during 
the best times identified for procreation. During this period, (vrajet) avoiding (enaam)
those days that are (varjam) set aside (parva) for religious performances i.e. the day of 
the full moon, the day of the no moon and the eighth day of the moon etc., a man 
(kaamyayaa) with a desire (rati) to procreate should (rataḥ) engage only with (sva) his

42. aninditaiḥ streevivaahairanindyaa bhavati prajaa,

own (daarani) wife (cha) and also maintain (tat) the (vrataḥ) resolve to be only with 
her. 3:45
(svaabhaavikaḥ) The natural (ṛituḥ) fertile period (streeṇaam) for women (smṛitaaḥ) is 
said to be (ṣhoḍasha) sixteen (raatrayaḥ) nights long, starting with the menstrual cycle. 
This (saardham) includes (chaturbhiḥ) the four (ahobhiḥ) days of the menstrual cycle, 
(itaraiḥ) which are criticized for copulation (sadvigarhitaiḥ) by the righteous. 3:46
(taasaam) Out of those sixteen nights, (aadyaaḥ) the first (chatasraḥ) four nights, the 
night (yaa) that is (ekaadashee) eleventh from the start of the menstrual cycle (cha) and 
the night that is (trayodashee) thirteenth, all of them (ninditaaḥ) have been criticized. 
(sheṣhaaḥ) The remaining (dasha) ten (raatrayaḥ) nights are considered (prashastaaḥ)
best for copulation. Out of that the day and night reserved for religious performances 
are to be avoided as well. 3:47

137
(aartave) Counting from the start of the menstrual cycle, (putraaḥ) male child(ren) 
(jaayante) are born out of copulation (yugmaasu) on the even nights and (striyaḥ)
female child(ren) are born out of copulation (ayugmaasu) on the odd (raatriṣhu) nights. 
(tasmaat) Hence, (putraarthee) those desirous of sons (samvishet) should go near their 
(striyam) wives (yugmaasu) on even nights. 3:48
When (punsaḥ) the man’s (shukre) semen is (adhike) stronger, (pumaan) a male child is 
conceived and when (striyaḥ) the female side is (adhike) stronger, (stree) a female child 
(bhavati) is conceived; when both (same) are equal in strength then either (apumaan) a 
nonbinary child is conceived (vaa) or a pair of (pun) male and (striyau) female children 
are conceived; (cha) and when both (kṣheeṇe) lack strength or (alpe) quantity then 
either there is (viparyayaḥ) no conception or miscarriages occur. 3:49
 
47. taasaamaadyaashchatasrastu ninditaikaadashee cha yaa,
trayodashee cha sheṣhaastu prashastaa dasha raatrayaḥ. taasaam aadyaaḥ chatasraḥ tu ninditaaḥ ekaadashee cha yaa,
trayodashee cha sheṣhaaḥ tu prashastaaḥ dasha raatrayaḥ.

49. pumaanpunso’dhike shukre stree bhavatyadhike striyaḥ,

मनुस्मृित अध्याय ३ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 3
138
Someone who (varjayan) stays away (striyaḥ) from copulation (aṣhṭaasu) during the 
eight nights i.e. the six nights that (nindyaasu) are criticized to be unclean (cha) and 
(anyaasu) the other two (raatriṣhu) nights of religious performances, (bhavati) becomes
(iva) like (brahmachaaree) a celebate, (yatra) even (tatra) when he/she (vasan) is 
(aashrame) in a different stage of life. 3:50
No monetary exchange for the marriage
The ideas presented in these shlokas may seem in conflict with the earlier shlokas 
describing the sagely and the discordant marriages. However, earlier Maharṣhi Manu was 
just describing the prevalent practices related to marriages and here in this section, he is 
providing his opinion against any kind monetary expectation from either side during the 
marriage. 
(vidvaan) The wise (pitaa) father (kanyaayaaḥ) of the bride (na)should not (gṛihṇeeyaat)
accept any (shulkam) monetary gift, (api) howsoever (aṇu) small, from the groom, (hi)
because if (lobhena) out of greed he (gṛihṇan) accepts (shulkam) money then for sure 
(naraḥ) he (syaat) becomes (apatyavikrayee) the seller of his children. 3:51
 
3:50 िनन्द्यास्व ास

िनन्द्यासु। अ ासु। च । अन्यासु। ि यः। राित्रषु। वजर्यन्॥ ब्र चारी ।एव । भवित । यत्र। तत्र। आश्रमे। वसन्॥

51. na kanyaayaaḥ pitaa vidvaan gṛihṇeeyaachchhulkamaṇvapi,
gṛihṇañchhulkaṅ hi lobhena syaannaro’patyavikrayee.
na kanyaayaaḥ pitaa vidvaan gṛihṇeeyaat shulkam aṇu api,
gṛihṇan shulkam hi lobhena syaat naraḥ apatyavikrayee.
मनुस्मृित अध्याय ३ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 3
139
(baandhavaaḥ) The relatives of the groom, (ye) who (mohaat) under the influence of 
greed, (upajeevanti) utilize (dhanaani) the wealth (stree) of females (vaa) or (yaanaani)
the vehicle (tu) and (vastram) clothes etc. provided by (naaree) the bride’s family, (te)
those (paapaaḥ) sinners (yaanti) attain (adho) lowly (gatim) stature. 3:52
(kechit) Some (aahuḥ) have said about the gift of a pair of (go) cow and (mithunam) ox 
as a token (shulkam) fee given by the groom (aarṣhe) in the sagely marriage. (tat) That
(api) too is (mṛiṣhaa) improper (eva) as well, because (alpaḥ) small (vaa) or (mahaan)
large monetary exchanges (evam) like this, (saḥ) are (taavat)(api) indeed (eva) like 
(vikrayaḥ) selling the bride. 3:53
When (jñaatayaḥ) the parents and near relatives (yaasaam) of the bride (na) do not 
(aadadate) accept any (shulkam) fee from the groom for the marriage, (saḥ) that 
marriage is (na) not (vikrayaḥ) a sale; (tat) that is (arhaṇam) dignifying (kumaareeṇaam)
the girls (cha) and is (aanṛishansyam) a show of love (kevalam) itself. 3:54

्
॥५२॥

Respect for females
(pitṛibhiḥ) The fathers, (bhraatṛibhiḥ) brothers, (patibhiḥ) husbands (cha) and (devaraiḥ)
brother-in-laws, (eepsubhiḥ) desirous of their (bahu)(kalyaaṇam) welfare and 
happiness, should (poojyaaḥ) respect (cha) and (bhooṣhayitavyaaḥ) bring gifts (etaaḥ)
for these females i.e. daughters, sisters, wives (tathaa) and sister-in-laws etc. 3:55
(yatra) Wherever (naaryaḥ) the women (poojyante) are respected, (devataaḥ) divine 
qualities are abundantly (ramante) present (tatra) there; (tu) and (yatra) where (etaaḥ)
they (na) are not (poojyante) respected, (sarvaaḥ) any (kriyaaḥ) efforts (aphalaaḥ) do 
not bring desired results (tatra) there. 3:56

arhaṇan tatkumaareeṇaamaanṛishansyañ cha kevalam.
yaasaam na aadadate shulkam jñaatayaḥ na saḥ vikrayaḥ,
arhaṇam tat kumaareeṇaam aanṛishansyam cha kevalam.

56. yatra naaryastu poojyante ramante tatra devataaḥ,
yatraitaastu na poojyante sarvaastatraaphalaaḥ kriyaaḥ. yatra naaryaḥ tu poojyante ramante tatra devataaḥ,
yatra etaaḥ tu na poojyante sarvaaḥ tatra aphalaaḥ kriyaaḥ.
मनुस्मृित अध्याय ३ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 3
141
(yatra) Where (jaamayaḥ) the ladies (shochanti) are grieving, (tat) that (kulam) family 
(vinashyati) gets destroyed (aashu) in no time; (tu) and (yatra) where (etaaḥ) they are 
(na) not (shochanti) grieving i.e. they are happy, (tat) that family (hi) indeed (vardhate)
experiences growth and prosperity (sarvadaa) forever. 3:57
(gehaani) The homes (yaani) that are (shapanti) cursed by (aprati)(poojitaaḥ)
disrespected (jaamayaḥ) women, (taani) those families suffer misfortune (samantataḥ)
from all sides and (vinashyanti) are destroyed by events (iva) similar to (kṛityaa) the 
catastrophic events that (hataani) cause mass destruction. 3:58
(tasmaat) Hence (naraiḥ) the humans (kaamaiḥ) desirous of their (nityam) continuous 
(bhooti) well being, should (sadaa) always and particularly (satkaareṣhu) on special 
occasions (cha) and (utsaveṣhu) festivals, (poojyaaḥ) respect (etaaḥ) these women and 
shower them with gifts of (bhooṣhaṇa) jewelry, (aachchhaadana) clothing and 
(ashanaiḥ) foods etc. 3:59

57. shochanti jaamayo yatra vinashyatyaashu tatkulam,
na shochanti tu yatraitaa vardhate taddhi sarvadaa.
shochanti jaamayaḥ yatra vinashyati aashu tat kulam,
na shochanti tu yatra etaaḥ vardhate tat hi sarvadaa.

taani kṛityaa hataani iva vinashyanti samantataḥ.
3:59 तस्मादेताः सदा प

मनुस्मृित अध्याय ३ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 3

(kule) In the family (yasmin) where (bharttaa) the husband is (nityam) always 
(santuṣhṭaḥ) happy and content (bhaaryayaa) with his wife (cha) and (tathaa)(eva)
similarly (bhaaryaa) the wife is happy and content (bhartraa) with her husband (eva) as 
well, (tatra) there (kalyaaṇam) prosperity (dhruvam) is established (vai) indeed. 3:60
(yadi) If (stree) the woman is not happy and is (na)(rocheta) disinterested (hi) then she 
(na) can not keep her (pumaansam) husband (pramodayet) happy either and (punaḥ)
again when (punsaḥ) the husband (apramodaat) is not happy, he is (na) not (pravarttate)
inclined towards (prajanam) procreation. 3:61

bhooti-kaamaiḥ naraiḥ nityam satkaareṣhu utsaveṣhu cha.

61. yadi hi stree na rocheta pumaansan na pramodayet, 
apramodaatpunaḥ punsaḥ prajanan na pravarttate.
yadi hi stree na rocheta pumaansam na pramodayet,
apramodaat punaḥ punsaḥ prajanam na pravarttate. 
मनुस्मृित अध्याय ३ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 3
143
In the current context, this shloka can also be understood as: when a woman is not 
interested then she should not be forced into doing something because her participation 
would be half hearted and that would not bring the desired results. 
(striyaam) Women’s (rochamaanaayaam) happiness brings (rochate) happiness (tu) to 
(tat) the (sarvam) entire (kulam) family (tu) and (tasyaam) their (arochamaanaayaam)
sadness causes (na)(rochate) unhappiness in (sarvam) everyone else (eva) as well. 3:62
The 63rd - 66th shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu. 
Routines and duties for the householders
(agnau) Using the fire that was brought in (vaivaahike) during the marriage, (gṛihee) a 
householder should (anvaahikeem) everyday without fail (kurveeta) perform all of 
(vidhaanam) the mandated (gṛihyam) household (karma) activities, (yathaa) as per 
(vidhi) the proper procedures. These activities include the (pañcha) five (yajña) yajña 
(cha) and (paktim) preparation of food for them. 3:67
(gṛihasthasya) In a household, (chullee) the stove, (peṣhaṇee) the grinder, (upaskaraḥ)
the broom, (kaṇḍanee) the mortar (cha) and (udakumbhaḥ) the water pot are (pañcha)

67. vaivaahike’gnau kurveeta gṛihyaṅ karma yathaavidhi, 
pañchayajñavidhaanañ cha paktiñ chaanvaahikeeṅ gṛihee. 
vaivaahike agnau kurveeta gṛihyam karma yathaa vidhi,
pañcha-yajña-vidhaanam cha paktim cha anvaahikeem gṛihee. 
मनुस्मृित अध्याय ३ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 3
144
the five (soonaaḥ) places where unintended violence can occur (cha) and (tu) hence 
(vaahayan) by using (yaaḥ) them (badhyate) one can get tied to sins. 3:68
(niṣhkṛityartham) For neutralizing the effect of (sarvaasaam) all of (taasaam) those 
unintended acts of violence (krameṇa) enumerated earlier, (maharṣhibhiḥ) the sages 
(klṛiptaaḥ) have devised the procedures of (pañcha) the five (mahaa) great (yajñaaḥ)
yajña which should be performed (gṛihamedhinaam) by the householders (prati)(aham)
everyday. 3:69
(adhyaapanam) The study and the teaching of the Vedas and God* the brahma fulfills 
(yajñaḥ) the duty (brahma) towards the God; (tarpaṇam) satisfying the mother, father 
and elders with food, service and care fulfills (yajñaḥ) the duty (pitṛi) towards elders; 
(homaḥ) making offering in the fire fulfills the duty (daivaḥ) towards mother nature; 
(baliḥ) offering a share of food to other animals fulfills the duty (bhautaḥ) towards other 
beings; (tu) and (poojanam) respecting and serving (atithi) guests fulfills (yajñaḥ) the 
duty (nṛi) towards humans. *Meditation is the study of God. 3:70

जनम
्

मनुस्मृित अध्याय ३ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 3
145
One (yaḥ) who, (shaktitaḥ) as permitted by his/her capabilities, (na) does not 
(haapayati) ignore the performance of (etaan) these (pañcha) five (mahaa) great 
(yajñaan) duties, (api) even (vasan) while residing (gṛihe) in his/her house (nityam)
everyday, (saḥ) he/she is (na) not (lipyate) impacted (soonaa)(doṣhaiḥ) by the ills of the 
unintended violences. 3:71
One (yaḥ) who (na) does not (nirvapati) distribute their fare share to the beings that fall 
(pañchaanaam) in the five categories, (devataa) divinities i.e. natural elements and 
scholars, (atithi) guests, (bhṛityaanaam) servants dependents, (pitṛeeṇaam) elders (cha)
and to (aatmanaḥ) one’s soul as well, (saḥ) he/she (ut)(shvasan) breathes but (na) does 
not (jeevati) live. 3:72
 
अध्यापनम्। ब्र य ः । िपतय ः ृ । तु। तपर्णम्॥ होमः । दैवः । बिलः । भौतः । नय ः ृ । अितिथपजनम ू ्॥
70. adhyaapanam brahmayajñaḥ pitṛiyajñastu tarpaṇam,
homo daivo balirbhauto nṛiyajño’tithipoojanam.
adhyaapanam brahma-yajñaḥ pitṛi-yajñaḥ tu tarpaṇam,
homaḥ daivaḥ baliḥ bhautaḥ nṛi-yajñaḥ atithi-poojanam.

72. devataa’tithibhṛityaanaam pitṛeeṇaamaatmanashcha yaḥ,
na nirvapati pañchaanaamuchchhvasanna sa jeevati.
devataa-atithi-bhṛityaanaam pitṛeeṇaam aatmanaḥ cha yaḥ,
na nirvapati pañchaanaam ut shvasan na saḥ jeevati.
मनुस्मृित अध्याय ३ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 3
146
These (pañcha) five (yajñaan) yajña (prachakṣhate) are also known as (ahutam) ahuta, 
(hutam) huta, (prahutam) prahuta, (braahmyam)(hutam) braahmyam huta (tathaa) and 
(praashitam) praashita 3:73
The brahma yajña involves only (japaḥ) chants and (ahutaḥ) no physical offerings; the 
deva yajña involves (hutaḥ) offerings (homaḥ) made in the fire; the balivaishvadeva 
yajña involves (baliḥ) sacrificing (prahutaḥ) a portion of own food (bhautikaḥ) for the 
benefit of other beings; the atithi yajña involves (hutam) offering respect and food to 
the ones (dvija) amongst the twice borns who deserve the (agrya) first (archaa)
obeisance i.e. (braahmyam) the braahmaṇa; and the pitṛi yajña involves (praashitam)
feeding and (tarpaṇam) satisfying (pitṛi) the elders. 3:74
Everyone (syaat) should, (nitya) on a daily basis, (yuktaḥ) engage (svadhyaaye) in 
meditation and in self study of the Vedas (cha) and (karmaṇi) perform the offerings in 
the fire (daive) for the divinities (eva) as well, (hi) because (iha) in this world, one
(yuktaḥ) engaged (karmaṇi) in the act of performing the offerings (daiva) for the

divinities (bibharti) sustains both (chara) the mobile and (acharam) the stationary 
creations present (idam) here. 3:75
(aahutiḥ) The offerings (samyak) properly (praastaa) made (agnau) in the fire, 
(upatiṣhṭhate) rise in the atmosphere and interact with the rays (aadityam) of the sun 
and help in the formation of clouds. (vṛiṣhṭiḥ) Rain (jaayate) results (aadityaat) from this 
interaction with the rays of the sun. (vṛiṣhṭeḥ) Rain produces (annam) grains and food 
(tataḥ) that sustains (prajaaḥ) the masses. 3:76
Importance of the householders
(yathaa) As (sarva) all (jantavaḥ) living beings (samaashritya) depend (vaayum) on air 
(vartante) for their existence and well being, (tathaa) so do (sarva) all the individuals 
(aashramaaḥ) in different stages of life, (vartante) for their sustenance, (aashritya)
depend (gṛihastham) on the householders. 3:77

(yasmaat) Since, (jñaanena) by providing the right knowledge to children in their 
formative years (cha) and (annena) by providing grains, food and all other means of 
sustenance (anu)(aham) everyday to others, (api)(eva) only (gṛihasthena) the 
householders (dhaaryante) sustain (aashramiṇaḥ) the individuals in all of the other 
(trayaḥ) three stages of life, (tasmaat) hence, (gṛihee) the householder (aashramaḥ)
stage is considered (jyeṣhṭha) the most important stage for the society. 3:78
(saḥ) That householder stage of life, (yaḥ) which (adhaaryaḥ) can not be maintained by 
someone (durbala) with a low control (indriyaiḥ) over one’s sensory organs, should be 
(prayatnena) effortfully (sandhaaryaḥ) undertaken by those (ichchhataa) who are
desirous of (nityam) continuous (sukham) happiness (iha) in this world (cha) and by 
those (ichchhataa) who are desirous of attaining (akṣhayam) the everlasting (svargam)
bliss of mokṣha. 3:79

मनुस्मृित अध्याय ३ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 3
149
For their sustenance, (ṛiṣhayaḥ) the sages, (pitaraḥ) the elderly, (devaaḥ) the scholars, 
(atithayaḥ) the guests, (bhootaani) the servant (tathaa) and other dependents, 
(aashaasate) look up to (kuṭumbibhyaḥ) the householders with hope, and hence, 
(tebhyaḥ) they, the householders, (vijaanataa) should understand and fulfill their 
(kaaryam) duties. 3:80
Five duties of the householders
(yathaa) Following (vidhi) the proper procedures, the householders (archayeta) should 
show their gratitude (ṛiṣheen) towards the sages (svaadhyaayena) by meditating and 
studying the Vedas, (devaan) towards the divinities of Mother Nature (homaiḥ) by 
making offerings in the fire, (pitṛeen) towards the elders (shraaddhaiḥ) by faithfully 
serving them, (nṛeen)towards scholarly humans (annaiḥ) by treating the guests properly
with food etc. (cha) and (bhootaani) towards all other beings (bali)(karmaṇaa) by 
sacrificing a portion of their own food and offering it first to others. 3:81
 
sukhañ chehechchhataa nityañ yo’dhaaryo durbalendriyaiḥ. saḥ sandhaaryaḥ prayatnena svargam akṣhayam ichchhataa,
sukham cha iha ichchhataa nityam yaḥ adhaaryaḥ durbala-indriyaiḥ.

(ahaḥ)(ahaḥ) Everyday, a householder (aavahan) should address (pitṛibhyaḥ) the elders 
(preetim) with love and respect (vaa) and (api) also (shraaddham) faithfully (kuryaat)
satisfy them (annaadyena) with food, (udakena) water, (payaḥ) milk, (moola) vegetables 
(vaa) and (phalaiḥ) fruits etc. 3:82
The 83rd shloka is not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
Procedure of the Balivaishvadeva yajña
(anu)(aham) Everyday, (braahmaṇaḥ) a twice born should take a portion of the food*
(siddhasya) cooked (agnau) in the fire (gṛihye) at home for the sacrifice 
(vaishva)(devasya) towards the nature’s divinities and (poorvakam) following (vidhi) the 
proper procedure, (kuryaat) should make (homam) offerings in fire, separate from the 
stove, (aabhyaḥ) for these (devataabhyaḥ) divinities that are mentioned in the following 
shlokas. *One should avoid the use of food that is sour, salty or fermented, for the 
offerings. 3:84
(aadau) Begin with the first offering (agneḥ) for the fire (cha) and then (somasya) for the 
cooling herbs, then (tayoḥ) for both of them (samastayoḥ) together (eva) as well (cha)

and then for all of (devebhyaḥ) the divinities (vishvebhyaḥ) in the entire world (cha) and

Next offering is (kuhvai) for the darkness on the no moon night, which is followed by

of the other beings. One should think of God’s (indra) grandeur while placing a portion

marudbhyaḥ iti tu dvaari kṣhipet apsu adbhyaḥ iti api,
vanaspatibhyaḥ iti evam musala-ulookhale haret.

middle (vaastu) of the home while thanking him (brahma) for the knowledge (tu) and 
(vaastoṣhpatibhyaam) for providing the habitat. 3:89
(cha) And (devebhyaḥ) for the rest of the divinities (vishvebhyaḥ) of the world, (eva) as 
well, a portion of (balim) the sacrificial food (utkṣhipet) should be placed (aakaashe) on 
the roof. A portion of the sacrificial food is required (bhootebhyaḥ) for the other animals 
(charebhyaḥ) who roam (divaa) during the day (cha) and for those (eva) as well 
(chaaribhyaḥ) who roam (naktañ) during the night. 3:90
(kurveeta) Place a portion of (balim) the sacrificial food (pṛiṣhṭha) at the back (vaastuni)
of the home, while thinking (sarvaatma)(bhootaye) of the all pervading God (tu) and 
(haret) place (sarvam)(sheṣham) the rest of (bali) the sacrificial food (dakṣhiṇataḥ) on 
the southern side while pledging to take care (pitṛibhyaḥ) of the elders. 3:91

And like this a portion of the sacrificial food should be (shanakaiḥ) carefully (nirvapet)

who are suffering from sickness due to their (paapa) sins. 3:92
The 93rd shloka is not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
Taking care of guests
(kṛitvaa) After completing (etat) this (karma) procedure of offering (bali)sacrificial food, 
one should (poorvam) first (aashayet) feed (atithim) the guests, if any, (evam)(cha) and 
then (vidhivat) follow the procedure of (dadyaat) giving (bhikṣhaam) food 
(brahmachaariṇe) to the students (bhikṣhave) who have come to ask for it. 3:94
 
pitṛibhyo balisheṣhan tu sarvan dakṣhiṇato haret.
pṛiṣhṭha-vaastuni kurveeta balim sarvaatma-bhootaye,
pitṛibhyaḥ bali-sheṣham tu sarvam dakṣhiṇataḥ haret.

The 95th – 98th shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
One should (vidhi)(poorvakam) properly (satkṛitya) welcome (atithaye) a guest 
(sampraaptaaya) who has arrived (cha) and (tu) then (yathaa) as per his/her (shakti)
capacity, the host (pradadyaat) should provide the guest with a comfortable (aasana)
seat, (udake) water and (annam) food (eva) as well. 3:99
The 100th shloka is not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
Comfortable seats made out of (tṛiṇaani) grass fibers, (bhoomiḥ) a place to rest, 
(udakam) water (cha) and (api) also (chaturthee) the fourth, (soonṛitaa) sweet 
welcoming (vaak) words, (sataam) a cultured (gehe) home is (na)(kadaachana) never 
(uchchhidyante) devoid of (etaani) these attributes. 3:101
(braahmaṇaḥ) A braahmaṇa who (nivasan) stays (tu) only for (eka) one (raatram) night 
(smṛitaḥ) is known as (atithiḥ) a guest (hi) because (yasmaat) whose (sthitaḥ) arrival and 
stay (anityam) is unpredictable, (tasmaat) he/she (uchyate) is said to be (atithiḥ) a 
guest. 3:102

Someone who is from (eka) the same (graameeṇam) village, (tathaa) and (api) also 
(saaṅgatikam) someone who is a long term friend, or someone (bhaaryaa) who has a 
spouse, (vaa) or someone who is the holder of (agnayaḥ) fires in his/her home, (yatra)
when these people (upasthitam) are present (gṛihe) at the house of (vipram) a twice 
born, they (na)should not be (vidyaat) considered (atithim) as guests i.e. the mandatory 
duty of serving a guest is not fulfilled by attending to these people. 3:103
(gṛihasthaaḥ) The householders (ye) who (upaasate) are desirous of (paakam) food 
cooked by (para)someone, (pretya) in their next lives, (tena) due to their greed for food, 
(te) those (abuddhayaḥ) ignorants are born (pashutaam) as animals and (vrajanti) roam 
around, depending on others (daayinaam) to give them (annaadi) food. 3:104

104. upaasate ye gṛihasthaaḥ parapaakamabuddhayaḥ,
मनुस्मृित अध्याय ३ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 3
157
(gṛihamedhinaa) The householders should ensure that (atithiḥ) a guest arriving (saayam)
in the evening (sooryoḍhaḥ) after sunset (apraṇodyaḥ) is not turned back and everyone, 
(tu) regardless of whether he/she (praaptaḥ) arrives (kaale) timely (vaa) or (akaale) at 
odd hours in (asya) their (gṛihe) home, (na) does not (vaset) remain (anashnan)
unfed. 3:105
(yat) Whatever is (na) not being (bhojayet) offered (atithim) to the guests, the 
householders should (na) not (ashneeyaat) consume (tat) that (svayam) themselves, 
(vai) as well. (poojanam) Serving (atithi) the guests increases (dhanyam) the wealth, 
(aayuṣhyam) the health, (yashasyam) the fame (vaa) and (svargyam) the happiness of 
the householders. 3:106
 
tena te pretya pashutaam vrajantyannaadidaayinaam.
upaasate ye gṛihasthaaḥ parapaakam abuddhayaḥ,
tena te pretya pashutaam vrajanti annaadi-daayinaam.

(aasana) The seat and (avasathau) the place of stay, (shayyaam) the bed, (anuvrajyaam)
the means of movement and (upaasanaam) the personal time offered to the guests 
should be based on the stature and the capability of the guest; (uttameṣhu) the guests
of high order (kuryaat) should be given (uttamam) utmost attention, (same) one of 
medium order should be offered (samam) medium attention and (heene) a guest of 
lower capabilities should be offered (heenam) the normal attention. 3:107
(yadi) If (anyaḥ) other (atithiḥ) guests (aavrajet) arrive after the (vaishva)(deve)
Balivaishvadeva yajña (nirvṛitte) has already been performed, (tu) then (tasya) they 
should (api) also be (pradadyaat) offered (annam) food (yathaa) as per the 
householder’s (shakti) capacity. However, if the food is cooked again then there is (na)
no need (haret) to take (balim) sacrificial portions out of it. 3:108
(vipraḥ) A braahmaṇa should (na) not (nivedayet) mention (sve) his/her (kula)(gotre)
lineage just (artham) for the purpose of getting (bhojana) food, (hi) because (te) those 
who (shansan) praise themselves (arthe) in order to influence the donor in giving them

more (bhojana) food, they (uchyate) are referred to (budhaiḥ) by the learned (iti) as the 
ones (vaantaashee) who eat someone’s vomit. 3:109
The 110th – 112th shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
Treating other visitors who do not qualify as guests
Besides the guests mentioned earlier, (itaraan) others including (sakhyaadeen) friends, 
who at times (aagataan) visit the host’s (gṛiham) home (saha) along with their 
(bhaaryayaa)spouse, should (api) also (satkṛitya) be welcomed (sampreetyaa) with love 
and (annam) food (bhojayet) should be fed to them (yathaa) as per the host’s (shakti)
capacity. 3:113
Who can be fed before the guests
(suvaasineeḥ) The newly weds, (kumaareeḥ) the little girls, (rogiṇaḥ) the sick (cha) or 
(garbhiṇeeḥ) pregnant (striyaḥ) women (eva) as well, all of (etaan) them (bhojayet)
should be fed (agre) before (atithibhyaḥ)the guests (avichaarayan) without a doubt. 3:114

113. itaraanapi sakhyaadeensampreetyaa gṛihamaagataan,
satkṛityaannañ yathaashakti bhojayetsaha bhaaryayaa.
itaraan api sakhyaadeen sampreetyaa gṛiham aagataan,
satkṛitya annam yathaa-shakti bhojayet saha bhaaryayaa.

मनुस्मृित अध्याय ३ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 3

The 115th shloka is not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
When should the host consume
(atha) Starting (vipreṣhu) with the scholarly guests, then (sveṣhu) the relatives (cha) and 
(bhṛityeṣhu) the servants (eva) as well, when all of them (bhuktavatsu) have consumed, 
(hi) indeed (tu) only (pashchaat) after (tataḥ) that (avashiṣhṭam) the remainder 
(bhuñjeeyaataam) should be consumed (dampatee) by the hosting couple. 3:116
(pashchaat) After (poojayitvaa) having satisfied (ṛiṣheen) the sages and God with 
meditation and study of the Vedas, (devaan) the mother nature’s divinites by making 
offerings in the fire, (devataaḥ) the divinities (gṛihyaaḥ) in and around the home i.e. 
other beings with food, (cha) and (manuṣhyaan) the guests (cha) and (pitṛeen) the elders 
by serving them, only (tataḥ) then (gṛihasthaḥ) the householder (bhavet) should (bhuk)
consume (sheṣha) the remainder. 3:117

114. suvaasineeḥ kumaareeshcha rogiṇo garbhiṇeeḥ striyaḥ,
atithibhyo’gra evaitaanbhojayedavichaarayan.
suvaasineeḥ kumaareeḥ cha rogiṇaḥ garbhiṇeeḥ striyaḥ,
atithibhyaḥ agre eva etaan bhojayet avichaarayan.

117. devaanṛiṣheenmanuṣhyaañshcha pitṛeengṛihyaashcha devataaḥ,
poojayitvaa tataḥ pashchaad gṛihasthaḥ sheṣhabhugbhavet.
devaan ṛiṣheen manuṣhyaan cha pitṛeen gṛihyaaḥ cha devataaḥ,
मनुस्मृित अध्याय ३ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 3
161
One (yaḥ) who (pachati) cooks (kevalam) only (kaaraṇaat) for (aatma) oneself, (saḥ)
he/she (bhuṅkte) consumes in (agham) sin (hi) because (etat) this has already been 
(vidheeyate) prescribed that only (shiṣhṭa) the remainder after (yajña) the yajña is 
proper (annam) food (ashanam) for the consumption (sataam) of the benevolent. 3:118
The 119th – 284th shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
A householder should (nityam)(nityam) always (bhavet) become (aashee) the consumer 
of (amṛita) the deathless (vaa) or (vighas) the sin free (bhojanaḥ) food; (sheṣham) the 
remainder from (yajña) the offerings into the fire (amṛitam) is the deathless food 
(tathaa)(tu) and (sheṣham) the remainder (bhukta) after feeding guests etc. is the food 
(vighasaḥ) free from any kind of sins. 3:285
Closing the discussion on the duties of the householders
(etat) This was (sarvam) everything (vidhaanam) about the procedures for the 
fulfillment of (paañcha) the five (yajñikam) duties, (abhihitam) described (vaḥ) for your 
 
poojayitvaa tataḥ pashchaat gṛihasthaḥ sheṣha-bhuk bhavet.

yajña-shiṣhṭa-ashanam hi etat sataam annam vidheeyate.

285. vighasaashee bhavennityan nityam vaa’mṛitabhojanaḥ,

benefit. Now (shrooyataam) listen to (iti) the (vidhaanam) rules around (mukhya) the

Chapter 4
When to start the householder phase
(uṣhitvaa) After completing his/her education while residing (gurau) with a teacher 
during (aadyam) the first (chaturtham)(bhaagam) quarter of one’s (aayuṣhaḥ) life, 
(dvijaḥ) a twice born, at the beginning of (dviteeyam) the second (bhaagam) quarter of 
one’s(aayuṣhaḥ) life, one should (kṛita)seek (daaraḥ) a spouse and (vaset) reside (gṛihe)
in a home i.e. accept the duties of a householder. 4:1
No harm to other beings
(anaapadi) During the times of no emergency, (vipraḥ) a twice born (jeevet) should, for 
his/her sustenance, (samaasthaaya) adopt (taam) those (vṛittiḥ) vocations (yaa) that 
(eva) either (adroheṇa) do not cause any harm (bhootaanaam) to any being (vaa) or 
(punaḥ) when such a vocation is not available then a vocation that causes (alpa) minimal 
(droheṇa) pain to other beings. 4:2
Accumulating wealth
One (kurveeta) should (svaiḥ) by his/her own (agarhitaiḥ) uncriticisable (karmabhiḥ)
actions, (akleshena) without harming his/her (shareerasya) body, earn and (sañchayam)
accumulate (dhana) wealth, (maatra) just enough (artham)to (prasiddhi) happily sustain

1. chaturthamaayuṣho bhaagamuṣhitvaa’’dyaṅ gurau dvijaḥ,
dviteeyamaayuṣho bhaagaṅ kṛitadaaro gṛihe vaset.
chaturtham aayuṣhaḥ bhaagam uṣhitvaa aadyam gurau dvijaḥ,
dviteeyam aayuṣhaḥ bhaagam kṛita-daaraḥ gṛihe vaset.
