2. adroheṇaiva bhootaanaamalpadroheṇa vaa punaḥ,
yaa vṛittistaan samaasthaaya vipro jeevedanaapadi.
adroheṇa eva bhootaanaam alpa-droheṇa vaa punaḥ,
yaa vṛittiḥ taam samaasthaaya vipraḥ jeevet anaapadi.
मनुस्मृित अध्याय ४ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 4
164
(yaatraa) the journey of life. In society, the function of accumulating wealth has been 
assigned to the vaishya only. If people from the other classes focus on accumulation of 
wealth then they will deviate from the duties assigned to their respective classes. 4:3
The 4th - 10th shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
Worthy occupations
(hetoḥ) For his/her (vṛitti) sustenance, (braahmaṇa) a twice born (na) should not 
(kathañchana) ever (vartteta) engage in the trickery (loka) of the worldly (vṛittam)
occupations. An arya (jeevet) should sustain himself/herself by engaging only in 
(ajihmaam) the uncorrupt, free from malice, (ashaṭhaam) non-deceitful and 
(shuddhaam) pure (jeevikaam) occupations, as recommended in the scriptures. 4:11
Virtue of contentment
(sukhaarthee) Someone desirous of happiness (bhavet) should become (sañyataḥ) self 
controlled (aasthaaya) by treating (santoṣham) contentment as (param) the highest 
virtue, (hi) because (santoṣha) contentment (moolam) is the root (sukham) of happiness

and (viparyayaḥ) the opposite i.e. discontentment (moolam) is the root (duḥkha) of 
sorrows. 4:12
(ataḥ) Hence (jeevan) for sustenance, (snaatakaḥ) a graduated (dvijaḥ) twice born 
should choose (anyatamayaa) from the sanctioned (vṛityaa) occupations (tu) and 
(dhaarayet) resolve to adhere (imaani) to these (vrataani) principles that result in 
enhancement of one’s happiness, (aayuṣhya) health, quality of life, (yashasyaani) fame, 
ultimately leading to (svarga) mokṣha. 4:13
One should (nityam) always (atandritaḥ) tirelessly (kuryaat) perform (karma) the duties 
(svakam) assigned to oneself (vedoditam) as per the Vedas. By (tat) their (kurvan)
performance (yathaa) as per one’s (shakti) capabilities, one (hi) indeed (praapnoti)
attains (paramaam) the ultimate (gatim) happiness and liberation. 4:14

14. vedoditan svakaṅ karma nityaṅ kuryaadatandritaḥ,
मनुस्मृित अध्याय ४ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 4
166
(na) Neither (eeheta) desire or try to (arthaan) get wealth, (prasaṅgena) by 
misrepresenting the facts, (na) nor (karmaṇaa) by engaging in acts that are (viruddhena)
against the scriptures, society or personal wellbeing, and (na) nor when 
(vidyamaaneṣhu) there is already enough (artheṣhu) wealth. (na) Do not try 
(yataḥ)(tataḥ) by hook or by crook methods (api) even (aartyaam) during emergencies 
or when suffering. 4:15
(kaamataḥ) Under the influence of strong desire, one should (na) not (prasajyeta) try to 
acquire (artheṣhu) the subject matters (sarveṣhu) of all (indriya) of the senses (cha) and 
(manasaa) with mental determination, effortfully (sannivarttayet) relieve oneself from
(ati) extreme (prasaktim) longing (eteṣhaam) for any of these. 4:16
Wealth that supports education
One (parityajet) should get rid (sarvaan) of all (arthaan) of those means and wealths 
that (virodhinaḥ) prevent him/her (svaadhyaayasya) from self study of the Vedas and 
 
taddhi kurvanyathaashakti praapnoti paramaaṅ gatim.
vedoditam svakam karma nityam kuryaat atandritaḥ,
tat hi kurvan yathaa-shakti praapnoti paramaam gatim.

indriya-artheṣhu sarveṣhu na prasajyeta kaamataḥ,
ati-prasaktim cha eteṣhaam manasaa sannivarttayet.

scriptures and (yathaa)(tathaa)(tu) howsoever possible, pursue (adhyaapayan) the 
study, (hi) because only (saa) that would help in (kṛityataa) achieving (kṛita) the purpose 
(asya) of one's life. 4:17
The 18th shloka is not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
Benefits of studying the scriptures
One should (nityam) always (avekṣheta) keep studying (cha) and revising (shaastraaṇi)
the scriptures including (vaidikaan) the Vedas (cha) and (nigamaan) their explanations
(eva) as well. This (aashu)(karaaṇi) expedites (vṛiddhi) the increase in one’s (buddhi)
intellect, (dhanyaani) wealth (cha) and (hitaani) welfare. 4:19
(yathaa)(yathaa)(hi) As (puruṣhaḥ) a person (sam)(adhi)(gachchhati) goes closer to or 
delves deeper into (shaastram) the scriptures, (tathaa)(tathaa) so does his/her 
(vijaanaati) knowledge and understanding increase (cha) and (asya) his/her (rochate)
interest (vijñaanam) in the science behind the scriptures develops further. 4:20

The five duties are mandatory
(sarvadaa) Always, (yathaa) as much as (shakti) permitted by the means, the five daily 
duties i.e. (ṛiṣhi)(yajñam) performance of self study and meditation, (deva)(yajñam)
performance of offerings in the fire, (bhoota)(yajñam) performance of sacrifices for the 
other beings, (nṛi)(yajñam) performance of services for the guests (cha) and 
(pitṛi)(yajñam) performance of services for the elders, should (na) not (haapayet) be 
deviated from. 4:21
The 22nd – 24th shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
The duty of performing yajña
The householder should (sadaa) always (juhuyaat) perform (hotram) the offerings (agni)
in fire (aadi) at the beginning as well as (ante) at the end (dyu) of the day (cha) and 
(nishoḥ) of the night i.e. at both of the times of transition (cha) and (eva) also (darshena)
the darsheṣhṭi yajña (ante) at the end of the first (ardha) half (maasa) of a month i.e. on 
the no moon day (cha) and (paurṇa) on the completion (maasena) of the month i.e. on 
the full moon day (hi) as well. 4:25

The 26th – 28th shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
The duty of serving guests
(kashchit) Any (atithiḥ) guest arriving at (asya) this householder’s (gehe) home should 
(na) not (vaset) stay (anarchitaḥ) unwelcomed without proper (aasana) seat, (ashana)
food, (adbhiḥ) water, (moola) vegetables, (phalena) fruits (vaa) and/or (shayyaabhiḥ)
bed etc., (shaktitaḥ) as permitted by the host’s means. 4:29
Guests that are to be welcomed and to be not welcomed
(paakhaṇḍinaḥ) The hypocrites, (vikarmasthaan) the criminals, the liars, the nonbelievers, (vaiḍaala)(vṛittikaan) the pretending opportunists, (shaṭhaan) the 
manipulators, (haitukaan) the sophists (cha) and (baka)(vṛitteen) the conniving persons
should (na) not (archayet) be welcomed (api) even (vaaṅ) with words (maatreṇa)
only. 4:30
 
25. agnihotrañ cha juhuyaadaadyante dyunishoḥ sadaa,
darshena chaardhamaasaante paurṇamaasena chaiva hi.
agnihotram cha juhuyaat aadi-ante dyu-nishoḥ sadaa,
darshena cha ardha-maasa-ante paurṇa-maasena cha eva hi.

(gṛiha)(medhinaḥ) The householders (poojayet) should welcome and serve (snaataan)
the graduates who adhere to (vrata) the resolve of studying and (shrotriyaan)
propagating (veda) the Vedic (vidyaa) knowledge, by offering them (havya) food and 
(kavyena) other necessary things as needed, (cha) while (varjayet) avoiding 
(vipareetaan) those who act contrarily. 4:31
(shaktitaḥ) As permitted by one’s means, (anuparodhataḥ) without harming one’s own 
well-being, (kartavyaḥ) it is the duty (gṛiha)(medhinaa) of a householder (daatavyam) to 
give food etc. to those (apachamaanebhyaḥ) who are not supposed to cook by 
themselves i.e. students and ascetics etc. (cha) and also give (samvibhaagaḥ) a portion 
(bhootebhyaḥ) to other incapable beings i.e. birds, animals and handicapped individuals 
etc. 4:32

(klṛipta) clipped, (daantaḥ) be in control of one’s senses, wear (shukla) clean (ambaraḥ)
clothes, (shuchiḥ) maintain internal and external hygiene (cha) and (nityam) always 
(syaat) remain (yuktaḥ) engaged (svaadhyaaye) in the study of the Vedas (cha) and in

Proximity with a menstruating woman
During (striyam) a woman’s (aartava)(darshane) menstruation period, one should (na)
not (pramattaḥ) lustfully (upagachchhet) get too close to her (cha) and should (na) not 
(api)(eva) even (shayeeta) sleep by (tayaa) her (saha) side (samaana) on the same 
(shayane) bed. 4:40
(hi) Because (prajñaa) the intellect, (tejaḥ) the brilliance, (balam) the strength, 
(chakṣhuḥ) the eyesight (cha) and (aayuḥ) the longevity (eva) as well, (narasya) of a 
person, (upagachchhataḥ) who goes close (rajasaa)(abhiplutaam) to a menstruating 
(naareem) woman, (praheeyate) is compromised. 4:41

Use of animals for travel
One should (na) not (vrajet) travel (dhuryaiḥ) by putting those animals in harness, that 
(avineetaiḥ) are untrained, (kṣhut) hungry, (peeḍitaiḥ) suffering (vyaadhi) from sickness, 
have (bhinna) mutilated (shṛiṅga) horns, (akṣhi) eyes or (khuraiḥ) hooves, (cha) or whose 
(baala) tail (adhi)(viroopitaiḥ) is wounded or mutilated. 4:67
One should (nityam) always (vrajet) travel using those animals that (vineetaiḥ) are well 
trained, (aashugaiḥ) swift, (varṇa)(roopa)(upasampannaiḥ) elegant looking (tu) and
 
prajñaa tejo balañ chakṣhuraayushchaiva praheeyate.

Choice of the residence
One should (na) not (samvaset) reside in the vicinity of (patitaiḥ) the undutiful, 
(chaaṇḍaalaiḥ) the cruel, (pulkasaiḥ) the outcasts, (moorkhaiḥ) the fools, (avaliptaiḥ) the 
egoists, (antyaiḥ) the ones who are outside the four varṇas (cha) and 
(antyaavasaayibhiḥ) the ones with malignant tendencies. 4:79
The 80th – 91st shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
Daily routine for meditation
One (budhyeta) should get up (braahme)(muhoorte) before twilight (cha) and then 
quietly (anuchintayet) dwell upon (dharma) the righteous conduct, (arthau) the ethical 
wealth, (kleshaan) the ailments (kaaya) of the body (cha) and (tat) their (moolaan)

The 95th – 127th shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
Abstinence on the sacred days
(snaatakaḥ) A scholarly (dvijaḥ) twice-born should (nityam) always (bhavet) be 
(brahmachaaree) the one practicing abstinence on the sacred days, which are 
(aṣhṭameem) the eighth and (chaturdasheem) the fourteenth day of the moon, 
(amaavaasyaam)the no moon day (cha) and (paurṇa)(maaseem)the full moon day, (api)
even if his spouse is (ṛitau) in the fertility period. 4:128
The 129th – 132nd shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
Inadvisable relationships
One should (na) not (upaseveta) have close relationships with (vairiṇam) an enemy,
(cha)(eva) as well as (vairiṇaḥ) the enemy’s (sahaayam) accomplice, (adhaarmikam) an 
unrighteous person, (taskaram) a thief (cha)(eva) as well as (parasya) someone else’s 
(yoṣhitam) wife. 4:133
 
94. ṛiṣhayo deerghasandhyatvaaddeerghamaayuravaapnuyuḥ,
prajñaañ yashashcha keerttiñ cha brahmavarchasameva cha.
ṛiṣhayaḥ deergha-sandhyatvaat deergham aayuḥ avaapnuyuḥ,
prajñaam yashaḥ cha keerttim cha brahma-varchasam eva cha.

(hi) Because (iha) in this (loke) world, there is (na)(kiñchana) nothing (vidyate) known to 
be (eedṛisham)so (anaayuṣhyam) detrimental to the longevity (puruṣhasya) of a person,

(daaraa) wife. 4:134
The 135th – 136th shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
Hope and positivity until death
(poorvaabhiḥ) Due to prior (asamṛiddhibhiḥ) setbacks one should (na) not (avamanyeta)
downplay (aatmaanam) oneself and (anu)(ichchhet)should desire and make efforts (aa)
until (mṛityoḥ) death, to earn enough (shriyam) wealth (na) without (manyeta)
considering (enaam) it (durlabhaam) impossible to attain. 4:137
Speak pleasant truth and treat others well
One (brooyaat) should speak (satyam) the truth and (brooyaat) speak words that are 
(priyam) pleasant to hear; one should (na) not (brooyaat) speak (satyam) the truth that 
is (apriyam) unpleasant; (cha) and one should (na) not (brooyaat) speak that which is 
 
adhaarmikam taskaram cha parasya eva cha yoṣhitam.

Duty of chanting mantras, performing yajña and studying Vedas
(yuktaḥ) Equipped with (maṅgala) auspicious (aachaara) conduct (cha) and (syaat) being 
(prayata) an industrious (aatmaa) soul who is (jitendriyaḥ) in control of the senses, one 
should (nityam) always (atandritaḥ) diligently (japet) chant the mantras (cha)(eva) as 
well as (juhuyaat) make offerings (agnim) in the fire. 4:145
(yuktaanaam) Those who are equipped with (maṅgala) auspicious (aachaara) conduct 
(cha) and are (nityam) always (prayata) diligently engaged in the upliftment 
(aatmanaam) of their soul, (cha)(eva) as well as, (japataam) chants and (juhvataam)
yajña, they (na) never (vidyate)(vinipaataḥ) gravitate towards sins. 4:146

(yathaa)(kaalam) As much as possible one should (nityam) always (atandritaḥ) diligently 
(abhyaset) practice (vedam) the study of the Vedas (eva) indeed, (hi) because (tam) that 
(aahuḥ) is said to be (asya) one’s (param) primary (dharmam) duty and (anyaḥ)
everything else (uchyate) is considered (upadharmaḥ) secondary. 4:147
(shauchena) With the purity of body and mind attained by (satatam) the persistent 
(abhyaasena) practice of (veda) the Vedas, (cha)(eva) as well as, (tapasaa) with 
fortitude (cha) and (adroheṇa) with non-violence (bhootaanaam) towards other beings, 
one is able (smarati) to remember his/her (paurvikeem) prior (jaatim) lives. 4:148
(sansmaran) After remembering one’s (paurvikeem) prior (jaatim) lives, one (punaḥ)
again gets back (abhyasate) to the practice (brahma) of the Vedas (eva) itself (cha) and

(abhyaasena) with the practice (brahma) of the Vedas one (ashnute) attains (anantam)

The 150th – 153rd shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
Respecting the elders
One (abhivaadayet)should bow (vṛiddhaan) to the elders (cha) and (dadyaat) offer them 
one’s (svakam) own (aasanam) seat (eva) as well. And then one (aaseeta) should sit 
(upa) close to them (kṛitaañjaliḥ) with clasped hands waiting for their instructions (cha)
and (gachchhataḥ) when they leave, one should see them off by (anu) following 
(pṛiṣhṭhataḥ) behind them (iyaat) for some distance. 4:154
Invest oneself in righteous behavior
One should (atandritaḥ) diligently (niṣheveta) invest himself/herself (sadaachaaram) in 
benevolent behavior by (samyak) properly (nibaddham) constraining (sveṣhu) all of 
his/her (karmasu) actions to conform (moolam) to the core (dharma) of righteousness

brahma abhyaasena cha ajasram anantam sukham ashnute.

(uditam) as revealed (shruti) in the Vedas and (smṛiti) the scriptures written

(aachaaraat) Due to benevolent behavior one (labhate) gains (aayuḥ) longevity, 
(eepsitaaḥ) desirable (prajaaḥ) children and (akṣhayyam) non depleting (dhanam)

indeed (bhavati) becomes (ninditaḥ) infamous (loke) in the World (cha)(eva) as well as
(bhaagee) eligible to suffer from (duḥkha) sorrows, (satatam) persistent (vyaadhitaḥ)
illnesses (cha) and (alpa) a lower (aayuḥ) life span. 4:157

(naraḥ) The person (yaḥ) who (heenaḥ) is devoid (sarva) of all (lakṣhaṇa) of the good 
characteristics related to education (api) but (sadaachaaravaan) is the observer of 
righteous conduct, (shraddadhaanaḥ) is faithful (cha) and (anasooyaḥ) is away from 
jealousy, malice etc., he/she (jeevati) lives (varṣhaaṇi) for one hundred (shatam)
years. 4:158
Controlling oneself instead of trying to control others
(yat)(yat) Whatever (karma) actions (vasham) are in the control (para) of others, one 
should (yatnena) carefully (varjayet) leave (tat)(tat) them aside (tu) and (yat)(yat)
whatever actions (syaat) are (aatma) in one’s (vasham) control, he/she should 
(yatnataḥ) diligently (seveta) focus on the completion of (tat)(tat) those tasks. 4:159
(sarvam) Everything that (vasham) is controlled (para) by someone else is the cause of 
(duḥkham) sorrows and (sarvam) everything that is under (aatma) one’s own (vasham)
 
duḥkhabhaagee cha satatam vyaadhito’lpaayureva cha.
duraachaaraḥ hi puruṣhaḥ loke bhavati ninditaḥ,
duḥkha-bhaagee cha satatam vyaadhitaḥ alpa-aayuḥ eva cha.

(braahmaṇaan) the braahmaṇa, (gaaḥ) the cows (cha) and (sarvaan) all of (tapasvinaḥ)
the hermits (eva) as well. 4:162

One (varjayet) should leave aside (naastikyam) the non-belief in God, (nindaam) the 
criticism (veda) of the Vedas, (kutsanam) the hatred (devataanaam) towards the

(cha) and (taikṣhṇyam) harshness. 4:163
Disciplining a child or a disciple
(putraat) A child (vaa) or (shiṣhyaat) a disciple, (tau) both of them (taaḍayet) can be 
beaten (tu) only (artham) for the purpose of (shiṣhṭi) teaching them and should (na)(eva)
never (nipaatayet) be punished (kruddhaḥ) out of anger, (anyatra) apart from them, 
(daṇḍam) a stick should (na) not (udyachchhet) be raised (parasya) against anyone
else. 4:164

मनुस्मृित अध्याय ४ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 4
185
The 165th – 169th shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
Outcome of unrighteous conduct
(hi) Because, (naraḥ) the person (yaḥ) who (adhaarmikaḥ) engages in unrighteous 
conduct, the one (yasya) whose (dhanam) wealth has been earned by means of 
(anṛitam) deceit and lie, (cha)(api) as well as the one (yaḥ) who (rataḥ) is engrossed in 
(hinsaa) violence, (asau) these (na) do not (nityam) ever (edhate) attain (sukham)
happiness (iha) in this World. 4:170
(pashyan) Considering the fact that (adhaarmikaaṇaam) the unrighteous and 
(paapaanaam) the sinners (aashu) soon experience their (viparyayam) downfall, one 
should (na) not (niveshayet) invest his/her (manaḥ) thoughts (adharme) in 
unrighteousness (api) even when (dharmeṇa) following righteousness (seedan) is 
uncomfortable and holds one back. 4:171
(iva) As feeding (gauḥ)* a cow does not produce milk instantaneously, (adharmaḥ) the 
evil deeds (charitaḥ) done (loke) in the World (na) do not (phalati) come to fruition 
 
anyatra putraat shiṣhyaat vaa shiṣhṭi-artham taaḍayet tu tau.

adhaarmikaḥ naraḥ yaḥ hi yasya cha api anṛitam dhanam,
hinsaa-rataḥ cha yaḥ nityam na iha asau sukham edhate.

(sadyaḥ) immediately, (tu) but, they (shanaiḥ) slowly (aavartamaanaḥ) corner (kartuḥ)
the perpetrator from all directions and (kṛintati) snip his/her (moolaani) roots i.e. 
destroy him/her completely. *The word gauḥ is also used for earth and in this context 
it implies that a seed sown in the earth does not bear fruits immediately. 4:172
(yadi) If the result of ill gotten wealth (na) does not show up in one’s (aatmani) own 
lifetime, then it shall show up during the lives (putreṣhu) of the sons inheriting that 
wealth and (chet) if it (na) does not show up during the lives (putreṣhu) of the sons, (tu)
then it shall show up during the lives (naptṛiṣhu) of the grandchildren, (tu) but 
(adharmaḥ) the misdeeds (kṛitaḥ) done (kartuḥ) by one (na) never (bhavati) remain 
(niṣhphalaḥ) without fruition (eva) indeed. 4:173
(taavat) Initially one (edhate) prospers (adharmeṇa) with the help of deceit and lies, 
(tataḥ) then (pashyati) experiences (bhadraaṇi) happiness and wellness through it and 
also (jayati) wins over his/her (sapatnaan) enemies, (tu) but eventually he/she 
(vinashyati) gets destroyed completely (samoolaḥ) along with one’s roots. 4:174

मनुस्मृित अध्याय ४ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 4
187
Conducts and etiquettes of the nobles
(aarya) The nobles (vṛitteṣhu) in their tendencies should be focused on (satya) the truth 
and (dharma) the righteousness (cha) and (sadaa) should always (aaramet) find 
happiness (shauche) in cleanliness (eva) as well. (cha) And keeping their (vaak) speech, 
(baahoo) arms and (udara)stomach (sañyataḥ) in control i.e. practicing pleasant speech, 
non-violence and absence of greed, they (shiṣhyaat) should teach (shiṣhyaan) the 
disciples (dharmeṇa) righteously. 4:175
(yau) Whatever (kaamau) desires and (artha) means of wealth (syaataam) are (varjitau)
forbidden (dharma) as per the code of righteous conduct, one should (pari) completely 
(tyajet) shy away from them, (cha)(api) as well as, from those (dharmam) righteous acts 
that (udarkam) may cause (asukha) sorrows in future (cha) or (vikruṣhṭam) disrepute 
(loka) in the society (eva) as well e.g. excessive donations without saving enough for the 
sustenance of one’s own family. 4:176

176. parityajedarthakaamau yau syaataan dharmavarjitau,
dharmañ chaapyasukhodarkan lokavikruṣhṭameva cha.
मनुस्मृित अध्याय ४ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 4
188
One should (na) neither unnecessarily (chapalaḥ) move around (paaṇi) the hands and 
(paada) the feet, (na) nor (chapalaḥ) roll (netra) eyes (cha) and, (na) nor (vaak) speak 
(chapalaḥ) without purpose, as these are considered the sign of immaturity and 
ignorance. One should neither (syaat) be (anṛijuḥ) deceitful (na) nor (eva) ever engage 
one’s (dheeḥ) mind (karma) in actions that could (droha) harm (para) others. 4:177
(maargam) The footsteps (sataam) of the benevolent sages, (yena) which were 
(yaataaḥ) followed by (asya) one’s (pitaraḥ) parents and (pitaamahaaḥ) grandparents, 
one (yaayaat) should follow (tena) them as well, because (gachchhan) by following 
(tena) those pathways one can (na) never be (riṣhyate) unhappy or retrogress. 4:178
(ṛitvik) A facilitator of the yajña, (purohita) a priest, (aachaaryaiḥ) a teacher, (maatula)
a maternal uncle, (atithi) a guest, (sañshriteḥ) a dependent, (baala) a child, (vṛiddha) an 
elder, (aaturaiḥ) a sick person, (vaidyaiḥ) a healer, (jñaati) a member of one’s clan, 
(sambandhi) a relative, (baandhavaiḥ) a friend,  4:179
 
parityajet artha-kaamau yau syaataam dharma-varjitau,
dharmam cha api asukha-udarkam loka-vikruṣhṭam eva cha.

(maataa) the mother, (pitṛibhyaam) the father, (yaameebhiḥ) a sister, (bhraatraa) a

Rules for accepting donations
(api) Even when (braahmam) a braahmaṇa (samarthaḥ) is eligible (prati)(graha) for 
receiving donations, he/she should (varjayet) refrain from having any (prasaṅgam)
attachment (tatra) to it or from bringing this topic again and again, (hi) because 
(prati)(graheṇa) by accepting donations out of greed, (tejaḥ) the self respect and the 
brilliance (asya) of that person (prashaamyati) diminishes (aashu) rapidly. 4:186

(avijñaaya) Without considering (vidhim) the procedures and the rules (prati)(grahe) for 
accepting various types of (dravyaaṇaam) objects and wealths, (dharmyam) as laid out 
in the code of righteous conduct, (praajñaḥ) a wise braahmaṇa should (na) not (kuryaat)
engage (prati)(graham) in acceptance of donations, (api) even if he/she (avaseedan) is 
suffering (kṣhudhaa) from extreme hunger. 4:187
The 188th – 189th shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
Rules for donating
(dvijaḥ) A twice-born, who (atapaaḥ) does not follow the rigors of righteousness and 
self-discipline (tu) and (anadheeyaanaḥ) does not follow the routines of yajña and the 
the study of the Vedas, but (ruchiḥ) is interested in (prati)(graha) receiving donations, 
he/she (eva) indeed (majjati) drowns in sins (saha) with (tena) that tendency, (iva) like 
(ashmaplavena) a boat made out of rock drowns (ambhasi) in water. 4:190
The 191st shloka is not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
(dharmavit) A person who has this the knowledge of the code of conduct should (na)
not (api) even (pra)(yachchhet) give (vaari) water (dvije) to a twice-born who is 
 
prati-graheṇa hi asya aashu braahmam tejaḥ prashaamyati.

(vaiḍaala)(vratike) conniving or (baka)(vratike) deceitful, (tu) or (vipre) to a braahmaṇa 
(avedavidi) who doesn’t study the Vedas any longer. 4:192
(api) Even if (dhanam) the wealth (arjitam) is earned (vidhinaa) righteously, when it 
(dattam) is donated to any of (eteṣhu) these (triṣhu) three, it (hi) indeed (bhavati)
becomes the reason (anarthaaya) for misfortunes and unhappiness for both (daatuḥ)
the donor (cha) and (aadaatuḥ) the donee in this life (eva)(api) as well as (paratra) in 
the next lives. 4:193
(yathaa) As a person (taran) trying to cross (udake) a water body, (plavena) with the 
help of a boat (upalena) made of stone, (nimajjati) goes under water for sure, (tathaa)
similarly those who (ichchhakau) are desirous of (daatṛi) donating and (prati) receiving 
donations but (ajñau) are ignorant of the related rules, (nimajjataḥ)sink (adhastaat) low 
in the ocean of sorrows. 4:194

Conniving and Deceitful
Someone who is unrighteous but wants to be seen (dhvajee) hoisting the flag (dharma)
of righteousness, who is (sadaa) always (lubdhaḥ) engrossed with greed, who is 
(chhaadmikaḥ) a pretender, who (dambhakaḥ) toots his/her horn (loka) in front of 
everyone, who (hinsraḥ) harms others, who tries to (abhi)(sandhakaḥ) befriend (sarva)
everyone regardless of their character, (jñeyaḥ) should be considered as the one with 
(vaiḍaala) conniving (vratikaḥ) tendencies. 4:195
(dvijaḥ) A twice-born who pretends to be (adho)(dṛiṣhṭiḥ) humble, is (naiṣhkṛitikaḥ)
vindictive, is (tatparaḥ) eager to (saadhana) achieve (svaartha) personal gains, is 
(shaṭhaḥ) a manipulator (cha) and is (mithyaa)(vineetaḥ) a sycophant, (charaḥ) conducts 
himself/herself with (baka) deceitful (vrata) tendencies. 4:196
 
यथा । प्लवेन। उपलेन । िनमज्जित ।उदके। तरन्॥ तथा । िनमज्जतः । अधस्तात्। अ ौ । दातप्रतीच्छकौ

The 197th – 200th shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
Recommendations for bathing
One should (na)(kadaachana) never (snaayaat) take a bath (parakeeya) in someone 
else’s (nipaaneṣhu) bathtub, (tu) because (snaatvaa) having bathed there, (duṣhkṛita)
the infections (kartuḥ) from the maker (nipaana) of the bathtub may (añshena) partly 
(lipyate) affect the bather as well. 4:201
The 202nd shloka is not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
One (samaacharet) should (nityam) always (snaanam) bathe (nadeeṣhu) in the rivers, 
(devakhaateṣhu) in the natural lakes, (taḍaageṣhu) in the ponds, (sarassu) in the water 
falls (cha) and (gartta) in the ground holes (prasravaṇeṣhu) with flowing water. 4:203
Follow the yamas and niyamas i.e. the rules
(budhaḥ) The wise should (na) not (kevalaan) only practice (niyamaan) the rules of 
societal conduct, but should (nityam) always (satatam) diligently (seveta) follow 
(yamaan) the rules of self-discipline as well, because (bhajan) by practicing only 
(niyamaan) the rules of conduct towards others (akurvaaṇaḥ) while not practicing 
(yamaan) self-discipline, (patati) causes one’s downfall. 4:204

The 205th – 225th shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu. 
Giving back to the society
One should (nityam) always perform (iṣhṭam) yajña (shraddhayaa) with devotion (cha)
and (atandritaḥ) diligently (kuryaat) create (poortam) facilities for the benefit of the 
society e.g. digging of wells, ponds etc., (hi) because the gains from (te) these deeds, 
when (kṛite) completed (shraddhaa) with devotion (cha) and (dhanaiḥ) by utilizing the 
money (su)(aagataiḥ) earned righteously, (bhavataḥ) are (akṣhaye) undiminished. 4:226
(aasaadya) After having identified (paatram) a deserving recipient, (shaktitaḥ) as much 
as permitted by one’s means, and (parituṣhṭena) for the contentment of the soul, one 
should (nityam) always (niṣheveta) fulfill (dharmam) the duty (daana) of giving 
(bhaavena) with devotion (aiṣhṭika) for the performance of yajña and (paurtikam) for 
the creation of facilities for the benefit of the society. 4:227

The 228th – 232nd shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
Items fit for donation
The donations of (vaari) the water, (anna) the food, (go) a cow, (mahee) the land, 
(vaasaḥ) the clothes, (tila) the sesame seeds, (kaañchana) the gold and (sarpiṣhaam) the 
clarified butter etc., (eva) amongst (sarveṣhaam) all of these (daanaanaam) donations, 
(daanam) the giving (brahma) of the knowledge of the Vedas (vishiṣhyate) is considered 
the best. 4:233
The 234th – 237th shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
Build up the virtues
(artham) For (sahaaya) attaining happiness (paraloka) in the next lives, (apeeḍayan)
without harming (sarva) any other (bhootaani) being, one should (shanaiḥ) slowly 
(sañchinuyaat) build up one’s (dharmam) virtues (iva) as (valmeekam) the white-ants 
(puttikaaḥ) build an anthill. 4:238
 
227. daanadharman niṣheveta nityamaiṣhṭikapaurtikam,
parituṣhṭena bhaavena paatramaasaadya shaktitaḥ. daana-dharmam niṣheveta nityam aiṣhṭika-paurtikam,
parituṣhṭena bhaavena paatram aasaadya shaktitaḥ.

vaari-anna-go-mahee-vaasaḥ-tila-kaañchana-sarpiṣhaam.

(hi) Because (artham) for (sahaaya) helping (amutra) in the next lives, (na) neither 
(maataa) the mother (cha) and (pitaa) the father from this life (tiṣhṭhataḥ) will stand by 
one’s side, (na) nor (putra) the son, nor (daaraa) the wife, and (na) nor (jñaatiḥ) the 
relatives, (kevalaḥ) only (dharmaḥ) the righteous and virtues (tiṣhṭhati) shall be 
there. 4:239
Every (jantuḥ) being (prajaayate) is born (ekaḥ) alone and (praleeyate) dies (ekaḥ) alone 
(eva) as well, (anubhuṅkte) enjoys the happiness and comforts resulting from its 
(sukṛitam) good deeds (ekaḥ) alone (cha)(eva) as well as suffers the consequences of 
(duṣhkṛitam) sins (ekaḥ) alone. 4:240
Upon one’s death, his/her (baandhavaaḥ) relatives (utsṛijya) keep (mṛitam) the dead 
(shareeram) body (samam) as (loṣhṭha) dirt and (kaaṣhṭha) wood (kṣhitau) on the earth 
to burn and (yaanti) leave, (vimukhaaḥ) turning their faces away, only (dharmaḥ) the 
virtues (gachchhati) go (anu) along (tam) with him/her. 4:241
 
paraloka-sahaaya-artham sarva-bhootaani apeeḍayan.

(tasmaat) Hence (artham) for (sahaaya) the help in the next lives, one should (nityam)
always (shanaiḥ) slowly (sañchinuyaat) build up one’s (dharmam) virtues (hi) because 
(sahaayena) with the help (dharmeṇa) of righteousness, one can (tarati) overcome 
(dustaram) grave (tamaḥ) sorrows and darkness. 4:242
Importance of righteousness
One who gives (dharma) righteousness (pradhaanam) the utmost importance, (hata)
destroys his/her (kilviṣham)sins (tapasaa) by following a resolute lifestyle and becomes 
(bhaasvantam) illuminated (khashareeriṇam) with the likeness of God. Upon death,
his/her (puruṣham) soul gets (aashu) expeditiously (nayati) taken (lokam) to the realm 
(para) of ultimate happiness. 4:243

Association with the benevolent
One who is (nineeṣhuḥ) desirous of (utkarṣham) upliftment of his/her (kulam) entire 
family, he/she should (nityam) always (aacharet) practice (sambandhaan) having 
association (saha) with (uttamaiḥ)(uttamaiḥ) the best and benevolent and (tyajet)
should stay away (adhamaan)(adhamaan) from the unrighteous and sinful. 4:244
(gachchhan) By going to meet (uttamaan)(uttamaan) the best and benevolent (cha) and 
(varjayan) leaving aside (heenaan)(heenaan) the unrighteous and sinful, (braahmaṇaḥ)
a twice-born (eti) gets (shreṣhṭhataam) to excellence and (pratyavaayena) by doing the 
contrary gets (shoodrataam) to inferiority. 4:245
(tathaa) Following this (vrataḥ) resolve of proper association, (dṛiḍhakaaree) a firm, 
(mṛiduḥ) humble, (daantaḥ) self controlled and (ahinsraḥ) non-violent twice-born, 
(asamvasan) by not associating (kroora)(aachaaraiḥ) with the cruel and by engaging 
(dama) in restraint over mind and (daanaabhyaam) in donation, (jayet) wins the right of 
entering (svargam) the realm of mokṣha. 4:246

The 247th – 254th shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu. 
Proper use of the speech
The one (yaḥ) who (santam) has (anyathaa) different thoughts (aatmaanam) inside but
(bhaaṣhate) speaks (anyathaa) on the contrary (satsu) amongst the benevolent, (saḥ)
he/she is (paapa)(kṛittamaḥ) a sinner (loke) in this world and is (stena) a thief 
(apahaarakaḥ) harming his/her (aatma) own self. 4:255
(sarve) All (arthaaḥ) of the conducts (niyataaḥ) are tied (vaachi) to the speech. 
Everything (moolaaḥ) is rooted (vaaṅ) in speech and (viniḥ)(sṛitaaḥ) is conducted (vaak)
through the speech. (naraḥ) The human (yaḥ) who (stenayet) misuses (taam) this
(vaacham) speech i.e. lies, (saḥ) he/she is susceptible to (sarva) all (steya)(kṛit) of the 
acts of thievery. 4:256

256. vaachyarthaa niyataaḥ sarve vaaṅmoolaa vaagviniḥ sṛitaaḥ, 
मनुस्मृित अध्याय ४ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 4
200
Staying detached
(gatvaa) Having become (aanṛiṇyam) free from the debts of (maharṣhi) the sages, (pitṛi)
the elders and (devaanaam) the divinites, (samaasajya) having entrusted (sarvam)
everything to one’s (putre) child (yathaa) as per (vidhi) the procedures, one (vaset)
should live (aashritaḥ) following (maadhya)(stham) the middle path i.e. the path of 
detachment. 4:257
Gains from meditation
(nityam) Everyday, one should sit (vivikte) in a secluded place and (ekaakee) by oneself 
(chintayet) think about one's (aatmanaḥ) own (hitam) welfare, (hi) because the one who 
(chintayaanaḥ) ponders (ekaakee) by oneself (adhi)(gachchhati) attains (param)
ultimate (shreyaḥ) happiness. 4:258
 
taan tu yaḥ stenayedvaachan sa sarvasteyakṛinnaraḥ. vaachi arthaaḥ niyataaḥ sarve vaaṅ-moolaaḥ vaak-viniḥ sṛitaaḥ,
taam tu yaḥ stenayet vaacham saḥ sarva-steya-kṛit naraḥ.

ु । सवर्म्। समासज्य । वसेत्। माध्यस्थम्। आिश्रतः ॥
257. maharṣhipitṛidevaanaaṅ gatvaa’’nṛiṇyañ yathaavidhi,
putre sarvan samaasajya vasenmaadhyasthamaashritaḥ. maharṣhi-pitṛi-devaanaam gatvaa aanṛiṇyam yathaa-vidhi,
putre sarvam samaasajya vaset maadhyastham aashritaḥ.
4:258 एकाक  िचन्तयेिन्नत्यंिविव ेिहतमात्मनः ।
एकाक  िचन्तयानो िह परंश्रेयोऽिधगच्छित ॥२५८॥
एकाक  । िचन्तयेत्। िनत्यम्। िविव े। िहतम्। आत्मनः॥एकाक  । िचन्तयानः । िह।परम्। श्रेयः । अिधगच्छित॥
258. ekaakee chintayennityam vivikte hitamaatmanaḥ,
ekaakee chintayaano hi parañ shreyo’dhigachchhati.
ekaakee chintayet nityam vivikte hitam aatmanaḥ,
ekaakee chintayaanaḥ hi param shreyaḥ adhigachchhati.
मनुस्मृित अध्याय ४ । Manusmṛiti Chapter 4
201
Conclusion of the householders’ duties
(eṣhaa) This (shaashvatee) universal (vṛittiḥ) duty (gṛihasthasya) of a householder 
(viprasya) twice-born (uditaa) has been revealed (cha) and (shubhaḥ) the auspicious 
(vrata)(kalpaḥ) resolutions that (vṛiddhi)(karaḥ) increase (sattva) the good tendencies 
(snaataka) of the graduates have been said as well. 4:259
(nityam) Always (vartayan) following (anena) this (vṛittena) code of conduct, (vipraḥ) the 
twice-born who (vit) is accomplished in the knowledge (veda) of the Vedas and 
(shaastra) the scriptures, (vyapeta) becoming free (kalmaṣhaḥ) from sins, (maheeyate)
attains greatness (loke) in the company of (brahma) God. 4:260

Chapter 5
The 1st – 4th shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
Unfit for consumption
(lashunam) Garlic, (gṛiñjanam) turnip, (palaaṇḍum) onion, (kavakaani) mushroom 
(cha)(eva) as well as other things that (prabhavaaṇi) grow (amedhya) in impure locations 
(abhakṣhyaaṇi) are not for the consumption (dvijaateenaam) by the twice-borns. 5:5
The 6th – 7th shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
(kṣheeram) The milk (goḥ) of a cow (anirdashaayaaḥ) for the first ten days after giving 
birth to a calf, (auṣhṭram) the camel’s milk, (aikashapham) the milk from any single toed 
animal like a horse, (aavikam) the sheep’s milk, (kṣheeram) the milk from a cow that is 
(sandhinee) ready to conceive again (tathaa) and (payaḥ) the milk (goḥ) from a cow 
(vivatsaayaaḥ) whose calf has died,  5:8

Fit for consumption
However, (shukteṣhu) out of the sour things, (dadhi) the yogurt (cha) and (sarvam) all 
things (sambhavam) made out of (dadhi) yogurt (cha)(eva) as well as (yaani) whatever

(moola) vegetables (cha) and (phalaiḥ) fruits, (bhakṣhyam) are edible. 5:10

(sarvam) All of the foods prepared from (yava) barley and (godhoomajam) wheat

The 26th – 44th shlokas are not considered to be written by Maharṣhi Manu.
Killing non-violent animals and eating meat is forbidden
One (yaḥ) who (hinasti) kills (ahinsakaani) non-violent (bhootaani) beings (ichchhayaa)
for fulfilling the desire of one’s (aatma) own (sukha) pleasure, (saḥ) he/she does (na)
not (edhate) get (kvachit) any (sukham) happiness (jeevan) in this life (cha)(eva) as well 
as (mṛitaḥ) upon his/her death. 5:45

One (yaḥ) who does (na) not (chikeerṣhati) desire (bandhana) to trap, (vadha) to kill or 
to cause (kleshaan) pain (praaṇinaam) to other beings, (saḥ) he/she is (hita)(prepsuḥ) a 
wellwisher (sarvasya) of everyone and (ashnute) gets (atyantam) a lot (sukham) of 
happiness. 5:46
One (yaḥ) who (na) does not (kiñchana) ever (hinasti) kill any being, (yat) whatever 
he/she (dhyaayati) thinks of, (kurute) does (cha) and (yatra) wherever he/she sets 
(badhnaati) his/her (dhṛitim) determination, he/she (avaapnoti) gets (tat) that 
(ayatnena) easily and effortlessly. 5:47
(maansam) Meat (na) can not (kvachit) ever (utpadyate) be produced (akṛitvaa) without 
causing (hinsaam) harm (praaṇinaam) to the beings (cha) and (vadhaḥ) killing (praaṇi)
 
sa jeevañshcha mṛitashchaiva na kvachitsukhamedhate.

saḥ jeevan cha mṛitaḥ cha eva na kvachit sukham edhate.

(anumantaa) The grantor of the permission, (nihantaa) the slayer of the animals,

Part - II
The Extensions 
in Manusmṛiti
(the shlokas that were added later on by others)
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय १ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 1
210
Extensions in Chapter 1
The shlokas 7th – 13th in the current version of Manusmṛiti talk about creation of a physical 
being called brahma who then created this Universe. Since the 6th shloka clearly states 
that the God does not assume physical forms, these seven shlokas do not conform to the 
basic philosophy Maharṣhi Manu is preaching and were most likely inserted by someone 
else later.
Creation of an entity called Brahma
योऽसावतीिन्द्रयग्रा ः स
ू
 मोऽव्य ः सनातनः ।
सवर्भ
ू
तमयोऽिचन्त्यः स एव स्वयम
ुद्बभौ ॥७॥
यः । असौ । अतीिन्द्रयग्रा ः । स मः
ू । अव्य ः । सनातनः ॥
सवर्भतमयः
ू । अिचन्त्यः । सः । एव । स्वयम्। उद्बभौ ॥
7. yo’saavateendriyagraahyaḥ sookṣhmo’vyaktaḥ sanaatanaḥ,
sarvabhootamayo’chintyaḥ sa eva svayamudbabhau.
yaḥ asau ateendriyagraahyaḥ sookṣhmaḥ avyaktaḥ sanaatanaḥ,
sarvabhootamayaḥ achintyaḥ saḥ eva svayam udbabhau.
(yaḥ) Who (asau) that is (sanaatanaḥ) eternal, (sookṣhmaḥ)subtle, (sarvabhootamayaḥ)
present in all creation, (avyaktaḥ) without physical characteristics, 
(ateendriyagraahyaḥ) beyond perception of the senses and (achintyaḥ) unfathomable 
by thoughts, (saḥ) he (udbabhau) manifested (svayam)(eva) himself. 1:7

8. so’bhidhyaaya shareeraatsvaatsisṛikṣhurvividhaaḥ prajaaḥ,
apa eva sasarjaadau taasu beejamavaasṛijat.
saḥ abhidhyaaya shareeraat svaat sisṛikṣhuḥ vividhaaḥ prajaaḥ,
apaḥ eva sasarja aadau taasu beejam avaasṛijat.
(saḥ) He, (sisṛikṣhuḥ) with a desire to make (vividhaaḥ) various (prajaaḥ) things and 
beings (svaat) from his own (shareeraat) body, (abhidhyaaya) carefully thought and 
(aadau) first (sasarja) created (apaḥ) dough (eva) like substances and (taasu) in those 
(avaasṛijat) induced activity which acted as (beejam) the seed of the creation. 1:8

9. tadaṇḍamabhavaddhaiman sahasraañshusamaprabham,
tasmiñjajñe svayam brahmaa sarvalokapitaamahaḥ. tat aṇḍam abhavat haimam sahasra-añshu-samaprabham,
tasmin jajñe svayam brahmaa sarva-loka-pitaamahaḥ.
(tat) That substance (abhavat) turned into (haimam) a golden (aṇḍam) egg 
(samaprabham) that had the luminosity of (sahasra) innumerable (añshu) rays. Then, 
(tasmin) from it (jajñe) emerged (svayam) by himself (brahmaa) Brahma, (pitaamahaḥ)
the forefather of (sarva) the entire (loka) universe. 1:9
आपो नारा इित प्रो ा आपो वैनरस

10. aapo naaraa iti proktaa aapo vai narasoonavaḥ,
taa yadasyaayanam poorvan tena naaraayaṇaḥ smṛitaḥ. aapaḥ naaraaḥ iti proktaaḥ aapaḥ vai nara-soonavaḥ,
taaḥ yat asya ayanam poorvam tena naaraayaṇaḥ smṛitaḥ.
(aapaḥ) All material things including water, mortal bodies etc. (iti) are also (proktaaḥ)
called (naaraaḥ) “Naaraa”. (aapaḥ) All of these material things are (vai) definitely (nara)
God’s (soonavaḥ) creations. Since God is omnipresent, (taaḥ) they are all (asya) God’s 
(ayanam) abode and God is their abode (yat) as well (poorvam)since the creation. (tena)
Due to this reason God is also (smṛitaḥ) called (naaraayaṇaḥ) “Naaraayaṇa” (Naaraa +
ayana) i.e. who abode is everywhere. 1:10

11. yattatkaaraṇamavyaktan nityan sadasadaatmakam,
tadvisṛiṣhṭaḥ sa puruṣho loke brahmeti keertyate.
yat tat kaaraṇam avyaktam nityam sat-asat-aatmakam,
tat visṛiṣhṭaḥ saḥ puruṣhaḥ loke brahmaa iti keertyate.
(tat) The (avyaktam) subtle and (nityam) eternal matter (yat) which is (kaaraṇam) the 
material cause of this universe, changed from its (asat) unrealized (aatmakam) state 
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय १ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 1
212
and manifested itself in (sat) a perceivable form. From (tat) it (puruṣhaḥ) a being 
(visṛiṣhṭaḥ) is created, (saḥ) who (iti) is (keertyate) known as (brahmaa) Brahmaa (loke)
in this World. 1:11

12. tasminnaṇḍe sa bhagavaanuṣhitvaa parivatsaram,
svayamevaatmano dhyaanaattadaṇḍamakaroddvidhaa. tasmin aṇḍe saḥ bhagavaan uṣhitvaa parivatsaram,
svayam eva aatmanaḥ dhyaanaat tat aṇḍam akarot dvidhaa.
(uṣhitvaa) After residing (tasmin) inside that (aṇḍe) egg (parivatsaram) for one year (saḥ)
he, (bhagavaan) the lord, (eva) by (svayam)(aatmanaḥ) his own (dhyaanaat) meditative 
powers, (akarot) broke (tat) that (aṇḍam) egg (dvidhaa) into two parts. 1:12

13. taabhyaan sa shakalaabhyaañ cha divam bhoomiñ cha nirmame,
madhye vyoma dishashchaaṣhṭaavapaan sthaanañ cha shaashvatam. taabhyaam saḥ shakalaabhyaam cha divam bhoomim cha nirmame,
madhye vyomaḥ dishaḥ cha aṣhṭau apaam sthaanam cha shaashvatam.
(cha) And then (saḥ) he took one of (taabhyaam) those (shakalaabhyaam) two parts and 
(nirmame) made (divam) all celestial bodies from it (cha) and from the other part he 
created (bhoomim) the earth. (madhye) In the middle of these he created (vyomaḥ)skies 
(cha) and (aṣhṭau) the eight (dishaḥ) directions. (cha) And on the earth he created the 
water bodies (sthaanam) to hold (apaam) the water (shaashvatam) as usual. 1:13
Importance of the knowledge of the basic elements
The 17th shloka digresses from the current topic of the creation.

यत्। मत्यर्वयवाः

तस्मात्। शरीरम्। इित । आह ः । तस्य । मितर्म ू ्। मनीिषणः ॥
17. yanmoortyavayavaaḥ sookṣhmaastasyemaanyaashrayanti ṣhaṭ,
tasmaachchhareeramityaahustasya moortim maneeṣhiṇaḥ. yat moortyavayavaaḥ sookṣhmaaḥ tasya imaani aashrayanti ṣhaṭ,
tasmaat shareeram iti aahuḥ tasya moortim maneeṣhiṇaḥ.
(yat) Because (imaani) these (ṣhaṭ) six (sookṣhmaaḥ) subtle elements, 
(moortyavayavaaḥ) the material cause of the Universe, (aashrayanti) are dependent 
(tasya) on God for their creation, (tasmaat) therefore, the learned, (maneeṣhiṇaḥ) who 
are in control of their mind, (aahuḥ) consider (iti) this (moortim) Universe as (tasya) his 
(shareeram) body. 1:17
Creation of the tangible things and perceptions
The 24th and 25th shlokas again talk about creation of tangibles while Maharṣhi Manu 
has already moved on to the topic of the revelation of the Vedas.
कालंकालिवभ ीं  न त्रािण ग्रहां
स्तथा ।
स रतः सागराञ्छैलान्समािन िवषमािण च ॥२४॥
कालम्। कालिवभ  न्। च । न त्रािण । ग्रहान्। तथा ॥ स रतः । सागरान्। शैलान्। समािन। िवषमािण । च ॥
24. kaalaṅ kaalavibhakteeñshcha nakṣhatraaṇi grahaanstathaa,
saritaḥ saagaraañchhailaansamaani viṣhamaaṇi cha.
kaalam kaalavibhakteen cha nakṣhatraaṇi grahaan tathaa,
saritaḥ saagaraan shailaan samaani viṣhamaaṇi cha.
(kaalam) The time (cha) and (kaalavibhakteen) the various divisions of time, 
(nakṣhatraaṇi) the stars, (grahaan) the planets, (tathaa) likewise (saritaḥ) the rivers, 
(saagaraan) the oceans, (shailaan) the mountains, (samaani) the plains (cha) and 
(viṣhamaaṇi) the uneven lands, 1:24
तपो वाचंरितंचैव कामंच क्रोधमेव च ।

ृ ंससजर्चैवेमांस्र  िमच्छिन्नमाः प्रजाः ॥२५॥
तपः । वाचम्। रितम्। च । एव । कामम्। च । क्रोधम्।एव । च ॥
सि म ृ ्। ससजर्। च । एव । इमाम्। स्र  म्। इच्छन्। इमाः । प्रजाः ॥
25. tapo vaachaṇ ratiñ chaiva kaamañ cha krodhameva cha,
sṛiṣhṭin sasarja chaivemaan sraṣhṭumichchhannimaaḥ prajaaḥ. tapaḥ vaacham ratim cha eva kaamam cha krodham eva cha,
sṛiṣhṭim sasarja cha eva imaam sraṣhṭum ichchhan imaaḥ prajaaḥ.
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय १ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 1
214
(tapaḥ) the fortitude, (vaacham) the speech (cha) and (ratim) the happiness, (eva) as 
well as (kaamam) the desire (cha) and (krodham) the anger (eva) as well as (imaam) the 
rest of (sṛiṣhṭim) the creation, God (sasarja) created everything with his (ichchhan)
desire of (sraṣhṭum) creation. Hence all of (imaaḥ) these are God’s(prajaaḥ) children.1:25
32nd through 41st shlokas describe creation of male and female, and then creation of 
Maharṣhi Manu’s lineage who in turn created everything in this universe. These shlokas
try to take the credit of creation away from God and assign it to some humans.

32. dvidhaa kṛitvaa’’tmano dehamardhena puruṣho’bhavat,
ardhena naaree tasyaan sa viraajamasṛijatprabhuḥ. dvidhaa kṛitvaa aatmanaḥ deham ardhena puruṣhaḥ abhavat,
ardhena naaree tasyaam saḥ viraajam asṛijat prabhuḥ.
(prabhuḥ) God (kṛitvaa) did (dvidhaa) two parts of (aatmanaḥ) his own (deham) body, 
(ardhena) one half (abhavat) became (puruṣhaḥ) a man and (ardhena) the other half 
(naaree) a woman. And then (tasyaam) in that woman (saḥ) he (asṛijat) conceived a 
person named (viraajam) Viraaṭ. 1:32

33. tapastaptvaa’sṛijadyan tu sa svayam puruṣho viraaṭ,
tam maam vittaasya sarvasya sraṣhṭaaran dvijasattamaaḥ. tapaḥ taptvaa asṛijat yam tu saḥ svayam puruṣhaḥ viraaṭ,
tam maam vitta asya sarvasya sraṣhṭaaram dvijasattamaaḥ.
(dvijasattamaaḥ) O Scholars! (saḥ) He, (puruṣhaḥ) the person named (viraaṭ) Viraaṭ
(svayam) himself (taptvaa) having (tapaḥ) planned and worked, (asṛijat) produced (tam)
one, (yam) who is none other than (maam) myself, Maharṣhi Manu. (vitta) Know myself

as the one who now (sraṣhṭaaram) provides all of the organization and direction 
(sarvasya) to everything (asya) in this World. 1:33

34. aham prajaa sisṛikṣhustu tapastaptvaa sudushcharam,

(tu) Then (aham) I (sisṛikṣhuḥ) with a desire to create (prajaaḥ) a population, (taptvaa)
worked (tapaḥ) hard (sudushcharam) overcoming obstacles and (aaditaḥ) initially 
(asṛijam) created (dasha) ten (maharṣheen) sages as (pateen) the guides and directors 
(prajaanaam) of the masses. 1:34

Pulastya, (pulaham) Pulaha, (kratum) Kratu, (prachetasam) Prachetaa, (vasiṣhṭham)

other (sapta) seven (bhooritejasaḥ) brilliant son in the lineage that were (devaan)

37. yakṣharakṣhaḥ pishaachaañshcha gandharvaapsaraso’suraan,
naagaansarpaansuparṇaañshcha pitṛeeṇaañ cha pṛithaggaṇaan. yakṣha-rakṣhaḥ pishaachaan cha gandharva-apsarasaḥ asuraan,
naagaan sarpaan suparṇaan cha pitṛeeṇaam cha pṛithak gaṇaan.
Various beings and things in (pṛithak) different (gaṇaan) categories, including, (yakṣha)
the revered, (rakṣhaḥ) the demons (cha) and (pishaachaan) the uncouth, (gandharva)
the singers, (apsarasaḥ) the dancers and (asuraan) the unmusical, (naagaan) the cobras, 
(sarpaan) the snakes (cha) and (suparṇaan) the eagles (cha) and (pitṛeeṇaam) the 
knowledgeable, 1:37 

Disappearance of Brahmaa
The 50th and 51st shlokas describe a physical entity who disappeared after creation. This 
is against the Vedic philosophy and hence they are not written by Maharṣhi Manu.
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय १ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 1
218
एतदन्तास्तु

एतत्। अन्ताः । तु। गतयः । ब्र ा । आद्याः । समदा ताः ु ॥ घोरे। अिस्मन्। भतसू ं
सारे। िनत्यम्। सततयाियिन॥
50. etadantaastu gatayo brahmaadyaaḥ samudaahṛitaaḥ,
ghore’sminbhootasansaare nityan satatayaayini.
etat antaaḥ tu gatayaḥ brahmaa aadyaaḥ samudaahṛitaaḥ,
ghore asmin bhoota-sansaare nityam satatayaayini.
This World is (ghore) full of sorrows. So far, I have (samudaahṛitaaḥ) enumerated with 
examples, (gatayaḥ) various types of beings and things (tu) that have been (bhoota)
created (asmin) in this (sansaare) World, (aadyaaḥ) from (brahmaa) the blissful 
Brahmaa* to (etat) these miserable immobile plants (antaaḥ) with inner consciousness 
only. These categories are (nityam) universal and (satatayaayini) remain the same in all 
of the cycles of creation. *Brahmaa is the first person to learn the knowledge of all of 
the four Vedas from the four sages. 1:50

51. evan sarvan sa sṛiṣhṭvedam maañ chaachintyaparaakramaḥ, 
aatmanyantardadhe bhooyaḥ kaalaṅ kaalena peeḍayan.
evam sarvam saḥ sṛiṣhṭvaa idam maam cha achintya-paraakramaḥ,
aatmani antardadhe bhooyaḥ kaalam kaalena peeḍayan.
(evam) Like this, (sṛiṣhṭvaa) after creating (sarvam) everything (idam) here (cha)
including (maam) myself and showing (achintya) unfathomable (paraakramaḥ)
enterprise in (peeḍayan) ending (kaalena) the the phase of inactivity and (bhooyaḥ)
starting (kaalam) the phase of creation, (saḥ) he (antardadhe) merged back (aatmani)
into the God and disappeared. 1:51
Death and reincarning of beings
The 55th and 56th shlokas talk about death and rebirth of beings, which is out of context.

55. tamo’yan tu samaashritya chiran tiṣhṭhati sendriyaḥ,
na cha svaṅ kurute karma tadotkramati moortitaḥ. tamaḥ ayam tu samaashritya chiram tiṣhṭhati sendriyaḥ,
na cha svam kurute karma tadaa utkramati moortitaḥ.
(ayam) The living being (samaashritya) under the influence of (tamaḥ) extreme 
ignorance, lives only for the sake of indulging in pleasures (sendriyaḥ) appeasing the 
senses, (cha) and (tiṣhṭhati) remains idle (chiram) for a long time. He (kurute) performs 
(na) no (karma) actions for (svam) his upliftment and (tadaa) then finally (utkramati)
leaves (moortitaḥ) the body. 1:55

56. yadaa’ṇumaatriko bhootvaa beejan sthaasnu chariṣhṇuḥ cha,
samaavishati sansṛiṣhṭastadaa moortim vimuñchati.
yadaa aṇumaatrikaḥ bhootvaa beejam sthaasnu chariṣhṇuḥ cha,
sam-aavishati sam-sṛiṣhṭaḥ tadaa moortim vimuñchati.
(yadaa) When that being i.e. the soul (aṇumaatrikaḥ) with its subtle existence 
(sam)(sṛiṣhṭaḥ) unites with othersubtle elements and (bhootvaa) becomes like (beejam)
a seed (sam)(aavishati) inserted into either (sthaasnu) immobile vegetation (cha) or in 
(chariṣhṇuḥ) a mobile being, (tadaa) then it (vimuñchati) assumes a new (moortim)
body.
1:56
Creation and propagation of Manusmṛiti
The 58th through 63rd shlokas interrupt the flow and hence are out of context. They also 
try to take the credit of the creation of this treatise away from Maharṣhi Manu.

(sṛiṣhṭavantaḥ) created (svaaḥ)(svaaḥ) their own (prajaaḥ) groups of disciples. 1:61

63. svaayambhuvaadyaaḥ saptaite manavo bhooritejasaḥ,

(aadyaaḥ) Starting with (svaayambhuva) the self created Maharṣhi Manu to (ete) these

(utpaadya) created (antare) in (sve)(sve) their own era and area, (sarvam) all of (chara)

sustained them. 1:63
The month of ancestors 
The 66th shloka is out of context and illogically talks about actions performed by dead 
ancestors.
िप येरा यहनी मासः प्रिवभागस्त
ुप योः ।
कमर्चे ास्वहः क
ृ
ष्णः श
ु
क्लः स्वप्नाय शवर्री ॥६६॥
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय १ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 1
222
िप ये। रा यहनी । मासः । प्रिवभागः । तु।प योः ॥ कमर्चे ासु। अहः । कृष्णः । शक्लः
ु । स्वप्नाय । शवर्री ॥
66. pitrye raatryahanee maasaḥ pravibhaagastu pakṣhayoḥ,
karmacheṣhṭaasvahaḥ kṛiṣhṇaḥ shuklaḥ svapnaaya sharvaree. pitrye raatryahanee maasaḥ pravibhaagaḥ tu pakṣhayoḥ,
karma-cheṣhṭaasu ahaḥ kṛiṣhṇaḥ shuklaḥ svapnaaya sharvaree.
(pitrye) For the ancestors (raatryahanee) one day and night is equivalent to one human 
(maasaḥ) month (tu) which is (pravibhaagaḥ) divided into (pakṣhayoḥ) two fortnights. 
(kṛiṣhṇaḥ) The waning phase of the moon is like (ahaḥ) the day for them (cheṣhṭaasu)
for the performance of (karma) actions and (shuklaḥ) the waxing phase is like their 
(sharvaree) night (svapnaaya) for sleeping. 1:66
Loss of Values as the eras progress
The 81st through 86th shlokas are out of context and illogically assign the blame for 
deterioration of the values to eras instead of human actions. They also talk about relaxing 
the code of conduct as the eras progress, which is against the Vedic wisdom.
चत
ु
ष्पात्सकलो धमर्ः सत्यंचैव क
ृ
तेय
ु
गे।
नाधम णागमः कि न्मन
ु
ष्यान्प्रित वतर्ते॥८१॥
चतष्पात ु ्। सकलः । धमर्ः । सत्यम्। च । एव । कृते। यगे

81. chatuṣhpaatsakalo dharmaḥ satyañ chaiva kṛite yuge,
naadharmeṇaagamaḥ kashchinmanuṣhyaanprati vartate.
chatuṣhpaat sakalaḥ dharmaḥ satyam cha eva kṛite yuge,
na adharmeṇa aagamaḥ kashchit manuṣhyaan prati vartate.
(kṛite) In the Satya (yuge) Era, (sakalaḥ) everyone follows all of (chatuṣhpaat) the four 
limbs of dharma i.e fortitude, knowledge, effort and charity (eva) as well and engages 
in (satyam) the truth (cha) and (dharmaḥ) the righteous conduct. (manuṣhyaan)
Amongst the humans, (na) no one (prati)(vartate) engages (kashchit) in any kind of 
(adharmeṇa) unrighteous behavior for any kind of (aagamaḥ) gain. 1:81
इतरेष्वागमाद्धमर्ः पादशस्त्ववरोिपतः । चौ रकान
ृ
तमायािभधर्मर् ापैित पादशः ॥८२॥
इतरेषु। आगमात्। धमर्ः । पादशः । तु। अवरोिपतः ॥ चौ रकानतमायािभः ृ । धमर्ः । च । अपैित ।पादशः ॥
82. itareṣhvaagamaaddharmaḥ paadashastvavaropitaḥ,
chaurikaanṛitamaayaabhirdharmashchaapaiti paadashaḥ. itareṣhu aagamaat dharmaḥ paadashaḥ tu avaropitaḥ,
chaurika-anṛita-maayaabhiḥ dharmaḥ cha apaiti paadashaḥ.
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय १ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 1
223
(itareṣhu) In each of the other three eras, (aagamaat) due to the desire for gains, 
(paadashaḥ) one limb of (dharmaḥ) dharma (avaropitaḥ) gets reduced successively. And 
due to increase in the tendencies to engage in (chaurika) theft, (anṛita) lie (cha) and
(maayaabhiḥ) deceit etc. (paadashaḥ) a limb of (dharmaḥ) the righteous behavior 
(apaiti) is lost in each era. 1:82

83. arogaaḥ sarvasiddhaarthaashchaturvarṣhashataayuṣhaḥ,
kṛite tretaadiṣhu hyeṣhaamaayurhrasati paadashaḥ. arogaaḥ sarva-siddhaarthaaḥ chatur-varṣha-shata-aayuṣhaḥ,
kṛite tretaadiṣhu hi eṣhaam aayuḥ hrasati paadashaḥ.
(kṛite) In the Satya Era, humans were (arogaaḥ) without any illness and (sarva) all of 
their (siddhaarthaaḥ) desires were fulfilled. They had (aayuṣhaḥ) a life span of (chatur)
four (shata) hundred (varṣha) years. (tretaadiṣhu) In each of the three successive eras, 
(eṣhaam) their (aayuḥ) lifespan (hi) indeed got (hrasati)reduced (paadashaḥ) by a fourth 
i.e. one hundred years per era. 1:83

84. vedoktamaayurmartyaanaamaashiṣhashchaiva karmaṇaam,
phalantyanuyugan loke prabhaavashcha shareeriṇaam.
vedoktam aayuḥ martyaanaam aashiṣhaḥ cha eva karmaṇaam,
phalanti anuyugam loke prabhaavaḥ cha shareeriṇaam.
(martyaanaam) For humans, their (aayuḥ) lifespan, (aashiṣhaḥ) rewards (karmaṇaam)
for their actions (cha) and (prabhaavaḥ) the impact (shareeriṇaam) on their bodies(eva)
as well, (vedoktam) as mentioned in the Vedas, (phalanti) come to fruition (anuyugam)
according to the era that (loke) the World in. 1:84

85. anye kṛitayuge dharmaastretaayaan dvaapare’pare,
anye kaliyuge nṛeeṇaañ yugahraasaanuroopataḥ. anye kṛita-yuge dharmaaḥ tretaayaam dvaapare apare,
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय १ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 1
224
anye kali-yuge nṛeeṇaam yuga-hraasa-anuroopataḥ.
(kṛita) In the Satya (yuge) Era, (dharmaaḥ) the righteous conduct (nṛeeṇaam) for 
mankind (anye) was different from what it is (tretaayaam) in the Tretaa and (dvaapare)
Dvaapara Era and (apare) again (anye) different (kali) in the Kali (yuge) Era. As (yuga)
the eras (anuroopataḥ) progress there is (hraasa) a gradual loss in values. 1:85

86. tapaḥ paraṅ kṛitayuge tretaayaañ jñaanamuchyate,
dvaapare yajñamevaahurdaanamekaṅ kalau yuge.
tapaḥ param kṛita-yuge tretaayaam jñaanam uchyate,
dvaapare yajñam eva aahuḥ daanam ekam kalau yuge.
(kṛita) In the Satya (yuge) Era, (tapaḥ) fortitude (uchyate) was considered (param) the 
most important virtue and (tretaayaam) in the Tretaa Era (jñaanam) the pursuit of 
knowledge was given utmost importance. (aahuḥ) It is said that (dvaapare) in the 
Dvaapara Era (yajñam) the righteous actions were important and (kalau) in the Kali
(yuge) Era (eva) the only (ekam) one left is (daanam) charity. 1:86
Supremacy of the Brahmaṇa
The 92nd – 104th shlokas try to praise the Brahmaṇa class based on their birth. This bias 
was introduced later and is against Maharṣhi Manu’s principles of equality.

92. oordhvan naabhermedhyataraḥ puruṣhaḥ parikeertitaḥ,
tasmaanmedhyataman tvasya mukhamuktan svayambhuvaa.
oordhvam naabheḥ medhyataraḥ puruṣhaḥ parikeertitaḥ,
tasmaat medhyatamam tu asya mukham uktam svayam-bhuvaa.
The upper half of (puruṣhaḥ) the human body (oordhvam) above (naabheḥ) the navel 
(parikeertitaḥ) is considered as (medhyataraḥ) purer. And (tu) hence (svayambhuvaa)
the self created Brahmaa (uktam) has stated (asya) its (mukham) mouth to be 
(medhyatamam) the purest (tasmaat) from that i.e. the upper half. 1:92

93. uttamaaṅgodbhavaajjyaiṣhṭhyaad brahmaṇashchaiva dhaaraṇaat,
sarvasyaivaasya sargasya dharmato braahmaṇaḥ prabhuḥ. uttama-aṅga-udbhavaat jyaiṣhṭhyaat brahmaṇaḥ cha eva dhaaraṇaat,
sarvasya eva asya sargasya dharmataḥ braahmaṇaḥ prabhuḥ.
(udbhavaat) Having born from (uttama) the best (aṅga) part i.e. the speech, 
(jyaiṣhṭhyaat) having born first amongst all classes (cha) and (dhaaraṇaat) being the 
holder (brahmaṇaḥ) of the Vedas (eva) as well, (braahmaṇaḥ) the Brahmaṇa is 
(dharmataḥ) by rule (prabhuḥ) the lord (asya) of this (sarvasya) entire (sargasya)
creation (eva) indeed. Someone is turned into a brahmaṇa through intensive verbal 
coaching by one’s teachers. 1:93

94. taṅ hi svayambhooḥ svaadaasyaattapastaptvaadito’sṛijat,
havyakavyaabhivaahyaaya sarvasyaasya cha guptaye.
tam hi svayambhooḥ svaat aasyaat tapaḥ taptvaa aaditaḥ asṛijat,
havya-kavya-abhi-vaahyaaya sarvasya asya cha guptaye.
(guptaye) For the protection, prosperity (cha) and maintenance of order (sarvasya)
everywhere (asya) in this creation, (svayambhooḥ) the self-created Brahmaa 
(tapaḥ)(taptvaa) with a lot of planning and effort, (aaditaḥ) first, (svaat) from his 
(aasyaat)speech (asṛijat) produced (tam) that Brahmaṇa who is(hi) indeed (vaahyaaya)
provides (abhi) a fair share (havya) to the divinities and (kavya) the elders. 1:94
यस्यास्येन सदाऽ िन्त हव्यािन ित्रिदवौकसः ।

95. yasyaasyena sadaa’shnanti havyaani tridivaukasaḥ,
kavyaani chaiva pitaraḥ kim bhootamadhikan tataḥ. yasya aasyena sadaa ashnanti havyaani tridivaukasaḥ,
kavyaani cha eva pitaraḥ kim bhootam adhikam tataḥ.
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय १ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 1
226
(aasyena) Through the mouth (yasya) of that brahmaṇa (tridivaukasaḥ) the divinities 
residing in the third region of existence (sadaa) always (ashnanti) consume (havyaani)
the offerings (cha) and (pitaraḥ) the ancestors take their (kavyaani) share (eva) as well. 
(kim) Which other (bhootam) being can be (adhikam) better than (tataḥ)that brahmaṇa! 
Implicitly, when the brahmaṇa chants Vedic mantras and help in making offerings in 
the fire, that is the best way to make offerings to the divinities and purification of the 
entire clan. Nothing can be better than this activity. 1:95

96. bhootaanaam praaṇinaḥ shreṣhṭhaaḥ praaṇinaam buddhijeevinaḥ,
buddhimatsu naraaḥ shreṣhṭhaaḥ nareṣhu braahmaṇaaḥ smṛitaaḥ. bhootaanaam praaṇinaḥ shreṣhṭhaaḥ praaṇinaam buddhijeevinaḥ,
buddhimatsu naraaḥ shreṣhṭhaaḥ nareṣhu braahmaṇaaḥ smṛitaaḥ.
(bhootaanaam) In all of the creation including the living beings and the non-living things, 
(praaṇinaḥ) the living beings (shreṣhṭhaaḥ) are better; (praaṇinaam) in the living beings, 
those who (buddhijeevinaḥ) possess some intellect are better; (buddhimatsu) in all of 
beings possessing intellect (naraaḥ) the humans (shreṣhṭhaaḥ) are better; and (nareṣhu)
amongst humans (braahmaṇaaḥ) the brahmaṇa (smṛitaaḥ) are said to be the best. 1:96

97. braahmaṇeṣhu cha vidvaanso vidvatsu kṛitabuddhayaḥ,
kṛitabuddhiṣhu kartaaraḥ kartṛiṣhu brahmavedinaḥ. braahmaṇeṣhu cha vidvaansaḥ vidvatsu kṛita-buddhayaḥ,
kṛita-buddhiṣhu kartaaraḥ kartṛiṣhu brahma-vedinaḥ.
(braahmaṇeṣhu) Amongst the brahmaṇa (vidvaansaḥ) the more scholarly are better; 
(vidvatsu) amongst the scholars those (buddhayaḥ) who understands (kṛita) the truth 
are better; (buddhiṣhu) amongst those who understand (kṛita) the truth, (kartaaraḥ) the 
ones who also act accordingly are better; (cha) and (kartṛiṣhu) amongst those whose 
conduct is based on truth, (vedinaḥ) one who has realized (brahma) the God are the 
best. 1:97

98. utpattireva viprasya moortirdharmasya shaashvatee,
sa hi dharmaarthamutpanno brahmabhooyaaya kalpate.
utpattiḥ eva viprasya moortiḥ dharmasya shaashvatee,
saḥ hi dharmaartham utpannaḥ brahma-bhooyaaya kalpate.
(utpattiḥ) The life (viprasya) of a brahmaṇa (eva) itself has to (shaashvatee) always be 
(moortiḥ) a living example (dharmasya) of the righteous conduct, (hi) because (saḥ) he 
is indeed (utpannaḥ) born (artham) for the purpose of (dharma) upholding the dharma 
and eventually (kalpate) becoming (bhooyaaya) eligible for (brahma) the realization of 
the God. 1:98

ब्रा णः । जायमानः । िह । पिथव्याम ृ ्। अिधजायते॥ ई रः । सवर्भतानाम ू ्। धमर्कोशस्य । ग ये

99. braahmaṇo jaayamaano hi pṛithivyaamadhijaayate,
eeshvaraḥ sarvabhootaanaan dharmakoshasya guptaye.
braahmaṇaḥ jaayamaanaḥ hi pṛithivyaam adhi-jaayate,
eeshvaraḥ sarva-bhootaanaam dharma-koshasya guptaye.
As soon as (braahmaṇaḥ) a brahmaṇa (jaayamaanaḥ) is born, he (hi) by default (jaayate)
becomes (adhi) in-charge (pṛithivyaam) of the earth because he (eeshvaraḥ) is capable 
(guptaye) of protecting (koshasya) the treasure of (dharma) the dharma for (sarva) all 
(bhootaanaam) of the beings. The birth of the brahmaṇa should be treated as the 
second birth i.e. when the teacher declares him/her to be a brahmaṇa. 1:99

100.sarvan svam braahmaṇasyedañ yatkiñchijjagateegatam,
shraiṣhṭhyenaabhijanenedan sarvam vai braahmaṇo’rhati.
sarvam svam braahmaṇasya idam yat kiñchit jagatee-gatam,
shraiṣhṭhyena abhi-janena idam sarvam vai braahmaṇaḥ arhati.
(yat)(kiñchit) Whatever (gatam) exists (jagatee) in the universe, (sarvam) all of (idam) it 
(svam) belongs (braahmaṇasya) to the brahmaṇa. As he is (shraiṣhṭhyena) the best and 
most eligible (abhi)(janena) amongst all humans, (braahmaṇaḥ) he (vai) indeed is 
(arhati) in-charge of (sarvam) all of (idam) it. Implicitly, since a brahmaṇa is the most 
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय १ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 1
228
knowledgeable, he would be happy and content and would be able to handle the 
resources impartially for the greater good. 1:100

स्वम्। एव । ब्रा णः । भङु् े। स्वम्। वस्ते। स्वम्। ददाित । च ॥

101.svameva braahmaṇo bhuṅkte svam vaste svan dadaati cha,
aanṛishansyaad braahmaṇasya bhuñjate heetare janaaḥ. svam eva braahmaṇaḥ bhuṅkte svam vaste svam dadaati cha,
aanṛishansyaat braahmaṇasya bhuñjate hi itare janaaḥ.
Since everything belongs to (braahmaṇaḥ) the brahmaṇa, whatever he (bhuṅkte)
consumes, (vaste) wears (cha) and (dadaati) donates (eva) as well, is considered from 
his (svam) own earnings. He is not a burden on society. (hi) Definitely (janaaḥ) the 
people (itare) from the other classes (bhuñjate) consume because (braahmaṇasya) of 
the brahmaṇa’s(aanṛishansyaat) compassion. Implicitly, everyone is in a better position 
to be able to earn because of the education provided by the brahmaṇa. 1:101

102. tasya karmavivekaarthañ sheṣhaaṇaamanupoorvashaḥ,
svaayambhuvo manurdheemaanidañ shaastramakalpayat.
tasya karma-vivekaartham sheṣhaaṇaam anupoorvashaḥ,
svaayambhuvaḥ manuḥ dheemaan idam shaastram akalpayat.
(artham) For the purpose of imparting (viveka) the knowledge (karma) of the duties and 
conduct (tasya) to those brahmaṇa and (sheṣhaaṇaam) to the remaining classes 
(anupoorvashaḥ) listed orderly as the kṣhatriya, the vaishya and the shoodra, I, (manuḥ)
Maharṣhi Manu (dheemaan) the intelligent (svaayam)(bhuvaḥ) son of the self-created, 
brought (idam) this (shaastram) treatise (akalpayat) to existence. 1:102

103. viduṣhaa braahmaṇenedamadhyetavyam prayatnataḥ,
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय १ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 1
229
shiṣhyebhyashcha pravaktavyan samyaṅnaanyena kenachit.
viduṣhaa braahmaṇena idam adhyetavyam prayatnataḥ,
shiṣhyebhyaḥ cha pravaktavyam samyak na anyena kenachit.
(idam) This treatise should be (prayatnataḥ) diligently (adhyetavyam)studied (viduṣhaa)
by the scholarly (braahmaṇena) brahmaṇa. (cha) And they then should (samyak)
properly (pravaktavyam) teach them (shiṣhyebhyaḥ) to their students belonging to all 
classes and both male and female, but (na) not (kenachit) to any (anyena) other, 
someone who acts against the dharma as laid out in the Vedas. 1:103

104. idañ shaastramadheeyaano braahmaṇaḥ shansitavrataḥ,
manovaagdehajairnityaṅ karmadoṣhairna lipyate.
idam shaastram adheeyaanaḥ braahmaṇaḥ shansitavrataḥ,
manaḥ-vaak-dehajaiḥ nityam karma-doṣhaiḥ na lipyate.
(braahmaṇaḥ) The brahmaṇa who (adheeyaanaḥ)study (idam) this (shaastram) treatise 
and incorporate its principles in their (shansitavrataḥ) praiseworthy conduct, (na) do 
not (nityam) ever (lipyate) engage in (doṣhaiḥ) unrighteous (karma) conduct with their 
(manaḥ) mind, (vaak) speech and (dehajaiḥ) body. 1:104
Benefits of studying Manusmṛiti
The 105th – 107th shlokas contain out of context glorification of Manusmṛiti.

105. punaati paṅktim vañshyaañshcha sapta sapta paraavaraan,
pṛithiveemapi chaivemaaṅ kṛitsnaameko’pi so’rhati.
punaati paṅktim vañshyaan cha sapta sapta paraavaraan,
pṛithiveem api cha eva imaam kṛitsnaam ekaḥ api saḥ arhati.
The one who diligently studies this treatise (paṅktim) line by line, he/she (punaati)
purifies his/her ancestors from (sapta) the seven (avaraan) prior generations (cha) and 
(vañshyaan) offsprings in (sapta) the seven (para) forthcoming generations (eva) as well
(cha) and (saḥ) he/she (ekaḥ) alone can fight (api) and (arhati) win over (imaam) this
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय १ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 1

(kṛitsnaam) entire (pṛithiveem) earth because he/she has the knowledge of the truth. 1:105

106. idan svastyayanañ shreṣhṭhamidam buddhivivardhanam,
idañ yashasyamaayuṣhyamidan niḥshreyasam param.
idam svasti-ayanam shreṣhṭham idam buddhi-vivardhanam,
idam yashasyam aayuṣhyam idam niḥshreyasam param.
(idam) This treatise is (ayanam) an abode of (svasti) well being; (idam) it is (shreṣhṭham)
the best (vivardhanam) for increasing (buddhi)the intellectual power; (idam) it increases 
(aayuṣhyam) longevity and (yashasyam) fame; and (idam) it facilitates the achievement 
of (param) the ultimate goal i.e. (niḥshreyasam) nirvaṇa. 1:106

107. asmindharmo’khilenokto guṇadoṣhau cha karmaṇaam,
chaturṇaamapi varṇaanaamaachaarashchaiva shaashvataḥ. asmin dharmaḥ akhilena uktaḥ guṇa-doṣhau cha karmaṇaam,
chaturṇaam api varṇaanaam aachaaraḥ cha eva shaashvataḥ.
(asmin) In this treatise, (akhilena) everything about (dharmaḥ) the righteous conduct, 
(guṇa) the advantages (cha) and (doṣhau) disadvantages (karmaṇaam) of various 
actions (cha) and (api) also about (shaashvataḥ) the universal (aachaaraḥ) rules of 
conduct (chaturṇaam) for the four (varṇaanaam) classes, (uktaḥ) is mentioned (eva) as 
well. 1:107
Contents of Manusmṛiti
The 111th – 118th shlokas are listing different topics discussed in the Manusmṛiti. This 
logically should be at the beginning of the treatise or as an appendix in the end and not 
embedded in the middle somewhere.

111. jagatashcha samutpattin sanskaaravidhimeva cha,
vratacharyopachaarañ cha snaanasya cha param vidhim.
jagataḥ cha sam-utpattim sanskaara-vidhim eva cha,
vratacharyaa upachaaram cha snaanasya cha param vidhim.
(sam)(utpattim) The creation of this (jagataḥ) universe in the first chapter; (cha) and 
(vidhim) the procedures of various (sanskaara) sacraments, (vratacharyaa) strictly 
following certain codes in certain stages of life (cha) and (upachaaram) providing 
services (eva) as well, in the second chapter; (cha) and (param) the ultimate (vidhim)
procedures (snaanasya) of bathing with knowledge i.e. the graduation, 1:111 

112. daaraadhigamanañ chaivam vivaahaanaañ cha lakṣhaṇam,

daaraadhi-gamanam cha evam vivaahaanaam cha lakṣhaṇam,
mahaayajña-vidhaanam cha shraaddha-kalpam cha shaashvatam.
(gamanam) finding (daaraadhi) suitable women for marriage, (lakṣhaṇam) the 
attributes of the different types (vivaahaanaam) of marriages, (vidhaanam) the 
procedures for the five (mahaa) great (yajña) sacraments (cha) and (shaashvatam) the 
universal (kalpam) way for (shraaddha) giving homage to ancestors, in the third chapter; 
1:112 

for different classes (cha) and (vrataani) the code of conduct (snaatakasya) for graduate 
householders (eva) as well, in the fourth chapter; what (bhakṣhya) can be consumed 
(cha) and what is (abhakṣhyam) forbidden, maintaining (shaucham) cleanliness of the

114.streedharmayogan taapasyam mokṣhan sannyaasameva cha,

(dharma)(yogam) the duties of (stree) the women, in the fifth chapter; the duties and 
conducts assigned (taapasyam) to the preparation for (cha) and (sannyaasam) the final 
renunciation stage of life (cha) and the details of (mokṣham) nirvaaṇa (eva) as well, in

seventh chapter; (vinirṇayam) the decision making (kaaryaaṇaam) in different matters 
(cha) and 1:114 

118. deshadharmaañjaatidharmaankuladharmaañshcha shaashvataan,
paakhaṇḍagaṇadharmaañshcha shaastre’sminnuktavaanmanuḥ. desha-dharmaan jaati-dharmaan kula-dharmaan cha shaashvataan,

in (asmin) this (shaastre) treatise (manuḥ) Maharṣhi Manu (uktavaan) has elaborated 
(shaashvataan) on the universal (dharmaan) attributes, duties and rights of everyone 
(cha) and everything from the perspective of (desha) area, (jaati) birth, (kula) lineage 
and (gaṇa) vices including (paakhaṇḍa) hypocrisy (cha) and deceitfulness etc. 1:118
The 119th shloka wrongfully declares Bhṛigu as the orator of this treatise.

तथा । इदम्। ययमू ्। अिप । अद्य । मत्सकाशात्। िनबोधत ॥
119. yathedamuktavaañchhaastram puraa pṛiṣhṭo manurmayaa,
tathedañ yooyamapyadya matsakaashaannibodhata.
yathaa idam uktavaan shaastram puraa pṛiṣhṭaḥ manuḥ mayaa,
tathaa idam yooyam api adya matsakaashaat nibodhata.
Sage Bhṛigu said, “(yathaa) As (manuḥ) Maharṣhi Manu (uktavaan) had elaborated in 
(idam) this (shaastram) treatise in response (pṛiṣhṭaḥ) to a question asked (mayaa) by 
myself (puraa) some time ago, so should (yooyam) you (api) also (nibodhata) listen to 
(idam) it (adya) now (tathaa) as is (matsakaashaat) from myself.” 1:119
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 2
235
Extensions in Chapter 2
Vedas contain all of the knowledge 
The 7th shloka suddenly interrupts the flow by changing the speech from an active 
discourse to a passive voice.
यः कि त्कस्यिचद्धम  मन
ु
ना प रक ितर्तः ।
स सव ऽिभिहतो वेदेसवर् ानमयो िह सः ॥७॥
यः । कि त्। कस्यिचत्। धमर्ः । मनना
ु । प रक ितर्तः ॥ सः । सवर्ः । अिभिहतः । वेदे। सवर् ानमयः । िह । सः ॥
7. yaḥ kashchitkasyachiddharmo manunaa parikeertitaḥ,
sa sarvo’bhihito vede sarvajñaanamayo hi saḥ. yaḥ kashchit kasyachit dharmaḥ manunaa pari-keertitaḥ,
saḥ sarvaḥ abhihitaḥ vede sarva-jñaanamayaḥ hi saḥ.
(yaḥ)(kashchit) Whatever (dharmaḥ) duties (manunaa) Maharṣhi Manu has 
(pari)(keertitaḥ) highlighted (kasyachit) for anyone, (sarvaḥ) all of (saḥ) them (abhihitaḥ)
are stated (vede) in the Vedas, (hi) because (saḥ) the Vedas (mayaḥ) are saturated with 
(sarva) all of (jñaana) the knowledge. 2:7
Sacraments for everyone
The 16th shloka is out of context as Maharṣhi Manu has not yet started the discourse on 
the sixteen sacraments.
िनषेकािदश्मशानान्तो मन्त्रैयर्स्योिदतो िविधः ।
तस्य शा ेऽिधकारोऽिस्मञ् ेयो नान्यस्य कस्यिचत
्
॥१६॥
िनषेकािद । श्मशानान्तः । मन्त्रैः । यस्य । उिदतः । िविधः॥
तस्य । शा े। अिधकारः । अिस्मन्।  ेयः । न। अन्यस्य । कस्यिचत्॥
16. niṣhekaadishmashaanaanto mantrairyasyodito vidhiḥ,
tasya shaastre’dhikaaro’smiñjñeyo naanyasya kasyachit.
niṣheka-aadi shmashaanaantaḥ mantraiḥ yasya uditaḥ vidhiḥ,
tasya shaastre adhikaaraḥ asmin jñeyaḥ na anyasya kasyachit.
(aadi) From (niṣheka) conception (antaḥ) to (shmashaana) cremation, (vidhiḥ) the 
procedures (yasya) for all of those sixteen sacraments alongwith the associated 
(mantraiḥ) mantras (uditaḥ) have been revealed. (tasya) The followers of these 
sacraments i.e. people of all four classes (adhikaaraḥ) have the right (jñeyaḥ) to study 
(asmin) this (shaastre) treatise and (na) not (anyasya) anybody (kasyachit) else who is a 
non-believer or is uncivilized. 2:16
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 2
236
Different kingdoms in the Aaryaavarta
The 19th shloka talks about kingdoms named after kings who showed up much later than 
Maharṣhi Manu in history.
क
ु  ेत्रंच मत्स्या  ह पञ्चालाः श
ू
रसेनकाः ।
एष ब्र िषर्देशो वैब्र ावतार्दनन्तरः ॥१९॥
कु  ेत्रम्। च । मत्स्याः । च । पञ्चालाः । शरसेनकाः
ू ॥एषः । ब्र िषर्देशः । वै। ब्र ावतार्त्। अनन्तरः ॥
19. kurukṣhetrañ cha matsyaashcha pañchaalaaḥ shoorasenakaaḥ, 
eṣha brahmarṣhidesho vai brahmaavartaadanantaraḥ. kurukṣhetram cha matsyaaḥ cha pañchaalaaḥ shoorasenakaaḥ, 
eṣhaḥ brahmarṣhideshaḥ vai brahmaavartaat anantaraḥ. 
The nation formed (anantaraḥ) after merging the kingdoms of (kurukṣhetram)
Kurukṣhetra, (matsyaaḥ) Matsya, (pañchaalaaḥ) Pañchaala (cha) and (shoorasenakaaḥ)
Shoorasenaka (brahmaavartaat) into the Brahmaavarta, (eṣhaḥ)that is (brahmarṣhi)the 
Brahmarṣhi (deshaḥ) nation (vai) indeed.
 2:19
Relocation of the Shoodra
The 24th shloka without any basis recommends against the relocation of the individuals 
from the upper three classes outside of the Aaryaavarta. 
एतािन्द्वजातयो देशान्सं
श्रयेरन्प्रयत्नतः ।
श
ू
द्रस्तु
यिस्मन्किस्मन्वा िनवसेद्व
ृ
ि किशर्तः ॥२४॥
एतान्। िद्वजातयः । देशान्। सं
श्रयेरन्। प्रयत्नतः ॥ शद्रः
ू । तु। यिस्मन्। किस्मन्। वा । िनवसेत्। वि किशर्तः ृ ॥
24. etaandvijaatayo deshaansañshrayeranprayatnataḥ, 
shoodrastu yasminkasminvaa nivasedvṛittikarshitaḥ. etaan dvijaatayaḥ deshaan sañshrayeran prayatnataḥ, 
shoodraḥ tu yasmin kasmin vaa nivaset vṛitti-karshitaḥ. 
(dvijaatayaḥ) The twice born i.e. the people from the three upper classes (prayatnataḥ)
should make efforts (sañshrayeran) to stay within (etaan) the land (deshaan) of the 
nation. (shoodraḥ) The servant class i.e. the shoodra should (tu) as well try (karshitaḥ)
to earn his/her (vṛitti) living (yasmin) in this land but can also (vaa) alternatively (nivaset)
live (kasmin) in some other country if things don’t work out here.
 2:24

मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 2

52. aayuṣhyam praaṅmukho bhuṅkte yashasyan dakṣhiṇaamukhaḥ,
shriyam pratyaṅmukho bhuṅkte ṛitam bhuṅkte hyudaṅmukhaḥ. aayuṣhyam praaṅ-mukhaḥ bhuṅkte yashasyam dakṣhiṇaa-mukhaḥ,
shriyam pratyaṅ-mukhaḥ bhuṅkte ṛitam bhuṅkte hi udaṅ-mukhaḥ.
The one who (bhuṅkte) eats (mukhaḥ) facing (praaṅ) east (aayuṣhyam) lives longer, the 
one who eats (mukhaḥ) facing (dakṣhiṇaa) south earns (yashasyam) fame, the one who 
(bhuṅkte) eats (mukhaḥ) facing (pratyaṅ) west earns (shriyam) wealth (hi) and the one 
who (bhuṅkte) eats (mukhaḥ) facing (udaṅ) north gets (ṛitam) the truth. 2:52
Sipping the water
The 61st – 62nd shlokas contradict some of the ideas conveyed by Maharṣhi Manu 
elsewhere. During the sacrament ceremonies the sipping of water is done publicly and 
hence the idea of solitude doesn’t apply in the current context of the sacraments. 
Previously, Maharṣhi Manu has not mentioned Shoodra in the sipping of the water 
context. Sudden reference to the Shoodra does not coincide with the flow of the 
information.
अन
ुष्णािभरफे नािभरिद्भस्तीथ न धमर्िवत
्
।
शौचेप्स
ु
ः सवर्दाऽऽचामेदेकान्तेप्राग

दङ्म 
खः ॥६१॥

ु। सवर्दा । आचामेत्।एकान्ते। प्राक्।उदङ्म खः॥
61. anuṣhṇaabhiraphenaabhiradbhisteerthena dharmavit,
shauchepsuḥ sarvadaa’’chaamedekaante praagudaṅmukhaḥ. anuṣhṇaabhiḥ aphenaabhiḥ adbhiḥ teerthena dharmavit,
shauchepsuḥ sarvadaa aachaamet ekaante praak udaṅ-mukhaḥ.
Pious souls (shauchepsuḥ) desirous of purification, should take clean (anuṣhṇaabhiḥ)
cold water (aphenaabhiḥ) devoid of any froth and then sit (ekaante) in solitude 
(mukhaḥ) facing (praak) east or (udaṅ) north (sarvadaa) each and every time and 
(aachaamet) sip (adbhiḥ) water (dharmavit) using the proper (teerthena) points in the 
hand as explained before in [2:59]. 2:61

vaishyo’dbhiḥ praashitaabhistu shoodraḥ spaṣhṭaabhirantataḥ. hṛidgaabhiḥ pooyate vipraḥ kaṇṭhagaabhiḥ tu bhoomipaḥ,

मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 2
238
(vipraḥ) A Braahmaṇa (pooyate) is purified when (adbhiḥ) the water (hṛidgaabhiḥ)
reaches his/her heart, (bhoomipaḥ) a Kṣhatriya (kaṇṭhagaabhiḥ) when it reaches the 
throat, (vaishyaḥ) a Vaishya when it (praashitaabhiḥ) reaches everywhere inside the 
mouth (tu) and (shoodraḥ) a Shoodra (spaṣhṭaabhiḥ) just by the touch of the water 
(antataḥ) on the ends of the lips itself. 2:62
Unequal status for the women
The Vedas grant equality to the women, to the extent that some of the sages mentioned 
as the custodians of the Vedic mantras are females. The 66th – 67th shlokas contradict this 
Vedic principle of equality.
अमिन्त्रका त
ु
काय यं ीणामाव
ृ
दशेषतः ।
सं
स्काराथ शरीरस्य यथाकालंयथाक्रमम
्
॥६६॥
अमिन्त्रका । तु। कायार्। इयम्।  ीणाम्। आवतृ ्। अशेषतः॥ सं
स्काराथर्म्। शरीरस्य । यथाकालम्। यथाक्रमम्॥
66. amantrikaa tu kaaryeyan streeṇaamaavṛidasheṣhataḥ,
sanskaaraarthañ shareerasya yathaakaalañ yathaakramam.
amantrikaa tu kaaryaa iyam streeṇaam aavṛit asheṣhataḥ,
sanskaara-artham shareerasya yathaa-kaalam yathaa-kramam.
(artham) For (sanskaara) the purification (shareerasya) of the body, (iyam) these
(kaaryaa) sacraments, (asheṣhataḥ) without skipping any of them, should (aavṛit) be 
repeated (streeṇaam) for the females as well (yathaa) at the right (kaalam) age and 
(yathaa) in the same (kramam) order, (tu) however (amantrikaa) without chanting the 
associated Vedic mantras. 2:66
वैवािहको िविधः  ीणांसं
स्कारो वैिदकः स्म
ृ
तः ।
पितसेवा ग
