रौ वासो ग
ृ
हाथ ऽिग्नप रिक्रया ॥६७॥
वैवािहकः । िविधः ।  ीणाम्। सं
स्कारः । वैिदकः । स्मतः ृ ॥ पितसेवा । गरौ
ु । वासः । गहाथर्ः ृ । अिग्नप रिक्रया ॥
67. vaivaahiko vidhiḥ streeṇaan sanskaaro vaidikaḥ smṛitaḥ,
patisevaa gurau vaaso gṛihaartho’gniparikriyaa.
vaivaahikaḥ vidhiḥ streeṇaam sanskaaraḥ vaidikaḥ smṛitaḥ,
pati-sevaa gurau vaasaḥ gṛiha-arthaḥ agni-parikriyaa.
(streeṇaam) For the ladies (vidhiḥ) the performance (vaivaahikaḥ) of marriage (smṛitaḥ)
is said to be equivalent to (vaidikaḥ) the sacred thread (sanskaaraḥ) sacrament, (sevaa)
serving (pati) the husband equivalent (vaasaḥ) to attaining knowledge (gurau) from a 
teacher and (arthaḥ) taking care of (gṛiha) the household chores (parikriyaa) equivalent 
to the performance of (agni) the yajña. 2:67
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 2
239
Posture of the student
The 70th shloka conflicts with some of the directives related to the directions mentioned 
elsewhere in Manusmṛiti. The recommended direction of the face can change based on 
the seasons and the weather conditions.
अध्येष्यमाणस्त्वाचान्तो यथाशा म
ु
दङ्म 
खः ।
ब्र ाञ्जिलकृ
तोऽध्याप्यो लघ
ु
वासा िजतेिन्द्रयः ॥७०॥
अध्येष्यमाणः । तु। आचान्तः । यथाशा म्। उदङ्म खः ॥ ब्र ाञ्जिलकृतः । अध्याप्यः । लघवासा
ु । िजतेिन्द्रयः ॥
70. adhyeṣhyamaaṇastvaachaanto yathaashaastramudaṅmukhaḥ,
brahmaañjalikṛito’dhyaapyo laghuvaasaa jitendriyaḥ. adhyeṣhyamaaṇaḥ tu aachaantaḥ yathaa shaastram udaṅ-mukhaḥ,
brahmaañjali-kṛitaḥ adhyaapyaḥ laghu-vaasaa jitendriyaḥ.
(tu) Then (aachaantaḥ) after having sipped water thrice (yathaa) as per the procedures 
outlined in (shaastram) the scriptures, a student, (adhyeṣhyamaaṇaḥ) desirous of 
learning, (vaasaa) wearing an attire made from (laghu) a lightweight fabric, should sit 
(mukhaḥ) facing (udaṅ) north, (brahmaañjali)(kṛitaḥ) with palms pressed together in the 
namaste pose and (adhyaapyaḥ) learn from a qualified teacher (jitendriyaḥ) who has 
won the control of his/her senses. 2:70
Eligibility for chanting om
The 75th shloka defines eligibility for chanting om. There is no such prerequisite for 
remembering God.
प्राक्क
ू
लान्पयर्पासीनः
ु
पिवत्रै ैव पािवतः ।
प्राणायामैि िभः प
ू
तस्तत ओङ
्कारमहर्ित ॥७५॥
प्राक्कूलान्। पयर्पासीनः
ु । पिवत्रैः । च । एव । पािवतः ॥ प्राणायामैः । ित्रिभः । पतः
ू । ततः । ओङ्कारम्। अहर्ित ॥
75. praakkoolaan paryupaaseenaḥ pavitraishchaiva paavitaḥ,
praaṇaayaamaistribhiḥ pootastata oṅkaaramarhati. praak-koolaan paryupaaseenaḥ pavitraiḥ cha eva paavitaḥ,
praaṇaayaamaiḥ tribhiḥ pootaḥ tataḥ oṅkaaram arhati.
One should (upaaseenaḥ) sit facing (praak) east (pari) on the top of (koolaan) a mat 
made out of grass that is (pavitraiḥ) clean (cha) and (paavitaḥ) pure (eva) as well and 
then (pootaḥ) purify oneself (tribhiḥ) with three (praaṇaayaamaiḥ) rounds of deep 
breathing; (tataḥ) then only one (arhati) becomes eligible (oṅkaaram) for chanting 
om.
2:75
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 2
240
Importance of the Gaayatree Mantra
In the 79th – 87th shlokas someone tries to emphasize that just the chanting of the 
Gaayatree mantra for a short duration of time is sufficient for mokṣha and the other acts 
like meditation, performing yajña etc. are not required. They also try to define the classes 
based on birth and assign higher status to braahmaṇa even if he/she does not engage in 
the acts of benevolence. All of this is in contradiction with the Vedic wisdom and Maharṣhi 
Manu’s teachings in some other shlokas.
सहस्रकृ
त्वस्त्वभ्यस्य बिहरेतित्त्रकं िद्वजः ।
महतोऽप्येनसो मासा वचेवािहिवर्मु
च्यते॥७९॥
सहस्रकृत्वः । तु। अभ्यस्य । बिहः । एतत्। ित्रकम्। िद्वजः॥
महतः । अिप । एनसः । मासात्। त्वचाऽइव । अिहः । िवमच्यते
ु ॥
79. sahasrakṛitvastvabhyasya bahiretattrikan dvijaḥ, 
mahato’pyenaso maasaattvachevaahirvimuchyate. sahasra-kṛitvaḥ tu abhyasya bahiḥ etat trikam dvijaḥ, 
mahataḥ api enasaḥ maasaat tvachaa-iva ahiḥ vimuchyate. 
(dvijaḥ) The twice born, who finds a place in solitude (bahiḥ) outside and (abhyasya)
diligently (kṛitvaḥ) performs the chants of the combination of (etat) these (trikam) three 
i.e. Om, the three basic qualities i.e. bhoorbhuvaḥ svaḥ and the gaayatree mantra, 
(sahasra) a thousand times everyday (maasaat) for a month, is (tu) indeed relieved from 
(api) even (mahataḥ) the gravest of the (enasaḥ) sins, (iva) like (ahiḥ) a snake 
(vimuchyate) is relieved from its (tvachaa) skin. 2:79
एतयचार्िवसं
य
ु
 ः कालेच िक्रयया स्वया ।
ब्र  ित्रयिवड्
योिनगर्हर्णांयाित साध
ु

॥८०॥
एतया । ऋचा । िवसं

80. etayarchaa visañyuktaḥ kaale cha kriyayaa svayaa, 
brahmakṣhatriyaviḍyonirgarhaṇaañ yaati saadhuṣhu. 
etayaa ṛichaa visañyuktaḥ kaale cha kriyayaa svayaa,
brahma-kṣhatriya-viṭ-yoniḥ garhaṇaam yaati saadhuṣhu. 
Whether (yoniḥ) born as (brahma) Braahmaṇa, (kṣhatriya) Kṣhatriya or (viṭ) Vaishya, a 
twice born who (visañyuktaḥ) does not engage in the chanting of (etayaa) this (ṛichaa)
mantra (cha) and (kaale) timely (kriyayaa) performance of (svayaa) his/her sacraments 
and duties (yaati) is subject (garhaṇaam) to criticism (saadhuṣhu) from the 
benevolent.2:80

ओङ्कारपिवर्काः
ू । ितस्रः । महाव्या तयः । अव्ययाः ॥ ित्रपदा । च । एव । सािवत्री । िव ेयम्। ब्र णः । मखम ु ्॥
81. oṅkaarapoorvikaastisro mahaavyaahṛitayo’vyayaaḥ,
tripadaa chaiva saavitree vijñeyam brahmaṇo mukham. oṅkaara-poorvikaaḥ tisraḥ mahaa-vyaahṛitayaḥ avyayaaḥ,
tripadaa cha eva saavitree vijñeyam brahmaṇaḥ mukham.
These (tisraḥ) three (mahaa) greatest (vyaahṛitayaḥ) qualities of God (poorvikaaḥ) when 
prefixed with (oṅkaara) om become (avyayaaḥ) ever lasting (cha) and together with the 
(tri) three (padaa) limbed (saavitree) Gaayatree mantra, they (vijñeyam) should (eva)
indeed be considered as (mukham) the face i.e. the best of (brahmaṇaḥ) the Vedic 
wisdom. 2:81
योऽधीतेऽहन्यहन्येतां

82. yo’dheete’hanyahanyetaanstreeṇi varṣhaaṇyatandritaḥ,
sa brahma paramabhyeti vaayubhootaḥ khamoorttimaan. yaḥ adheete ahani-ahani etaan treeṇi varṣhaaṇi atandritaḥ,
saḥ brahma param abhyeti vaayu-bhootaḥ khamoorttimaan.
(saḥ) One (yaḥ) who (atandritaḥ) industriously (adheete) studies and chants (etaan)
these (ahani)(ahani) everyday (treeṇi) for three (varṣhaaṇi) years, (khamoorttimaan)
becomes subtle like sky, (vaayu)(bhootaḥ) is able to traverse regions like air and 
(abhyeti) realizes (brahma)(param) the ultimate. 2:82
एका रंपरंब्र  प्राणायामः परंतपः ।

83. ekaakṣharam param brahma praaṇaayaamaḥ paran tapaḥ,
saavitryaastu paran naasti maunaatsatyam vishiṣhyate. eka-akṣharam param brahma praaṇaayaamaḥ parantapaḥ,
saavitryaaḥ tu param na asti maunaat satyam vishiṣhyate.
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 2
242
(eka)(akṣharam) The monosyllable Om is (param) the best name for (brahma) God, 
(praaṇaayaamaḥ) breath control is (param) the best (tapaḥ) exercise to build fortitude, 
(tu) there (asti) is (na) nothing (param) better than (saavitryaaḥ) the Gaayatree mantra 
and (satyam) truth (vishiṣhyate) stands out (maunaat) compared to silence. 2:83
 रिन्त सवार्वैिदक्यो ज

ु ॥ अ रम्। दष्करम ु ्।  ेयम्। ब्र  । च । एव । प्रजापितः ॥
84. kṣharanti sarvaa vaidikyo juhotiyajatikriyaaḥ,
akṣharan duṣhkarañ jñeyam brahma chaiva prajaapatiḥ. kṣharanti sarvaaḥ vaidikyaḥ juhoti-yajati-kriyaaḥ,
akṣharam duṣhkaram jñeyam brahma cha eva prajaapatiḥ.
The effects of (sarvaaḥ) all of (vaidikyaḥ) the Vedic (kriyaaḥ) activities like (juhoti)
making offerings, (yajati) performing yajña etc. (kṣharanti) deplete, (cha) however, 
(jñeyam) consider the effects of the (duṣhkaram) most difficult to achieve, the 
realization of (akṣharam) the indestructible (brahma) God, (prajaapatiḥ) the lord of 
masses, as permanent (eva) indeed. 2:84

85. vidhiyajñaajjapayajño vishiṣhṭo dashabhirguṇaiḥ,
upaañshuḥ syaachchhataguṇaḥ saahasro maanasaḥ smṛitaḥ. vidhi-yajñaat japa-yajñaḥ vishiṣhṭaḥ dashabhiḥ guṇaiḥ,
upaañshuḥ syaat shata-guṇaḥ saahasraḥ maanasaḥ smṛitaḥ.
(japa)(yajñaḥ) The persistent chanting is considered (dashabhiḥ) ten (guṇaiḥ) times 
(vishiṣhṭaḥ) better than the performance of (vidhi)(yajñaat) the procedural offerings; 
(upaañshuḥ) soft chants (syaat) are (shata) one hundred (guṇaḥ) times better and 
(maanasaḥ) the mental chants are (smṛitaḥ) said to be (saahasraḥ) a thousand times 
better. 2:85
येपाकय ा त्वारो िविधय समिन्वताः ।
सव तेजपय स्य कलांनाहर्िन्त षोडशीम

॥८६॥
ये। पाकय ाः । चत्वारः । िविधय समिन्वताः ॥ सव । ते। जपय स्य । कलाम्। न। अहर्िन्त ।षोडशीम्॥
86. ye paakayajñaashchatvaaro vidhiyajñasamanvitaaḥ,
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 2
243
sarve te japayajñasya kalaan naarhanti ṣhoḍasheem. ye paaka-yajñaaḥ chatvaaraḥ vidhi-yajña-samanvitaaḥ,
sarve te japa-yajñasya kalaam na arhanti ṣhoḍasheem.
(ye) These (vidhi)(yajña) procedural offerings involving offering of (paaka) the cooked 
grains, (samanvitaaḥ) along with (chatvaaraḥ) the four daily (yajñaaḥ) activities i.e. 
routine offerings in the fire, offering food to animals and the less fortunate individuals, 
taking care of the elders and offering food and comfort to guests; (sarve) all of (te) them 
together (arhanti) offer (na) not even the (ṣhoḍasheem)(kalaam) one sixteenth of the 
value (japa)(yajñasya) of the persistent chanting. 2:86

87. japyenaiva tu sansidhyed braahmaṇo naatra sañshayaḥ,
kuryaadanyanna vaa kuryaan maitro braahmaṇa uchyate. japyena eva tu sansidhyet braahmaṇaḥ na atra sañshayaḥ,
kuryaat anyat na vaa kuryaat maitraḥ braahmaṇaḥ uchyate.
(atra) There is (na) no (sañshayaḥ) doubt that (braahmaṇaḥ) a scholar (sansidhyet) can 
attain extraordinary abilities (eva)(tu) just (japyena) by practicing the persistent chants. 
It (uchyate) is said that regardless of whether he/she (kuryaat) performs (anyat) other 
acts of benevolence and offerings (vaa) or (na) does not (kuryaat) perform them, this 
(braahmaṇaḥ) scholar remains (maitraḥ) dear to others and to God. 2:87
Learning Vedas without permission
The 116th shloka contradicts Maharṣhi Manu’s principles of no boundation on the study 
of the Vedas.
ब्र यस्त्वननु
 ातमधीयानादवाप्नु
यात
्
। स ब्र स्तेय सं
य
ु
 ो नरकं प्रितपद्यते॥११६॥
ब्र  । यः । तु। अनन ातम ु ्। अधीयानात्। अवाप्नयात ु ्॥ सः । ब्र स्तेय । सं
य ः
ु ।नरकम्। प्रितपद्यते॥
116. brahma yastvananujñaatamadheeyaanaadavaapnuyaat,
sa brahmasteya sañyukto narakam pratipadyate. brahma yaḥ tu ananujñaatam adheeyaanaat avaapnuyaat,
saḥ brahma-steya sañyuktaḥ narakam prati-padyate.
(yaḥ)(tu) Whosoever, (avaapnuyaat) learns (brahma) Vedas (adheeyaanaat) from a
teacher (ananujñaatam) without teacher’s explicit permission, (saḥ) he/she is 
considered (steya) a thief (sañyuktaḥ) united with (brahma) Vedic knowledge in error 
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 2
244
and (prati)(padyate) begets (narakam) sorrows. This rule may be applicable in order to 
maintain order in the classroom and to prevent the evil minded from acquiring and 
misusing the knowledge. However, there appears no reason to apply this to someone 
who studies the scriptures by oneself. 2:116
Minimalistic approach
Maharṣhi Manu consistently prescribes a careful study of the Vedas. The 118th shloka
appears out of context and provides an easy way out of the rigors of studying the Vedas.
सािवत्रीमात्रसारोऽिप वरंिवप्रः स
ु
यिन्त्रतः ।
नायिन्त्रति वेदोऽिप सवार्शी सवर्िवक्रयी ॥११८॥
सािवत्रीमात्रसारः । अिप । वरम्। िवप्रः । सयिन्त्रतः
ु ॥ न। अयिन्त्रतः । ित्रवेदः । अिप । सवार्शी । सवर्िवक्रयी॥
118. saavitreemaatrasaaro’pi varam vipraḥ suyantritaḥ,
naayantritastrivedo’pi sarvaashee sarvavikrayee. saavitree-maatra-saaraḥ api varam vipraḥ suyantritaḥ,
na ayantritaḥ trivedaḥ api sarva-aashee sarva-vikrayee.
(vipraḥ) A Braahmaṇa who has learnt and implemented (saaraḥ) the essence of 
(maatra) only (saavitree) the Gaayatree mantra and is (api) also (suyantritaḥ) in control 
of one’s senses is (varam) the best and (na) not the one who (trivedaḥ) has mastered all 
three types of knowledges but (ayantritaḥ) has no control over one’s senses and 
(aashee) consumes (sarva) everything and (api) also (vikrayee) trades in (sarva)
everything, even the forbidden substances. It is implied that knowledge that is not 
implemented in one’s own lifestyle is of no use and leads to hypocrisy. 2:118
The 123rd shloka interrupts the flow between the prior and the subsequent shlokas and 
conflicts with Maharṣhi Manu’s laws of equality for women as well.
नामधेयस्य येके िचदिभवादंन जानते।
तान्प्रा ोऽहिमित ब्र
ू
याित् यः सवार्स्तथैव च ॥१२३॥
नामधेयस्य । ये। के िचत्। अिभवादम्। न। जानते॥
तान्। प्रा ः । अहम्। इित । ब्रयात ू ्। ि यः । सवार्ः । तथा । एव । च ॥
123. naamadheyasya ye kechidabhivaadan na jaanate,
taanpraajño’hamiti brooyaat striyaḥ sarvaastathaiva cha. naamadheyasya ye kechit abhivaadam na jaanate,
taan praajñaḥ aham iti brooyaat striyaḥ sarvaaḥ tathaa eva cha.
(ye)(kechit) Whosoever (na) does not (jaanate) know the ways of properly replying 
(abhivaadam) to a greetings (naamadheyasya) along with the greeter’s name (cha) and 
(tathaa) similarly (sarvaaḥ) all of (striyaḥ) the women (eva) as well, (praajñaḥ) the wise 
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 2
245
should not greet (taan) them with the full sentence mentioned in the prior shloka 
(2:122) and (brooyaat) should just say, “(iti) This is (aham) myself”. A presumption that 
women are uneducated and do not know the proper etiquettes of greetings is implied 
by the author of this shloka. 2:123
Greeting the people in kinship and social circle
The 130th – 135th shlokas are out of the context of the student phase of life, during which 
the students are not supposed to be in touch with their families.

मातलान ु ्। च । िपतव्यान ृ ्। च ।  शरानु ्। ऋित्वजः । ग नु ्॥ असौ । अहम्। इित । ब्रयात ू ्। प्रत्यत्थाय ु । यवीयसः॥
130. maatulaañshcha pitṛivyaañshcha shvashuraanṛitvijo guroon, 
asaavahamiti brooyaat pratyutthaaya yaveeyasaḥ. maatulaan cha pitṛivyaan cha shvashuraan ṛitvijaḥ guroon,
asau aham iti brooyaat pratyutthaaya yaveeyasaḥ. 
When meeting (maatulaan) the mother’s brothers, (pitṛivyaan) the father’s brothers, 
(shvashuraan) the father-in-laws, (ṛitvijaḥ) the priests (cha) and (guroon) the teachers, 
one should (prati)(utthaaya) after getting up, greet them by (iti)(brooyaat) saying, 
“(aham) I am (asau) …”, (yaveeyasaḥ) even if they are younger in age. The level of 
education is not the only criterion for respect, kinship and social norms are also 
important. 2:130

131. maatṛiṣhvasaa maatulaanee shvashrooratha pitṛiṣhvasaa,

(maatṛiṣhvasaa) Mother’s sisters, (maatulaanee) mother’s brother’s wife, (shvashrooḥ)
mother-in-laws (atha) and (pitṛiṣhvasaa) father’s sisters (sampoojyaa) should be 
respected (guru)(patneevat) similarly as the teacher’s wife because (taaḥ) they are 
(samaaḥ) at the same level as (guru) the teacher’s (bhaaryayaa) wife. 2:131

132. bhraaturbhaaryopasaṅgraahyaa savarṇaa’hanyahanyapi,

One should (upa) seek and greet (bhraatuḥ) the elder brother's (bhaaryaa) wife, who is 
from (savarṇaa) the same varṇa, similarly as one would greet the brother i.e. 
(saṅgraahyaa) by touching her feet (ahani)(ahani) everyday. (tu) And similarly 
(sambandhi)(yoṣhitaḥ) the wives of other elders who are related or are from (jñaati) the 
same varṇa (upa)(saṅgraahyaa) should be greeted (api) as well whenever one 
(viproṣhya) returns from a journey. 2:132

133. piturbhaginyaam maatushcha jyaayasyaañ cha svasaryapi,

(pituḥ) The father’s (bhaginyaam) sister, (maatuḥ) the mother’s sister (cha) and 
(jyaayasyaam) the elder (svasari) sister (api) as well, (vṛittim)(aatiṣhṭhet) should be

respectable (taabhyaḥ) of them. 2:133

134. dashaabdaakhyam paurasakhyam pañchaabdaakhyaṅ kalaabhṛitaam,
tryabdapoorvañ shrotriyaaṇaan svalpenaapi svayoniṣhu. dasha-abda-aakhyam paura-sakhyam pañcha-abda-aakhyam kalaa-bhṛitaam,
tri-abda-poorvam shrotriyaaṇaam svalpena api svayoniṣhu.
(paura) The citizens of the society, (aakhyam) whose age difference is up to (dasha) ten 
(abda) years, (kalaa)(bhṛitaam) people engaged in the same trade (aakhyam) whose age 
difference is up to (pañcha) five (abda) years and (shrotriyaaṇaam) scholars whose age 
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 2
247
difference is (poorvam) up to (tri) three (abda) years (sakhyam) should be treated like 
friends, however, (svayoniṣhu) within the family (api) even (svalpena) minor differences 
matter. 2:134

ब्रा णस्तु
तयोः िपता ॥१३५॥
ब्रा णम्। दशवषर्म्। तु। शतवषर्म्। तु। भिमपम ू ्॥ िपतापत्रौ
ु । िवजानीयात्। ब्रा णः । तु। तयोः । िपता ॥
135. braahmaṇan dashavarṣhan tu shatavarṣhan tu bhoomipam,
pitaaputrau vijaaneeyaad braahmaṇastu tayoḥ pitaa. braahmaṇam dasha-varṣham tu shata-varṣham tu bhoomipam,
pitaa-putrau vijaaneeyaat braahmaṇaḥ tu tayoḥ pitaa.
(braahmaṇam) A braahmaṇa who is only (dasha) ten (varṣham) years old (tu) and 
(bhoomipam) a kṣhatriya king who is (shata) one hundred (varṣham) years old, 
(vijaaneeyaat) should be considered as (pitaa) father and (putrau) son (tu) and (tayoḥ)
out of both (braahmaṇaḥ) the braahmaṇa should be treated as (pitaa) the father (tu)
indeed. 2:135
Comparison between mother, father and teacher
The 145th shloka conflicts with the idea proposed in the prior shloka and with the flow as 
well.
उपाध्यायान्दशाचायर्आचायार्णांशतंिपता ।
सह ंत
ु
िपतन्माता
ॄ
गौरवेणाित रच्यते॥१४५॥
उपाध्यायान्। दशाचायर्ः । आचायार्णाम्। शतम्। िपता ॥ सह म्। तु। िपतन
ॄ्। माता । गौरवेण । अित रच्यते॥
145. upaadhyaayaandashaachaarya aachaaryaaṇaañ shatam pitaa,
sahastran tu pitṛeenmaataa gauraveṇaatirichyate. upaadhyaayaan dasha-aachaaryaḥ aachaaryaaṇaam shatam pitaa,
sahastram tu pitṛeen maataa gauraveṇa atirichyate.
(aachaaryaḥ) An aachaarya over (dasha) ten (upaadhyaayaan) upaadhyaaya, (pitaa) a 
father over (shatam) one hundred (aachaaryaaṇaam) aachaarya and (maataa) a mother 
(atirichyate) exceeds (gauraveṇa) in importance over (tu) even (sahastram) one 
thousand (pitṛeen) fathers. 2:145
Importance and discipline of the Upanayana Sanskaara
The 169th – 174th shlokas bring forward some ideas like three births instead of two, 
saavitree being the mother and the impropriety of chanting Vedic mantras prior to 
Upanayana sanskaara. These ideas do not conform to Vedas or to Maharṣhi Manu’s 
teachings presented elsewhere.
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 2
248
मात
ु
रग्रेऽिधजननंिद्वतीयंमौिञ्जबन्धने।
त

तीयंय दी ायांिद्वजस्य श्र
ुितचोदनात्

मातः

169. maaturagre’dhijananan dviteeyam mauñjibandhane,
tṛiteeyañ yajñadeekṣhaayaan dvijasya shrutichodanaat. maatuḥ agre adhi-jananam dviteeyam mauñji-bandhane,
tṛiteeyam yajña-deekṣhaayaam dvijasya shruti-chodanaat.
(chodanaat) As directed in (shruti) the Vedas, (dvijasya) for the twice born, (agre) the 
first (adhi)(jananam) birth is (maatuḥ) from the mother, (dviteeyam) the second is when 
(mauñji) the girdle (bandhane) is tied and (tṛiteeyam) the third is when he/she 
(deekṣhaayaam) becomes eligible (yajña) for performing yajña i.e. becomes a 
householder. 2:169

170. tatra yad brahmajanmaasya mauñjeebandhanachihnitam,

(tatra) Out of the three births, (yat) the (janma) birth (chihnitam) memorialized by 
(bandhana) tying (mauñjee) the girdle is (asya) his/her birth in (brahma) knowledge, 
(tatra) after which (aachaarya) the teacher performing the sacrament (uchyate) is said 
to be equivalent to (asya) his/her (pitaa) father (tu) and (saavitree) Gaayatree mantra
to (maataa) the mother. 2:170

171. vedapradaanaadaachaaryam pitaram parichakṣhate,

(aachaaryam) The teacher (chakṣhate) is said to be (pari) equivalent to (pitaram) the 
father (hi) because he/she (pradaanaat) provides (veda) the knowledge of the Vedas.

(aa) Before (bandhanaat) the tying of (mauñjee) the girdle i.e. the Upanayana 
Sanskaara, (asmin) this child is (na) not (yujyate) responsible for (kiñchit) any of his/her 
(karma) actions and duties. 2:171

172. naabhivyaahaarayed brahma svadhaaninayanaadṛite,
shoodreṇa hi samastaavadyaavadvede na jaayate. na abhi-vyaahaarayet brahma svadhaaninayanaat ṛite,

(yaavat) Until someone is (jaayate) born into (vede) the vedas i.e. his/her Upanayana 
Sanskaara has been performed, (na) do not (abhi)(vyaahaarayet) involve him/her in any 
practice of (brahma) the Vedas (ṛite) except (svadhaaninayanaat) the rites for the dead,
(hi) because (taavat) until then, one is (samaḥ) like (shoodreṇa) a low class ignorant. 2:172

173. kṛitopanayanasyaasya vrataadeshanamiṣhyate,

(kṛita) Upon the performance (upanayanasya) of the Upanayana Sanskaara, (asya) one 
(aadeshanam) is instructed about (vrata) the disciplines and the conducts one is 
required to follow (cha) and then he/she (eva) should (vidhi)(poorvakam) properly 
(iṣhyate) study and (grahaṇam) learn (brahmaṇaḥ) the Vedas (krameṇa) in a proper 
sequence. 2:173

174. yadyasya vihitañ charma yatsootrañ yaa cha mekhalaa,

मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 2
250
(yat) Whatever (vihitam) the rules are (yasya) for (charma) the leather of the seat, (yat)
for (sootram) the sacred thread, (yaa) for (mekhalaa) the girdle, (yaḥ) for (daṇḍaḥ) the 
staff (cha) and (yat) for (vasanam) the clothes, (tat)(tat) those guidelines are part 
(vrateṣhu) of the discipline to be observed (asya) by them (api) as well. 2:174
The 181st shloka presents a method of atonement by worshiping a physical god. Vedas do 
not call for the worship of physical gods. Also this shloka is out of place because all of the 
methods of atonement are discussed in the eleventh chapter.
स्वप्नेिसक्त्वा ब्र चारी िद्वजः श

स्नात्वा । अकर् म्। अचर्ियत्वा । ित्रः । पनमार्म ु ्। इित । ऋचम्। जपेत्॥
181. svapne siktvaa brahmachaaree dvijaḥ shukramakaamataḥ,
snaatvaa’rkamarchayitvaa triḥ punarmaamityṛichañ japet. svapne siktvaa brahmachaaree dvijaḥ shukram akaamataḥ,
snaatvaa arkam archayitvaa triḥ punarmaam iti ṛicham japet.
In case (akaamataḥ) an undesirable (siktvaa) discharge of (shukram) sexual fluids takes 
place (svapne) while sleeping, (dvijaḥ) the twice born (brahmachaaree) student 
(snaatvaa) after bathing and (archayitvaa) worshiping (arkam) the Sun God, (japet)
should chant (iti) the (punarmaam) punarmaam (ṛicham) mantra (Yajurveda 4:15) (triḥ)
thrice with a determination to never repeat the mistake again. 2:181
Importance of seeking endowment
The 187th – 188th shlokas start to discuss the topic of seeking endowment again when 
Maharṣhi Manu has already moved on to the next topic. They also discuss penances for 
digressions, a topic that is covered in the eleventh chapter. These shlokas hence do not 
conform to the flow.
अक
ृ
त्वा भै चरणमसिमध्य च पावकम
्
। अनात
ु
रः स रात्रमवक िणर्व्रतंचरेत
्
॥१८७॥
अकृत्वा । भै चरणम्। असिमध्य । च । पावकम्॥ अनातुरः । स रात्रम्। अवक िणर्व्रतम्। चरेत्॥
187. akṛitvaa bhaikṣhacharaṇamasamidhya cha paavakam,
anaaturaḥ saptaraatramavakeerṇivratañ charet. akṛitvaa bhaikṣha-charaṇam asamidhya cha paavakam,
anaaturaḥ sapta-raatram avakeerṇi-vratam charet.
(anaaturaḥ) Without any sickness, if a student, continuously for (sapta)seven (raatram)
days, (akṛitvaa) does not engage in (bhaikṣha)(charaṇam) begging for endowment (cha)
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 2

or (asamidhya) in offerings (paavakam) in the fire, then he/she should (charet) perform 
(vratam) a penance called (avakeerṇi) avakeerṇee. 2:187

188. bhaikṣheṇa vartayennityan naikaannaadee bhaved vratee, 
bhaikṣheṇa vratino vṛittirupavaasasamaa smṛitaa. bhaikṣheṇa vartayet nityam na eka-annaadee bhavet vratee,
bhaikṣheṇa vratinaḥ vṛittiḥ upavaasa-samaa smṛitaa. 
(vratee) A student should (nityam) always (vartayet) sustain oneself only (bhaikṣheṇa)
by the consumption of the alms. He/she (bhavet) should also (na) not beg 
(eka)(annaadee) routinely from the same source again and again. (vṛittiḥ) Sustaining 
(vratinaḥ) oneself (bhaikṣheṇa) on the benefactions only (smṛitaa) is said to be (samaa)
equivalent (upavaasa) to fasting. 2:188
Partaking in food offered in the memory of the deceased 
The 189th – 190th shlokas discuss a practice called shraaddha in which food is offered in 
the memory of the deceased. This practice is supported neither in the Vedas nor by 
Maharṣhi Manu. 
व्रतवद्देवदैवत्येिप येकमर्ण्यथिषर्वत
्
।
काममभ्यिथर्तोऽ ीयाद
्
व्रतमस्य न ल
ु
प्यते॥१८९॥
व्रतवत्।देवदैवत्ये। िप ये। कमर्िण । अथ । ऋिषवत्॥ कामम्। अभ्यिथर्तः। अ ीयात्। व्रतम्। अस्य ।न। लप्यते
ु ॥
189. vratavaddevadaivatye pitrye karmaṇyatharṣhivat, 
kaamamabhyarthito’shneeyaad vratamasya na lupyate. vratavat devadaivatye pitrye karmaṇi atha ṛiṣhivat,
kaamam abhyarthitaḥ ashneeyaat vratam asya na lupyate. 
A student (ashneeyaat) can partake in food when one is (kaamam) purposely and 
respectfully (abhyarthitaḥ) invited (vratavat) as a scholar (deva)(daivatye) for pleasing 
the divinities (atha) or (ṛiṣhivat) as a sage (karmaṇi) for pleasing (pitrye) the deceased 
elders. This (na) does not (lupyate) diminish (asya) one’s (vratam) discipline that he/she 
is supposed to observe. 2:189

पिद ंमनीिषिभः । राजन्यवैश्ययोस्त्वेवंनैतत्कमर्िवधीयते॥१९०॥
ब्र णस्य । एव । कमर्। एतत्। उपिद म्। मनीिषिभः ॥ राजन्यवैश्ययोः । तु। एवम्। न। एतत्। कमर्। िवधीयते॥
190. brahmaṇasyaiva karmaitadupadiṣhṭam maneeṣhibhiḥ,

raajanyavaishyayostvevan naitatkarma vidheeyate. brahmaṇasya eva karma etat upadiṣhṭam maneeṣhibhiḥ,

(upadiṣhṭam) As decreed (maneeṣhibhiḥ) by the sages, (etat) this (karma) partaking in 
food on special occasions is (eva) only (brahmaṇasya) for the students from braahmaṇa 
class. There is (na) no (vidheeyate) provision for the students from (raajanya)the warrior 
(evam) and (vaishyayoḥ) the merchant class (tu) to (karma) participate in (etat) these 
feasts. 2:190
Result of criticizing the teacher
The 201stshloka exaggerates punishments and makes misstatement as well. Creating fear 
psychosis is not Maharṣhi Manu’s style of preaching. While residing with the guru, a 
student is the responsibility of the guru and he/she consumes the food granted by the 
guru. Logically there can be no punishment for an universally acceptable activity.
परीवादात्खरो भवित  ा वैभवित िनन्दकः ।
प रभो ा क
ृ
िमभर्वित क टो भवित मत्सरी ॥२०१॥
परीवादात्। खरः । भवित ।  ा । वै। भवित । िनन्दकः ॥ प रभो ा । कृिमः । भवित । क टः । भवित । मत्सरी॥
201. pareevaadaatkharo bhavati shvaa vai bhavati nindakaḥ,
paribhoktaa kṛimirbhavati keeṭo bhavati matsaree.
pareevaadaat kharaḥ bhavati shvaa vai bhavati nindakaḥ,
pari-bhoktaa kṛimiḥ bhavati keeṭaḥ bhavati matsaree.
A student who (pareevaadaat) points out one’s teacher’s faults (bhavati) becomes 
(kharaḥ) a donkey in the next life, one (nindakaḥ) who unfairly criticizes the teacher 
(bhavati) becomes (shvaa) a dog (vai) indeed, one (pari)(bhoktaa) who takes from the 
teacher (bhavati) becomes (kṛimiḥ) a worm and the (matsaree) one who is jealous of the 
teacher (bhavati) becomes (keeṭaḥ) an insect. 2:201
Others deserving respect similar to a teacher 
The 207th – 211th shlokas discuss the respect that needs to be accorded to the family
member of the teacher. These conflict with Maharṣhi Manu’s prepositions elsewhere that 
only the teacher deserves special respect and services. These also indirectly talk about 
multiple wives of the teacher from different classes. Maharṣhi Manu has clearly said 
elsewhere that a twice born can have only one wife and can remarry only upon her death.

207. shreyaḥsu guruvad vṛittin nityameva samaacharet,

(shreyaḥsu) The experts of their fields should (eva) also be (nityam) always 
(sam)(aacharet) bestowed the same (vṛittim) respect (guruvat) as the teacher, (cha) and 
(aaryeṣhu) the benevolent (putreṣhu) children (guru) of the teacher (cha) and (guroḥ)
teacher’s (eva) as well as (sva) one’s own (bandhuṣhu) relatives too. 2:207

बालः । समानजन्मा । वा । िशष्यः । वा । य कमर्िण ॥ अध्यापयन्। ग सु तः

208. baalaḥ samaanajanmaa vaa shiṣhyo vaa yajñakarmaṇi,
adhyaapayangurusuto guruvanmaanamarhati.
baalaḥ samaana-janmaa vaa shiṣhyaḥ vaa yajña-karmaṇi,
adhyaapayan guru-sutaḥ guruvat maanam arhati.
(guru) The teacher’s (sutaḥ) child, (baalaḥ) young (vaa) or (samaana) of similar (janmaa)
age, who is also being (shiṣhyaḥ) trained (karmaṇi) in the performance (yajña) of the 
yajña (vaa) and (adhyaapayan) is acting as a teacher’s apprentice, (arhati) deserves the 
same (maanam) respect (guruvat) as the teacher. 2:208

209. utsaadanañ cha gaatraaṇaan snaapanochchhiṣhṭabhojane,
na kuryaad guruputrasya paadayoshchaavanejanam.
utsaadanam cha gaatraaṇaam snaapana-uchchhiṣhṭa-bhojane,
na kuryaat guru-putrasya paadayoḥ cha avanejanam.
Even though the teacher’s child should be respected as the teacher himself/herself, one 
(kuryaat) should (na) not (utsaadanam) massage (gaatraaṇaam) the body of (guru) the 
teacher’s (putrasya) child (cha) or (snaapana) bathe him/her or offer him/her (bhojane)
the food obtained by begging and (uchchhiṣhṭa) consume the remainder (cha) or 
(avanejanam) wash his/her (paadayoḥ) feet. 2:209

210. guruvatpratipoojyaaḥ syuḥ savarṇaa guruyoṣhitaḥ,
asavarṇaastu sampoojyaaḥ pratyutthaanaabhivaadanaiḥ. guruvat prati-poojyaaḥ syuḥ savarṇaaḥ guru-yoṣhitaḥ,
asavarṇaaḥ tu sam-poojyaaḥ pratyutthaana abhivaadanaiḥ.
(yoṣhitaḥ) The spouses of (guru) the teacher, (savarṇaaḥ) who belong to the equivalent 
class (syuḥ) should be (prati)(poojyaaḥ) respected (guruvat) similar to the teacher 
himself/herself. (tu) However, it is sufficient, (sam)(poojyaaḥ) as a sign of respect, 
(pratyutthaana) to get up and (abhivaadanaiḥ) greet the spouses that are (asavarṇaaḥ)
not from the same class. 2:210

211. abhyañjanan snaapanañ cha gaatrotsaadanameva cha,
gurupatnyaa na kaaryaaṇi keshaanaañ cha prasaadhanam. abhi-añjanam snaapanam cha gaatra-utsaadanam eva cha,
guru-patnyaa na kaaryaaṇi keshaanaam cha prasaadhanam.
One (na)(kaaryaaṇi)should refrain from applying (abhi)(añjanam) ointment on the body 
of (guru) the teacher’s (patnyaa) spouse (cha) or (snaapanam) bathing him/her (cha) or 
(utsaadanam) massaging his/her (gaatra) body (eva) as well (cha) or (prasaadhanam)
taking care of his/her (keshaanaam) hairs. 2:211
Three types of goals - righteousness, wealth and fulfillment of desires
The 224th shloka shloka out of context talks about choice between three kinds of goals. 
Maharṣhi Manu, though a proponent of a balance between the three, has elsewhere 
clearly favored righteousness over the other two in case of a conflict.
धमार्थार्व
ु
च्यतेश्रेयः कामाथ  धमर्एव च ।
अथर्एवेह वा श्रेयि वगर्इित त
ु
िस्थितः ॥२२४॥
धमार्थ  ।उच्यते। श्रेयः । कामाथ  । धमर्ः । एव । च ॥ अथर्ः ।एव । इह। वा । श्रेयः । ित्रवगर्ः । इित । तु। िस्थितः ॥
224. dharmaarthaavuchyate shreyaḥ kaamaarthau dharma eva cha,
artha eveha vaa shreyastrivarga iti tu sthitiḥ. dharma-arthau uchyate shreyaḥ kaama-arthau dharmaḥ eva cha,
arthaḥ eva iha vaa shreyaḥ trivargaḥ iti tu sthitiḥ.
(iha) In this world, some (uchyate) say that pursuit of (dharma) righteousness and 
(arthau) wealth is (shreyaḥ) the best use of one's life, some others follow the pursuit of 
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 2
255
(arthau) wealth and (kaama) fulfillment of desires (cha) and some others think that just 
pursuit of (arthaḥ) wealth (eva) only (vaa) or of (dharmaḥ) righteousness (eva) only is 
(shreyaḥ) the best; (iti) this is (tu) the real (sthitiḥ) situation of (trivargaḥ) these three 
goals. Maintaining a balance in all three of them is extremely difficult. 2:224
Respect for teacher, mother, father, brother and elders
The 225th – 226th shlokas are out of context and provide metaphorical equivalents for 
different individuals. The current context is the student life in which one is not supposed 
to have any interaction with the family members.

225. aachaaryo brahmaṇo moortiḥ pitaa moortiḥ prajaapateḥ,
maataa pṛithivyaa moortistu bhraataa svo moortiraatmanaḥ. aachaaryaḥ brahmaṇaḥ moortiḥ pitaa moortiḥ prajaapateḥ,
maataa pṛithivyaaḥ moortiḥ tu bhraataa svaḥ moortiḥ aatmanaḥ.
(aachaaryaḥ) The teacher is the living (moortiḥ) image (brahmaṇaḥ) of the grantor of 
the Vedas; (pitaa) the father is the living (moortiḥ) image (prajaapateḥ) of the sustainer 
of masses; (maataa) the mother is the living (moortiḥ) image (pṛithivyaaḥ) of Mother 
Earth (tu) and (bhraataa) the brother is (aatmanaḥ) one’s (svaḥ) own (moortiḥ) image.

226. aachaaryashcha pitaa chaiva maataa bhraataa cha poorvajaḥ,

na aartena api avamantavyaaḥ braahmaṇena visheṣhataḥ.
(api) Even (aartena) out of anger or pain, one (na) should not (avamantavyaaḥ) show 
disrespect towards (aachaaryaḥ) the teacher, (pitaa) the father, (maataa) the mother, 
(bhraataa) a sibling (cha) or (poorvajaḥ) an elder (eva) as well (cha) and (visheṣhataḥ)
especially (braahmaṇena) towards a braahmaṇa. 2:226
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 2

Repaying the debts of the teacher and the parents
The 227th – 237th shlokas are out of context for the student phase. These also contain 
exaggerated statements, ignoring the fact that elders should be in renunciation in the 
later half of their life. It is not impossible to repay the debt of the teachers and parents. 
It is easily repaid by passing on the teachings and values to the next generation.
यंमातािपतरौ क्लेशंसहेतेसम्भवेनणाम
ॄ ्
।
न तस्य िनष्क
ृ
ितः शक्या कत 
ु
वषर्शतैरिप ॥२२७॥
यम्। मातािपतरौ । क्लेशम्। सहेते। सम्भवे।नणाम
ॄ ्॥ न। तस्य । िनष्कृितः । शक्या । कतर्मु्। वषर्शतैः । अिप ॥
227. yam maataapitarau kleshan sahete sambhave nṛeeṇaam,
na tasya niṣhkṛitiḥ shakyaa kartum varṣhashatairapi. yam maataa-pitarau klesham sahete sambhave nṛeeṇaam,
na tasya niṣhkṛitiḥ shakyaa kartum varṣha-shataiḥ api.
(yam) Those (klesham) pains and troubles that (maataa) the mother and (pitarau) the 
father (sahete) endure during (sambhave) rearing (nṛeeṇaam) the children, (tasya) their 
(niṣhkṛitiḥ) repayment (shakyaa) can (na) not (kartum) be done (api) even (shataiḥ) in 
one hundred (varṣha) years. 2:227

तपः सव समाप्यते॥२२८॥
तयोः । िनत्यम्। िप्रयम्। कुयार्त्। आचायर्स्य । च । सवर्दा ॥ तेषु। एव । ित्रषु। त ेषु ु। तपः । सवर्म्। समाप्यते॥
228. tayornityam priyaṅ kuryaadaachaaryasya cha sarvadaa,
teṣhveva triṣhu tuṣhṭeṣhu tapaḥ sarvan samaapyate. tayoḥ nityam priyam kuryaat aachaaryasya cha sarvadaa,
teṣhu eva triṣhu tuṣhṭeṣhu tapaḥ sarvam samaapyate.
One should (nityam) everyday and (sarvadaa) always (kuryaat) perform deeds that 
(priyam) please (tayoḥ) both of the parents (cha) and (aachaaryasya) the teachers (eva)
as well, because when (triṣhu) three (teṣhu) of them (tuṣhṭeṣhu) are pleased, (sarvam)
all of (tapaḥ) the penance (samaapyate) is done. Once the householders are blessed 
with the children, their parents should leave the house and enter the vaanaprastha
stage i.e. preparation of the detachment by staying in the forest. 2:228

229. teṣhaan trayaaṇaañ shushrooṣhaa paraman tapa uchyate,

मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 2
257
teṣhaam trayaaṇaam shushrooṣhaa paramam tapaḥ uchyate,
na taiḥ an-abhyanujñaataḥ dharmam anyam samaacharet.
(shushrooṣhaa) The service (teṣhaam) of these (trayaaṇaam) three (uchyate) is said to 
be (paramam) the ultimate (tapaḥ) penance and one (na) should not (sam)(aacharet)
engage in any (anyam) other (dharmam) activity (an) without (taiḥ) their 
(abhyanujñaataḥ) permission. 2:229
त एव िह त्रयो लोकास्त एव त्रय आश्रमाः ।
त एव िह त्रयो वेदास्त एवो ा योऽग्नयः ॥२३०॥
ते। एव । िह ।त्रयः । लोकाः । ते। एव ।त्रयः । आश्रमाः ॥
ते। एव । िह ।त्रयः । वेदाः । ते। एव ।उ ाः ।त्रयः । अग्नयः ॥
230. ta eva hi trayo lokaasta eva traya aashramaaḥ,
ta eva hi trayo vedaasta evoktaastrayo’gnayaḥ. te eva hi trayaḥ lokaaḥ te eva trayaḥ aashramaaḥ,
te eva hi trayaḥ vedaaḥ te eva uktaaḥ trayaḥ agnayaḥ.
For everyone, (te) they are (eva)(hi) indeed (trayaḥ) the three (lokaaḥ) regions of 
existence, the mother is the earth region, the father is the sky and the teacher is the 
illuminated celestial world; (te) they are (trayaḥ) the three (aashramaaḥ) stages of life 
(eva) as well, the mother represents the student phase, the father represents the 
householder phase and the teacher represents the renunciation phase; (te) they are (hi)
indeed (trayaḥ) the three (vedaaḥ) types of knowledge (eva) as well, the mother 
represents the knowledge of God, the father represents the knowledge of action and 
duties and the teacher represents the knowledge of facts; and (te) they are (uktaaḥ)said 
to be (trayaḥ) the three main (agnayaḥ) types of fires (eva) as well, 2:230

231. pitaa vai gaarhapatyo’gnirmaataa’gnirdakṣhiṇaḥ smṛitaḥ,
gururaahavaneeyastu saa’gnitretaa gareeyasee. pitaa vai gaarhapatyaḥ agniḥ maataa agniḥ dakṣhiṇaḥ smṛitaḥ,
guruḥ aahavaneeyaḥ tu saa agni-tretaa gareeyasee.
(pitaa) The father is the main (agniḥ) fire (gaarhapatyaḥ) sustaining the household (vai)
indeed, (maataa) the mother (smṛitaḥ) is said to be (agniḥ) the fire (dakṣhiṇaḥ) in the 
southern direction that sustains the guests etc. (tu) and (guruḥ) the teacher is the fire 
of the yajña (aahavaneeyaḥ) meant for oblations. (saa) The group of these (tretaa) three

(agni) fires (gareeyasee) is the supreme. There are five types of fires. The remaining two 
are sabhyaa and aavasadhyaa.

232. triṣhvapramaadyanneteṣhu treenllokaanvijayedgṛihee,

(gṛihee) A householder, who (svavapuṣhaa) himself/herself serves (eteṣhu)these (triṣhu)
three (apramaadyan) without any carelessness, he/she (vijayet) wins over (treen) the 
three (lokaan) regions of existence, (modate) attains happiness and (deepyamaanaḥ)
shines (devavat) like the celestial bodies shine (divi) in the celestial world. 2:232

233. iman lokam maatṛibhaktyaa pitṛibhaktyaa tu madhyamam, 
gurushushrooṣhayaa tvevam brahmalokan samashnute. imam lokam maatṛi-bhaktyaa pitṛi-bhaktyaa tu madhyamam,

(bhaktyaa) Devotion towards (maatṛi) the mother is like winning over (imam) this 
(lokam) region i.e. the earth; (tu) and (bhaktyaa) devotion towards (pitṛi) the father is 
like winning over (madhyamam) the middle region i.e. the sky; (tu)(evam) and 
(shushrooṣhayaa) serving (guru) the teacher is like (sam)(ashnute) winning over 
(brahma)(lokam) the heavens. 2:233
सव तस्या ता धमार्यस्यैतेत्रय आ ताः ।

234. sarve tasyaadṛitaa dharmaa yasyaite traya aadṛitaaḥ, 
anaadṛitaastu yasyaite sarvaastasyaaphalaaḥ kriyaaḥ. sarve tasya aadṛitaaḥ dharmaaḥ yasya ete trayaḥ aadṛitaaḥ, 
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 2
259
anaadṛitaaḥ tu yasya ete sarvaaḥ tasya aphalaaḥ kriyaaḥ.
(yasya) Whosoever (aadṛitaaḥ) maintains respect (ete) for these (trayaḥ) three, he/she 
is deemed (aadṛitaaḥ) to have respected and fulfilled (sarve) all of (tasya) his/her 
(dharmaaḥ) duties (tu) and those (yasya) who (anaadṛitaaḥ) disrespect (ete)these three, 
(sarvaaḥ) all of (tasya) their (kriyaaḥ) efforts are (aphalaaḥ) fruitless. 2:234

235. yaavattrayaste jeeveyustaavannaanyan samaacharet,
teṣhveva nityañ shushrooṣhaaṅ kuryaatpriyahite rataḥ. yaavat trayaḥ te jeeveyuḥ taavat na anyam sam-aacharet,
teṣhu eva nityam shushrooṣhaam kuryaat priya-hite rataḥ.
(yaavat) When (te) these (trayaḥ) three (jeeveyuḥ) are alive, (taavat) until that time one 
(sam)(aacharet) should focus on (na) nothing (anyam) else except them. One should be 
(rataḥ) engrossed into activities that they (priya) like and that (hite) benefit them (eva)
as well and (kuryaat) should perform (teṣhu) their (shushrooṣhaam) service (nityam)
everyday. 2:235
तेषामन
ु
परोधेन पार यंयद्यदाचरेत्
। त िन्नवेदये ेभ्यो मनोवचनकमर्िभः ॥२३६॥
तेषाम्। अनपरोधेन ु । पार यम्। यतऽयत ् ्। आचरेत्॥ ततऽतत ् ्। िनवेदयेत्। तेभ्यः । मनोवचनकमर्िभः ॥
236. teṣhaamanuparodhena paaratryañ yadyadaacharet,
tattannivedayettebhyo manovachanakarmabhiḥ. teṣhaam anuparodhena paaratryam yat yat aacharet,
tat tat nivedayet tebhyaḥ mano-vachana-karmabhiḥ.
With (teṣhaam) their (anuparodhena) permission, (yat)(yat) whatever actions and 
interactions (aacharet) are undertaken (paaratryam) in the World, utilizing one’s (mano)
mind, (vachana) speech and other (karmabhiḥ) faculties, (tat)(tat) those actions and 
interactions (nivedayet) should be conveyed (tebhyaḥ) to them. 2:236

237. triṣhveteṣhvitikṛityaṅ hi puruṣhasya samaapyate,
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय २ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 2
260
eṣha dharmaḥ paraḥ saakṣhaadupadharmo’nya uchyate. triṣhu eteṣhu iti kṛityam hi puruṣhasya samaapyate,
eṣhaḥ dharmaḥ paraḥ saakṣhaat upadharmaḥ anyaḥ uchyate.
(hi) By serving (eteṣhu) these (triṣhu) three, (puruṣhasya) one’s (iti) assigned (kṛityam)
duties (samaapyate) are completely fulfilled. (eṣhaḥ) This is (paraḥ) the ultimate 
(dharmaḥ) responsibility (saakṣhaat) here and every (anyaḥ) other duty (uchyate) is said 
to be (upadharmaḥ) secondary. 2:237
The 244th shloka exaggerates by declaring just one action to result in nirvaṇa. Maharṣhi 
Manu attributes nirvaṇa to be the result of all actions over multiple lives.

ू । ग मु ्॥ सः । गच्छित । अञ्जसा । िवप्रः । ब्र णः । सद्म । शा तम्॥
244. aa samaapteḥ shareerasya yastu shushrooṣhate gurum,
sa gachchhatyañjasaa vipro brahmaṇaḥ sadma shaashvatam. aa samaapteḥ shareerasya yaḥ tu shushrooṣhate gurum,
saḥ gachchhati añjasaa vipraḥ brahmaṇaḥ sadma shaashvatam.
One (yaḥ) who (shushrooṣhate) serves (gurum) the teacher (aa) until (samaapteḥ) the 
end (shareerasya) of his/her body i.e. death, (saḥ) that (vipraḥ) scholar (tu) indeed 
(añjasaa) quickly (gachchhati) attains a place (brahmaṇaḥ) in God's (sadma) abode 
(shaashvatam) forever. 2:244
Gifts for the teacher’s family in case of his/her death
The 247th - 248th shlokas bind one to a particular guru and his/her family in case of guru’s 
death. Though the idea of taking care of guru’s family upon his/her death is noble, 
however, Maharṣhi Manu advises to learn from several teachers. Hence tying oneself to 
one guru’s family or to a certain conduct is not logical.

247. aachaarye tu khalu prete guruputre guṇaanvite,
gurudaare sapiṇḍe vaa guruvad vṛittimaacharet. aachaarye tu khalu prete guru-putre guṇaanvite,
guru-daare sapiṇḍe vaa guruvat vṛittim aacharet.
(khalu) In case (aachaarye) the teacher (prete) dies before receiving gifts, (tu) then the 
student should (vṛittim) bestow the gifts (guṇaanvite) to a qualified (putre) child (guru)

for the teacher. 2:247

248. eteṣhvavidyaamaaneṣhu snaanaasanavihaaravaan,
prayuñjaano’gnishushrooṣhaan saadhayeddehamaatmanaḥ. eteṣhu avidyaamaaneṣhu snaana-aasana-vihaaravaan,

If (eteṣhu) any of these (avidyaamaaneṣhu) are not available then the student should 
routinely (saadhayet) tame his/her (aatmanaḥ) own (deham) body by (snaana) bathing, 
(aasana) sitting in meditation (vihaaravaan) in a secluded place and (prayuñjaanaḥ)
diligently (shushrooṣhaan) serve (agni) the fire i.e. perform yajña. 2:248
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ३ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 3

Extensions in Chapter 3
Women not fit for marriage
The 11th – 19th shlokas interrupt the flow by going back to disqualification criteria while 
Maharṣhi Manu has already moved on to the desirable traits. These shlokas also seem to 
suggest that there is nothing wrong with having multiple wives. There is an inherent 
contradiction between shlokas 12th-13th and 14th-19th, the prior set suggesting a marriage 
between a braahmaṇa and a shoodra and later forbidding it. All of these ideas are in 
contradiction with Maharṣhi Manu’s main discourse.
यस्यास्त
ु
न भवेद
्
भ्राता न िव ायेत वा िपता ।
नोपयच्छेत तांप्रा ः प
ु
ित्रकाधमर्शङ
्
कया ॥११॥
यस्याः । तु। न। भवेत्। भ्राता । न। िव ायेत । वा । िपता ॥ न। उपयच्छेत । ताम्। प्रा ः । पित्रकाधमर्शङ ु ्कया ॥
11. yasyaastu na bhaved bhraataa na vijñaayeta vaa pitaa,
nopayachchheta taam praajñaḥ putrikaadharmashaṅkayaa. yasyaaḥ tu na bhavet bhraataa na vijñaayeta vaa pitaa,
na upayachchheta taam praajñaḥ putrikaa-dharma-shaṅkayaa.
One (yasyaaḥ) who (na) does not (bhavet) have (bhraataa) a brother (vaa) or the one 
where there is (na) no (vijñaayeta) knowledge of his/her (pitaa) father (tu) and the one 
where there is (shaṅkayaa) a doubt that (putrikaa)(dharma) the first son would need to 
be given to the maternal grandparents for adoption because they did not have a male 
child, (praajñaḥ) the wise (na) do not (upayachchheta) marry (taam) such a person. 3:11

ु। क्रमशः । अवराः ॥
12. savarṇaa’gre dvijaateenaam prashastaa daarakarmaṇi,
kaamatastu pravṛittaanaamimaaḥ syuḥ kramasho’varaaḥ. savarṇaa agre dvijaateenaam prashastaa daara-karmaṇi,
kaamataḥ tu pravṛittaanaam imaaḥ syuḥ kramashaḥ avaraaḥ.
(dvijaateenaam) For the twice born it is (prashastaa) best to (agre) first (daara)(karmaṇi)
marry a person (savarṇaa) from the same class, (tu) however, (pravṛittaanaam) when 
overtaken by (kaamataḥ) lust (imaaḥ) they (syuḥ) can also choose spouses (avaraaḥ)
from the lower classes (kramashaḥ) in the following order. 3:12

13. shoodraiva bhaaryaa shoodrasya saa cha svaa cha vishaḥ smṛite,
te cha svaa chaiva raajñashcha taashcha svaa chaagrajanmanaḥ. shoodraa eva bhaaryaa shoodrasya saa cha svaa cha vishaḥ smṛite,
te cha svaa cha eva raajñaḥ cha taaḥ cha svaa cha agra-janmanaḥ.
(shoodrasya) A shoodra’s (bhaaryaa) wife can (eva) only be (shoodraa) from the shoodra
class; (cha) and (smṛite) it is said that (vishaḥ) for the vaishya it can be (saa) her i.e. a 
shoodra (cha) and the one (svaa) from their own class i.e. a vaishya; (cha) and (raajñaḥ)
for a kṣhatriya the wife can be from (te) both the shoodra (cha) and the vaishya classes
(eva) as well as the one (svaa) from their own class i.e. a kṣhatriya; (cha) and finally 
(agra)(janmanaḥ) for a first-born i.e. a braahmaṇa it can be all of (taaḥ) them (cha) and 
the one (svaa) from their own class as well. 3:13

14. na braahmaṇakṣhatriyayoraapadyapi hi tiṣhṭhatoḥ,

(kasmiñshchit) Whatever (api) may be (vṛittaante) the circumstances, (api) even (hi) if 
(tiṣhṭhatoḥ) they are (aapadi) desperate, it is (na) not (upadishyate) recommended that 
(braahmaṇa) the braahmaṇa and (kṣhatriyayoḥ) the kṣhatriya take (shoodraa) a 
shoodra as their (bhaaryaa) wife. 3:14

At times (mohaat) under the influence of lust, (dvijaatayaḥ) the twice borns 
(udvahantaḥ) marry (striyam) a woman from (heena) the lower (jaati) class and (aashu)

16. shoodraavedee patatyatrerutathyatanayasya cha,
shaunakasya sutotpattyaa tadapatyatayaa bhṛigoḥ. shoodraa-vedee patati atreḥ utathya-tanayasya cha,
shaunakasya suta-utpattyaa tat apatyatayaa bhṛigoḥ.
In the opinion (atreḥ) of sage Atri (cha) and of (utathya) sage Utathya’s (tanayasya) son 
Gautama, a twice born (patati) falls from grace (vedee) on marrying (shoodraa) a 
shoodra; (shaunakasya) as per sage Shaunaka, one falls from grace when he gets (suta)
a son (utpattyaa) delivered by a shoodra; and (bhṛigoḥ) according to sage Bhṛigu, one 
falls from grace even (tat) when (apatyatayaa) a grandson is born from a shoodra. 3:16

17. shoodraañ shayanamaaropya braahmaṇo yaatyadhogatim,

(aaropya) Just by (shayanam) sleeping with (shoodraam) a shoodra woman, 
(braahmaṇaḥ) a braahmaṇa (yaati) begets (adho)(gatim) a fall from grace and 
(janayitvaa) by producing (sutam) a child (tasyaam) with her, he (heeyate) loses his 
(braahmaṇyaat) braahmaṇa stature (eva) altogether. 3:17

18. daivapitryaatitheyaani tatpradhaanaani yasya tu,

(tu) And in (yasya) whose home, (daiva) the divinities, (pitrya) elders and (atitheyaani)
guests are cared for under (tat) her (pradhaanaani)supervision i.e. of a shoodra woman, 
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ३ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 3
265
these (devaaḥ) divinities and (pitṛi) elders (na) do not (ashnanti) partake in (tat) these 
offerings (cha) and (saḥ) that person (na) does not (gachchhati) go (svargam) to heaven.

19. vṛiṣhaleephenapeetasya niḥshvaasopahatasya cha,
tasyaañ chaiva prasootasya niṣhkṛitirna vidheeyate. vṛiṣhalee-phena-peetasya niḥshvaasa-upahatasya cha,
tasyaam cha eva prasootasya niṣhkṛitiḥ na vidheeyate.
One who (peetasya) has tasted (phena) the saliva of (vṛiṣhalee) a shoodra woman (cha)
and (upahatasya) has felt her (niḥshvaasa) breath on his face (cha) and the one who 
(prasootasya) is born from (tasyaam) that woman (eva) as well, there exists (na) no 
(vidheeyate) procedure for their (niṣhkṛitiḥ) atonement. 3:19
Marriage rites for different classes
The 22nd - 26th shlokas interrupt the flow and start going into the suitability of different 
types of rites without first describing them. They also present conflicting ideas and hence 
were most likely added by different individuals at different times.
यो यस्य धम्य  वणर्स्य ग
ु
णदोषौ च यस्य यौ ।
तद्वः सव प्रव यािम प्रसवेच ग
ु
णाग
ु
णान
्
॥२२॥
यः । यस्य । धम्यर्ः । वणर्स्य । गणदोषौ

22. yo yasya dharmyo varṇasya guṇadoṣhau cha yasya yau,
tadvaḥ sarvam pravakṣhyaami prasave cha guṇaaguṇaan. yaḥ yasya dharmyaḥ varṇasya guṇa-doṣhau cha yasya yau,
tat vaḥ sarvam pravakṣhyaami prasave cha guṇa-aguṇaan.
(yaḥ) What are (dharmyaḥ) the proper types of marriage rites (yasya) for any (varṇasya)
particular class, (yau) what are (yasya) their (guṇa) benefits (cha) and (doṣhau) issues, 
(cha) and what are (guṇa) the benefits and (aguṇaan) the problems (prasave) of 
reproducing in each of them, I shall now (pravakṣhyaami) recite (sarvam) all of (tat)
them (vaḥ) for your benefit. 3:22

23. ṣhaḍaanupoorvyaa viprasya kṣhatrasya chaturo’varaan,
viṭshoodrayostu taaneva vidyaaddharmyaanaraakṣhasaan. ṣhaṭ aanupoorvyaa viprasya kṣhatrasya chaturaḥ avaraan,
viṭ shoodrayoḥ tu taan eva vidyaat dharmyaan araakṣhasaan.
(aanupoorvyaa) In the order they were mentioned, the first (ṣhaṭ) six are suitable 
(viprasya) for the braahmaṇa, (avaraan) the last (chaturaḥ) four are suitable 
(kṣhatrasya) for the kṣhatriya, and for (viṭ) the vaishya (tu) and (shoodrayoḥ) the
shoodra (vidyaat) consider (taan) the same last four (araakṣhasaan) except the demonic
rite (dharmyaan) as suitable rites (eva) as well. 3:23

24. chaturo braahmaṇasyaadyaan prashastaan kavayo viduḥ,
raakṣhasaṅ kṣhatriyasyaikamaasuram vaishyashoodrayoḥ. chaturaḥ braahmaṇasya aadyaan prashastaan kavayaḥ viduḥ,
raakṣhasam kṣhatriyasya ekam aasuram vaishya-shoodrayoḥ.
(kavayaḥ) As per the ones with deep knowledge, (aadyaan) the first (chaturaḥ) four 
(viduḥ) are considered (prashastaan) as the best (braahmaṇasya) for the braahmaṇa, 
(raakṣhasam) the demonic rite is (kṣhatriyasya) for the kṣhatriya and (ekam) only 
(aasuram) the discordant rite is for (vaishya) the vaishya and (shoodrayoḥ) the shoodra.

25. pañchaanaan tu trayo dharmyaa dvaavadharmyau smṛitaaviha,
paishaachashchaasurashchaiva na kartavyau kadaachana. pañchaanaam tu trayaḥ dharmyaaḥ dvau adharmyau smṛitau iha,
paishaachaḥ cha aasuraḥ cha eva na kartavyau kadaachana.
(iha) In this World, (tu) out of the last (pañchaanaam) five rites, (trayaḥ) three are 
considered (dharmyaaḥ) as righteous and (dvau) two (smṛitau) are considered 
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ३ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 3
267
(adharmyau) as sinful, hence (aasuraḥ) the discordant rite (cha) and (paishaachaḥ) the 
hateful rite (eva) as well should (na)(kadaachana) never (kartavyau) be engaged into.

26. pṛithak pṛithagvaa mishrau vaa vivaahau poorvachoditau,
gaandharvo raakṣhasashchaiva dharmyau kṣhatrasya tau smṛitau. pṛithak pṛithak vaa mishrau vaa vivaahau poorva-choditau,
gaandharvaḥ raakṣhasaḥ cha eva dharmyau kṣhatrasya tau smṛitau.
(tau) Both of (poorva) the previously (choditau) indicated (vivaahau) rites, i.e.
(gaandharvaḥ) the artistic (cha) and (raakṣhasaḥ) the demonic, whether conducted 
(pṛithak)(pṛithak) individually (vaa) or when (mishrau) mixed together (eva) as well, 
(smṛitau) are considered as (dharmyau) righteous (kṣhatrasya) for the kṣhatriya. 3:11
The 35th - 38th shlokas are interrupting the flow. The 34th shloka introduces a new 
procedure on top of the eight already described. The remaining shlokas illogically describe 
a person to relieve the sins of prior and forthcoming generations, which gives a free pass 
to the forthcoming generations to commit sins without any repercussions.
अिद्भरेव िद्वजा याणांकन्यादानंिविशष्यते।इतरेषांत
ु
वणार्नािमतरेतरकाम्यया ॥३५॥
अिद्भः । एव । िद्वजा याणाम्। कन्यादानम्। िविशष्यते॥ इतरेषाम्। तु। वणार्नाम्। इतरेतर । काम्यया ॥
35. adbhireva dvijaagryaaṇaaṅ kanyaadaanam vishiṣhyate,
itareṣhaan tu varṇaanaamitaretarakaamyayaa.
adbhiḥ eva dvijaagryaaṇaam kanyaa-daanam vishiṣhyate,
itareṣhaam tu varṇaanaam itaretara kaamyayaa.
It is (vishiṣhyate) best (eva) indeed to pledge after taking (adbhiḥ) water in the palm 
before (daanam) transferring the responsibility of (kanyaa) the bride to 
(dvijaagryaaṇaam) a braahmaṇa groom. (tu) However, (itareṣhaam) amongst the other 
(varṇaanaam) classes, (itaretara) just (kaamyayaa) an agreement without the use of 
water is sufficient. 3:35

36. yo yasyaiṣhaam vivaahaanaam manunaa keerttito guṇaḥ,
sarvañ shṛiṇuta tam vipraaḥ sarvaṅ keertayato mama. yaḥ yasya eṣhaam vivaahaanaam manunaa keerttitaḥ guṇaḥ, 
sarvam shṛiṇuta tam vipraaḥ sarvam keertayataḥ mama.
(vipraaḥ) O scholars! (eṣhaam) In these (vivaahaanaam) marriages, (yaḥ) whatever 
(guṇaḥ) qualities (keerttitaḥ) were explained (manunaa) by Maharṣhi Manu (yasya) for 
each one of them, (shṛiṇuta) listen to (sarvam) all of (tam) them (keertayataḥ) as recited 
(mama) by myself. 3:36

37. dasha poorvaanparaanvañshyaanaatmaanañ chaikaviñshakam,
braahmeeputraḥ sukṛitakṛinmochayedenasaḥ pitṛeen. dasha poorvaan paraan vañshyaan aatmaanam cha eka-viñshakam, 
braahmee-putraḥ sukṛitakṛit mochayet enasaḥ pitṛeen.
(sukṛitakṛit) A righteous (putraḥ) child born out of (braahmee) godly marriage
(mochayet) relieves (enasaḥ) the sins of (pitṛeen) the ancestors from (dasha) ten 
(poorvaan) prior (vañshyaan) generations, children from ten (paraan) forthcoming 
generations (cha) and the (viñshakam) twenty (eka) first, his/her (aatmaanam) own 
generation as well. 3:37

38. daivoḍhaajaḥ sutashchaiva sapta sapta paraavaraan,
aarṣhoḍhaajaḥ sutastreenstreenṣhaṭṣhaṭkaayoḍhaajaḥ sutaḥ. daivoḍhaajaḥ sutaḥ cha eva sapta sapta para-avaraan, 
aarṣhoḍhaajaḥ sutaḥ treen treen ṣhaṭ ṣhaṭ kaayoḍhaajaḥ sutaḥ.
Similarly (sutaḥ) the child (daivoḍhaajaḥ) born out of scholarly marriage, relieves from 
sins (sapta) the seven (para) prior and (sapta) the seven (avaraan) forthcoming 
generations(eva) as well; (sutaḥ) the child (aarṣhoḍhaajaḥ) born out of sagely marriage, 
relieves from sins (treen) the three prior and (treen) the three forthcoming generations; 
(cha) and (sutaḥ) the child (kaayoḍhaajaḥ) born out of arranged marriage, relieves from 
sins (ṣhaṭ) the six prior and (ṣhaṭ) the six forthcoming generations. 3:38

Holding hands and making promises during a marriage
The 43rd - 44th shlokas interrupt the flow. Maharṣhi Manu has not listed any classes while 
describing the eight types of marriages and the sudden reference to classes in these 
shlokas doesn’t appear proper. Additionally, the procedures mentioned in these shlokas 
can not be followed in all eight types of marriages.
पािणग्रहणसं
स्कारः सवणार्स
ू
पिदश्यते। असवणार्स्वयं ेयो िविध द्वाहकमर्िण ॥४३॥
पािणग्रहणसं
स्कारः । सवणार्सु। उपिदश्यते॥ असवणार्सु। अयम्।  ेयः । िविधः । उद्वाहकमर्िण ॥
43. paaṇigrahaṇasanskaaraḥ savarṇaasoopadishyate,
asavarṇaasvayañ jñeyo vidhirudvaahakarmaṇi. paaṇi-grahaṇa-sanskaaraḥ savarṇaasu upadishyate, 
asavarṇaasu ayam jñeyaḥ vidhiḥ udvaaha-karmaṇi.
(sanskaaraḥ) The procedure of the groom (grahaṇa) holding (paaṇi) the hand of the 
bride and making promises (udvaaha)(karmaṇi) during the marriage (upadishyate) is
said to be applicable only when the bride is (savarṇaasu) from the same class. When 
she is (asavarṇaasu) not from the same class, then (ayam) these (vidhiḥ) procedures 
(jñeyaḥ) should be considered. 3:43
शरः  ित्रयया ग्रा ः प्रतोदो वैश्यकन्यया ।
वसनस्य दशा ग्रा ा श
ू
द्रयोत्कृ वेदने॥४४॥
शरः ।  ित्रयया । ग्रा ः । प्रतोदः । वैश्यकन्यया ॥ वसनस्य । दशा । ग्रा ा । शद्रया
ू । उत्कृ वेदने॥
44. sharaḥ kṣhatriyayaa graahyaḥ pratodo vaishyakanyayaa,
vasanasya dashaa graahyaa shoodrayotkṛiṣhṭavedane. sharaḥ kṣhatriyayaa graahyaḥ pratodaḥ vaishya-kanyayaa, 
vasanasya dashaa graahyaa shoodrayaa utkṛiṣhṭa-vedane.
(vedane) During a marriage where the groom or the bride is from (utkṛiṣhṭa) a higher 
class, as applicable, he/she should (graahyaḥ) hold on to, (sharaḥ) an arrow that is there 
in (kṣhatriyayaa) a kṣhatriya bride’s/groom’s hand, (pratodaḥ) a whip that is there in 
(vaishya) a vaishya (kanyayaa) bride’s/groom’s hand or (dashaa)(graahyaa) to the 
corner of (shoodrayaa) a shoodra bride’s/groom’s (vasanasya) dress. 3:44
Improper activities
The 63rd - 66th shlokas interrupt the flow and present certain ideas related to vocations 
that are contrary to the Vedas and Maharṣhi Manu’s philosophy.
क
ुिववाहैः िक्रयालोपैव दानध्ययनेन च ।
क
ु
लान्यक

लतांयािन्त ब्रा णाितक्रमेण च ॥६३॥

270
कुिववाहैः । िक्रयालोपैः । वेदानध्ययनेन । च ॥ कुलािन । अकुलताम्। यािन्त । ब्रा णाितक्रमेण । च ॥
63. kuvivaahaiḥ kriyaalopairvedaanadhyayanena cha,
kulaanyakulataañ yaanti braahmaṇaatikrameṇa cha. kuvivaahaiḥ kriyaa-lopaiḥ veda-anadhyayanena cha, 
kulaani akulataam yaanti braahmaṇa-atikrameṇa cha.
(kuvivaahaiḥ) Due to engagement in criticized wedding practices, (lopaiḥ) due to the 
absence of (kriyaa) the yajña and other sacred performances from their lives, 
(anadhyayanena) due to not studying (veda) the Vedas (cha) and (atikrameṇa) due to 
showing disrespect towards (braahmaṇa) the braahmaṇa, (kulaani) families (yaanti)
beget (akulataam) the break-down of their values. 3:63

64. shilpena vyavahaareṇa shoodraapatyaishcha kevalaiḥ,
gobhirashvaishcha yaanaishcha kṛiṣhyaa raajopasevayaa. shilpena vyavahaareṇa shoodraa-apatyaiḥ cha kevalaiḥ, 
gobhiḥ ashvaiḥ cha yaanaiḥ cha kṛiṣhyaa raajaa-upasevayaa.
(vyavahaareṇa) Due to engagement in only (shilpena) artistic vocations, (apatyaiḥ) due 
to procreation (kevalaiḥ) only with (shoodraa) a shoodra woman, due to trading (gobhiḥ)

engagement in agriculture (cha) and (upasevayaa) due to serving (raajaa) the king,3:64

65. ayaajyayaajanaishchaiva naastikyena cha karmaṇaam,

(ayaajyayaajanaiḥ) due to getting the yajña performed by unworthy individuals (cha)
and (naastikyena) due to lack of faith in (karmaṇaam) righteousness, God and Vedas, 
(kulaani) the families (vinashyanti) perish (aashu) quickly (cha) and (eva) also the ones 
(yaani) that are (heenaani) without (mantrataḥ) the study of the Vedas. 3:65

66. mantratastu samṛiddhaani kulaanyalpadhanaanyapi,

(tu) On the contrary, (kulaani) the families (samṛiddhaani) fulfilled (mantrataḥ) with the 
study of the Vedas, (api) even if their (dhanaani) material wealth (alpa) is limited, 
(gachchhanti) are (saṅkhyaam) counted alongside (kula) the families with special status 
(cha) and (karṣhanti) attract (mahat) a lot of (yashaḥ) fame. 3:66
Feeding a scholar in lieu of the elders
The 83rd shloka justifies feeding a braahmaṇa in lieu of feeding the elders and also 
absolves one of responsibility towards the other yajña.
एकमप्याशयेिद्वप्रंिपत्रथ पाञ्चयि के।
न चैवात्राशयेित्किञ्चद्वै देवंप्रितिद्वजम्
॥८३॥
एकम्। अिप । आशयेत्। िवप्रम्। िपत्रथ । पाञ्चयि के॥
न। च । एव । अत्र । आशयेत्। िकिञ्चत्। वै देवम्। प्रित । िद्वजम्॥
83. ekamapyaashayedvipram pitrarthe paañchayajñike,
na chaivaatraashayetkiñchidvaishvadevam prati dvijam. ekam api aashayet vipram pitrarthe paañcha-yajñike, 
na cha eva atra aashayet kiñchit vaishva-devam prati dvijam.
(paañcha) Out of the five daily (yajñike) yajña, the requirement (pitrarthe) for serving 
the elders can be satisfied (aashayet) by finding and feeding (api) just (ekam) one 
(vipram) scholar (cha) and (eva) after (atra) that the householder (na) does not need 
(aashayet) to feed (kiñchit) another (dvijam) braahmaṇa (prati) for (vaishva)(devam)
satisfying the requirement of sacrificing food for other beings. 3:83
Outcome of the Balivaishvadeva yajña
The 93rd shloka interrupts the flow and declares salvation to be the result of just one 
action i.e. the performance of sacrifices.

93. evañ yaḥ sarvabhootaani braahmaṇo nityamarchati,
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ३ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 3
272
sa gachchhati paran sthaanan tejomoorti patharjunaa. evam yaḥ sarva-bhootaani braahmaṇaḥ nityam archati, 
saḥ gachchhati param sthaanam tejaḥ-moortiḥ pathaa ṛijunaa.
(braahmaṇaḥ) The twice born (yaḥ) who (nityam) always (archati) serves (sarva) all 
(bhootaani) beings (evam) like this, (saḥ) he/she is (moortiḥ) the image of (tejaḥ)
fortitude and following this (ṛijunaa)straightforward (pathaa) path, he/she (gachchhati)
attains (param) the highest (sthaanam) place i.e. mokṣha. 3:93
Result of making donations
The 95th - 98th shlokas interrupt the flow of information on the procedures related to the 
five duties. They also appear to assign the braahmaṇa class to individual by birth instead 
on one’s qualification and intellectual capacity.

95. yatpuṇyaphalamaapnoti gaan datvaa vidhivadguroḥ,
tatpuṇyaphalamaapnoti bhikṣhaan datvaa dvijo gṛihee. yat puṇya-phalam aapnoti gaam datvaa vidhivat guroḥ,

(puṇya)(phalam) The virtue (yat) that one (aapnoti) gets by (vidhivat) properly (datvaa)
giving (gaam) a cow to his/her (guroḥ) guru, (dvijaḥ) a twice born (gṛihee) householder 
(aapnoti) gets (tat) that same (puṇya)(phalam) virtue just by (datvaa) giving (bhikṣhaam)
alms. 3:95

96. bhikṣhaamapyudapaatram vaa satkṛitya vidhipoorvakam,

A householder should (vidhi)(poorvakam) properly (satkṛitya) welcome (viduṣhe) a 
scholar who is an expert in the field of (veda) Vedic (tattva)(artha) wisdom and

(vaa) or (uda) water (paatram) container (api) as well. 3:96

97. nashayanti havyakavyaani naraaṇaamavijaanataam,
bhasmeebhooteṣhu vipreṣhu mohaaddattaani daatṛibhiḥ. nashayanti havya-kavyaani naraaṇaam avijaanataam, 
bhasmee-bhooteṣhu vipreṣhu mohaat dattaani daatṛibhiḥ.
When (mohaat) out of ignorance, (dattaani) donations are made, (daatṛibhiḥ) by donors, 
(vipreṣhu) to braahmaṇa whose (bhooteṣhu) intellect has been (bhasmee) destroyed, 
then those donations, made either (havya) towards a divinity or (kavyaani) for an 
ancestor, (nashayanti) are of no avail to those (avijaanataam) ignorant (naraaṇaam)
humans. 3:97

98. vidyaatapaḥ samṛiddheṣhu hutam vipramukhaagniṣhu,
nistaarayati durgaachcha mahatashchaiva kilviṣhaat. vidyaa-tapaḥ samṛiddheṣhu hutam vipra-mukha-agniṣhu, 
nistaarayati durgaat cha mahataḥ cha eva kilviṣhaat.
On the contrary, when donations are made, (samṛiddheṣhu) to a prosperous (vipra)
braahmaṇa whose (mukha) face radiates with (agniṣhu) the fire of (vidyaa) knowledge 
(cha) and (tapaḥ) fortitude, they are considered as (hutam) offerings to divinities and 
(nistaarayati)relieves one from (mahataḥ) grave (durgaat)sorrows (cha) and (kilviṣhaat)
sins (eva) as well. 3:98
Treating a Braahmaṇa guest
The 100th shloka interrupts the flow and also attributes just one error to the loss of all 
virtues.

100. shilaanapyuñchhato nityam pañchaagneenapi juhvataḥ,
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ३ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 3

sarvan sukṛitamaadatte braahmaṇo’narchito vasan. shilaan api uñchhataḥ nityam pañcha-agneen api juhvataḥ,

One who survives by foraging for (uñchhataḥ) the remaining (shilaan) grains from an 
harvested field i.e. considers everyone else before oneself and (api) also (nityam)
regularly performs (juhvataḥ) offerings in all (pañcha) five (agneen) types of fires, 
however errs by (anarchitaḥ) not attending to (braahmaṇaḥ) a braahmaṇa visiting 
his/her (vasan) house, (sarvam) all of his/her (sukṛitam) virtue (aadatte) are taken away.
3:100
Treating a non-Braahmaṇa guest
The 110th - 112th shlokas interrupt the flow between 109th and 113th shlokas. The idea of 
qualifying guests with their class is not in harmony with Maharṣhi Manu’s general 
philosophy.
न ब्रा णस्य त्वितिथगर्हेृ
राजन्य उच्यते।

ू । सखा । च ।एव ।  ातयः । ग ः

110. na braahmaṇasya tvatithirgṛihe raajanya uchyate, 
vaishyashoodrau sakhaa chaiva jñaatayo gurureva cha. na braahmaṇasya tu atithiḥ gṛihe raajanyaḥ uchyate, 
vaishya-shoodrau sakhaa cha eva jñaatayaḥ guruḥ eva cha. 
(tu) If (raajanyaḥ) the kṣhatriya, (vaishya) the vaishya, (shoodrau) the shoodra, (sakhaa)
friends (cha) and (jñaatayaḥ) relatives (cha) and (eva) even (guruḥ) the teacher visit 
(gṛihe) the house (braahmaṇasya) of a braahmaṇa, they (na) do not qualify (uchyate) to 
be called (atithiḥ) guests. 3:110

111. yadi tvatithidharmeṇa kṣhatriyo gṛihamaavrajet, 
bhuktavatsooktavipreṣhu kaamam tamapi bhojayet. yadi tu atithi-dharmeṇa kṣhatriyaḥ gṛiham aavrajet, 
bhuktavatsu uktaḥ vipreṣhu kaamam tam api bhojayet. 
And (yadi) if (kṣhatriyaḥ) a kṣhatriya (aavrajet) shows up (atithi)(dharmeṇa) as a guest 
(gṛiham) at the home of a braahmaṇa, (tu) then after the (uktaḥ)(vipreṣhu) braahmaṇa 
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ३ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 3
275
guests (bhuktavatsu) have been fed, (tam) he/she i.e. the kṣhatriya (bhojayet)should be 
fed (api) as well (kaamam) as desired. 3:111

112. vaishyashoodraavapi praaptau kuṭumbe’tithidharmiṇau,
bhojayetsaha bhṛityaistaavaanṛishansyam prayojayan. vaishya-shoodrau api praaptau kuṭumbe atithi-dharmiṇau,

If (vaishya) a vaishya or (shoodrau) a shoodra (praaptau) come (dharmiṇau) as (atithi)
guests (kuṭumbe) to the home of a braahmaṇa (api) as well, (prayojayan) treating (tau)
both of them (aanṛishansyam) humanly, he/she (bhojayet) should feed them (saha)
along with (bhṛityaiḥ) the servants. 3:112
Consuming before feeding the guests
The 115th shloka discusses the consequences of eating before the guests have been fed, 
even before discussing the proper time for the hosts to consume the food.
अद वा त
ु
य एतेभ्यः प
ू
व भ
ु
ङ
् े ऽिवच णः ।
स भ
ु
ञ्जानो न जानाित  ग
ृ
ध्रैजर्िग्धमात्मनः ॥११५॥
अद वा । तु। यः ।एतेभ्यः । पवर्मू ्। भङु् े। अिवच णः॥
सः । भञ्जानः
ु । न। जानाित ।  गध्रैः ृ । जिग्धम्। आत्मनः ॥
115. adattvaa tu ya etebhyaḥ poorvam bhuṅkte’vichakṣhaṇaḥ,
sa bhuñjaano na jaanaati shvagṛidhrairjagdhimaatmanaḥ. adattvaa tu yaḥ etebhyaḥ poorvam bhuṅkte avichakṣhaṇaḥ, 
saḥ bhuñjaanaḥ na jaanaati shva-gṛidhraiḥ jagdhim aatmanaḥ.
(avichakṣhaṇaḥ) The ignorant (yaḥ) who (bhuṅkte) consumes (poorvam) before 
(adattvaa) giving food (etebhyaḥ) to these individuals first, (bhuñjaanaḥ) while 
consuming (saḥ) he/she (na) does not (jaanaati) know that upon his/her death, (shva)
dogs and (gṛidhraiḥ) vultures (jagdhim) shall feast (aatmanaḥ) on his body. 3:115
The 119th - 284th shlokas primarily focus on the procedure of Sharaaddha i.e. feeding 
braahmaṇa for the nourishment of the dead ancestors. This procedure is not sanctified in 
the Vedas. The current topic being discussed by Maharṣhi Manu is of the five routine yajña 
and this procedure of Sharaaddha is not part of those five daily sacraments. Apart from 
this, most of the shlokas are in conflict with the ideas conveyed by Maharṣhi Manu 
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ३ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 3
276
elsewhere. These shlokas also present conflict amongst themselves indicating that these 
were not even added by just one person but are the handiwork of multiple individuals 
belonging to different eras.

119. raajartviksnaatakaguroonpriyashvashuramaatulaan,
arhayenmadhuparkeṇa parisamvatsaraatpunaḥ. raajaa-ṛitvik-snaataka-guroon priya-shvashura-maatulaan, 
arhayet madhuparkeṇa pari-samvatsaraat punaḥ.
When (raajaa) the king, (ṛitvik) the priest, (snaataka) the scholar, (guroon) the guru, 
(priya) a dear friend, brother or son-in-law, (shvashura) the father-in-law, (maatulaan)
the maternal uncle visit (punaḥ) again (pari)(samvatsaraat) after an interval of a year or 
more, they (arhayet) should be welcomed (madhu)(parkeṇa) with a sweet mixture of 
honey, yogurt, milk, butter and sugar. 3:119

120. raajaa cha shrotriyashchaiva yajñakarmaṇyupasthitau,
madhuparkeṇa sampoojyau na tvayajña iti sthitiḥ. raajaa cha shrotriyaḥ cha eva yajña-karmaṇi upasthitau, 
madhu-parkeṇa sampoojyau na tu ayajñe iti sthitiḥ.
(raajaa) The king (cha) or (shrotriyaḥ) a scholar of the Vedas (eva) as well, (sampoojyau)
should be welcomed (madhu)(parkeṇa) with a sweet mixture only when they 
(upasthitau) have come (karmaṇi) for the performance of (yajña) yajña. (iti) This (sthitiḥ)
kind of welcome is (na) not required (tu) if the visit is (ayajñe) not for yajña. 3:120
Sacrificial offerings by wife
सायंत्वन्नस्य िसद्धस्य पत्न्यमन्त्रंबिलंहरेत्

वै देवम्। िह । नाम । एतत्। सायम्। प्रातः । िवधीयते॥
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ३ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 3

121. saayan tvannasya siddhasya patnyamantram baliṅ haret,
vaishvadevaṅ hi naamaitatsaayam praatarvidheeyate. saayam tu annasya siddhasya patnee amantram balim haret, 
vaishva-devam hi naama etat saayam praataḥ vidheeyate.
(saayam) In the evening (tu) as well, after (annasya) the food (siddhasya) has been 
cooked, (patnee) the lady of the house (haret) should take a portion out (balim) for 
sacrifice (amantram) without chanting the related mantras, (hi) because (etat)this yajña 
(naama) named (vaishva)(devam) Balivaishvadeva (vidheeyate) is prescribed for both 
(praataḥ) mornings and (saayam) evenings. 3:121
Offerings in the memory of deceased ancestors
िपत

िपतय म ृ ्। तु। िनवर्त्यर्। िवप्रः । च । इन्द ये

122. pitṛiyajñan tu nirvartya viprashchendukṣhaye’gnimaan,
piṇḍaanvaahaaryakañ shraaddhaṅ kuryaanmaasaanumaasikam.
pitṛi-yajñam tu nirvartya vipraḥ cha indukṣhaye agnimaan,
piṇḍa-anu-aahaaryakam shraaddham kuryaat maasa-anu-maasikam.
(maasa) Month (anu) after (maasikam) month (indukṣhaye) on the day of no moon, 
(vipraḥ) a twice born, (agnimaan) who diligently and regularly makes offerings in the 
fire, (nirvartya) after having completed (pitṛi)(yajñam) serving the elders, should (tu)
also (shraaddham) faithfully (kuryaat) perform (piṇḍa)(anu)(aahaaryakam) the 
donations of rice balls in the memory of the deceased ancestors. 3:122

(budhaaḥ) The scholars (viduḥ) call this (maasikam) monthly donation of rice balls,
(shraaddham) faithfully done (pitṛeeṇaam) for the ancestors as (anu)(aahaaryam)

124. tatra ye bhojaneeyaaḥ syurye cha varjyaa dvijottamaaḥ,
yaavantashchaiva yaishchaannaistaanpravakṣhyaamyasheṣhataḥ. tatra ye bhojaneeyaaḥ syuḥ ye cha varjyaa dvijottamaaḥ,
yaavantaḥ cha eva yaiḥ cha annaiḥ taan pravakṣhyaami asheṣhataḥ.
(tatra) During the procedure of shraaddha, (dvijottamaaḥ) the best amongst the 
braahmaṇa (ye) who (syuḥ) should be (bhojaneeyaaḥ) fed (cha) and those (ye) who 
(varjyaa) should be avoided, (cha) and (yaavantaḥ) how many should be fed, (cha) and 
(yaiḥ) with how many types of (annaiḥ) foods (eva) as well, (pravakṣhyaami) I will now 
describe (taan) those aspects (asheṣhataḥ) without leaving anything out. 3:124

125. dvau daive pitṛikaarye treenekaikamubhayatra vaa,
bhojayetsusamṛiddho’pi na prasajjeta vistare. dvau daive pitṛi-kaarye treen eka-ekam ubhayatra vaa,
bhojayet susamṛiddhaḥ api na prasajjeta vistare.
(api) Even (susamṛiddhaḥ) the wealthy should invite only (dvau) two braahmaṇa (daive)
for the performance of offerings in the fire and (treen) three (kaarye) for the offerings 
(pitṛi) for the ancestors. (vaa) Alternatively, one (bhojayet) can feed (eka)(ekam) only 
one braahmaṇa each (ubhayatra) for both the performances and (na) not (prasajjeta)
go (vistare) overboard with these activities. 3:125

126. satkriyaan deshakaalau cha shaucham braahmaṇasampadaḥ,

pañcha etaan vistaraḥ hanti tasmaat na eeheta vistaram.
(etaan) These (pañcha) five aspects, (satkriyaam) the welcome, (desha) the place, 
(kaalau) the time, (shaucham) the cleanliness (cha) and (sampadaḥ) the quality of the
(braahmaṇa) braahmaṇa, (hanti) are compromised (vistaraḥ) by the tendency to go 
overboard with these performances, and (tasmaat) hence the host (na) should not 
(eeheta) desire to (vistaram) overdo the invitations. 3:126

127. prathitaa pretakṛityaiṣhaa pitryan naama vidhukṣhaye,
tasminyuktasyaiti nityam pretakṛityaiva laukikee. prathitaa preta-kṛityaa eṣhaa pitryam naama vidhukṣhaye, 
tasmin yuktasya eti nityam preta-kṛityaa eva laukikee.
(eṣhaa) This procedure (prathitaa) traditionally (kṛityaa) performed (vidhukṣhaye) on 
the day of no moon (preta) for pleasing the deceased (naama) is called (pitryam)
pitryam. The (nityam) regular (yuktasya) performers (tasmin) of this (eti) are blessed 
(laukikee) with offspring who (kṛityaa) would perform it for them upon their (preta)
death (eva) as well. 3:127

128. shrotriyaayaiva deyaani havyakavyaani daatṛibhiḥ,

(daatṛibhiḥ) The donors should ensure that (deyaani) the donations (havya) towards the 
divinities and (kavyaani) towards the ancestors (eva) as well, are made only to 
(arhattamaaya) a qualified (vipraaya) twice born (shrotriyaaya) scholar of the Vedas, 
because only (dattam) giving (tasmai) to him/her (mahaa)(phalam) is fruitful. 3:128

129. ekaikamapi vidvaansan daive pitrye cha bhojayet,

during the performances (daive) towards the divinities (cha) and (pitrye) towards the 
ancestors, (aapnoti) gains (puṣhkalam) a lot of (phalam) rewards, which is (na) not 
possible (api) even by feeding (bahoon) many (amantrajñaan) who are without the 
knowledge of the Vedas. 3:129

130. dooraadeva pareekṣheta braahmaṇam vedapaaragam,
teerthan taddhavyakavyaanaam pradaane so’tithiḥ smṛitaḥ. dooraat eva pareekṣheta braahmaṇam veda-paaragam,

(dooraat) From a distance (eva) itself, the host (pareekṣheta) should examine 
(braahmaṇam) the braahmaṇa for his/her (paaragam) expertise (veda) in the Vedas, 
before inviting him/her inside the home, because only (tat) such scholar of the Vedas, 
(teertham) who is capable of guiding towards mokṣha, (smṛitaḥ) can be thought of as 
(atithiḥ) a guest and (saḥ) he/she is really (pradaane) worthy of donations made (havya)
towards the divinities and (kavyaanaam) towards the ancestors. 3:130

132. jñaanotkṛiṣhṭaaya deyaani kavyaani cha haveeṇṣhi cha,
na hi hastaavasṛigdigdhau rudhireṇaiva shuddhyataḥ. jñaana-utkṛiṣhṭaaya deyaani kavyaani cha haveeṇṣhi cha,

The donations (haveeṇṣhi) towards the divinities (cha) and (kavyaani) towards the 
ancestors, (deyaani)should be given only (utkṛiṣhṭaaya) to the best (jñaana)scholar, (hi)
because (hastau) the hands (digdhau) soiled (asṛig) with blood (na) can not 
(shuddhyataḥ) be cleaned (rudhireṇa) with blood (eva) as well i.e. feeding an unscholarly 
would only increase ignorance. 3:132

133. yaavato grasate graasaanhavyakavyeṣhvamantravit,

(yaavataḥ) As many (graasaan) morsels of food meant (havya) for the divinities and 
(kavyeṣhu) for the ancestors, (amantravit) an unscholarly (grasate) eats, he/she, (pretya)
after his/her death, (grasate) has to eat (taavataḥ) that many (deepta) heated (shoola)
pikes, (ṛiṣhṭi) double edged swords and (ayoguḍaan) iron balls. 3:133
 ानिन ाः िद्वजाः के िच पोिन ास्तथाऽपरे।
तपः स्वाध्यायिन ा  कमर्िन ास्तथाऽपरे॥१३४॥
 ानिन ाः । िद्वजाः । के िचत्। तपोिन ाः । तथा । अपरे॥ तपः । स्वाध्यायिन ाः । च । कमर्िन ाः । तथा । अपरे॥
134. jñaananiṣhṭhaaḥ dvijaaḥ kechit taponiṣhṭhaastathaa’pare,
tapaḥ svaadhyaayaniṣhṭhaashcha karmaniṣhṭhaastathaa’pare. jñaana-niṣhṭhaaḥ dvijaaḥ kechit tapo-niṣhṭhaaḥ tathaa apare,
tapaḥ svaadhyaaya-niṣhṭhaaḥ cha karma-niṣhṭhaaḥ tathaa apare.
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ३ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 3
282
(kechit) Some (dvijaaḥ) braahmaṇa (niṣhṭhaaḥ) are focused (jñaana) on knowledge 
(tathaa) while (apare) some others (niṣhṭhaaḥ) are focused (tapo) on penance and 
fortitude, some (niṣhṭhaaḥ) are focused on both (tapaḥ) fortitude (cha) and 
(svaadhyaaya) self study (tathaa) while (apare) some others (niṣhṭhaaḥ) are focused 
only (karma) on duties and actions. This can also be thought of as the four stages of life, 
students are focused on attaining knowledge, the householders on actions, those 
preparing for renunciation on penance and fortitude, and the ascetics on fortitude and 
self study. 3:134

135. jñaananiṣhṭheṣhu kavyaani pratiṣhṭhaapyaani yatnataḥ,

(kavyaani) The offering for the ancestors should be (yatnataḥ) effortfully 
(pratiṣhṭhaapyaani) given only to the braahmaṇa (niṣhṭheṣhu) who are focused (jñaana)
on knowledge, (tu) however, (havyaani)the offerings for the divinites can (api)(eva) also 
be given (sarveṣhu) to all of (chaturṣhu) the four types (yathaa) as deemed (nyaayam)
proper. 3:135

136. ashrotriyaḥ pitaa yasya putraḥ syaadvedapaaragaḥ,

(putraḥ) The son (yasya) whose (pitaa) father is (ashrotriyaḥ) unscholarly, but (syaat) is 
himself (paaragaḥ) an expert (veda) in the Vedas, (vaa) or (putraḥ) the son whose (pitaa)
father (syaat) is (paaragaḥ) an expert (veda) in the Vedas, but he himself (syaat) is 
(ashrotriyaḥ) unscholarly, 3:136

137. jyaayaansamanayorvidyaadyasya syaachchhrotriyaḥ pitaa,
mantrasampoojanaarthan tu satkaaramitaro’rhati. jyaayaansam anayoḥ vidyaat yasya syaat shrotriyaḥ pitaa, 
mantra-sampoojana-artham tu satkaaram itaraḥ arhati.
(anayoḥ) out of them, the son (yasya) whose (pitaa) father (syaat) is (shrotriyaḥ)
scholarly (vidyaat) is considered (jyaayaansam) better for the offerings for the 
ancestors. (tu) However, (artham) for (sampoojana) the offerings requiring (mantra)
chanting of the Vedic mantras, (itaraḥ) the other one i.e. the scholarly son (arhati)
deserves (satkaaram) respect and welcome. 3:137
Feeding friends in lieu of a braahmaṇa

ग्रहः ॥
न। अ रम्। न। िमत्रम्। यम्। िवद्या म्। श्राद्धे। भोजयेत्। िद्वजम्॥
138. na shraaddhe bhojayenmitran dhanaiḥ kaaryo’sya saṅgrahaḥ,
naarin na mitrañ yam vidyaattañ shraaddhe bhojayed dvijam. na shraaddhe bhojayet mitram dhanaiḥ kaaryaḥ asya saṅgrahaḥ, 
na arim na mitram yam vidyaattam shraaddhe bhojayet dvijam.
One should (na) not (bhojayet) feed (mitram) a friend and consider (shraaddhe) the duty 
towards ancestors completed. (kaaryaḥ) The respect towards a friend can be shown 
(dhanaiḥ)(saṅgrahaḥ) by sharing wealth (asya) with him/her. However, someone (yam)
who (vidyaattam) can be considered (na) neither (mitram) a friend (na) nor (arim) an 
enemy, only that (dvijam) braahmaṇa (bhojayet) should be fed (shraaddhe) for 
fulfillment of one’s duty towards the ancestors. 3:138
यस्य िमत्रप्रधानािन श्राद्धािन च हवींिष च ।
तस्य प्रेत्य फलंनािस्त श्राद्धेषु
च हिवष्षु
च ॥१३९॥
यस्य । िमत्रप्रधानािन । श्राद्धािन । च । हवींिष । च ॥ तस्य । प्रेत्य । फलम्। न। अिस्त । श्राद्धेषु। च ।हिवष्षु। च ॥
139. yasya mitrapradhaanaani shraaddhaani cha haveeṇṣhi cha,
tasya pretya phalan naasti shraaddheṣhu cha haviṣhṣhu cha. yasya mitra-pradhaanaani shraaddhaani cha haveeṇṣhi cha, 
tasya pretya phalam na asti shraaddheṣhu cha haviṣhṣhu cha.
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ३ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 3
284
(yasya) Whose donations (shraaddhaani) towards the ancestors (cha) and (haveeṇṣhi)
towards the divinities are directed (pradhaanaani) primarily (mitra) to friends, (phalam)
the fruits of these donations made (shraaddheṣhu) towards the ancestors (cha) or 
(haviṣhṣhu) towards the divinities, (na) are not (asti) available in (tasya) his/her (pretya)
afterlife. 3:139
यः सङ
्
गतािन क
ु
 तेमोहाच्छ्राद्धेन मानवः ।
स स्वगार्च्च्यवतेलोकाच्छ्राद्धिमत्रो िद्वजाधमः ॥१४०॥
यः । सङ्गतािन । कु ते। मोहात्। श्राद्धेन। मानवः ॥ सः । स्वगार्त्। च्यवते। लोकात्। श्राद्धिमत्रः । िद्वजाधमः॥
140. yaḥ saṅgataani kurute mohaachchhraaddhena maanavaḥ, 
sa svargaachchyavate lokaachchhraaddhamitro dvijaadhamaḥ. yaḥ saṅgataani kurute mohaat shraaddhena maanavaḥ, 
saḥ svargaat chyavate lokaat shraaddha-mitraḥ dvija-adhamaḥ. 
(dvija) A twice born (maanavaḥ) human, (yaḥ) who (mohaat) under the influence of 
attachment, (kurute) tries (shraaddhena) to please the ancestors by feeding his/her 
(saṅgataani) friends, (saḥ) he/she, (adhamaḥ) a lowly manipulator of (shraaddha) this 
tradition by pleasing his/her (mitraḥ) friends, (chyavate) becomes unworthy (svargaat)
of the heavenly (lokaat) region; and vice versa, a braahmaṇa who makes friends with 
the sole intention of feasting on the offering made for the friends’ ancestors, that 
braahmaṇa falls from grace too.
 3:140
सम्भोजनी साऽिभिहता पैशाची दि णा िद्वजैः ।
इहैवास्तेत
ु
सा लोकेगौरन्धेवैकवेश्मिन ॥१४१॥
सम्भोजनी । सा । अिभिहता । पैशाची । दि णा । िद्वजैः ॥
इह। एव । आस्ते। तु। सा । लोके। गौः । अन्धा । इव । एकवेश्मिन ॥
141. sambhojanee saa’bhihitaa paishaachee dakṣhiṇaa dvijaiḥ, 
ihaivaaste tu saa loke gaurandhevaikaveshmani. sambhojanee saa abhihitaa paishaachee dakṣhiṇaa dvijaiḥ, 
iha eva aaste tu saa loke gauḥ andhaa iva eka-veshmani. 
(dvijaiḥ) The scholars have declared (dakṣhiṇaa) the donations (saa) that are made 
(abhihitaa) favoring (sambhojanee) the friends and family as (paishaachee) despicable 
offerings and (iva) as (andhaa) a blind (gauḥ) cow (veshmani) remains only inside (eka) 
one barn, (tu) so are (saa) these offerings that (aaste) are left back (iha) in this (loke)
world (eva) itself i.e. do not accompany the donor in the afterlife. 3:141
यथे रणेबीजम
