142. yatheriṇe beejamuptvaa na vaptaa labhate phalam,
tathaa’nṛiche havirdatvaa na daataa labhate phalam. yathaa eeriṇe beejam uptvaa na vaptaa labhate phalam, 
tathaa anṛiche haviḥ datvaa na daataa labhate phalam.
(yathaa) As (vaptaa) the sower who (uptvaa) sows (beejam) seeds (eeriṇe) in infertile 
land (labhate) gets (na) no (phalam) fruits, (tathaa)similarly (daataa) the donor (datvaa)
donating (haviḥ) offerings (anṛiche) to the unscholarly (labhate) gains (na) no (phalam)
benefits either. 3:142

143. daatṛeenpratigraheetṛeeñshcha kurute phalabhaaginaḥ,
viduṣhe dakṣhiṇaan datvaa vidhivat pretya cheha cha. daatṛeen pratigraheetṛeen cha kurute phala-bhaaginaḥ, 
viduṣhe dakṣhiṇaam datvaa vidhivat pretya cha iha cha.
Those who (vidhivat) properly (datvaa) give (dakṣhiṇaam) offerings (viduṣhe) to the 
scholars, (kurute) make both (daatṛeen) the donors (cha) and (pratigraheetṛeen) the 
donees (bhaaginaḥ) eligible for (phala) fruits (iha) in this world (cha) and (pretya) in the 
afterlife (cha) as well. 3:143
कामंश्राद्धेऽचर्येिन्मत्रंनािभ पमिप त्व रम

144. kaamañ shraaddhe’rchayenmitran naabhiroopamapi tvarim,
dviṣhataa hi havirbhuktam bhavati pretya niṣhphalam. kaamam shraaddhe archayet mitram na abhi-roopam api tu arim,
dviṣhataa hi haviḥ bhuktam bhavati pretya niṣhphalam.
In case a scholar is not available for accepting the offerings made (shraaddhe) towards 
the ancestors, then it is (kaamam) desirable (archayet) to offer them (mitram) to a 
friend, but (na) not (arim) to an enemy (api) even (tu) if he/she is (abhi)(roopam)
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ३ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 3
286
scholarly, (hi) because (haviḥ) the offerings (bhuktam) consumed by someone 
(dviṣhataa) harboring ill feelings (bhavati) become (niṣhphalam) fruitless (pretya) in the 
afterlife. 3:144

145. yatnena bhojayechchhraaddhe bahvṛicham vedapaaragam,
shaakhaantagamathaadhvaryuñ chhandogan tu samaaptikam. yatnena bhojayet shraaddhe bahu ṛicham veda-paaragam, 
shaakhaantagam atha adhvaryum chhandogam tu samaaptikam.
One should (yatnena) effortfully (bhojayet) feed (shraaddhe) the offerings made 
towards the ancestors, to a scholar who is (paaragam) an expert (veda) in the Vedas, 
well versed in (bahu) a lot (ṛicham) of mantras and (shaakhaantagam) different 
branches of the Vedic studies (atha) or (adhvaryum) an expert in the performance of the 
yajña who has studied the Vedas (samaaptikam) along with the six limbs including 
(chhandogam) the study of the poetic meters etc. (tu) as well. 3:145

146. eṣhaamanyatamo yasya bhuñjeeta shraaddhamarchitaḥ,
pitṛeeṇaan tasya tṛiptiḥ syaachchhaashvatee saaptapauruṣhee. eṣhaam anyatamaḥ yasya bhuñjeeta shraaddham architaḥ, 
pitṛeeṇaam tasya tṛiptiḥ syaat shaashvatee saapta-pauruṣhee.
The one (yasya) whose (shraaddham) offerings made towards the ancestors (bhuñjeeta)
are consumed by (architaḥ) a duly welcomed scholar (anyatamaḥ) out (eṣhaam) of these 
categories, (saapta)seven (pauruṣhee) generations of (tasya) his (pitṛeeṇaam) ancestors 
(syaat) become (tṛiptiḥ) content (shaashvatee) forever. 3:146

147. eṣha vai prathamaḥ kalpaḥ pradaane havyakavyayoḥ,
anukalpastvayañ jñeyaḥ sadaa sadbhiranuṣhṭhitaḥ.

eṣhaḥ vai prathamaḥ kalpaḥ pradaane havya-kavyayoḥ,
anukalpaḥ tu ayam jñeyaḥ sadaa sadbhiḥ anuṣhṭhitaḥ.
(eṣhaḥ) This procedure (pradaane) of donating (havya) towards the divinities and 
(kavyayoḥ) towards the ancestors is (vai) indeed (prathamaḥ) the primary (kalpaḥ)
directive. (tu) Also (jñeyaḥ) consider (ayam) this (anukalpaḥ) alternative method that is 
(sadaa) always (anuṣhṭhitaḥ) followed (sadbhiḥ) by the benevolent as well. 3:147

148. maataamaham maatulañ cha svasreeyañ shvashuraṅ gurum,
dauhitram viṭpatim bandhumṛitvigyaajyau cha bhojayet. maataamaham maatulam cha svasreeyam shvashuram gurum,
dauhitram viṭpatim bandhum ṛitvik-yaajyau cha bhojayet.
(maataamaham) The maternal grandfather, (maatulam) the maternal uncle, 
(svasreeyam) the sister’s son, (shvashuram) the father-in-law, (gurum) the teacher, 
(dauhitram) the daughter’s son, (viṭpatim) the daughter’s husband, (bandhum) other 
relatives, (ṛitvik) the priest (cha) and other (yaajyau) performers of the yajña (bhojayet)
can also be fed while donating towards the ancestors. 3:148

149. na braahmaṇam pareekṣhate daive karmaṇi dharmavit,
pitryai karmaṇi tu praapte pareekṣheta prayatnataḥ. na braahmaṇam pareekṣhate daive karmaṇi dharmavit,
pitryai karmaṇi tu praapte pareekṣheta prayatnataḥ.
(dharmavit) The righteous householders should (na) not (pareekṣhate) try to qualify 
(braahmaṇam) a braahmaṇa (karmaṇi) for the performance of offering (daive) towards 
the divinities, (tu) however, (praapte) on the occasion (karmaṇi) of the performance of 
offering (pitryai) towards the ancestors, they should (prayatnataḥ) effortfully 
(pareekṣheta) examine and qualify braahmaṇa beforehand. 3:149
Traits of an unqualified braahmaṇa

150. ye stenapatitakleebaa ye cha naastikavṛittayaḥ,
taan havyakavyayorvipraananarhaanmanurabraveet. ye stena-patita-kleebaaḥ ye cha naastika-vṛittayaḥ,
taan havya-kavyayoḥ vipraan anarhaan manuḥ abraveet.
The ones (ye) who are (stena) thieves, are (patita) fallen from grace or are (kleebaaḥ)
transgenders (cha) and the ones (ye) who are (vṛittayaḥ) with tendencies of (naastika)
not believing in God and the Vedas, (taan) those (vipraan) braahmaṇa are (anarhaan)
not worthy of receiving (havya) the offering towards the divinities or (kavyayoḥ) the 
offering towards the ancestors, so (abraveet) said (manuḥ) Maharṣhi Manu. 3:150

151. jaṭilañ chaanadheeyaanan durbalaṅ kitavan tathaa,
yaajanti cha ye poogaanstaañshcha shraaddhe na bhojayet. jaṭilam cha anadheeyaanam durbalam kitavam tathaa,
yaajanti cha ye poogaan taan cha shraaddhe na bhojayet.
The ones who (anadheeyaanam) do not study, (jaṭilam) have uncouth hairs or
(durbalam) weak bodies, (tathaa) or (kitavam) gamble (cha) and the ones (ye) who 
(yaajanti) perform yajña (poogaan) with a lot of people, (taan) they should (na) not 
(bhojayet) be fed (shraaddhe) the offering towards the ancestors. 3:151

152. chikitsakaan devalakaan maansavikrayiṇastathaa,
vipaṇena cha jeevanto varjyaaḥ syurhavyakavyayoḥ. chikitsakaan devalakaan maansa-vikrayiṇaḥ tathaa,
vipaṇena cha jeevantaḥ varjyaaḥ syuḥ havya-kavyayoḥ.
(chikitsakaan) The healers, (devalakaan) the employees of a temple (tathaa) or
(vikrayiṇaḥ) the traders (maansa) of meat (cha) and those who (vipaṇena) trade 
(jeevantaḥ) for a living, (syuḥ) are (varjyaaḥ) forbidden to receive (havya) the offering 
towards the divinities or (kavyayoḥ) the offering towards the ancestors as well. 3:152

153. preṣhyo graamasya raajñashcha kunakhee shyaavadantakaḥ, 
pratiroddhaa guroshchaiva tyaktaagnirvaardhuṣhistathaa. preṣhyaḥ graamasya raajñaḥ cha kunakhee shyaava-dantakaḥ, 
prati-roddhaa guroḥ cha eva tyakta-agniḥ vaardhuṣhiḥ tathaa. 
(preṣhyaḥ) The servants (graamasya) of the village (cha) or (raajñaḥ) the king, the ones 
(kunakhee) with deformed nails (cha) or (shyaava) black (dantakaḥ) teeth, the ones who 
(prati)(roddhaa) oppose one’s (guroḥ) teacher, the ones who have (tyakta) given up the 
maintenance of five types of (agniḥ) fires, (tathaa) and (vaardhuṣhiḥ) the loan sharks 
are forbidden (eva) as well. 3:153

154. yakṣhmee cha pashupaalashcha parivettaa niraakṛitiḥ, 
brahmadviṭ parivittishcha gaṇaabhyantara eva cha. yakṣhmee cha pashupaalaḥ cha parivettaa niraakṛitiḥ, 
brahmadviṭ parivittiḥ cha gaṇa-abhyantaraḥ eva cha. 
The ones (yakṣhmee) suffering from tuberculosis, the ones (pashupaalaḥ) who rear 
animals for a living, the ones (parivettaa) who marry before their elder brother, the ones 
(niraakṛitiḥ) who denounce the yajña and other religious activities, the ones 
(brahmadviṭ) who harbor malice towards braahmaṇa, (parivittiḥ) the elder brother who 
is unmarried while his younger brother is married (cha) and (gaṇa) the ones 
(abhyantaraḥ) practicing another faith are forbidden (eva) as well. 3:154

155. kusheelavo’vakeerṇee cha vṛiṣhaleepatireva cha,

(avakeerṇee) fornicators, (cha) or are (patiḥ) the husbands of (vṛiṣhalee) the shoodra

(cha) or (kaaṇaḥ) are one-eyed, (cha) or are the ones (yasya) whose wife’s (upa)(patiḥ)
boyfriend lives (gṛihe) in the same house, they are forbidden (eva) as well. 3:155

156. bhṛitakaadhyaapako yashcha bhṛitakaadhyaapitastathaa,
shoodrashiṣhyo gurushchaiva vaagduṣhṭaḥ kuṇḍagolakau. bhṛitaka-adhyaapakaḥ yaḥ cha bhṛitaka-adhyaapitaḥ tathaa,
shoodra-shiṣhyaḥ guruḥ cha eva vaak-duṣhṭaḥ kuṇḍa-golakau.
The ones (yaḥ) who (bhṛitaka) are salaried as (adhyaapakaḥ) teachers, (cha) or 
(adhyaapitaḥ) have been taught by (bhṛitaka) a salaried teacher, (tathaa) or (shiṣhyaḥ)
are the disciples of (shoodra) a shoodra, (cha) or (guruḥ) teach a shoodra, or (duṣhṭaḥ)
have a foul (vaak) speech, or (kuṇḍa) are born from the mothers’ boyfriend during their 
fathers’ lifetime or even (golakau) after the fathers’ death, they are forbidden (eva) as 
well. 3:156

157. akaaraṇaparityaktaa maataapitrorgurostathaa,
braahmairyaunaishcha sambandhaiḥ sañyogam patitairgataḥ. akaaraṇa-parityaktaa maataa-pitroḥ guroḥ tathaa,
braahmaiḥ yaunaiḥ cha sambandhaiḥ sañyogam patitaiḥ gataḥ.
The ones who (akaaraṇa) without any valid reason, (parityaktaa) sever their 
relationships with their (maataa) mother, (pitroḥ) father or (guroḥ) the teachers, 
(tathaa) or the ones who (gataḥ) establish (braahmaiḥ) educational, (yaunaiḥ) marital 
(cha) or (sañyogam) friendly (sambandhaiḥ) relationships (patitaiḥ) with the outcasts, 
they are forbidden as well. 3:157

158. agaaradaahee garadaḥ kuṇḍaashee somavikrayee,

sycophants, or (tailikaḥ) deal in oil, or (kaarakaḥ) give (kooṭa) false testimony, or 
adulterate merchandise, they are forbidden as well. 3:158

159. pitraa vivadamaanashcha kitavo madyapastathaa,

The ones who, (vivadamaanaḥ) quarrel (pitraa) with their fathers, (cha) or are (kitavaḥ)
conniving, (tathaa) or are (madyapaḥ) alcoholic, or are (rogee)suffering from sicknesses 
(paapa) attributable to sins, (cha) or are (abhishastaḥ) disreputed, or are (daambhikaḥ)
hypocrites, or (vikrayee) trade in (rasa) juices and nectars, they are forbidden as well.

161. bhraamaree gaṇḍamaalee cha shvitryatho pishunastathaa,

of the neck glands, (atho) or (shvitree) vitiligo, (tathaa) or the ones who are (pishunaḥ)
gossipers, (unmattaḥ) mentally sick, (andhaḥ) blind, (cha) or (nindakaḥ) the denouncers 
of (veda) the Vedas, they (syuḥ) are (varjyaaḥ) forbidden (eva) as well. 3:161

162. hastigo’shvoṣhṭradamako nakṣhatrairyashcha jeevati,
pakṣhiṇaam poṣhako yashcha yuddhaachaaryastathaiva cha. hasti-go-ashva-uṣhṭra-damakaḥ nakṣhatraiḥ yaḥ cha jeevati,

The one (yaḥ) who (damakaḥ) trains (hasti) elephants, (go) cows, (ashva) horses and 
(uṣhṭra) camels, (cha) or (jeevati) survives (nakṣhatraiḥ) on astrology, (cha) or the one 
(yaḥ) who (poṣhakaḥ) nurtures (pakṣhiṇaam) birds, (cha) or (aachaaryaḥ) trains others 
(yuddha) for battle, they are forbidden (tathaa)(eva) as well. 3:162

164. shvakreeḍee shyenajeevee cha kanyaadooṣhaka eva cha,

eagles, (cha) or (dooṣhakaḥ) rapes (kanyaa) a girl, (cha) or is (hinsraḥ) a murderer, (cha)

yajña i.e. for multiple yajamana at a time, they are forbidden (eva) as well. 3:164

167. etaan vigarhitaachaaraanapaaṅkteyaan dvijaadhamaan,
dvijaatipravaro vidvaanubhayatra vivarjayet. etaan vigarhita aachaaraan apaaṅkteyaan dvijaadhamaan,
dvijaati-pravaraḥ vidvaan ubhayatra vivarjayet.
The (pravaraḥ) best (vidvaan) scholars amongst (dvijaati) the twice born, (ubhayatra)
during the performance of both types of offerings, (vivarjayet) should leave aside
(etaan) these (adhamaan) lowly (dvija) braahmaṇa whose (aachaaraan) conducts are 
(vigarhita) condemnable and who are (apaaṅkteyaan) unworthy of sitting alongside of 
other braahmaṇa. 3:167

168. brahmaṇastvanadheeyaanastṛiṇaagniriva shaamyati,
tasmai havyan na daatavyan na hi bhasmani hooyate. brahmaṇaḥ tu anadheeyaanaḥ tṛiṇa-agniḥ iva shaamyati,
tasmai havyam na daatavyam na hi bhasmani hooyate.
(anadheeyaanaḥ) An uneducated (brahmaṇaḥ) braahmaṇa is (iva) like (agniḥ) fire in 
(tṛiṇa) hay (tu) which (shaamyati) goes out quickly leaving only ash behind. (na) Do not 
(daatavyam) give (havyam) offerings (tasmai) to him/her (hi) because (hooyate)
offerings are made in fire and (na) not (bhasmani) on ashes. 3:168

169. apaaṅktadaane yo daaturbhavatyoordhvam phalodayaḥ,
daive haviṣhi pitrye vaa tatpravakṣhyaamyasheṣhataḥ. apaaṅktadaane yaḥ daatuḥ bhavati oordhvam phala-udayaḥ,
daive haviṣhi pitrye vaa tat pravakṣhyaami asheṣhataḥ.
Now (asheṣhataḥ) without leaving anything aside, (pravakṣhyaami) I shall cover in detail 
the (phala)(udayaḥ) consequences (tat) that (bhavati) are faced (oordhvam) in the 
afterlife by those (daatuḥ) donors, (yaḥ) who give (haviṣhi) the offerings meant (daive)
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ३ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 3

for the divinities (vaa) or (pitrye) the ancestors, to the braahmaṇa who are

170. avratairyad dvijairbhuktam parivetraadibhistathaa, 
apaaṅkteyairyadanyaishcha tadvai rakṣhaansi bhuñjate. 
avrataiḥ yat dvijaiḥ bhuktam parivetraadibhiḥ tathaa,
apaaṅkteyaiḥ yat anyaiḥ cha tat vai rakṣhaansi bhuñjate. 
(yat) Those meals that are (bhuktam) consumed by (dvijaiḥ) braahmaṇa who (avrataiḥ)
do not follow the routines of yajña, (tathaa) or who (parivetraadibhiḥ) jump queue or 
are jumped etc., (cha) and (yat) those that are consumed (anyaiḥ) by others who are 
(apaaṅkteyaiḥ) unworthy of sitting alongside of other braahmaṇa, (tat) they are (vai)
indeed the meals (bhuñjate) consumed (rakṣhaansi) by demons. 3:170

171. daaraa’gnihotrasañyogaṅ kurute yo’graje sthite, 
parivettaa sa vijñeyaḥ parivittistu poorvajaḥ. daaraa-agnihotra-sañyogam kurute yaḥ agraje sthite,
parivettaa saḥ vijñeyaḥ parivittiḥ tu poorvajaḥ. 
(vijñeyaḥ) Know (saḥ) that person (yaḥ) who duly (sañyogam) marries (daaraa) a woman 
(kurute) following (agnihotra) the procedures of yajña, while his (agraje) elder brother 
(sthite) is still unmarried, as (parivettaa) the queue jumper (tu) and his (poorvajaḥ) elder 
brother as (parivittiḥ) the jumped. 3:171

(parivittiḥ) The jumped, (parivettaa) the queue jumper (cha) and (yayaa) the girl he
(parividyate) marries, (daatṛi) her parents and (pañchamaaḥ) fifth, (yaajaka) the priest 
of the ceremony, (sarve) all of (te) these (yaanti) go (narakam) to hell. 3:172

173. bhraaturmṛitasya bhaaryaayaañ yo’nurajyeta kaamataḥ,
dharmeṇaapi niyuktaayaan sa jñeyo didhiṣhoopatiḥ. bhraatuḥ mṛitasya bhaaryaayaam yaḥ anurajyeta kaamataḥ,
dharmeṇa api niyuktaayaam saḥ jñeyaḥ didhiṣhoopatiḥ.
One (yaḥ) who (anurajyeta) copulates (bhaaryaayaam) with the wife of his (mṛitasya)
dead (bhraatuḥ) brother, (kaamataḥ) out of lust or (api) even if he is (dharmeṇa)
righteously (niyuktaayaam) appointed to impregnate her, (jñeyaḥ) consider (saḥ) him as 
(didhiṣhoopatiḥ) the husband of a remarried woman. 3:173

174. paradaareṣhu jaayete dvau sutau kuṇḍagolakau,
patyau jeevati kuṇḍaḥ syaanmṛite bhartari golakaḥ. para-daareṣhu jaayete dvau sutau kuṇḍa-golakau,
patyau jeevati kuṇḍaḥ syaat mṛite bhartari golakaḥ.
The (dvau) two types of (sutau) sons (jaayete) born from (para) someone else’s 
(daareṣhu) wife are called (kuṇḍa) kuṇḍa and (golakau) golaka; one born from a woman 
whose (patyau) husband (jeevati) is alive (syaat) is called (kuṇḍaḥ) kuṇḍa and one from 
a woman whose (bhartari) husband (mṛite) is dead is called (golakaḥ) golaka. 3:174

175. tau tu jaatau parakṣhetre praaṇinau pretya cheha cha,
dattaani havyakavyaani naashayete pradaayinaam. tau tu jaatau para-kṣhetre praaṇinau pretya cha iha cha,
dattaani havya-kavyaani naashayete pradaayinaam.

(tau)(tu) Both of these (praaṇinau) beings (jaatau) born from (para) someone else’s 
(kṣhetre) wife, (naashayete) destroy the effects of the offerings, (pradaayinaam) granted 
to them (dattaani) by donors, (havya) towards the divinities (cha) and (kavyaani)
towards the ancestors, (iha) in this world (cha) as well (pretya) for the afterlife. 3:175

176. apaaṅktyo yaavataḥ paaṅktyaanbhuñjaanaananupashyati, 
taavataan na phalam pretya daataa praapnoti baalishaḥ. apaaṅktyaḥ yaavataḥ paaṅktyaan bhuñjaanaan anupashyati,
taavataam na phalam pretya daataa praapnoti baalishaḥ. 
Even if (apaaṅktyaḥ) an unworthy braahmaṇa (anupashyati)sees (yaavataḥ) many other 
(paaṅktyaan) worthy braahmaṇa (bhuñjaanaan) feasting, (phalam) the virtue of feeding 
(taavataam) that many braahmaṇa is (na) not (praapnoti) available for that (baalishaḥ)
amateurish (daataa) donor (pretya) in his/her afterlife. 3:176

177. veekṣhyaandho navateḥ kaaṇaḥ ṣhaṣhṭeḥ shvitree shatasya tu, 
paaparogee sahasrasya daaturnaashayate phalam. veekṣhya andhaḥ navateḥ kaaṇaḥ ṣhaṣhṭeḥ shvitree shatasya tu,
paapa-rogee sahasrasya daatuḥ naashayate phalam. 
And if this unworthy braahmaṇa, who (veekṣhya) sees other worthy braahmaṇa 
feasting, (andhaḥ) is blind (tu) then (naashayate) destroys (daatuḥ) the donor’s (phalam)
virtue of feeding (navateḥ) ninety braahmaṇa, (kaaṇaḥ) is one-eyed then destroys the 
virtue of feeding (ṣhaṣhṭeḥ) sixty, is suffering from (shvitree) Vitiligo then destroys the 
virtue of feeding (shatasya) one hundred, or (rogee) suffers from sickness related to 
(paapa) sins then destroys the virtue of feeding (sahasrasya) one thousand braahmaṇa.
How would a blind see others feasting? These illogical statements put a stamp of 
certainty on these shlokas being extensions. 3:177

178. yaavataḥ sanspṛishedaṅgairbraahmaṇaañchhoodrayaajakaḥ,
taavataan na bhaveddaatuḥ phalan daanasya paurtikam. yaavataḥ sanspṛishet aṅgaiḥ braahmaṇaan shoodra-yaajakaḥ,
taavataam na bhavet daatuḥ phalam daanasya paurtikam.
(yaavataḥ) As many (braahmaṇaan) braahmaṇa are (aṅgaiḥ) physically (sanspṛishet)
touched by a braahmaṇa who helps (shoodra) shoodra (yaajakaḥ) with yajña, (daatuḥ)
the donor (na) does not (bhavet) get (paurtikam)(phalam) the virtue (daanasya) of 
donating to (taavataam) that many braahmaṇa. 3:178

179. vedavichchaapi vipro’sya lobhaat kṛitvaa pratigraham,

(cha) And (api) even (vipraḥ) a scholar (vedavit) acquainted with the Vedas, (lobhaat)
who out of greed (kṛitvaa)(prati)(graham) receives (asya) their donations, (kṣhipram)
quickly (vrajati) gets (vinaasham) destroyed (iva) like (aama) an unbaked (paatram) pot 
decays (ambhasi) under water. 3:179

180. somavikrayiṇe viṣhṭhaa bhiṣhaje pooyashoṇitam,
naṣhṭan devalake dattamapratiṣhṭhan tu vaardhuṣhau. soma-vikrayiṇe viṣhṭhaa bhiṣhaje pooya-shoṇitam,
naṣhṭam devalake dattam apratiṣhṭham tu vaardhuṣhau.
(dattam) Donations made, to a braahmaṇa who (vikrayiṇe) trades in (soma) the soma
herb are like (viṣhṭhaa) feces, (bhiṣhaje) to a healer are like (pooya) pus and infected 
(shoṇitam) blood, (devalake) to the one employed in a temple get (naṣhṭam) destroyed 
i.e. are fruitless (tu) and (vaardhuṣhau) to a loan shark (apratiṣhṭham) bring infamy. 3:180

181. yattu vaaṇijake dattan neha naamutra tadbhavet,
bhasmaneeva hutaṅ havyan tathaa paunarbhave dvije. yat tu vaaṇijake dattam na iha na amutra tat bhavet,
bhasmani iva hutam havyam tathaa paunaḥ-bhave dvije.
(tu) And (yat) those (dattam) donations made (vaaṇijake) to a braahmaṇa whose 
primary vocation is trading, (tat) they (bhavet) are fruitful (na) neither (iha) here (na)
nor (amutra) there i.e. in the afterlife; (tathaa) and similarly the donations made (dvije)
to a braahmaṇa who (bhave) is the son born (paunaḥ) of a remarried woman, are (iva)
like (havyam) offerings (hutam) made (bhasmani) in the ashes. 3:181

182. itareṣhu tvapaaṅktyeṣhu yathoddiṣhṭeṣhvasaadhuṣhu,
medo’sṛiṅmaansamaajjaa’sthi vadantyannam maneeṣhiṇaḥ. itareṣhu tu apaaṅktyeṣhu yathaa-uddiṣhṭeṣhu asaadhuṣhu,

(tu) And (annam) the grains fed (itareṣhu) to these (apaaṅktyeṣhu) unworthy of sitting 
alongside other braahmaṇa and also (yathaa) to other (uddiṣhṭeṣhu) lowly and 
(asaadhuṣhu) unkind braahmaṇa, are (vadanti) called (maneeṣhiṇaḥ) by wise as the 
equivalent of (medaḥ) suet, (asṛiṅ) blood, (maansa) meat, (maajjaa) marrow and (asthi)
bones. 3:182

183. apaaṅktyopahataa paṅktiḥ paavyate yairdvijottamaiḥ,
taannibodhata kaartsnyena dvijaagryaanpaṅktipaavanaan. apaaṅktya upahataa paṅktiḥ paavyate yaiḥ dvija-uttamaiḥ,

Now (nibodhata) learn (kaartsnyena) completely (taan) about those 
(paṅkti)(paavanaan) purifying and (uttamaiḥ) superior (dvija) braahmaṇa who are 
(agryaan) foremost (dvija) amongst the twice borns and (yaiḥ) who (paavyate) purify

(paṅktiḥ) the rows that were (upahataa) sullied by the braahmaṇa (apaaṅktya)
unworthy of sitting in those rows. 3:183
Traits of a qualified braahmaṇa 
अ याः सव ष
ुवेदेषु

ु
च ।

ि पावनाः ॥१८४॥
अ याः । सव षु। वेदेषु। सवर्प्रवचनेषु। च ॥ श्रोित्रय । अन्वयजाः । च । एव । िव ेयाः । पङ्ि पावनाः ॥
184. agryaaḥ sarveṣhu vedeṣhu sarvapravachaneṣhu cha, 
shrotriyaanvayajaashchaiva vijñeyaaḥ paṅktipaavanaaḥ. agryaaḥ sarveṣhu vedeṣhu sarva-pravachaneṣhu cha,
shrotriya-anvayajaaḥ cha eva vijñeyaaḥ paṅkti-paavanaaḥ. 
The braahmaṇa who are (agryaaḥ) the foremost in the delivery of (sarva) all of 
(pravachaneṣhu) discourses (vedeṣhu) on the Vedas (cha) and (sarveṣhu) all of their limbs 
(cha) and are also (anvayajaaḥ) born in the lineage of (shrotriya) the Vedic scholars, they 
(vijñeyaaḥ) should (eva) indeed be considered as the ones who (paavanaaḥ) purify 
(paṅkti) the congregations they attend. 3:184

185. triṇaachiketaḥ pañchaagnistrisuparṇaḥ ṣhaḍaṅgavit, 
brahmadeyaatmasantaano jyeṣhṭhasaamaga eva cha. triṇaachiketaḥ pañcha-agniḥ tri-suparṇaḥ ṣhaḍ-aṅgavit,
brahmadeya-aatma-santaanaḥ jyeṣhṭha-saamagaḥ eva cha. 
The braahmaṇa (triṇaachiketaḥ) who implements the resolve described in 
kaṭhopaniṣhad, who is the bearer of (pañcha) the five types of (agniḥ) fires, 
(trisuparṇaḥ) who implements the resolve described in ṛigveda, (vit) who has deep 
knowledge of (ṣhaḍ) the six (aṅga) limbs of Vedic study, who is (santaanaḥ) the child 
(brahmadeya)(aatma) of the parents married through the godly marriage procedure 
(cha) and who is (jyeṣhṭha) a mature (saamagaḥ) singer of the hymns from the 
Saamaveda (eva) as well,  3:185

186. vedaarthavitpravaktaa cha brahmachaaree sahasradaḥ, 
shataayushchaiva vijñeyaa braahmaṇaaḥ paṅktipaavanaaḥ. vedaarthavit pravaktaa cha brahmachaaree sahasradaḥ, 
shata-aayuḥ cha eva vijñeyaaḥ braahmaṇaaḥ paṅkti-paavanaaḥ. 
(vit) who knows (vedaartha) the intricacies of the Vedas (cha) and (pravaktaa) delivers
discourses on them, who is (brahmachaaree) a celebate, who (sahasradaḥ) has donated 
one thousand cows (cha) and who has (aayuḥ) an age of (shata) one hundred years (eva)
as well, (vijñeyaaḥ) consider these (braahmaṇaaḥ) braahmaṇa as the ones who 
(paavanaaḥ) purify (paṅkti) the congregations they attend. 3:186

187. poorvedyuraparedyurvaa shraaddhakarmaṇyupasthite, 
nimantrayeta tryavaraansamyagvipraanyathoditaan. poorvedyuḥ aparedyuḥ vaa shraaddha-karmaṇi upasthite,
nimantrayeta tryavaraan samyak vipraan yathaa uditaan. 
When the day of (karmaṇi) performance of (shraaddha) the offerings for the ancestors 
(upasthite) arrives, then (poorvedyuḥ) a day before that (vaa) or (aparedyuḥ) a day after 
that, (tryavaraan) three (vipraan) braahmaṇa, (yathaa) as (uditaan) revealed before,
should be (samyak) properly (nimantrayeta) invited. 3:187

188. nimantrito dvijaḥ pitrye niyataatmaa bhavetsadaa, 
na cha chhandaansyadheeyeeta yasya shraaddhañ cha tadbhavet. nimantritaḥ dvijaḥ pitrye niyata-aatmaa bhavet sadaa,
na cha chhandaansi adheeyeeta yasya shraaddham cha tat bhavet. 
(dvijaḥ) The braahmaṇa (nimantritaḥ) invited for the performance of (pitrye) offerings 
for the ancestors, should (sadaa) always (bhavet)remain (niyata)(aatmaa) under control 
(cha) and should (na) refrain from (adheeyeeta) chanting (chhandaansi) the Vedic 
mantras (cha) and the host, at (yasya) whose house (shraaddham) the offerings are 
performed, (bhavet) should do (tat) the same. 3:188

sitting. 3:189

invited for the performances (havya) towards the divinities and (kavye) towards the 
ancestors, (atikraaman) step over the boundaries of the proper conduct (api) even 
(kathañchit) by a bit, then those (paapaḥ) sinners (vrajet) roam as (sookarataam) pigs in 
the next life. 3:190

Traits of forefathers
अक्रोधनाः शौचपराः सततंब्र चा रणः ।

192. akrodhanaaḥ shauchaparaaḥ satatam brahmachaariṇaḥ,
nyastashastraa mahaabhaagaaḥ pitaraḥ poorvadevataaḥ. akrodhanaaḥ shauchaparaaḥ satatam brahmachaariṇaḥ,
ni-asta-shastraaḥ mahaa-bhaagaaḥ pitaraḥ poorva-devataaḥ.
(pitaraḥ) The ancestors are (akrodhanaaḥ) devoid of anger, (shauchaparaaḥ) eager 
towards cleanliness, (satatam) persistent (brahmachaariṇaḥ) celibates, 
(ni)(asta)(shastraaḥ) without any weapon, (mahaa)(bhaagaaḥ) extremely righteous and 
(poorva) the foremost (devataaḥ) divinities since the beginning of the creation. 3:192

(sarveṣhaam) all of (eteṣhaam) these ancestors, (yasmaat) their (utpattiḥ) origins (cha)
and (api) also (taan) those (niyamaiḥ) rules related to (ye) who (syuḥ) should 
(upacharyaaḥ) serve (yaiḥ) which ones of them. 3:193

196. daityadaanavayakṣhaaṇaaṅ gandharvoragarakṣhasaam,

of (daitya) the ones with big teeth, (daanava) the giants, (yakṣhaaṇaam) the revered, 
(gandharva) the singers, (uraga) the crawlers, (rakṣhasaam) the demons, (suparṇa) the 
fliers and the gliders (cha) and (kinnaraaṇaam) the eunuchs. 3:196

teṣhaam api iha vijñeyam putra-pautram anantakam.
(tu) And (anantakam) the numerous (putra) sons and (pautram) grandsons etc. born in 
the lineage (teṣhaam) of all of (ete) these (mukhyaaḥ) key (pitṛeeṇaam)(gaṇaaḥ) persons 
(ye) who (parikeerttitaaḥ) have been mentioned so far, they should (api) also (vijñeyam)
be considered as forefathers (iha) in this world. 3:200
ऋिषभ्यः िपतरो जाताः िपत

201. ṛiṣhibhyaḥ pitaro jaataaḥ pitṛibhyo devamaanavaaḥ,
devebhyastu jagatsarvañ charan sthaaṇvanupoorvashaḥ. ṛiṣhibhyaḥ pitaraḥ jaataaḥ pitṛibhyaḥ deva-maanavaaḥ,
devebhyaḥ tu jagat sarvam charam sthaaṇu anupoorvashaḥ.
(ṛiṣhibhyaḥ) From these sages (pitaraḥ) the forefathers (jaataaḥ) were born, (pitṛibhyaḥ)
from the forefathers both (deva) the divinites and (maanavaaḥ) the humans were born 
(tu) and (devebhyaḥ) from the divinities (sarvam) everything (charam) mobile or 
(sthaaṇu) stationary was born (anupoorvashaḥ) gradually (jagat) in this universe. 3:201
Procedure of making offerings to the ancestors
राजतैभार्जनैरेषामथो वा राजतािन्वतैः । वायर्िप श्रद्धया द म यायोपकल्पते॥२०२॥
राजतैः । भाजनैः ।एषाम्। अथो । वा । राजतािन्वतैः ॥ वा र । अिप । श्रद्धया । द म्। अ याय । उपकल्पते॥
202. raajatairbhaajanaireṣhaamatho vaa raajataanvitaiḥ,
vaaryapi shraddhayaa dattamakṣhayaayopakalpate. raajataiḥ bhaajanaiḥ eṣhaam atho vaa raajataanvitaiḥ,
vaari api shraddhayaa dattam akṣhayaaya upakalpate.
Even (shraddhayaa) faithful (dattam) offering of (api) just (vaari) water (eṣhaam) to 
these forefathers, (bhaajanaiḥ) from the utensils (raajataiḥ) made out of the silver 
metal (atho)(vaa) or (raajataanvitaiḥ) out of an alloy of the silver metal, (upakalpate)
creates (akṣhayaaya) undiminishing happiness for the offerors. 3:202
देवकायार्द

देवकायार्त्। िद्वजातीनाम्। िपतकायर्म ृ ्। िविशष्यते॥ दैवम्। िह । िपतकायर्स्य ृ । पवर्मू ्। आप्यायनम्। श्रतमु ्॥
203. devakaaryaaddvijaateenaam pitṛikaaryam vishiṣhyate,
daivaṅ hi pitṛikaaryasya poorvamaapyaayanañ shrutam.
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ३ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 3
307
deva-kaaryaat dvijaateenaam pitṛi-kaaryam vishiṣhyate,
daivam hi pitṛi-kaaryasya poorvam aapyaayanam shrutam.
(dvijaateenaam) For the twice borns, (kaaryam) making offerings (pitṛi) for the ancestors 
(vishiṣhyate) is more important than (kaaryaat) making offerings (deva) for the 
divinities, (hi) because the offerings (daivam) for the divinities is merely (shrutam)
considered as necessary (poorvam) prelude and (aapyaayanam) epilogue to (kaaryasya)
the offerings (pitṛi) for the ancestors. 3:203

िस । िह । िवलम्पिन्त ु । श्राद्धम्। आर विजर्तम्॥
204. teṣhaamaarakṣhabhootan tu poorvan daivan niyojayet,
rakṣhaansi hi vilumpanti shraaddhamaarakṣhavarjitam. teṣhaam aarakṣha-bhootam tu poorvam daivam niyojayet,
rakṣhaansi hi vilumpanti shraaddham aarakṣha-varjitam.
(daivam) The divinities (niyojayet) should be invoked (poorvam) first (tu)(aarakṣha) for 
the protections (teṣhaam) of these offerings made for (bhootam) the ancestors, (hi)
because (rakṣhaansi) the demons (vilumpanti) destroy (shraaddham) the offerings that 
are (varjitam) not (aarakṣha) protected. 3:204
दैवाद्यन्तंतदीहेत िपत्राद्यन्तंन तद्भवेत्
।
िपत्राद्यन्तंत्वीहमानः ि प्रंनश्यित सान्वयः ॥२०५॥
दैवाद्यन्तम्। तत्। ईहेत । िपत्राद्यन्तम्। न। तत्। भवेत्॥ िपत्राद्यन्तम्। तु। ईहमानः । ि प्रम्। नश्यित । सान्वयः ॥
205. daivaadyantan tadeeheta pitraadyantan na tadbhavet,
pitraadyantan tveehamaanaḥ kṣhipran nashyati saanvayaḥ. daiva-aadyantam tat eeheta pitra-aadyantam na tat bhavet,
pitra-aadyantam tu eehamaanaḥ kṣhipram nashyati saanvayaḥ.
(tat) That (eeheta) procedure of making offerings should (aadyantam) begin and end 
with the offerings (daiva) for the divinities and (tat) it (bhavet) should (na) not 
(aadyantam) begin or end with the offerings (pitra) for the ancestors. A person 
(eehamaanaḥ) desirous of making offerings (pitra) for the ancestors (aadyantam) in the 
beginning or at the end gets (kṣhipram) quickly (nashyati) destroyed (tu) indeed, 
(saanvayaḥ) along with his/her lineage. 3:205

206. shuchin desham viviktañ cha gomayenopalepayet,
dakṣhiṇaapravaṇañ chaiva prayatnenopapaadayet. shuchim desham viviktam cha gomayena upalepayet,
dakṣhiṇaa-pravaṇam cha eva prayatnena upapaadayet.
(upapaadayet) For the performance of offerings, (upalepayet) a thin coating (gomayena)
of cow dung should be applied over (shuchim) a clean (cha) and (viviktam) secluded 
(desham) place (cha) and that place (prayatnena)should effortfully be (pravaṇam) made 
sloping (dakṣhiṇaa) towards the southern direction (eva) as well. 3:206

207. avakaasheṣhu chokṣheṣhu nadeeteereṣhu chaiva hi,
vivikteṣhu cha tuṣhyanti dattena pitaraḥ sadaa. avakaasheṣhu cha ukṣheṣhu nadee-teereṣhu cha eva hi,
vivikteṣhu cha tuṣhyanti dattena pitaraḥ sadaa.
(pitaraḥ) The ancestors are (sadaa) always (tuṣhyanti)satisfied (dattena) by the offerings 
made (avakaasheṣhu) at open spaces (ukṣheṣhu) purified by sprinkling water (cha) or 
(nadee) at the river (teereṣhu) banks (cha) and (vivikteṣhu) at secluded places (eva)(hi)
as well. 3:207

(aasaneṣhu) The cushions, (barhiṣhmatsu) made out of grass fibers, (upaklṛipteṣhu)
properly laid out (pṛithak)(pṛithak) separately and purified (upaspṛiṣhṭa) by sprinkling 
(udakaan) water on them, should be (samyak) properly and respectfully (upaveshayet)
offered (taan) to these (vipraan) braahmaṇa as seats. 3:208

209. upaveshya tu taanvipraanaasaneṣhvajugupsitaan,

them, (poorvakam) starting with the ones who are designated to help (deva) with the 
offerings for the divinities. 3:209

210. teṣhaamudakamaaneeya sapavitraanstilaanapi,
agnau kuryaadanujñaato braahmaṇo braahmaṇaiḥ saha. teṣhaam udakam aaneeya sapavitraan tilaan api,

Besides (teṣhaam) these offerings, the host (braahmaṇaḥ) braahmaṇa should (api) also 
(aaneeya) bring (udakam) water (sapavitraan) along with clean (tilaan) sesame seeds 
and (anujñaataḥ) after taking the permission of the invited guests, (saha) accompanied 
(braahmaṇaiḥ) by those braahmaṇa, he/she (kuryaat) should make offerings (agnau) in 
the fire. 3:210

211. agneḥ somayamaabhyaañ cha kṛitvaa’’pyaayanamaaditaḥ,
havirdaanena vidhivatpashchaatsantarpayetpitṛeen. agneḥ soma-yamaabhyaam cha kṛitvaa aapyaayanam aaditaḥ,

(aaditaḥ) Starting (daanena) with giving (haviḥ)the offerings (agneḥ) for the fire divinity, 
(soma) the divinity of the cooling herbs (cha) and (yamaabhyaam) the death divinity and 
(pashchaat) after (kṛitvaa) having (aapyaayanam) satisfied them, one should (vidhivat)
properly (santarpayet) satisfy (pitṛeen) the ancestors. 3:211

212. agnyabhaave tu viprasya paaṇaavevopapaadayet,
yo hyagniḥ sa dvijo viprairmantradarshibhiruchyate. agni abhaave tu viprasya paaṇau eva upapaadayet,
yaḥ hi agniḥ saḥ dvijaḥ vipraiḥ mantra-darshibhiḥ uchyate.
If (agni) the fire (abhaave) is not available (tu) then the offering mentioned in the prior 
shloka (upapaadayet) should be placed on (viprasya) the braahmaṇa’s (paaṇau) hands
(eva) itself, (hi) because it (uchyate) has been said (vipraiḥ) by the sages (darshibhiḥ) well 
acquainted (mantra) with the Vedas, “(yaḥ) that (agniḥ) fire is (saḥ) the (dvijaḥ)
braahmaṇa indeed”. 3:212

213. akrodhanaansuprasaadaanvadantyetaanpuraatanaan,
lokasyaapyaayane yuktaañchhraaddhadevaandvijottamaan. akrodhanaan suprasaadaan vadanti etaan puraatanaan,
lokasya aapyaayane yuktaan shraaddha-devaan dvija-uttamaan.
They also (vadanti) call (etaan) these (uttamaan) superiors amongst (dvija) the twiceborns, who (akrodhanaan) are free from anger, (suprasaadaan) are happy, 
(puraatanaan) have been acclaimed since a long time and (yuktaan) are engaged 
(aapyaayane) in the upliftment (lokasya) of the world, as (devaan) the divinities 
presiding over (shraaddha) the process of offerings for the ancestors. 3:213

214. apasavyamagnau kṛitvaa sarvamaavṛitya vikramam,

(kṛitvaa) Having made offerings (agnau) in the fire (apasavyam) while wearing the 
sacred thread on the right shoulder, one should (vikramam) sequentially (aavṛitya)
arrange (sarvam) all of the remaining materials in the southern direction, after which

215. treenstu tasmaaddhaviḥ sheṣhaatpiṇḍaankṛitvaa samaahitaḥ,

One (kṛitvaa) should make (treen) three (piṇḍaan) piles* (tasmaat) from the materials 
(sheṣhaat) left after (haviḥ) the offerings in the fire, (tu) and while (mukhaḥ) facing 
(dakṣhiṇaa) south (samaahitaḥ) with a concentrated mind, (nirvapet) should keep them 
down on grass (eva) as well, in a fashion similar (vidhinaa) to the procedure of 
(audakena) sprinkling the water, *one pile for the ancestors from each of the three 
preceding generations. 3:215

216. nyupya piṇḍaanstatastaanstu prayato vidhipoorvakam,

(tu) And (nyupya) after having (prayataḥ) effortfully placed (taan) those three (piṇḍaan)
piles (tataḥ) there (poorvakam) as per (vidhi) the prescribed norms, one (nimṛijyaat)
should wipe (lepa) any leftovers stuck (tam) to one’s (hastam) hands (teṣhu) on the 
(darbheṣhu) grass, (bhaaginaam) considering it for the ancestors as well. 3:216

217. aachamyodakparaavṛitya triraayamya shanairasoon,
ṣhaḍṛitooñshcha namaskuryaatpitṛeeneva cha mantravit.
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ३ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 3
312
aachamya udak paraavṛitya triḥ aayamya shanaiḥ asoon,
ṣhaḍ ṛitoon cha namaḥ-kuryaat pitṛeen eva cha mantravit. 
Then (paraavṛitya) facing the opposite direction i.e. north, (aachamya) having sipped 
(udak) water (cha) and (aayamya) having controlled one’s breathing by performing (triḥ)
three cycles of (shanaiḥ)slow (asoon) breaths, (mantravit)the apprehender of the Vedas 
(kuryaat) should (namaḥ) bow to the divinities of (ṣhaḍ) the six (ṛitoon) seasons (cha)
and (pitṛeen) to the ancestors (eva) as well.

avajighrechcha taanpiṇḍaanyathaanyuptaansamaahitaḥ. udakam ninayet sheṣham shanaiḥ piṇḍa-antike punaḥ, 
avajighret cha taan piṇḍaan yathaanyuptaan samaahitaḥ. 
One should (punaḥ) again (shanaiḥ) slowly (ninayet) disperse (sheṣham) the remaining 
(udakam) water (antike) near those three (piṇḍa) piles (cha) and then should 
(samaahitaḥ) with focus, (avajighret) smell (taan) those (piṇḍaan) piles 
(yathaanyuptaan) in the order they were placed. 3:218

220. dhriyamaaṇe tu pitari poorveṣhaameva nirvapet,
vipravadvaa’pi tañ shraaddhe svakam pitaramaashayet. dhriyamaaṇe tu pitari poorveṣhaam eva nirvapet,

(tu) If one’s (pitari) father (dhriyamaaṇe) is still alive, (eva) even then the procedure 
(nirvapet)should be completed (poorveṣhaam) for the ancestors from prior generations. 
(shraaddhe) During this procedure, one can (api) also (vaa) optionally have (tam) one’s 
(svakam) own (pitaram) father seated and (aashayet) fed (vipravat) similar to the 
braahmaṇa. 3:220

221. pitaa yasya nivṛittaḥ syaajjeevechchaapi pitaamahaḥ,

and (pitaamahaḥ) the grandfather (api) is still (jeevet) alive, then (saḥ) one should first

followed by the offerings (keertayet) in the name (prapitaamaham) of the great 
grandfather etc. 3:221

(vaa) Optionally (pitaamahaḥ) the grandfather (bhuñjeeta) can feast (tat) on those 
(shraaddham) offerings, (iti) so (abraveet) said (manuḥ) Maharṣhi Manu. (vaa) Or 
(samanujñaataḥ) having obtained the permission of the grandfather, as per (svayam)
his/her own (kaamam) desire, the host (samaacharet) can choose and invite the 
braahmaṇa (eva) as well, who would consume those offerings. 3:222

229. naasramaapaatayejjaatu na kupyennaanṛitam vadet, 
na paadena spṛishedannañ na chaitadavadhoonayet. na asram aapaatayet jaatu na kupyet na anṛitam vadet,

During this procedure, the host (na) should not (jaatu) ever (aapaatayet) shed (asram)
a single tear, should (na) not (kupyet) get angry, should (na) not (vadet) tell (anṛitam)
lies, should (na) not (spṛishet) touch (annam) the food or the container (paadena) with 
feet (cha) and should (na) not (avadhoonayet) throw (etat) the food in the container.

230. asraṅ gamayati pretaankopo’reenanṛitañ shunaḥ, 
paadasparshastu rakṣhaansi duṣhkṛiteenavadhoonanam. asram gamayati pretaan kopaḥ areen anṛitam shunaḥ,

At that time, (asram) the tears (gamayati)send the food (pretaan) to the ghosts, (kopaḥ)
anger sends it (areen) to the enemies, (anṛitam) lies send it (shunaḥ) to dogs, (sparshaḥ)
touching with (paada) feet sends it (rakṣhaansi) to demons (tu) and (avadhoonanam)
throwing sends it (duṣhkṛiteen) to the sinners. 3:230

(dadyaat) should be given (amatsaraḥ) without any sorrow or attachment (cha) and

(kuryaat) engage in (kathaaḥ) discussions and stories (brahmodyaaḥ) related to God.

232. svaadhyaayañ shraavayetpitrye dharmashaastraaṇi chaiva hi,

(pitrye) During this procedure of offerings for the ancestors, one should (hi) indeed 
(shraavayet) listen to discourses about (svaadhyaayam)self study, (shaastraaṇi) treatise

233. harṣhayedbraahmaṇaanstuṣhṭo bhojayechcha shanaiḥ shanaiḥ,
annaadyenaasakṛichchaitaan guṇaishcha parichodayet. harṣhayet braahmaṇaan tuṣhṭaḥ bhojayet cha shanaiḥ shanaiḥ,
annaadyena asakṛit cha etaan guṇaiḥ cha parichodayet.
(tuṣhṭaḥ) The contented host (harṣhayet) should please (braahmaṇaan) the braahmaṇa 
(cha) and (bhojayet) offer them food (shanaiḥ)(shanaiḥ) slowly and gradually. (cha) And 
the host (parichodayet) should inspire them to consume more by (asakṛit) repeatedly 
reciting (guṇaiḥ) the qualities (anna)(aadyena) of the food items (cha) and offering food
(etaan) to them. 3:233

234. vratasthamapi dauhitrañ shraaddhe yatnena bhojayet,
kutapañ chaasane dadyaattilaishcha vikirenmaheem. vratastham api dauhitram shraaddhe yatnena bhojayet,
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ३ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 3
318
kutapam cha aasane dadyaat tilaiḥ cha vikiret maheem.
If (dauhitram)the daughter’s son is (vratastham) a determined student (api) as well then 
he should be (yatnena) effortfully (bhojayet) fed (shraaddhe) during this procedure of 
making offerings for the ancestors. He (dadyaat) should be given (kutapam) a blanket 
(aasane) to sit on (cha) and (tilaiḥ) the sesame seeds (vikiret) should be dispersed 
(maheem) on the ground at that place. 3:234

235. treeṇi shraaddhe pavitraaṇi dauhitraḥ kutapastilaaḥ,
treeṇi chaatra prashansanti shauchamakrodhamatvaraam. treeṇi shraaddhe pavitraaṇi dauhitraḥ kutapaḥ tilaaḥ,
treeṇi cha atra prashansanti shaucham akrodham atvaraam.
(shraaddhe) During this procedure of offerings for the ancestors, (dauhitraḥ) the 
daughter’s son, (kutapaḥ) the blanket and (tilaaḥ) the sesame seeds, these (treeṇi) three 
are considered (pavitraaṇi) pure. (cha) And (treeṇi) the three aspects that (prashansanti)
are praised (atra) here are (shaucham) cleanliness, (akrodham) absence of anger and 
(atvaraam) no rush. 3:235

236. atyuṣhṇan sarvamannan syaadbhuñjeeranste cha vaagyataaḥ,
na cha dvijaatayo brooyurdaatraa pṛiṣhṭaa havirguṇaan. ati-uṣhṇam sarvam annam syaat bhuñjeeran te cha vaagyataaḥ,
na cha dvijaatayaḥ brooyuḥ daatraa pṛiṣhṭaa haviḥ guṇaan.
(sarvam) All (annam) of the food (syaat) should be (ati) very (uṣhṇam) hot i.e. freshly 
cooked (cha) and (te) those (dvijaatayaḥ) braahmaṇa (bhuñjeeran) should consume it 
(vaagyataaḥ) while controlling their speech i.e. quietly. (cha) And they should (na) not 
(brooyuḥ) say anything (guṇaan) about the quality (haviḥ) of the offerings even when 
specifically (pṛiṣhṭaa) asked (daatraa) by the host. 3:236

237. yaavaduṣhṇam bhavatyannañ yaavadashnanti vaagyataaḥ,
pitarastaavadashnanti yaavannoktaa havirguṇaaḥ. yaavat uṣhṇam bhavati annam yaavat ashnanti vaagyataaḥ,
pitaraḥ taavat ashnanti yaavat na uktaa haviḥ guṇaaḥ.
(yaavat) Until when (annam) the food (bhavati) remains (uṣhṇam) hot, (yaavat) until 
when the braahmaṇa (ashnanti) eat (vaagyataaḥ) quietly and (yaavat) until when they 
(na) do not (uktaa) mention (guṇaaḥ) the quality (haviḥ) of the offerings, only (taavat)
till then (pitaraḥ) the ancestors (ashnanti) consume the offerings. 3:237

238. yadveṣhṭitashiraa bhuṅkte yadbhuṅkte dakṣhiṇaamukhaḥ,
sopaanatkashcha yadbhuṅkte tadvai rakṣhaansi bhuñjate. yat veṣhṭitashiraa bhuṅkte yat bhuṅkte dakṣhiṇaa-mukhaḥ,
sopaanatkaḥ cha yat bhuṅkte tat vai rakṣhaansi bhuñjate.
(yat) The food (bhuṅkte) consumed by one whose (shiraa) head (veṣhṭita) is covered, by 
one who (mukhaḥ) is facing (dakṣhiṇaa) south, (cha) or by one who (sopaanatkaḥ) is 
wearing shoes, (tat) that food is (vai) indeed (bhuñjate) consumed (rakṣhaansi) by the 
demons. 3:238

239. chaṇḍaalashcha varaahashcha kukkuṭaḥ shvaa tathaiva cha,

(chaṇḍaalaḥ) A predacious human, (varaahaḥ) a pig, (kukkuṭaḥ) a rooster, (shvaa) a dog, 
(rajasvalaa) a menstruating woman (tathaa) or (ṣhaṇḍhaḥ) a transgender (eva) as well,
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ३ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 3

should (na) not (eekṣheran) be able to see (ashnataḥ) the feasting (dvijaan) braahmaṇa.

240. home pradaane bhojye cha yadebhirabhiveekṣhyate,
daive karmaṇi pitrye vaa tadgachchhatyayathaatatham. home pradaane bhojye cha yat ebhiḥ abhiveekṣhyate,
daive karmaṇi pitrye vaa tat gachchhati ayathaatatham.
(karmaṇi) During the performance of (daive) offerings for the divinities (vaa) or (pitrye)
the ancestors, (home) offerings in the fire, (pradaane) charitable donations (cha) or 
(bhojye) feeding the braahmaṇa, (yat) whatever (ebhiḥ)things (abhiveekṣhyate) are seen 
by these individuals or animals, (tat) they all (gachchhati) go (ayathaatatham) haywire.

241. ghraaṇena sookaro hanti pakṣhavaatena kukkuṭaḥ,
shvaa tu dṛiṣhṭinipaatena sparshenaavaravarṇajaḥ. ghraaṇena sookaraḥ hanti pakṣha-vaatena kukkuṭaḥ,
shvaa tu dṛiṣhṭi-nipaatena sparshena avara-varṇa-jaḥ.
(sookaraḥ) A pig (hanti) destroys the utility of those things (ghraaṇena) by smelling
them, (kukkuṭaḥ) a rooster (pakṣha) by fanning (vaatena) air on them, (shvaa) a dog 
(nipaatena) by casting its (dṛiṣhṭi) eye on them (tu) and (avaravarṇajaḥ) an individual
born in lower cast (sparshena) by touching them. 3:241

242. khañjo vaa yadi vaa kaaṇo daatuḥ preṣhyo’pi vaa bhavet,

321
heena-atirikta-gaatraḥ vaa tam api apanayet punaḥ.
(yadi) If a person (khañjaḥ) with a defective limb (vaa) or (kaaṇaḥ) with a defective eye, 
(vaa) or someone with disproportionate, (heena) missing (vaa) or (atirikta) extra 
(gaatraḥ) organs, shows up at that place, (tam) he/she should (api) also be (punaḥ)
immediately (apanayet) removed, (vaa)(api) even if he/she (bhavet) is (preṣhyaḥ) a 
servant (daatuḥ) of the host. 3:242

243. braahmaṇam bhikṣhukam vaa’pi bhojanaarthamupasthitam,
braahmaṇairabhyanujñaataḥ shaktitaḥ pratipoojayet. braahmaṇam bhikṣhukam vaa api bhojanaartham upasthitam,
braahmaṇaiḥ abhi-anujñaataḥ shaktitaḥ prati-poojayet.
If (braahmaṇam) a braahmaṇa (vaa) or (bhikṣhukam) a beggar (upasthitam) shows up 
(bhojanaartham) looking for food, then (abhi)(anujñaataḥ) after seeking the permission 
(braahmaṇaiḥ) of the invited braahmaṇa, they should (api) also (prati)(poojayet) be 
served (shaktitaḥ) as permitted by the means of the host. 3:243

244. saarvavarṇikamannaadyan sanneeyaaplaavya vaariṇaa,
samutsṛijedbhuktavataamagrato vikiranbhuvi. saarva-varṇikam annaadyam sanneeya aaplaavya vaariṇaa,
samutsṛijet bhuktavataam agrataḥ vikiran bhuvi.
The left over (annaadyam) foods (saarva) of all (varṇikam) kinds should be (sanneeya)
taken and (aaplaavya) mixed together (vaariṇaa) with water and then should (vikiran)
be spread and (sam)(utsṛijet) dropped on the mats placed (bhuvi) on the earth (agrataḥ)
in front (bhuktavataam) of the feasted braahmaṇa. 3:244

245. asanskṛitaprameetaanaan tyaaginaaṅ kulayoṣhitaam,
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ३ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 3
322
uchchhiṣhṭam bhaagadheyan syaaddarbheṣhu vikirashcha yaḥ. asanskṛita-prameetaanaam tyaaginaam kula-yoṣhitaam,
uchchhiṣhṭam bhaagadheyam syaat darbheṣhu vikiraḥ cha yaḥ.
(yaḥ) The food (vikiraḥ) scattered (darbheṣhu) on the grass mats (cha) and other 
(uchchhiṣhṭam) leftover food (syaat) is (bhaagadheyam) meant (prameetaanaam) for 
those dead children (asanskṛita) whose cremation rites were not performed and for 
those (tyaaginaam) who have forsaken (kula) cultured (yoṣhitaam) women. 3:245

246. uchchheṣhaṇam bhoomigatamajihmasyaashaṭhasya cha,
daasavargasya tatpitrye bhaagadheyam prachakṣhate. uchchheṣhaṇam bhoomi-gatam ajihmasya ashaṭhasya cha,
daasa-vargasya tat pitrye bhaagadheyam prachakṣhate.
(pitrye) During the process of making offerings for the ancestors, (uchchheṣhaṇam) the 
leftover food (tat) that (gatam) fell (bhoomi) on the ground, (prachakṣhate) is said to be 
(bhaagadheyam) meant (vargasya) for the group of (daasa) servants that are 
(ashaṭhasya) free from malice (cha) and are (ajihmasya) not conniving. 3:246

247. aasapiṇḍakriyaakarma dvijaateḥ sansthitasya tu,
adaivam bhojayechchhraaddham piṇḍamekan tu nirvapet. aa sapiṇḍa-kriyaa-karma dvijaateḥ sansthitasya tu,

(tu) In case of (dvijaateḥ) a twice born’s recent (sansthitasya) death, (aa) until (sapiṇḍa)
all of the associated rites (kriyaa) prescribed after death are (karma) completed, 
(nirvapet) perform (shraaddham) offerings for his/her soul by just (bhojayet) feeding 
one braahmaṇa (tu) with (ekam) one (piṇḍam) pile of offerings, (adaivam) without 
performing offerings for the divinities before or after it. 3:247

248. sahapiṇḍakriyaayaan tu kṛitaayaamasya dharmataḥ,
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ३ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 3
323

anayaa eva aavṛitaa kaaryam piṇḍa-nirvapaṇam sutaiḥ.
(tu) However, once all of (saha) the associated (piṇḍa) rites (kriyaayaam) prescribed 
after death (kṛitaayaam) are completed for this individual, then (asya) his/her (sutaiḥ)
children should (dharmataḥ) righteously (nirvapaṇam) complete (kaaryam) the process 
(piṇḍa) of making offerings (aavṛitaa) following (anayaa)(eva) the entire procedure 
discussed earlier. 3:248

249. shraaddham bhuktvaa ya uchchhiṣhṭam vṛiṣhalaaya prayachchhati,
sa mooḍho narakañ yaati kaalasootramavaakshiraaḥ. shraaddham bhuktvaa yaḥ uchchhiṣhṭam vṛiṣhalaaya prayachchhati,
saḥ mooḍhaḥ narakam yaati kaala-sootram avaak-shiraaḥ.
(bhuktvaa) Having feasted (shraaddham) on these offering, the braahmaṇa (yaḥ) who 
(prayachchhati) gives his (uchchhiṣhṭam) leftovers (vṛiṣhalaaya) to a shoodra, (saḥ) he is 
a (mooḍhaḥ) fool, (avaak) with a fallen (shiraaḥ) head i.e. discredited, who (yaati) goes 
(narakam) to the hell named (kaala)(sootram) kaalasootra. 3:249

250. shraaddhabhugvṛiṣhaleetalpan tadaharyo’dhigachchhati,
tasyaaḥ pureeṣhe tanmaasam pitarastasya sherate. shraaddha-bhuk vṛiṣhalee-talpam tat ahaḥ yaḥ adhigachchhati,
tasyaaḥ pureeṣhe tat maasam pitaraḥ tasya sherate.
The one (yaḥ) who after (bhuk) feasting (shraaddha) on these offering, (adhigachchhati)
goes (talpam) to bed (vṛiṣhalee) with a shoodra woman on (tat) that same (ahaḥ) day, 
(tasya) his (pitaraḥ) ancestors (sherate) sleep (pureeṣhe) in the feces of (tasyaaḥ) that 
shoodra woman for (tat) that entire (maasam) month. 3:250

251. pṛiṣhṭvaa svaditamityevan tṛiptaanaachaamayettataḥ,
aachaantaañshchaanujaaneeyaadabhito ramyataamiti. pṛiṣhṭvaa svaditam iti evam tṛiptaan aachaamayet tataḥ,
aachaantaan cha anujaaneeyaat abhitaḥ ramyataam iti.
“(svaditam) Did you enjoy the delicious food?” (tataḥ) after (pṛiṣhṭvaa) asking (iti) this, 
(aachaamayet) offer water to those (tṛiptaan) contented braahmaṇa (evam)(cha) and 
after they have (aachaantaan) had water, (anujaaneeyaat) humbly request them, (iti)
“Please (ramyataam) take some rest (abhitaḥ) here.” 3:251

252. svadhaa’stvityeva tam brooyurbraahmaṇaastadanantaram,
svadhaakaaraḥ paraṅ hyaasheeḥ sarveṣhu pitṛikarmasu. svadhaa astu iti eva tam brooyuḥ braahmaṇaaḥ tat anantaram,

(anantaram) After (tat) that (braahmaṇaaḥ) the braahmaṇa should (eva) as well bless 
(tam) the host by (brooyuḥ) saying, (iti) “May there (astu) be (svadhaa) happiness” (hi)
because (sarveṣhu) in all of (karmasu) the procedures of offerings (pitṛi) for the 
ancestors, (svadhaakaaraḥ) blessings for happiness are considered (param)the ultimate 
(aasheeḥ) blessings. 3:252

253. tato bhuktavataan teṣhaamannasheṣhan nivedayet,

(tataḥ) Once (dvijaiḥ) the braahmaṇa (bhuktavataam) have been fed, (nivedayet)
humbly ask (teṣhaam) them about (sheṣham) the remaining (anna) food and (tataḥ)

then (anujñaataḥ) with their permission (kuryaat) do (tathaa) as they (yathaa)(brooyuḥ)
say. 3:253

254. pitrye svaditamityeva vaachyaṅ goṣhṭhe tu sushrutam,
sampannamityabhyudaye daive ruchitamityapi. pitrye svaditam iti eva vaachyam goṣhṭhe tu sushrutam,
sampannam iti abhyudaye daive ruchitam iti api.
(pitrye) While making the offerings for the ancestors, the host (vaachyam) should ask 
(iti) this to the braahmaṇa, “Was the food (svaditam) delicious?”, (eva) as well as, 
(goṣhṭhe) while discussing the virtues of the ancestors, “Was everything (sushrutam)
worth listening to?”, (abhyudaye) while planning the family future, (iti) “how should 
(sampannam) the prosperity be maintained?”, (tu) and (api) also (daive) while making 
the offerings for the divinities, (iti) “Was everything (ruchitam) pleasurable?” 3:254

अपरा ः । तथा । दभार्ः । वास्तसम्पादनम ु ्। ितलाः ॥ सि ः ृ । मि ः ृ । िद्वजाः । च । अ याः । श्राद्धकमर्सु। सम्पदः ॥
255. aparaahṇastathaa darbhaa vaastusampaadanan tilaaḥ,
sṛiṣhṭirmṛiṣhṭirdvijaashchaagryaaḥ shraaddhakarmasu sampadaḥ. aparaahṇaḥ tathaa darbhaaḥ vaastu-sampaadanam tilaaḥ,
sṛiṣhṭiḥ mṛiṣhṭiḥ dvijaaḥ cha agryaaḥ shraaddha-karmasu sampadaḥ.
(aparaahṇaḥ) The time of the afternoon, (darbhaaḥ) the grass mats, (sampaadanam) a 
clean and well arranged (vaastu) house (tathaa) and (tilaaḥ)sesame seeds, (sṛiṣhṭiḥ) the 
food that is (mṛiṣhṭiḥ) cleaned and cooked properly (cha) and (agryaaḥ) the topmost 
(dvijaaḥ) braahmaṇa, these are considered as (sampadaḥ) the wealth (karmasu) during 
the procedure (shraaddha) of making offeringsfor the ancestors. 3:255

256. darbhaaḥ pavitram poorvaahṇo haviṣhyaaṇi cha sarvashaḥ,
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ३ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 3

pavitrañ yachcha poorvoktam vijñeyaa havyasampadaḥ. darbhaaḥ pavitram poorvaahṇaḥ haviṣhyaaṇi cha sarvashaḥ,
pavitram yat cha poorvoktam vijñeyaaaḥ havya-sampadaḥ.
(darbhaaḥ) The grass mats, (pavitram) the purifying chants of the mantras, 
(poorvaahṇaḥ) the time before noon (cha) and (sarvashaḥ) all of (haviṣhyaaṇi) the 
materials meant for offerings, (cha) as well as, those (pavitram) pious thing (yat) that 
were mentioned (poorvoktam) in the prior shloka, (vijñeyaaaḥ) consider all of them as 
(sampadaḥ) the wealth (havya) of the procedure of making offerings for the divinities.

257. munyannaani payaḥ somo maansañ yachchaanupaskṛitam,
akṣhaaralavaṇañ chaiva prakṛityaa haviruchyate. muni-annaani payaḥ somaḥ maansam yat cha anupaskṛitam,
akṣhaara-lavaṇam cha eva prakṛityaa haviḥ uchyate.
(annaani) The food items recommended for (muni) the people in the third stage of their 
life i.e. preparation for renunciation, (payaḥ) milk, (somaḥ) juices (cha) and those 
(maansam) meats (yat) that (anupaskṛitam) are free from foul odor and other defects 
(cha) and (akṣhaara)(lavaṇam) the rock salt (eva) as well, these things (prakṛityaa) by 
their nature (uchyate) are said to good (haviḥ) for making offerings. 3:257

258. visṛijya braahmaṇaanstaanstu niyato vaagyataḥ shuchiḥ,

(tu) After (visṛijya)seeing off (taan) those (braahmaṇaan) braahmaṇa that were invited, 
the host should (vaagyataḥ) silently and (aakaaṅkṣhan) expectantly face (dakṣhiṇaam)
the southern (disham) direction with (shuchiḥ) a clean and (niyataḥ) focused mind and 
(yaacheta) ask (pitṛeen) the ancestors (imaan) for these (varaan) boons. 3:258
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ३ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 3

दातारो नोऽिभवधर्न्तांवेदाः सन्तितरेव च ।

259. daataaro no’bhivardhantaam vedaaḥ santatireva cha,
shraddhaa cha no maa vyagamadbahudeyañ cha no’stviti. daataaraḥ naḥ abhi-vardhantaam vedaaḥ santatiḥ eva cha,
shraddhaa cha naḥ maa vyagamat bahu-deyam cha naḥ astu iti.
Ask for (iti) this, “In (naḥ) our lineage, may the number of (daataaraḥ) donors, (vedaaḥ)
students and teachers of the Vedas (cha) and (santatiḥ) offsprings (eva) as well (abhi)
always (vardhantaam) increase, may (naḥ) we (maa) never (vyagamat) move away 
(shraddhaa) from faith (cha) and devotion (cha) and may there (astu) be (bahu) plenty 
of wealth (naḥ) for us (deyam) to donate.” 3:259

260. evan nirvapaṇaṅ kṛitvaa piṇḍaanstaanstadanantaram,
gaam vipramajamagnim vaa praashayedapsu vaa kṣhipet. evam nirvapaṇam kṛitvaa piṇḍaan taan tat anantaram,
gaam vipram ajam agnim vaa praashayet apsu vaa kṣhipet.
(tat)(anantaram) After (kṛitvaa) having (nirvapaṇam) completed the performance of 
offerings (evam) like this, the host should take the remainder of (taan) those three 
(piṇḍaan) piles and should either (praashayet) feed it to (gaam) a cow, (vipram) a 
braahmaṇa, (ajam) a goat (vaa) or (agnim) to the fire (vaa) or (kṣhipet) throw it (apsu)
in the water. 3:260

261. piṇḍanirvapaṇaṅ kechit parastaadeva kurvate,

328

(kechit) Some scholars recommend (kurvate)(nirvapaṇam) disposing off (piṇḍa) the piles 
(parastaat)(eva) immediately after feeding the braahmaṇa, some (anye) others 
recommend (khaadayanti) feeding them (vayobhiḥ) to birds and some recommend 
(prakṣhipanti) throwing them (anale) into fire (vaa) or (apsu) into water bodies. 3:261

262. pativrataa dharmapatnee pitṛipoojanatatparaa,
madhyaman tu tataḥ piṇḍamadyaatsamyaksutaarthinee. pati-vrataa dharma-patnee pitṛi-poojana-tatparaa,

A (dharma) righteous and (pati)(vrataa) devoted (patnee) wife who is (tatparaa) eager 
(poojana) to serve (pitṛi) the ancestors and (sutaarthinee) desires a son, she should take 
(madhyamam) the middle (piṇḍam) pile from (tataḥ) there and (tu) then (adyaat)should 
eat it (samyak) properly with devotion. 3:262

263. aayuṣhmantan sutan soote yashomedhaasamanvitam,
dhanavantam prajaavantan saattvikan dhaarmikan tathaa. aayuṣhmantam sutam soote yasho-medhaa-samanvitam,
dhanavantam prajaavantam saattvikam dhaarmikam tathaa.
The lady who consumes this pile (soote) gives birth (sutam) to a son who 
(aayuṣhmantam) has longevity, (samanvitam) is blessed with (medhaa) intellect and 
(yasho) fame and is (dhanavantam) the holder of wealth, (prajaavantam) children, 
(saattvikam) purity (tathaa) and (dhaarmikam) righteousness. 3:263
प्र ाल्य हस्तावाचम्य  ाितप्रायंप्रकल्पयेत

264. prakṣhaalya hastaavaachamya jñaatipraayam prakalpayet,
jñaatibhyaḥ satkṛitan dattvaa baandhavaanapi bhojayet.
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ३ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 3
329
prakṣhaalya hastau aachamya jñaati-praayam prakalpayet,
jñaatibhyaḥ satkṛitam dattvaa baandhavaan api bhojayet. 
And then (prakṣhaalya) having washed (hastau) both hands and (aachamya) having 
sipped water, the host (prakalpayet) should serve (praayam) several individuals from 
his/her (jñaati) clan/class and after (dattvaa) having given (satkṛitam) a proper welcome 
(jñaatibhyaḥ) to his/her clan, one should (api) also (bhojayet) feed his/her 
(baandhavaan) family members and relatives. 3:264

265. uchchheṣhaṇan tu tattiṣhṭhedyaavadvipraa visarjitaaḥ, 
tato gṛihabaliṅ kuryaaditi dharmo vyavasthitaḥ. ut-sheṣhaṇam tu tat tiṣhṭhet yaavat vipraaḥ visarjitaaḥ, 
tataḥ gṛiha-balim kuryaat iti dharmaḥ vyavasthitaḥ. 
(tu) Let (tat) that (ut)(sheṣhaṇam) remaining food (tiṣhṭhet) be as is (yaavat) until 
(vipraaḥ)the braahmaṇa (visarjitaaḥ) have departed, and (tataḥ)then (kuryaat) perform 
(gṛiha)(balim) Balivaishvadeva yajña, (iti) this (vyavasthitaḥ) is sanctified (dharmaḥ) in 
the code of conduct. 3:265

266. haviryachchiraraatraaya yachchaanantyaaya kalpate, 
pitṛibhyo vidhivaddattan tatpravakṣhyaamyasheṣhataḥ. haviḥ yat chira-raatraaya yat cha aanantyaaya kalpate,
pitṛibhyaḥ vidhivat dattam tat pravakṣhyaami asheṣhataḥ. 
For (yat) how (chira)(raatraaya) long do these (haviḥ) offerings (vidhivat) properly 
(dattam) given (pitṛibhyaḥ) for the ancestors (kalpate) keep them (aanantyaaya)
satisfied (cha) and happy, I will now (pravakṣhyaami) describe (tat) that (asheṣhataḥ) in 
its entirety. 3:266

267. tilairvreehiyavairmaaṣhairadbhirmoolaphalena vaa,
dattena maasan tṛipyanti vidhivatpitaro nṛeeṇaam. tilaiḥ vreehi-yavaiḥ maaṣhaiḥ adbhiḥ moola-phalena vaa,
dattena maasam tṛipyanti vidhivat pitaraḥ nṛeeṇaam.
With the offerings of (tilaiḥ) the sesame seeds, (vreehi) rice, (yavaiḥ) barley, (maaṣhaiḥ)
lentils, (adbhiḥ) water, (moola) root vegetables (vaa) or (phalena) fruits, that are 
(vidhivat) properly (dattena) given, (pitaraḥ) the ancestors (nṛeeṇaam) of the humans 
(tṛipyanti) remain content (maasam) for one month. 3:267

268. dvau maasau matsyamaansena treen maasaan haariṇena tu,
aurabhreṇaatha chaturaḥ shaakunenaatha pañcha vai. dvau maasau matsya-maansena treen maasaan haariṇena tu,
aurabhreṇa atha chaturaḥ shaakunena atha pañcha vai.
(dvau) For two (maasau) months (maansena) with the meat (matsya) of the fishes, 
(treen) for three (maasaan) months with the meat (haariṇena) from a deer, (chaturaḥ)
for four months with the meat (aurabhreṇa) from a ram (atha)(tu) and (pañcha) for five 
months with the meat (shaakunena) from the birds (vai) indeed. 3:268

269. ṣhaṇmaasaañshchhaagamaansena paarṣhatena cha sapta vai,
aṣhṭaaveṇasya maansena rauraveṇa navaiva tu. ṣhaṇ-maasaan chhaaga-maansena paarṣhatena cha sapta vai,
aṣhṭau eṇasya maansena rauraveṇa nava eva tu.
(ṣhaṇ) For six (maasaan) months (maansena) with the meat (chhaaga) of a goat, (sapta)
for seven months with the meat (paarṣhatena) from a spotted deer (vai) indeed, 
(aṣhṭau) for eight months (maansena) with the meat (eṇasya) of a blackbuck (cha)(tu)
and (nava) for nine months with the meat (rauraveṇa) from a golden deer (eva) as well.

270. dashamaasaanstu tṛipyanti varaahamahiṣhaamiṣhaiḥ,
shashakoormayostu maansena maasaanekaadashaiva tu. dasha-maasaan tu tṛipyanti varaaha-mahiṣha-aamiṣhaiḥ,

(tu) And they (tṛipyanti) remain content (dasha) for ten (maasaan) months with the 
offerings (aamiṣhaiḥ) of the meat (varaaha) of a boar and (mahiṣha) a buffalo (tu) and 
(ekaadasha) for eleven (maasaan) months (maansena) with the meat of (shasha) a 
rabbit (tu) and (koormayoḥ) a turtle (eva) as well. 3:270

271. samvatsaran tu gavyena payasaa paayasena cha,
vaardhreeṇasasya maansena tṛiptirdvaadashavaarṣhikee. samvatsaram tu gavyena payasaa paayasena cha,
vaardhreeṇasasya maansena tṛiptiḥ dvaadasha-vaarṣhikee.
(tu) And (samvatsaram) for the whole year (gavyena) with the cow’s (payasaa) milk (cha)
and (paayasena) its pudding and remain (tṛiptiḥ) content (dvaadasha) for twelve 
(vaarṣhikee) years (maansena) with the meat (vaardhreeṇasasya) of an old goat with 
long ears. 3:271

272. kaalashaakam mahaashalkaaḥ khaḍgalohaamiṣham madhu,
aanantyaayaiva kalpyante munyannaani cha sarvashaḥ. kaala-shaakam mahaa-shalkaaḥ khaḍga-loha-aamiṣham madhu,
aanantyaaya eva kalpyante muni-annaani cha sarvashaḥ.
Feeding (kaala)(shaakam) the white jute plant, (mahaa)(shalkaaḥ) a fish with a lot of 
scales, (aamiṣham) the meat of (khaḍga) a rhinoceros or of (loha) a red goat, (madhu)
honey (cha) and (sarvashaḥ) all kind of (annaani) foods suitable for (muni) the people in 
the Vaanprastha stage of life (eva) as well, (kalpyante) enables the ancestors to be 
content (aanantyaaya) forever. 3:272

273. yatkiñchinmadhunaa mishram pradadyaattu trayodasheem,
tadapyakṣhayameva syaadvarṣhaasu cha maghaasu cha. yat kiñchit madhunaa mishram pradadyaat tu trayodasheem,
tat api akṣhayam eva syaat varṣhaasu cha maghaasu cha.
(varṣhaasu) During the rainy season (cha) and (maghaasu) under the prominence of the 
Royal constellation, (tu)(trayodasheem) on the thirteen day of the moon, (kiñchit)
anything (yat) that is (pradadyaat) given after (mishram) mixing it (madhunaa) with 
honey, (tat) that thing (syaat) is (api) also the one giving (akṣhayam) undiminishing 
pleasure (eva) indeed. 3:273

274. api naḥ sa kule jaayaadyo no dadyaat tryodasheem,
paayasam madhusarpibhyaam praakchhaaye kuñjarasya cha. api naḥ saḥ kule jaayaat yaḥ naḥ dadyaat tryodasheem,
paayasam madhusarpibhyaam praak-chhaaye kuñjarasya cha.
May (saḥ) he be (api) also (jaayaat) born in (naḥ) our (kule) family, (yaḥ) who, 
(tryodasheem) on the thirteenth day of the moon (cha) and when (kuñjarasya) the 
elephant’s (chhaaye) shadow falls (praak) towards east i.e. in the afternoon, (dadyaat)
gives (naḥ) for us, (paayasam) the pudding mixed (madhu) with honey and 
(sarpibhyaam) clarified butter! So wish the ancestors. 3:274

275. yadyaddadaati vidhivat samyak shraddhaasamanvitaḥ,
tattatpitṛeeṇaam bhavati paratraanantamakṣhayam. yat yat dadaati vidhivat samyak shraddhaa-samanvitaḥ,
tat tat pitṛeeṇaam bhavati paratra-aanantam akṣhayam.
(yat)(yat) Whatever is (vidhivat) properly (dadaati) given (samanvitaḥ) with (samyak)
unerring (shraddhaa) faith and devotion, (tat)(tat) that (bhavati) becomes the cause of 
(aanantam) the endless and (akṣhayam) undiminishing (paratra) salvation (pitṛeeṇaam)
for the ancestors. 3:275

276. kṛiṣhṇapakṣhe dashamyaadau varjayitvaa chaturdasheem, 
shraaddhe prashastaastithayo yathaitaa na tathetaraaḥ. kṛiṣhṇa-pakṣhe dashami-aadau varjayitvaa chaturdasheem,
shraaddhe prashastaaḥ tithayaḥ yathaa etaa na tathaa itaraaḥ. 
(kṛiṣhṇa) During the waning (pakṣhe) phase of the moon, (aadau) starting (dashami)
from the tenth day of the moon, all days (varjayitvaa) except (chaturdasheem) the 
fourteenth day of the moon (prashastaaḥ) are considered the best (tithayaḥ) days 
(shraaddhe) for making offerings for the ancestors; (yathaa) as (etaa) these days are, 
(tathaa) so are (na) not (itaraaḥ) the others. 3:276

277. yukṣhu kurvan dinarkṣheṣhu sarvaankaamaansamashnute, 
ayukṣhu tu pitṛeensarvaanprajaam praapnoti puṣhkalaam. yukṣhu kurvan dina-ṛikṣheṣhu sarvaan kaamaan samashnute,
ayukṣhu tu pitṛeen sarvaan prajaam praapnoti puṣhkalaam. 
The one who (kurvan) performs these offerings (yukṣhu) on the even (dina) days of the 
moon and under even numbered (ṛikṣheṣhu) constellations, (sarvaan) all of his/her 
(kaamaan) desires (samashnute) are fulfilled (tu) and the one who makes the offerings 
(sarvaan) for all of (pitṛeen) the ancestors (ayukṣhu) on the odd days of the moon and 
under odd numbered constellations (praapnoti) gets (puṣhkalaam) a lot of (prajaam)
offsprings. 3:277

278. yathaa chaivaaparaḥ pakṣhaḥ poorvapakṣhaadvishiṣhyate, 
tathaa shraaddhasya poorvaahṇaadaparaahṇo vishiṣhyate. yathaa cha eva aparaḥ pakṣhaḥ poorva-pakṣhaat vishiṣhyate,
tathaa shraaddhasya poorvaahṇaat aparaahṇaḥ vishiṣhyate. 
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ३ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 3
334
(cha) And (yathaa)(eva) as (poorva) compared to the prior (pakṣhaat) phase i.e the 
waxing phase of the moon, (aparaḥ) the later (pakṣhaḥ) phase i.e. the waning phase 
(vishiṣhyate) is considered better (shraaddhasya) for these offerings, (tathaa) so is 
(aparaahṇaḥ) the afternoon time (vishiṣhyate) considered better (poorvaahṇaat) than 
the before noon time. 3:278
प्राचीनावीितना सम्यगपसव्यमतिन्द्रणा ।
िप यमािनधनात्काय िविधवद्दभर्पािणना ॥२७९॥
प्राचीनावीितना । सम्यक्। अपसव्यम्। अतिन्द्रणा ॥ िप यम्। आ । िनधनात्। कायर्म्। िविधवत्। दभर्पािणना ॥
279. praacheenaaveetinaa samyagapasavyamatandriṇaa,
pitryamaanidhanaatkaaryam vidhivaddarbhapaaṇinaa. praacheena-aaveetinaa samyak apasavyam atandriṇaa,
pitryam aa nidhanaat kaaryam vidhivat darbha-paaṇinaa.
(praacheena)(aaveetinaa) Wearing the sacred thread on the right shoulder, (darbha)
with grass (paaṇinaa) in one’s hands, (apasavyam) proceeding from left to right, one 
should (atandriṇaa) tirelessly and (vidhivat) duly (kaaryam) perform (pitryam) the 
offerings for the ancestors (samyak) in its entirety, (aa) until (nidhanaat) one’s death.
3:279

ू । च ।एव । अिचरोिदते॥
280. raatrau shraaddhan na kurveeta raakṣhasee keertitaa hi saa,
sandhyayorubhayoshchaiva soorye chaivaachirodite. raatrau shraaddham na kurveeta raakṣhasee keertitaa hi saa,
sandhyayoḥ ubhayoḥ cha eva soorye cha eva achirodite.
(na) Neither (kurveeta) perform (shraaddham) these offerings (raatrau) during the night 
(hi) because (saa) the night (keertitaa) is said to be (raakṣhasee) demonic (cha) nor 
(ubhayoḥ) at the both (sandhyayoḥ) of the times of transitions i.e. dawn and dusk (eva)
as well, (cha) and not (eva) even (achirodite)(soorye) immediately after the sunrise i.e. 
until the noon time. 3:280
अनेन िविधना श्राद्धंित्ररब्धस्येह िनवर्पेत
्
।
हेमन्तग्रीष्मवषार्सुपाञ्चयि कमन्वहम्
॥२८१॥
अनेन । िविधना । श्राद्धम्। ित्रः । अब्धस्य । इह। िनवर्पेत्॥ हेमन्तग्रीष्मवषार्सु। पाञ्चयि कम्। अनऽअहम ु ्॥
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ३ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 3
335
281. anena vidhinaa shraaddhan trirabdhasyeha nirvapet,
hemantagreeṣhmavarṣhaasu paañchayajñikamanvaham. anena vidhinaa shraaddham triḥ abdhasya iha nirvapet,
hemanta-greeṣhma-varṣhaasu paañcha-yajñikam anu-aham.
(anena) Following this (vidhinaa) procedure (shraaddham) these offerings (nirvapet)
should be completed at least (triḥ) three (abdhasya) times (iha) every year, (hemanta)
in the pre-winter season, (greeṣhma) in the summer season and (varṣhaasu) in the rainy 
season, however, the offerings falling under (paañcha) the five routine (yajñikam) yajña 
should be performed (anu)(aham) daily. 3:281
न पैत

282. na paitṛiyajñiyo homo laukike’gnau vidheeyate,
na darshena vinaa shraaddhamaahitaagnerdvijanmanaḥ. na paitṛi-yajñiyaḥ homaḥ laukike agnau vidheeyate,
na darshena vinaa shraaddham aahita-agneḥ dvijanmanaḥ.
It is (na) not (vidheeyate) recommended (homaḥ) to burn these offerings (paitṛi) for the 
ancestors (agnau) in the fire lit (laukike) for the routine (yajñiyaḥ) yajña. (dvijanmanaḥ)
A braahmaṇa who (aahita) maintains (agneḥ) the sacred fire should (na) not undertake 
(shraaddham) these offerings on any day (vinaa) except (darshena) the day of no moon.
3:282

283. yadeva tarpayatyaadbhiḥ pitṛeensnaatvaa dvijottamaḥ,
tenaiva kṛitsnamaapnoti pitṛiyajñakriyaaphalam. yat eva tarpayatya adbhiḥ pitṛeen snaatvaa dvijottamaḥ,
tena eva kṛitsnam aapnoti pitṛi-yajña-kriyaa-phalam.
(dvijottamaḥ) A braahmaṇa who (snaatvaa) after having taken a bath, (tarpayatya)
satisfies (pitṛeen) the ancestors (eva) just by offering them (yat)(adbhiḥ) waters, (tena)
by that offering (eva) itself he/she (aapnoti) begets (kṛitsnam) all (phalam) of the fruits 
associated (kriyaa) with the performance of the entire (yajña) procedure of the offerings 
(pitṛi) for the ancestors. 3:283

284. vasoon vadanti tu pitṛeen rudraañshchaiva pitaamahaan,
prapitaamahaanstathaa’’dityaañchhrutireṣhaa sanaatanee. vasoon vadanti tu pitṛeen rudraan cha eva pitaamahaan,

The learned (vadanti) say (pitṛeen) the fathers to be (vasoon) the source of wealth, 
(pitaamahaan) the grandfathers (rudraan) the upholders of justice (tu)(cha)(tathaa) and 
(prapitaamahaan) the great-grandfathers (adityaan) the source of enlightenment (eva)
as well; (eṣhaa) this is (sanaatanee) a universal (shrutiḥ) saying. 3:284

Extensions in Chapter 4
Different occupations for sustenance
The 4th – 10th shlokas interrupt the flow and also present ideas that are not coherent with 
the duties of the four classes prescribed in the Vedas.
ऋताम
ृ

ृ

ऋतामताभ्याम ृ ्। जीवेत्। तु। मतेनृ । प्रमतेनृ । वा ॥ सत्यानताभ्याम ृ ्। अिप । वा । न।  व या
ृ । कदाचन ॥
4. ṛitaamṛitaabhyaañ jeevettu mṛitena pramṛitena vaa,
satyaanṛitaabhyaamapi vaa na shvavṛittyaa kadaachana. ṛita-amṛitaabhyaam jeevet tu mṛitena pramṛitena vaa,
satya-anṛitaabhyaam api vaa na shva-vṛittyaa kadaachana.
One (jeevet)should sustain oneself by engaging in occupations that are (ṛita) universally 
acceptable and (amṛitaabhyaam) do not hurt pride, (vaa) or those that (mṛitena) hurt 
the pride and (pramṛitena) are akin to living multiple deaths, (vaa) or (api) even those 
that are (satya) truthful but (anṛitaabhyaam) not universally acceptable, (tu) but 
(na)(kadaachana) never in those (vṛittyaa) occupations that involve sycophancy like 
(shva) a dog. 4:4

5. ṛitamuñchhashilañ jñeyamamṛitan syaadayaachitam,
mṛitan tu yaachitam bhaikṣham pramṛitaṅ karṣhaṇan smṛitam. ṛitam uñchha-shilam jñeyam amṛitam syaat ayaachitam,
mṛitam tu yaachitam bhaikṣham pramṛitam karṣhaṇam smṛitam.
(jñeyam) Consider (uñchha)(shilam) picking the post harvest remains from a field as 
(ṛitam) universally acceptable. Getting sustenance (ayaachitam) without begging for it 
(syaat) does (amṛitam) not hurt pride. (yaachitam) Begging (bhaikṣham) for food is like 
(mṛitam) death as it hurts one’s pride. (tu) And engaging in labor intensive occupations 
like (karṣhaṇam) agriculture (smṛitam) are said to be (pramṛitam) living multiple deaths.
4:5

6. satyaanṛitan tu vaaṇijyan tena chaivaapi jeevyate,
sevaa shvavṛittiraakhyaataa tasmaattaam parivarjayet. satya-anṛitam tu vaaṇijyam tena cha eva api jeevyate,
sevaa shva-vṛittiḥ aakhyaataa tasmaat taam pari-varjayet.
(vaaṇijyam) The trading occupation is (satya) truthful (tu) but (anṛitam) not considered 
universally acceptable (cha) and one can (api)(eva) even (jeevyate)sustain oneself (tena)
with that. However, (sevaa)(vṛittiḥ) being an employee who is completely dependent 
on someone (aakhyaataa) is said to be akin to slavery involving sycophancy like (shva)
a dog and (tasmaat) hence (taam) it should be (pari) completely (varjayet) avoided. 4:6

7. kushooladhaanyako vaasyaatkumbheedhaanyaka eva vaa,
tryahaihiko vaa’pibhavedashvastanika eva vaa. kushoola-dhaanyakaḥ vaa syaat kumbhee-dhaanyakaḥ eva vaa,
tri-aha ehikaḥ vaa api bhavet ashvastanikaḥ eva vaa.
A twice-born (syaat) may be the one (dhaanyakaḥ) hoarding food (kushoola) in a granary 
(vaa) or the one (dhaanyakaḥ) keeping (eva) only (kumbhee) one earthen pot full at a 
time, (vaa) or (api) even (bhavet) remain the one (ehikaḥ) desirous of keeping rations 
for (tri) three (aha) days only (vaa) or the one (ashvastanikaḥ) keeping (eva) only today’s 
worth. 4:7

8. chaturṇaamapi chaiteṣhaan dvijaanaaṅ gṛihamedhinaam,

(eteṣhaam) Out of these (chaturṇaam) four types of (dvijaanaam) twice born 
(gṛihamedhinaam) householders, (paraḥ)(paraḥ) the later ones (jñeyaḥ) should be 
considered (jyaayaan) more distinguished than the prior ones in the order they were

mentioned, because by displaying (dharmataḥ) righteous restraint they (jittamaḥ) win 
(loka) over the World. 4:8

9. ṣhaṭkarmaiko bhavatyeṣhaan tribhiranyaḥ pravarttate,
dvaabhyaamekashchaturthastu brahmasatreṇa jeevati. ṣhaṭ karma ekaḥ bhavati eṣhaam tribhiḥ anyaḥ pravarttate,
dvaabhyaam ekaḥ chaturthaḥ tu brahma-satreṇa jeevati.
(eṣhaam) Out of these (ekaḥ) the first one (bhavati) may (pravarttate) be engaged (ṣhaṭ)
in six types of (karma) occupations, (anyaḥ) the second one (tribhiḥ) in three types and 
the third (ekaḥ) one (dvaabhyaam) in two types, (tu) however, (chaturthaḥ) the fourth 
one (jeevati) sustains oneself only (brahma)(satreṇa) by the study of the Vedas. 4:9

10. varttayañshcha shiloñchhaabhyaamagnihotraparaayaṇaḥ,
iṣhṭeeḥ paarvaayanaanteeyaaḥ kevalaa nirvapetsadaa. varttayan cha shiloñchhaabhyaam agnihotra-paraayaṇaḥ,
iṣhṭeeḥ paarva-ayana-anteeyaaḥ kevalaaḥ nirvapet sadaa.
Even the twice born who (varttayan) sustains by (shiloñchhaabhyaam) picking the post 
harvest remains from a field, should (sadaa) always (paraayaṇaḥ) remain diligent 
(agnihotra) in the performance of offerings in the fire (cha) and (kevalaaḥ) at least 
(nirvapet) complete the offerings (iṣhṭeeḥ) for fulfillment of specific desires, (paarva) for 
festivals including no moon and full moon days, (ayana) for the solstices and 
(anteeyaaḥ) for the year ends. 4:10
Act in accordance with one’s constraints
The 18th shloka interrupts the flow and presents an idea irrelevant to present context.

18. vayasaḥ karmaṇo’rthasya shrutasyaabhijanasya cha,
veṣhavaagbuddhisaaroopyamaacharanvicharediha. vayasaḥ karmaṇaḥ arthasya shrutasya abhijanasya cha,
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ४ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 4
340
veṣha-vaak-buddhi-saaroopyam aacharan vicharet iha.
One (aacharan)(vicharet) should conduct oneself (iha) in this world while keeping one’s 
(veṣha) dress, (vaak) speech and (buddhi) intellect (saaroopyam) in accordance with 
one’s (vayasaḥ) age, (karmaṇaḥ) occupation, (arthasya) wealth, (abhijanasya) lineage 
(cha) and (shrutasya) the Vedas. 4:18
Alternatives to the yajña
The 22nd – 24th shlokas present some alternatives to the yajña. However, Maharṣhi Manu 
had earlier declared the yajña to be mandatory for the householders. These alternatives, 
hence can’t absolve one from the yajña.
एतानेकेमहाय ान्य शा िवदो जनाः । अनीहमानाः सततिमिन्द्रयेष्वेव ज
ु
 ित ॥२२॥
एतान्। एके। महाय ान्। य शा िवदः । जनाः ॥ अनीहमानाः । सततम्। इिन्द्रयेषु। एव । ज ित ु ॥
22. etaaneke mahaayajñaan yajñashaastravido janaaḥ,
aneehamaanaaḥ satatamindriyeṣhveva juhvati. etaan eke mahaa-yajñaan yajña-shaastra-vidaḥ janaaḥ,
aneehamaanaaḥ satatam indriyeṣhu eva juhvati.
(eke) A few of the (janaaḥ) scholars who are (vidaḥ) experts (shaastra) in the treatise 
(yajña) of the yajña, (aneehamaanaaḥ) choose not to perform (etaan) these 
(mahaa)(yajñaan) five routine yajña physically (eva) but (satatam) persistently perform 
yajña by (juhvati) sacrificing and curtailing the pleasures that feed their (indriyeṣhu)
senses. 4:22
वाच्येकेज
ु
 ित प्राणंप्राणेवाचंच सवर्दा ।
वािच प्राणेच पश्यन्तो य िनवर्ि म याम ृ ्
॥२३॥
वािच ।एके। ज ित ु । प्राणम्। प्राणे। वाचम्। च । सवर्दा॥ वािच । प्राणे। च ।पश्यन्तः । य िनवर्ि म ृ ्। अ याम॥्
23. vaachyeke juhvati praaṇam praaṇe vaachañ cha sarvadaa,
vaachi praaṇe cha pashyanto yajñanirvṛittimakṣhayaam. vaachi eke juhvati praaṇam praaṇe vaacham cha sarvadaa,
vaachi praaṇe cha pashyantaḥ yajña-nirvṛittim akṣhayaam.
(eke) Some (sarvadaa) always (juhvati) surrender (praaṇam) the breath (vaachi) to the 
speech (cha) and (vaacham) the speech (praaṇe) to the breath (cha) and (pashyantaḥ)
view the control (praaṇe) of the breath and (vaachi) of the speech as (akṣhayaam) the 
undiminishing (nirvṛittim) relief from the duties (yajña) of the yajña. 4:23

ु ॥
24. jñaanenaivaapare vipraa yajantyetairmakhaiḥ sadaa,
jñaanamoolaaṅ kriyaameṣhaam pashyanto jñaanachakṣhuṣhaa. jñaanena eva apare vipraaḥ yajanti etaiḥ makhaiḥ sadaa,
jñaana-moolaam kriyaam eṣhaam pashyantaḥ jñaana-chakṣhuṣhaa.
(apare) Some other (vipraaḥ) braahmaṇa (pashyantaḥ) see (eṣhaam) these (kriyaam)
procedures (chakṣhuṣhaa) from the viewpoint (jñaana) of the knowledge and find them 
(moolaam) to be rooted (jñaana) in the knowledge and hence (sadaa) always (yajanti)
perform (etaiḥ) these (makhaiḥ) yajña (jñaanena) by the pursuit of the knowledge (eva)
itself. 4:24
Offerings after harvest, change of seasons, solstice and year
The 26th – 28th shlokas call for offerings of animals in the yajña. This is against the 
teachings of the Vedas and against Maharṣhi Manu’s doctrines as well.
सस्यान्तेनवसस्ये 
्
या तथत्वर्न्तेिद्वजोऽध्वरैः ।
पश
ु
ना त्वयनस्यादौ समान्तेसौिमकै मर्खैः ॥२६॥
सस्यान्ते। नवसस्ये ्
या । तथा । ऋतऽअन्ते
ु । िद्वजः । अध्वरैः ॥
पशना
ु । तु। अयनस्य । आदौ । समान्ते। सौिमकै ः । मखैः ॥
26. sasyaante navasasyeṣhṭyaa tathartvante dvijo’dhvaraiḥ,
pashunaa tvayanasyaadau samaante saumikairmakhaiḥ. sasya-ante navasasyeṣhṭyaa tathaa ṛitu-ante dvijaḥ adhvaraiḥ,
pashunaa tu ayanasya aadau sama-ante saumikaiḥ makhaiḥ.
When (sasya) the grains (ante) have ripened, (dvijaḥ) a twice-born should, 
(navasasyeṣhṭyaa) perform the offerings of the new grains in the fire. And (tathaa)
similarly, (ante) at the end of (ṛitu) the seasons perform (adhvaraiḥ) non-violent yajña, 
(aadau) at the beginning (ayanasya) of the solstice perform (pashunaa) animal sacrifice 
(tu) and (ante) at the end (sama) of the year perform an elaborate (makhaiḥ) yajña called 
(saumikaiḥ) Somayaaga. 4:26

27. naaniṣhṭvaa navasasyeṣhṭyaa pashunaa chaagnimaandvijaḥ,
navaannamadyaanmaansam vaa deerghamaayurjijeeviṣhuḥ.
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ४ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 4
342
na aniṣhṭvaa nava-sasyeṣhṭyaa pashunaa cha agnimaan dvijaḥ,
nava-annam adyaat maansam vaa deergham aayuḥ jijeeviṣhuḥ.
(dvijaḥ) A twice-born who is (agnimaan) the bearer of the fire and (jijeeviṣhuḥ) desires 
to live (deergham) a long (aayuḥ) life, should (na) not (adyaat) consume (nava) new 
(annam) grains (vaa) or (maansam) meat (aniṣhṭvaa) without the performance of 
offerings (nava) of the new (sasyeṣhṭyaa) grains (cha) and (pashunaa) animals in the fire.
4:27
नवेनानिचर्ता  स्य पश
ुहव्येन चाग्नयः ।
प्राणानेवा 
ु
िमच्छिन्त नवान्नािमषगिद्धर्नः ॥२८॥
नवेन। अनिचर्ताः । िह। अस्य । पशहव्येन ु । च । अग्नयः॥ प्राणान्।एव । अ मु्। इच्छिन्त । नवान्नािमषगिद्धर्नः॥
28. navenaanarchitaa hyasya pashuhavyena chaagnayaḥ,
praaṇaanevaattumichchhanti navaannaamiṣhagarddhinaḥ. navena anarchitaaḥ hi asya pashu-havyena cha agnayaḥ,
praaṇaan eva attum ichchhanti nava-anna-aamiṣha-garddhinaḥ.
(eva)(hi) Because, (agnayaḥ) the fires (anarchitaaḥ) that have not been satisfied 
(havyena) with the offerings (navena) of new grains (cha) and (pashu) animals, 
(ichchhanti) desire (attum) to consume (praaṇaan) the spirit (asya) of the person 
(garddhinaḥ) who consumes these (nava) new (anna) grains and (aamiṣha) meats 
without making the offerings. 4:28
A graduate should not remain hungry
The 33rd – 34th shlokas interrupt the flow by deviating from the current topic of the duties 
of the householder.
राजतो धनमिन्वच्छेत्सं
सीदन्स्नातकः  
ु
धा ।

33. raajato dhanamanvichchhet sanseedan snaatakaḥ kṣhudhaa,
yaajyaantevaasinorvaa’pi na tvanyata iti sthitiḥ. raajataḥ dhanam anu-ichchhet sanseedan snaatakaḥ kṣhudhaa,
yaajya-antevaasinoḥ vaa api na tu anyataḥ iti sthitiḥ.
(snaatakaḥ) A graduate who (sanseedan) is disconcerted (kṣhudhaa) due to hunger, 
(anu)(ichchhet) can desire (dhanam) food/money (raajataḥ) from the king, (yaajya) a 
householder who performs yajña (vaa) or (api) even his/her (antevaasinoḥ) disciples (tu)
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ४ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 4
343
but (na) not (anyataḥ) from anybody else, (iti) this rule is (sthitiḥ) established in the 
scriptures. 4:33
न सीदेत्स्नातको िवप्रः  
ु

34. na seedet snaatako vipraḥ kṣhudhaa shaktaḥ kathañchana, 
na jeerṇamalavadvaasaa bhavechcha vibhave sati. na seedet snaatakaḥ vipraḥ kṣhudhaa shaktaḥ kathañchana,
na jeerṇa-malavat vaasaa bhavet cha vibhave sati. 
(shaktaḥ) A capable (snaatakaḥ) graduate (vipraḥ) twice-born should (na) not 
(kathañchana) ever (seedet) suffer (kṣhudhaa) from hunger due to laziness (cha) and 
should (na) not (bhavet) remain (jeerṇa) in ragged or (malavat) dirty (vaasaa) clothes 
(vibhave) when sufficient wealth (sati) is available. 4:34
Do’s and don’ts for a twice-born 
The 36th – 39th shlokas present some irrelevant and impractical instructions that are in 
contradiction with ideas Maharṣhi Manu has proposed elsewhere.

36. vaiṇaveen dhaarayedyaṣhṭin sodakañ cha kamaṇḍalum, 
yajñopaveetam vedañ cha shubhe raukme cha kuṇḍale. vaiṇaveem dhaarayet yaṣhṭim sodakam cha kamaṇḍalum,
yajñopaveetam vedam cha shubhe raukme cha kuṇḍale. 
A householder (dhaarayet)should carry (vaiṇaveem) a bamboo (yaṣhṭim) staff (cha) and 
(kamaṇḍalum) an oblong pot (sodakam) filled with water, wear (yajñopaveetam) sacred 
thread (cha) and (shubhe) bright (raukme) golden (kuṇḍale) earrings (cha) and be the 
bearer (vedam) of the Vedas. 4:36
