37. nekṣhetodyantamaadityan naastañ yaantaṅ kadaachana, 
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ४ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 4
344
nopasṛiṣhṭan na vaaristhan na madhyan nabhaso gatam. na eekṣheta udyantam aadityam na astam yaantam kadaachana,
na upasṛiṣhṭam na vaaristham na madhyam nabhasaḥ gatam.
One should (na) not (kadaachana) ever (eekṣheta) see (aadityam) the sun while it 
(udyantam) is rising or (yaantam) is going (astam)to set, (upasṛiṣhṭam) during an eclipse, 
when it (gatam) has gone (madhyam) to the middle (nabhasaḥ) of the sky or its 
(vaaristham) reflection in water. 4:37

38. na laṅghayedvatsatantreen na pradhaavechcha varṣhati,
na chodake nireekṣheta svaṇ roopamiti dhaaraṇaa. na laṅghayet vatsatantreem na pradhaavet cha varṣhati,
na cha udake nireekṣheta svam roopam iti dhaaraṇaa.
(iti) It (dhaaraṇaa) is believed that one should (na) not (laṅghayet) step over (tantreem)
the leash (vatsa) of a calf (cha) or (pradhaavet) run while it (varṣhati) is raining (cha) or 
(nireekṣheta) watch one’s (svam) own (roopam) reflection (udake) in the water. 4:38

39. mṛidaṅ gaan daivatam vipraṅ ghṛitam madhu chatuṣhpatham,
pradakṣhiṇaani kurveeta prajñaataañshcha vanaspateen. mṛidam gaam daivatam vipram ghṛitam madhu chatuṣhpatham,
pradakṣhiṇaani kurveeta prajñaataan cha vanaspateen.
One should walk (kurveeta) while keeping (mṛidam) a pile of soil, (gaam) a cow, 
(daivatam) a temple, (vipram) a braahmaṇa, (ghṛitam) a butter container, (madhu) a 
honey container, (chatuṣhpatham) a road junction (cha) and (prajñaataan) the famous 
(vanaspateen) trees and plants (pradakṣhiṇaani) on one’s right side. 4:39

43. naashneeyaadbhaaryayaa saardhan nainaameekṣheta chaashnateem, 
kṣhuvateeñ jṛimbhamaaṇaam vaa na chaaseenaañ yathaasukham. na ashneeyaat bhaaryayaa saardham na enaam eekṣheta cha ashnateem,
kṣhuvateem jṛimbhamaaṇaam vaa na cha aaseenaam yathaa-sukham. 
One should (na) neither (ashneeyaat) eat (saardham) along (bhaaryayaa) with one’s 
spouse (cha) and (na) nor (eekṣheta)should one watch (enaam) her (ashnateem) eating, 
(kṣhuvateem) sneezing, (jṛimbhamaaṇaam) yawning (vaa) or (aaseenaam) sitting in 
(yathaa) whatever posture that (sukham) pleases her. 4:43

44. naañjayanteen svake netre na chaabhyaktaamanaavṛitaam, 
na pashyetprasavanteeñ cha tejaskaamo dvijottamaḥ. na añjayanteem svake netre na cha abhyaktaam anaavṛitaam,
na pashyet prasavanteem cha tejaḥ kaamaḥ dvijottamaḥ. 
(dvijottamaḥ) A braahmaṇa (kaamaḥ) who is desirous of (tejaḥ) brilliance should (na)
not (pashyet) watch a lady (añjayanteem) putting liners around (svake) her (netre) eyes, 
(anaavṛitaam) without clothes, (abhyaktaam) getting an oil massage (cha) or 
(prasavanteem) undergoing labor. 4:44

One should (na) not (adyaat) consume (annam) food (vaasaa) while wearing (eka) only 
one piece of clothing; one should (na) not (aacharet) take (snaanam) a bath (nagnaḥ)
naked; one (kurveeta) should (na) not (mootram) urinate (pathi) on a pathway, 
(bhasmani) on a pile of ash or inside (go) a cows’ (vraje) barn. 4:45

49. tiraskṛityochcharet kaaṣhṭhaloṣhṭhapatratṛiṇaadinaa, 
niyamya prayato vaachan samveetaaṅgo’vaguṇṭhitaḥ. tiraḥ-kṛitya uchcharet kaaṣhṭha-loṣhṭha-patra-tṛiṇa-aadinaa,
niyamya prayataḥ vaacham samveetaaṅgaḥ avaguṇṭhitaḥ. 
(kṛitya) After having (tiraḥ) hidden oneself behind (kaaṣhṭha) some wooden planks, 
(loṣhṭha) a pile of dirt, (patra) leaves or (tṛiṇa) bushes (aadinaa) etc., (prayataḥ)
effortfully keeping one’s (vaacham) speech (niyamya) in control, (avaguṇṭhitaḥ)
covering oneself with clothes and (samveetaaṅgaḥ) keeping the bodily organs huddled, 
one (uchcharet) may discharge the feces and the urine. 4:49

50. mootrochchaarasamutsargan divaa kuryaadudaṅmukhaḥ, 
dakṣhiṇaabhimukho raatrau sandhyayoshcha tathaa divaa. mootra-uchchaara-samutsargam divaa kuryaat udaṅ-mukhaḥ, 
dakṣhiṇa-abhimukhaḥ raatrau sandhyayoḥ cha tathaa divaa. 
One (kuryaat) should (uchchaara) (samutsargam) discharge the feces and (mootra) the 
urine while (mukhaḥ) facing (udaṅ) the northern direction (divaa) during the day (cha)
and (sandhyayoḥ) at dawn or at dusk (tathaa) similar (divaa) to the day and while 
(abhimukhaḥ) facing (dakṣhiṇa) the southern direction (raatrau) during the night. 4:50

51. chhaayaayaamandhakaare vaa raatraavahani vaa dvijaḥ, 
yathaasukhamukhaḥ kuryaatpraaṇabaadhaabhayeṣhu cha. chhaayaayaam andhakaare vaa raatrau ahani vaa dvijaḥ, 
yathaa-sukha-mukhaḥ kuryaat praaṇa-baadhaa-bhayeṣhu cha. 
(andhakaare) In case of darkness (chhaayaayaam) due to thick clouds or fog etc., 
(raatrau) during the night (vaa) or (ahani) the day (vaa) or (baadhaa) in case of threat 
(praaṇa) to life (bhayeṣhu) from a fearful situation, (dvijaḥ) a twice-born (kuryaat) can 
do it, (yathaa) as (sukha) suitable (mukhaḥ) facing any convenient direction. 4:51
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ४ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 4

प्रत्यिग्नंप्रितस

प्रितऽअिग्नम्। प्रितसयर्मू ्। च । प्रितसोमोदकिद्वजान्॥ प्रितगाम्। प्रितवातम्। च । प्र ा । नश्यित । मेहतः ॥
52. pratyagnim pratisooryañ cha pratisomodakadvijaan,
pratigaam prativaatañ cha prajñaa nashyati mehataḥ. prati-agnim prati-sooryam cha prati-soma-udaka-dvijaan,
prati-gaam prati-vaatam cha prajñaa nashyati mehataḥ.
(mehataḥ) Discharging feces etc. while (prati) facing (agnim) the fire, (prati)(sooryam)
the sun, (prati)(soma) the moon, (dvijaan) the braahmaṇa, (udaka) the water, 
(prati)(gaam) a cow (cha) or (prati)(vaatam) the wind, (nashyati) destroys one’s 
(prajñaa) intellect. 4:52
Interacting with fire

53. naagnim mukhenopadhamennagnaan nekṣheta cha striyam,
naamedhyam prakṣhipedagnau na cha paadau prataapayet. na agnim mukhena upadhamet nagnaam na eekṣheta cha striyam,
na amedhyam prakṣhipet agnau na cha paadau prataapayet.
One should (na) neither (upadhamet) blow (agnim) the fire (mukhena) with one’s mouth 
(na)(cha) nor (eekṣheta) should see (nagnaam) a naked (striyam) woman. One should 
(na) neither (prakṣhipet) throw (amedhyam) an unwarranted thing (agnau) in the fire 
(na)(cha) nor (prataapayet) should warm one’s (paadau) feet with it. 4:53

54. adhastaannopadadhyaachcha na chainamabhilaṅghayet,
na chainam paadataḥ kuryaanna praaṇabaadhamaacharet. adhastaat na upadadhyaat cha na cha enam abhi-laṅghayet,
na cha enam paadataḥ kuryaat na praaṇa-baadham aacharet.
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ४ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 4
349
One should (na) neither keep the fire (adhastaat) under one’s (upadadhyaat) bed 
(cha)(na) nor (abhi)(laṅghayet) should step over (enam) it. One (kuryaat) should (na)
neither touch or kick (enam) it (paadataḥ) with feet (na)(cha) nor (aacharet) should do 
anything with it that could (baadham) jeopardize (praaṇa) a life. 4:54
Miscellaneous forbidden actions

55. naashneeyaatsandhivelaayaan na gachchhennaapi samvishet, 
na chaiva pralikhedbhoomin naatmanopaharetsrajam. na ashneeyaat sandhi-velaayaam na gachchhet na api samvishet,
na cha eva pralikhet bhoomim na aatmana upaharet srajam. 
(velaayaam) At the time of (sandhi) transition between day and night i.e. at dawn or at 
dusk, one should (na) neither (ashneeyaat) eat (na) nor (gachchhet) go somewhere, (na)
neither (samvishet) take rest (na) nor (pralikhet) carve (bhoomim) the ground (cha) and 
should (na) not (aatmana) himself/herself (upaharet) remove (srajam) the garland from 
one’s neck (api)(eva) as well.

56. naapsu mootram pureeṣham vaa ṣhṭheevanam vaa samutsṛijet, 
amedhyaliptam anyat vaa lohitam vaa viṣhaaṇi vaa. na apsu mootram pureeṣham vaa ṣhṭheevanam vaa sam-utsṛijet,
amedhya-liptam anyat vaa lohitam vaa viṣhaaṇi vaa. 
One should (na) not (sam)(utsṛijet) discharge (mootram) the urine, (pureeṣham) the 
feces, (ṣhṭheevanam) the spit, (vaa) or (anyat) any other (amedhya)(liptam) pollutant
including (lohitam) the blood (vaa) or (viṣhaaṇi) the poison etc. (apsu) in the water. 4:56

57. naikaḥ svapechchhoonyagehe shreyaansan na prabodhayet, 
nodakyayaa’bhibhaaṣheta yajñaṅ gachchhenna chaavṛitaḥ. na ekaḥ svapet shoonya-gehe shreyaansam na prabodhayet,
na udakyayaa abhibhaaṣheta yajñam gachchhet na cha avṛitaḥ. 
One should (na) neither (svapet)sleep (ekaḥ) alone in (shoonya) a deserted (gehe) house 
(na) nor (prabodhayet) point out faults (shreyaansam) of the superiors. One should (na)
not (abhi)(bhaaṣheta) talk (udakyayaa) to a menstruating woman (cha) and should (na)
not (gachchhet) go (yajñam) to a yajña (avṛitaḥ) unless chosen as a priest. 4:57

58. agnyaagaare gavaaṅ goṣhṭhe braahmaṇaanaañ cha sannidhau, 
svaadhyaaye bhojane chaiva dakṣhiṇam paaṇimuddharet. agni-aagaare gavaam goṣhṭhe braahmaṇaanaam cha sannidhau,
svaadhyaaye bhojane cha eva dakṣhiṇam paaṇim uddharet. 
One should keep one’s (dakṣhiṇam) right (paaṇim) hand (uddharet) exposed in (agni)
the fire (aagaare) house, in (gavaam) the cow (goṣhṭhe) barn, (sannidhau) in the 
proximity (braahmaṇaanaam) of the braahmaṇa, (svaadhyaaye) during the study of the 
scriptures (cha) and (bhojane) while eating (eva) as well.

59. na vaarayedgaan dhayanteen na chaachakṣheeta kasyachit, 
na diveendraayudhan dṛiṣhṭvaa kasyachiddarshayedbudhaḥ. na vaarayet gaam dhayanteem na cha aachakṣheeta kasyachit,

One should (na) neither (vaarayet) interrupt (gaam) a cow (dhayanteem) who is drinking 
water or is suckling its calf (na)(cha) nor (aa)(chakṣheeta) instruct (kasyachit) someone 
else to do it. In case (budhaḥ) a wise person (dṛiṣhṭvaa) should see (indra)(aayudham) a

60. naadhaarmike vased graame na vyaadhibahule bhṛisham,
naikaḥ prapadyetaadhvaanan na chiram parvate vaset. na adhaarmike vaset graame na vyaadhi-bahule bhṛisham,
na ekaḥ prapadyeta adhvaanam na chiram parvate vaset.
One should (na) neither (vaset) stay (graame) in a village where most of the population 
engage (adhaarmike) in unrighteous conduct (na) nor where (bhṛisham) a highly
(vyaadhi) infectious disease (bahule) is rampant. One should (na) neither (prapadyeta)
travel (ekaḥ) alone (adhvaanam) on a deserted pathway (na) nor (vaset) stay (parvate)
on a mountain (chiram) for a long time. 4:60

61. na shoodraraajye nivasennaadhaarmikajanaavṛite,
na paakhaṇḍigaṇaakraante nopasṛiṣhṭe’ntyajairnṛibhiḥ. na shoodra-raajye nivaset na adhaarmika-jana-aavṛite,
na paakhaṇḍi-gaṇa-aakraante na upasṛiṣhṭe antyajaiḥ nṛibhiḥ.
A twice-born should (na) neither (nivaset) reside (raajye) in the kingdom (shoodra) of a 
shoodra king (na) nor in a place (aavṛite) filled with (adhaarmika) unrighteous (jana)
people, (na) neither in a place (aakraante) infested (gaṇa) by the groups (paakhaṇḍi) of 
hypocrites (na) nor where (nṛibhiḥ) humans (antyajaiḥ) born from parents who are not 
from the four varṇas are (upasṛiṣhṭe) in majority. 4:61

62. na bhuñjeetoddhṛitasnehan naatisauhityamaacharet,
naatiprage naatisaayam na saayam praataraashitaḥ. na bhuñjeeta uddhṛita-sneham na ati-sauhityam aacharet,

One should (na) neither (bhuñjeeta) consume the food that (uddhṛita) has been stripped 
(sneham) of fat (na) nor (aacharet) should practice (ati) over (sauhityam) indulgence, 
should eat (na) neither (ati) very (prage) early in the morning (na) nor (ati) very (saayam)
late at night. And in case one (aashitaḥ) has over eaten (praataḥ) in the morning then 
he/she should (na) not eat altogether (saayam) in the evening. 4:62

63. na kurveeta vṛithaa cheṣhṭaan na vaaryañjalinaa pibet,

are expected (na) nor (pibet) drink (vaari) water (añjalinaa) from one’s palm, (na)
neither (bhakṣhayet) eat (bhakṣhyaan) the food (utsaṅge) keeping it in one’s lap (na) nor 
(syaat) be (kutoohalee) eager (jaatu) to know unnecessary details about others. 4:63

64. na nṛityedathavaa gaayenna vaaditraaṇi vaadayet,

ू ॥
65. na paadau dhaavayetkaansye kadaachidapi bhaajane,
na bhinnabhaaṇḍe bhuñjeeta na bhaavapratidooṣhite. na paadau dhaavayet kaansye kadaachit api bhaajane,
na bhinna-bhaaṇḍe bhuñjeeta na bhaava-prati-dooṣhite.
One should (na) neither (kadaachit) ever (dhaavayet) wash one’s (paadau) feet 
(kaansye) in a bronze (bhaajane) pot, (na) nor (api) ever (bhuñjeeta) eat from (bhinna) a 
chipped (bhaaṇḍe) plate, and (na) nor from a plate that (bhaava)seems (prati)(dooṣhite)
repulsive. 4:65
Avoid clothes worn by others
उपानहौ च वास  ध
ृ
तमन्यैनर्धारयेत
्
। उपवीतमलङ
्
कारंस्रजंकरकमेव च ॥६६॥
उपानहौ । च । वासः । च । धतमृ ्। अन्यैः । न। धारयेत्॥उपवीतम्। अलङ्कारम्। स्रजम्। करकम्। एव । च ॥
66. upaanahau cha vaasashcha dhṛitamanyairna dhaarayet,
upaveetamalaṅkaaran srajaṅ karakameva cha. upaanahau cha vaasaḥ cha dhṛitam anyaiḥ na dhaarayet,
upaveetam alaṅkaaram srajam karakam eva cha.
One should (na) not (dhaarayet) wear or use (vaasaḥ) the clothes, (upaanahau) the 
shoes, (upaveetam) the sacred thread, (alaṅkaaram) the ornaments, (srajam) the 
garland (cha)(eva) as well as (karakam) the oblong vessel, (dhṛitam) that have been 
worn or used (anyaiḥ) by others. 4:66
The 69th – 78th shlokas present some irrelevant and impractical instructions that are in 
contradiction with ideas Maharṣhi Manu has proposed elsewhere.

69. baalaatapaḥ pretadhoomo varjyam bhinnan tathaa’’sanam, 
na chhindyaannakhalomaani dantairnotpaaṭayennakhaan. baala-aatapaḥ preta-dhoomaḥ varjyam bhinnam tathaa aasanam,
na chhindyaat nakha-lomaani dantaiḥ na utpaaṭayet nakhaan. 
One (varjyam) should avoid (aatapaḥ) the light (baala) from the morning sun, 
(dhoomaḥ) the smoke (preta) from a funeral pyre (tathaa) and (bhinnam) a broken 
(aasanam) seat. One should (na) not (chhindyaat) pull one’s (lomaani) hairs and (nakha)
nails and should (na) not (utpaaṭayet) bite (nakhaan) the nails (dantaiḥ) with teeth. 4:69

70. na mṛilloṣhṭhañ cha mṛidneeyaanna chchhindyaatkarajaistṛiṇam, 
na karma niṣhphalaṅ kuryaannaayatyaamasukhodayam. na mṛid-loṣhṭham cha mṛidneeyaat na chhindyaat karajaiḥ tṛiṇam,
na karma niṣhphalam kuryaat na aayatyaam asukha-udayam. 
Without a reason, one should (na) neither (mṛidneeyaat) crush (loṣhṭham) a lump (mṛid)
of soil (na) nor (chhindyaat) break (tṛiṇam) the blades of grass (karajaiḥ) with fingers, 
(cha) and (na) nor should one (kuryaat) perform (karma) a task where (niṣhphalam) no 
result or (asukha) a negative (udayam) outcome in the future (aayatyaam) is expected.

71. loṣhṭhamardee tṛiṇachchhedee nakhakhaadee cha yo naraḥ, 
sa vinaasham vrajatyaashu soochako’shuchireva. loṣhṭha-mardee tṛiṇa-chchhedee nakha-khaadee cha yaḥ naraḥ, 
saḥ vinaasham vrajati aashu soochakaḥ ashuchiḥ eva. 
(naraḥ) The human (yaḥ) who is (mardee) the crusher (loṣhṭha) of a lump of soil, 
(chhedee) the breaker (tṛiṇa) of the blades of grass (cha) or (khaadee) the biter (nakha)
of one’s nails, (eva) as well as the one who is (soochakaḥ) an informer or is (ashuchiḥ)
unclean, (saḥ) he/she (aashu) expeditiously (vrajati) goes (vinaasham) to doom. 4:71

72. na vigarhya kathaaṅ kuryaad bahirmaalyan na dhaarayet,
gavaañ cha yaanam pṛiṣhṭhena sarvathaiva vigarhitam. na vigarhya kathaam kuryaat bahiḥ maalyam na dhaarayet,
gavaam cha yaanam pṛiṣhṭhena sarvathaa eva vigarhitam.
One should (na) neither (kuryaat) engage in (vigarhya) harmful, egoistical and 
condemnable (kathaam) speech (na) nor (dhaarayet) wear (maalyam) a garland (bahiḥ)
exposed over the hairs or the clothes. (cha) And (yaanam) riding (pṛiṣhṭhena) on the 
back (gavaam) of a cow or a bull is (sarvathaa) universally (vigarhitam) condemned (eva)
indeed. 4:72

अद्वारेण । च । न। अतीयात्। ग्रामम्। वा । वेश्म । वा । आवतमृ ्॥ रात्रौ । च । व मृ लािन ू । दरतः

73. advaareṇa cha naateeyaad graamam vaa veshma vaa’’vṛitam,
raatrau cha vṛikṣhamoolaani doorataḥ parivarjayet. advaareṇa cha na ateeyaat graamam vaa veshma vaa aavṛitam,
raatrau cha vṛikṣha-moolaani doorataḥ parivarjayet.
One should (na) not (ateeyaat) enter (graamam) a village (vaa) or (veshma) a house that 
is (aavṛitam) surrounded by a wall, (vaa)(advaareṇa) in any other way except through 
the gate. (cha) And (raatrau) at night one (parivarjayet) should leave aside (moolaani)
the roots (vṛikṣha) of a tree (doorataḥ) from a distance. 4:73
ना ैः क्र डेत्कदािच ु

74. naakṣhaiḥ kreeḍetkadaachittu svayan nopaanahau haret,
shayanastho na bhuñjeeta na paaṇisthan na chaasane. na akṣhaiḥ kreeḍet kadaachit tu svayam na upaanahau haret,
shayanasthaḥ na bhuñjeeta na paaṇistham na cha aasane.
One should (na) neither (kadaachit)(tu) ever (kreeḍet) play (akṣhaiḥ) with dices i.e. 
gamble (na) nor (haret) carry (upaanahau) shoes (svayam) himself/herself. One should

(na) not (bhuñjeeta) consume (shayanasthaḥ) while lying down and (na) not eat after 
placing the food (paaṇistham) on one’s palm (cha) or (aasane) on the seat. 4:74
सव च ितलसम्बद्धंनाद्यादस्तिमतेरवौ ।

75. sarvañ cha tilasambaddhan naadyaadastamite ravau,
na cha nagnaḥ shayeeteha na chochchhiṣhṭaḥ kvachid vrajet. sarvam cha tila-sambaddham na adyaat astamite ravau,
na cha nagnaḥ shayeeta iha na cha uchchhiṣhṭaḥ kvachit vrajet.
(iha) In this world, one should (na) neither (adyaat) consume (sarvam) any food item
(sambaddham) containing (tila) sesame seeds (astamite)(ravau) after sunset, (na)(cha)
nor (shayeeta) sleep (nagnaḥ) naked, (na)(cha) nor (kvachit) ever (vrajet) roam around 
with (uchchhiṣhṭaḥ) an unrinsed mouth after eating. 4:75

76. aardrapaadastu bhuñjeeta naardrapaadastu samvishet,
aardrapaadastu bhuñjaano deerghamaayuravaapnuyaat. aardra-paadaḥ tu bhuñjeeta na aardra-paadaḥ tu samvishet,
aardra-paadaḥ tu bhuñjaanaḥ deergham aayuḥ avaapnuyaat.
One (bhuñjeeta) should consume after (aardra) having rinsed one’s (paadaḥ) feet, (tu)
but (na) not (samvishet)take rest (aardra) with wet (paadaḥ) feet, because (bhuñjaanaḥ)
the one who eats (tu) after (aardra) washing one’s (paadaḥ) feet (avaapnuyaat) begets 
(deergham) a long (aayuḥ) life. 4:76

One should (na) not (prapadyeta) try to go to (karhichit) any (durgam) inaccessible or 
pathless place (achakṣhuḥ)(viṣhayam) with poor visibility, (na) nor (udeekṣheta)see (viṇ)

78. adhitiṣhṭhenna keshaanstu na bhasmaasthikapaalikaaḥ,
na kaarpaasaasthi na tuṣhaandeerghamaayurjijeeviṣhuḥ. adhitiṣhṭhet na keshaan tu na bhasma-asthi-kapaalikaaḥ,
na kaarpaasa-asthi na tuṣhaan deergham aayuḥ jijeeviṣhuḥ.
Someone (jijeeviṣhuḥ) desirous of (deergham) a long (aayuḥ) life should (na) not 
(adhitiṣhṭhet) sit on (keshaan) hairs, (bhasma) ash, (asthi) bones, (kapaalikaaḥ) broken 
pots, (kaarpaasa) cotton (asthi) wood (tu) or (tuṣhaan) hay. 4:78
The 80th – 91st shlokas imply a birth based caste system and classify various types of hells 
for the afterlife. Both of these concepts are anti Vedic and do not conform to the 
teachings of Maharṣhi Manu elsewhere in this treatise.
Giving or preaching to a shoodra
न श
ू
द्राय मितंदद्यान्नोिच्छ ंन हिवष्कृ
तम
्
।
न चास्योपिदशेद्धम न चास्य व्रतमािदशेत्
॥८०॥
न। शद्राय ू । मितम्। दद्यात्। न। उिच्छ म्। न। हिवष्कृतम्॥
न। च । अस्य ।उपिदशेत्। धमर्म्। न। च । अस्य । व्रतम्। आिदशेत्॥
80. na shoodraaya matin dadyaannochchhiṣhṭan na haviṣhkṛitam,
na chaasyopadisheddharman na chaasya vratamaadishet. na shoodraaya matim dadyaat na uchchhiṣhṭam na haviṣhkṛitam,
na cha asya upadishet dharmam na cha asya vratam aadishet.
One should (na) not (dadyaat) give (matim) advice, (uchchhiṣhṭam) leftover food or 
(haviṣhkṛitam) a portion of the offerings (shoodraaya) to a shoodra; (cha) and should
(na) neither (upadishet) preach (dharmam) righteousness (asya) to him (na)(cha) nor 
(aadishet) guide (asya) him (vratam) towards the prescribed resolves and penances. 4:80
यो  स्य धमर्माच ेय ैवािदशित व्रतम
्
।
सोऽसं
व
ृ
तंनाम तमः सह तेनैव मज्जित ॥८१॥
यः । िह। अस्य । धमर्म्। आच े। यः । च । एव । आिदशित । व्रतम्॥
सः । असं
वतमृ ्। नाम । तमः । सह। तेन। एव । मज्जित ॥
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ४ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 4
358
81. yo hyasya dharmamaachaṣhṭe yashchaivaadishati vratam,
so’samvṛitan naama tamaḥ saha tenaiva majjati. yaḥ hi asya dharmam aachaṣhṭe yaḥ cha eva aadishati vratam,
saḥ asamvṛitam naama tamaḥ saha tena eva majjati.
(hi) Because (saḥ) he, (yaḥ) who (aachaṣhṭe) tries to preach (dharmam) righteousness 
(asya) to him (cha)(eva) as well as, the one (yaḥ) who (aadishati) guides him (vratam)
towards the prescribed resolves and penances, (majjati) sinks into (tamaḥ) the hell 
(naama) named (asamvṛitam) Asamvṛita, (saha) along with (tena) that shoodra (eva) as 
well. 4:81
Hygiene of the head
न सं
हताभ्यांपािणभ्यांकण्ड
ूयेदात्मनः िशरः ।
न स्प
ृ
शेच्चैतद
ु
िच्छ ो न च स्नायािद्वना ततः ॥८२॥
न। सं
हताभ्याम्। पािणभ्याम्। कण्डू
येत्। आत्मनः । िशरः ॥
न। स्पशेतृ ्। च ।एतत्। उिच्छ ः । न। च । स्नायात्। िवना । ततः ॥
82. na saṅhataabhyaam paaṇibhyaaṅ kaṇḍooyedaatmanaḥ shiraḥ,
na spṛishechchaitaduchchhiṣhṭo na cha snaayaadvinaa tataḥ. na saṅhataabhyaam paaṇibhyaam kaṇḍooyet aatmanaḥ shiraḥ,
na spṛishet cha etat uchchhiṣhṭaḥ na cha snaayaat vinaa tataḥ.
One should (na) neither (kaṇḍooyet) scratch (aatmanaḥ) one’s (shiraḥ) head 
(saṅhataabhyaam) simultaneously (paaṇibhyaam) with both hands, (na)(cha) nor 
(spṛishet) touch (etat) it (uchchhiṣhṭaḥ) with soiled hands (cha) and (na) nor (snaayaat)
take a bath (vinaa) without washing (tataḥ) it. 4:82
के शग्रहान्प्रहारां
  िशरस्येतािन्ववजर्येत

के शग्रहान्। प्रहारान्। च । िशरिस । एतान्। िववजर्येत्॥
िशरः । स्नातः । च । तैलेन ।न। अङ्गम्। िकिञ्चत्। अिप । स्पशेतृ ्॥
83. keshagrahaanprahaaraañshcha shirasyetaanvivarjayet,
shiraḥ snaatashcha tailena naaṅgaṅ kiñchidapi spṛishet. kesha-grahaan prahaaraan cha shirasi etaan vivarjayet,
shiraḥ snaataḥ cha tailena na aṅgam kiñchit api spṛishet.
While fighting (etaan)these (vivarjayet)should be left out, (grahaan) holding and pulling 
of (kesha) hairs (cha) and (prahaaraan) striking blows (shirasi) to the head. (cha) And
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ४ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 4

(snaataḥ) after applying (tailena) oil on one’s (shiraḥ) head, one should (na) not 
(spṛishet) touch (kiñchit)(api) any other (aṅgam) body part with oiled hands. 4:83
Avoid taking donations from

84. na raajñaḥ pratigṛihṇeeyaadaraajanyaprasootitaḥ,
soonaachakradhvajavataam veshenaiva cha jeevataam. na raajñaḥ prati-gṛihṇeeyaat araajanya-prasootitaḥ,
soonaa-chakra-dhvajavataam veshena eva cha jeevataam.
One should (na) neither (prati)(gṛihṇeeyaat) accept donations (raajñaḥ) from a king 
(araajanya)(prasootitaḥ) who is not born from kṣhatriya parents, nor from people 
(jeevataam) whose occupations are related to (soonaa) a slaughter house, (chakra) a
wheel i.e. oil extraction, pottery etc., (dhvajavataam) liquor vending (cha) or (veshena)
a prostitution house (eva) as well. 4:84
दशसू
नासमंचक्रं दशचक्रसमो ध्वजः । दशध्वजसमो वेशो दशवेशसमो न

पः ॥८५॥

85. dashasoonaasamañ chakran dashachakrasamo dhvajaḥ,
dashadhvajasamo vesho dashaveshasamo nṛipaḥ. dasha-soonaa-samam chakram dasha-chakra-samaḥ dhvajaḥ,
dasha-dhvaja-samaḥ veshaḥ dasha-vesha-samaḥ nṛipaḥ.
(chakram) An oil manufacturer (samam) is equivalent to (dasha) ten (soonaa) butchers, 
(dhvajaḥ) a liquor vendor (samaḥ) is equivalent to (dasha) ten (chakra) oil 
manufacturers, (veshaḥ) a prostitution racketeer (samaḥ) is equivalent to (dasha) ten 
(dhvaja) liquor vendors and (nṛipaḥ) a king not from kṣhatriya lineage (samaḥ) is 
equivalent to (dasha) ten (vesha) prostitution racketeers. 4:85

86. dashasoonaasahasraaṇi yo vaahayati saunikaḥ,
tena tulyaḥ smṛito raajaa ghorastasya pratigrahaḥ. dasha-soonaa-sahasraaṇi yaḥ vaahayati saunikaḥ,
tena tulyaḥ smṛitaḥ raajaa ghoraḥ tasya prati-grahaḥ.
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ४ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 4
360
(saunikaḥ) A butcher (yaḥ) who (vaahayati) maintains (dasha) ten (sahasraaṇi) thousand 
(soonaa) slaughter houses, (tulyaḥ) equivalent (tena) to him, (smṛitaḥ) is considered the 
non-kṣhatriya (raajaa) king. (prati)(grahaḥ) Accepting donations (tasya) from that king 
(ghoraḥ) is extremely sinful. 4:86

87. yo raajñaḥ pratigṛihṇaati lubdhasyochchhaastravarttinaḥ, 
sa paryaayeṇa yaateemaannarakaanekaviñshatim. yaḥ raajñaḥ prati-gṛihṇaati lubdhasya ut shaastra-varttinaḥ, 
saḥ paryaayeṇa yaati imaan narakaan ekaviñshatim. 
The braahmaṇa (yaḥ) who (prati)(gṛihṇaati) accepts donations (raajñaḥ) from (ut) such 
a king, who (varttinaḥ) has circumvented (shaastra) the directives of the scriptures
(lubdhasya) out of greed, (saḥ) he has (paryaayeṇa) to sequentially (yaati) go through all 
of (imaan) these (ekaviñshatim) twenty one types of (narakaan) hells. 4:87
Twenty-one types of hells

91. etadvidanto vidvaanso braahmaṇaa brahmavaadinaḥ,
na raajñaḥ pratigṛihṇanti pretya shreyo’bhikaaṅkṣhiṇaḥ. etat vidantaḥ vidvaansaḥ braahmaṇaaḥ brahma-vaadinaḥ,
na raajñaḥ prati-gṛihṇanti pretya shreyaḥ abhi-dhraakaaṅkṣhiṇaḥ.
(vidantaḥ) Knowing (etat) this fact (vidvaansaḥ) the scholarly (braahmaṇaaḥ)
braahmaṇa who are (vaadinaḥ) the preachers (brahma) of the vedas and are 
(abhi)(kaaṅkṣhiṇaḥ) desirous of (shreyaḥ) nirvaaṇa (pretya) upon death, (na) do not 
(prati)(gṛihṇanti) accept donations (raajñaḥ) from a unrighteous king. 4:91
The 95th – 127th shlokas identify the time periods that are suitable and those that are 
unsuitable for the study of the Vedas. They also recommend pauses in this study. This 
however, goes against Maharṣhi Manu’s recommendations of daily study of the Vedas 
without fail.
Time periods recommended for the study of the Vedas

95. shraavaṇyaam prauṣhṭhapadyaam vaa’pyupaakṛitya yathaavidhi,
yuktashchhandaansyadheeyeeta maasaanvipro’rdhapañchamaan. shraavaṇyaam prauṣhṭhapadyaam vaa api upaakṛitya yathaa-vidhi,
yuktaḥ chhandaansi adheeyeeta maasaan vipraḥ ardha-pañchamaan.
(shraavaṇyaam) At the end of the month of Shraavaṇa (vaa) or (prauṣhṭhapadyaam) at 
the end of the month of Bhaadrapada (api) as well i.e. on a full moon day in August or 
September, (upaakṛitya) starting with the performance of (yathaa)(vidhi) the proper 
rituals, (vipraḥ) a braahmaṇa should (yuktaḥ) commit (ardha) a half less than 
(pañchamaan) five i.e. four and a half (maasaan) month long period (adheeyeeta) for 
the study (chhandaansi) of the Vedas. 4:95

96. puṣhye tu chhandasaaṅ kuryaad bahirutsarjanan dvijaḥ,
maaghashuklasya vaa praapte poorvaahṇe prathame’hani. puṣhye tu chhandasaam kuryaat bahiḥ utsarjanam dvijaḥ,
maagha-shuklasya vaa praapte poorvaahṇe prathame ahani.
(tu) And depending on the day of start, when (praapte) arrives (prathame) the first 
(ahani) day (shuklasya) of the new moon of either (puṣhye) Pauṣha month (vaa) or 
(maagha) Maagha month i.e. in January or February, (poorvaahṇe) before the 
afternoon, (dvijaḥ) the braahmaṇa (kuryaat) should (bahiḥ) come out of his/her home 
and (utsarjanam) conclude this (chhandasaam) study of the Vedas. 4:96

97. yathaashaastran tu kṛitvaivamutsargañ chhandasaam bahiḥ,

(tu) And (kṛitvaa) after having (utsargam) concluded the study (chhandasaam) of the 
Vedas (evam) like this (yathaa) in accordance (shaastram) with the scriptures, (bahiḥ)

outside his/her home, one (viramet) should pause the study for that (raatrim) night 
(pakṣhiṇeem) of the start of the new phase of the moon and (tat)(eva)similary, the next 
(ekam) one (ahaḥ) day and (nisham) night as well. 4:97

98. ata oordhvan tu chhandaansi shukleṣhu niyataḥ paṭhet,
vedaaṅgaani cha sarvaaṇi kṛiṣhṇapakṣheṣhu sampaṭhet. ataḥ oordhvam tu chhandaansi shukleṣhu niyataḥ paṭhet,
veda-aṅgaani cha sarvaaṇi kṛiṣhṇa-pakṣheṣhu sampaṭhet.
(tu) And (oordhvam) after (ataḥ) this, one should (niyataḥ) make it a rule (paṭhet) to 
study (chhandaansi) the Vedas (shukleṣhu) during the waxing phase of the moon (cha)
and (sampaṭhet) to study (sarvaaṇi) all (aṅgaani) of the other scriptures that facilitate
the understanding (veda) of the Vedas, (kṛiṣhṇa) during the waning (pakṣheṣhu) phase 
of the moon. 4:98

99. naavispaṣhṭamadheeyeeta na shoodrajanasannidhau,
na nishaante parishraanto brahmaadheetya punaḥ svapet. na avispaṣhṭam adheeyeeta na shoodra-jana-sannidhau,
na nishaante parishraantaḥ brahma-adheetya punaḥ svapet.
One should (na) neither chant the mantras (avispaṣhṭam) indistinctly (na) nor 
(adheeyeeta) study the Vedas (sannidhau) in the company (shoodra)(jana) of the 
shoodra. And (adheetya) after studying (brahma) the Vedas near (nishaante) the end of 
the night, one should (na) not (svapet) sleep (punaḥ) again even if he/she 
(parishraantaḥ) is tired. 4:99

100. yathoditena vidhinaa nityañ chhandaskṛitam paṭhet,
brahma chhandaskṛitañ chaiva dvijo yukto hyanaapadi.
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ४ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 4
364
yathaa uditena vidhinaa nityam chhandaḥ-kṛitam paṭhet,
brahma chhandaḥ-kṛitam cha eva dvijaḥ yuktaḥ hi anaapadi.
(vidhinaa) Following the procedures (yathaa) as (uditena) brought forward in the 
scriptures, one should (nityam) always (paṭhet) chant the mantras (chhandaḥ) in the 
poetic meters they were (kṛitam) created in (cha) and (anaapadi) in the times of no 
emergencies, (yuktaḥ) equipped with resolve, (dvijaḥ) a twice born should (hi) definitely
study (chhandaḥ)(kṛitam) the Vedas (eva) as well as (brahma) the braahmaṇa treatises.
4:100
Time periods not recommended for the study of the Vedas

101. imaannityamanadhyaayaanadheeyaano vivarjayet,
adhyaapanañ cha kurvaaṇaḥ shiṣhyaaṇaam vidhipoorvakam. imaan nityam anadhyaayaan adheeyaanaḥ vivarjayet,
adhyaapanam cha kurvaaṇaḥ shiṣhyaaṇaam vidhi-poorvakam.
(adheeyaanaḥ) The one who studies the Vedas (cha) and (kurvaaṇaḥ) the one who 
(vidhi)(poorvakam) properly (adhyaapanam) teaches them (shiṣhyaaṇaam) to the 
students, both should (nityam) always (vivarjayet) leave aside (imaan) these times 
(anadhyaayaan) that are not suitable for the study of the scriptures. 4:101

102. karṇashrave’nile raatrau divaa paansusamoohane,
etau varṣhaasvanadhyaayaavadhyaayajñaaḥ prachakṣhate. karṇa-shrave anile raatrau divaa paansusamoohane,
etau varṣhaasu anadhyaayau adhyaayajñaaḥ prachakṣhate.
(varṣhaasu) In the rainy season, when (raatrau) during the night, the sound (anile) of the 
wind (shrave) is loudly audible (karṇa) in the ears and when (divaa) during the day, 
(paansusamoohane) the dust storm is raging, (adhyaayajñaaḥ) the masters of the 
education (prachakṣhate) have termed (etau) both of these times as (anadhyaayau)
unsuitable for study. 4:102

103. vidyutstanitavarṣheṣhu maholkaanaañ cha samplave, 
aakaalikamanadhyaayameteṣhu manurabraveet. vidyut-stanita-varṣheṣhu mahaa-ulkaanaam cha samplave,
aakaalikam anadhyaayam eteṣhu manuḥ abraveet. 
When (vidyut)(stanita) lightning and thunder accompany (varṣheṣhu) the rain (cha) and 
(samplave) when there is a deluge of (mahaa) large (ulkaanaam) meteors, (manuḥ)
Maharṣhi Manu (abraveet) has said (eteṣhu) these times to be (anadhyaayam)
unsuitable for study, (aakaalikam) until the same time on the next day. 4:103

ृ । च । अभ्रदशर्ने॥
104. etaanstvabhyuditaanvidyaadyadaa praaduṣhkṛitaagniṣhu, 
tadaa vidyaadanadhyaayamanṛitau chaabhradarshane. etaan tu abhyuditaan vidyaat yadaa praaduḥ-kṛita agniṣhu,
tadaa vidyaat anadhyaayam anṛitau cha abhra-darshane. 
(yadaa) When at the time (kṛita) of the yajña, (praaduḥ) during the start of (agniṣhu) the 
fire (etaan) any of these factors mentioned prior, (vidyaat) are seen (abhyuditaan) as 
showing up, (tu) then (vidyaat) consider (tadaa) that time to be (anadhyaayam)
unsuitable for study, in the rainy season, (cha) as well as, when (abhra) clouds 
(darshane) appear (anṛitau) in any other season. 4:104

105. nirghaate bhoomichalane jyotiṣhaañ chopasarjane, 
etaanaakaalikaanvidyaadanadhyaayaanṛitaavapi. nirghaate bhoomi-chalane jyotiṣhaam cha upasarjane,
etaan aa-kaalikaan vidyaat anadhyaayaan ṛitau api. 
(nirghaate) During a hurricane, (bhoomi)(chalane) an earthquake (cha) and (upasarjane)
an eclipse (jyotiṣhaam) of the sun or the moon, (aa) until (etaan) these (kaalikaan) are 
over, (vidyaat) consider that time to be (anadhyaayaan) unsuitable for study, (api) even 
if it happens (ṛitau) during the rainy season. 4:105

106. praaduṣhkṛiteṣhvagniṣhu tu vidyutstanitaniḥsvane, 
sajyotiḥ syaadanadhyaayaḥ sheṣhe raatrau yathaa divaa. praaduḥ-kṛiteṣhu agniṣhu tu vidyut-stanita-niḥsvane,
sajyotiḥ syaat anadhyaayaḥ sheṣhe raatrau yathaa divaa. 
(kṛiteṣhu) At the time of the morning yajña, (agniṣhu) when the fire (praaduḥ) is being 
lit, if (vidyut) (stanita) (niḥsvane) lightning and thunder occur (tu) then it is 
(anadhyaayaḥ) inadvisable to study until (sajyotiḥ) the daylight (syaat) is (sheṣhe)
remaining i.e. till the sunset. And (yathaa) similar to (divaa) the day, if this happens 
(raatrau) during the night then the rest of the night remains unsuitable for study. 4:106

107. nityaanadhyaaya eva syaad graameṣhu nagareṣhu cha, 
dharmanaipuṇyakaamaanaam pootigandhe cha sarvadaa. nitya anadhyaayaḥ eva syaat graameṣhu nagareṣhu cha,
dharma-naipuṇya-kaamaanaam pooti-gandhe cha sarvadaa. 
(kaamaanaam) For the ones desirous of (naipuṇya) excellence (dharma) in 
righteousness, it (syaat) is (nitya) always (anadhyaayaḥ) inadvisable to study 
(graameṣhu) in the villages (cha)(eva) as well as (nagareṣhu) the cities, (cha) and also to 
avoid the places (pooti) with foul (gandhe) odor, (sarvadaa) forever. 4:107

108. antargatashave graame vṛiṣhalasya cha sannidhau,

It is (anadhyaayaḥ) inadvisable to study, (graame) in the village where (shave) a corpse 
(antaḥ)(gata) is present, (sannidhau) in the company (vṛiṣhalasya) of a shoodra,

(rudyamaane) in presence of crying (cha) and wailing, (cha) and (samavaaye) in between 
a crowd (janasya) of humans. 4:108

109. udake madhyaraatre cha viṇmootrasya visarjane, 
uchchhiṣhṭaḥ shraaddhabhuk chaiva manasaa’pi na chintayet. udake madhya-raatre cha viṇ-mootrasya visarjane,
uchchhiṣhṭaḥ shraaddha-bhuk cha eva manasaa api na chintayet. 
(udake) When surrounded by water, (madhya) during the middle (raatre) of the night, 
(visarjane) while discharging (viṇ) the feces (cha) and (mootrasya) the urine, 
(uchchhiṣhṭaḥ) while the hands and mouth are soiled with food, (cha)(eva) as well as, 
(bhuk) while feasting (shraaddha) in a shraaddha ceremony, one should (na) not (api)
even (chintayet) ponder over the mantras (manasaa) mentality. 4:109

110. pratigṛihya dvijo vidvaanekoddiṣhṭasya ketanam, 
tryahan na keertayed brahma raajño raahoshcha sootake. prati-gṛihya dvijaḥ vidvaan eka-uddiṣhṭasya ketanam,
tri-aham na keertayet brahma raajñaḥ raahoḥ cha sootake. 
(vidvaan) A scholarly (dvijaḥ) braahmaṇa should (na) not (keertayet) recite (brahma) the 
Vedas for (tri) three (aham) days (prati)(gṛihya) after accepting (eka) a solo (ketanam)
invitation to a ceremony organized (uddiṣhṭasya) for the purpose of making the 
offerings for the ancestors, as well as, when (raajñaḥ) the king (cha) or the conceptual
celestial body (raahoḥ) Raahu (sootake) have become impure, the king due to a birth or 
a death in his family and the Raahu due to a solar or lunar eclipse. 4:110

111. yaavadekaanudiṣhṭasya gandho lepashcha tiṣhṭhati, 
viprasya viduṣho dehe taavad brahma na keertayet.

yaavat eka-anu-diṣhṭasya gandhaḥ lepaḥ cha tiṣhṭhati,
viprasya viduṣhaḥ dehe taavat brahma na keertayet. 
(yaavat) As long as (gandhaḥ) the fragrances (cha) and (lepaḥ) the ointments provided 
during (eka) (anu) (diṣhṭasya) the solo ceremony done for the ancestors, (tiṣhṭhati) stay
(dehe) on the body (viduṣhaḥ) of the scholarly (viprasya) braahmaṇa, (taavat) until then 
he/she should (na) not (keertayet) recite (brahma) the Vedas. 4:111

112. shayaanaḥ prauḍhapaadashcha kṛitvaa chaivaavasakthikaam, 
naadheeyeetaamiṣhañ jagdhvaa sootakaannaadyameva cha. shayaanaḥ prauḍha-paadaḥ cha kṛitvaa cha eva avasakthikaam,
na adheeyeeta aamiṣham jagdhvaa sootaka-annaadyam eva cha. 
The Vedas should (na) not (adheeyeeta) be studied while one is either (shayaanaḥ) lying 
down, (cha) or sitting with (kṛitvaa) (paadaḥ) feet spread like (prauḍha) the elderly, 
(cha)(eva) or (avasakthikaam) squatting, or (jagdhvaa) after having consumed 
(aamiṣham) meat, (cha)(eva) or after eating (annaadyam) grains etc. from a household 
(sootaka) rendered impure due to a birth or a death in the family.

113. neehaare baaṇashabde cha sandhyayoreva chobhayoḥ, 
amaavaasyaachaturdashyoḥ paurṇamaasyaṣhṭakaasu cha. neehaare baaṇa-shabde cha sandhyayoḥ eva cha ubhayoḥ, 
amaavaasyaa-chaturdashyoḥ paurṇamaasee-aṣhṭakaasu cha. 
Neither (neehaare) during fog, (cha) nor (shabde) when the noise (baaṇa) from shooting 
arrows is being heard, (eva) as well as, (cha) nor (ubhayoḥ) at both (sandhyayoḥ) of the 
times of the transition between day and night, (cha) and nor (aṣhṭakaasu) on the eighth 
or (chaturdashyoḥ) the fourteenth day of the moon or (paurṇamaasee) the day of the 
full moon or (amaavaasyaa) of the no moon. 4:113

114. amaavaasyaa guruṅ hanti shiṣhyaṅ hanti chaturdashee,
brahmaaṣhṭakaapaurṇamaasyau tasmaattaaḥ parivarjayet. amaavaasyaa gurum hanti shiṣhyam hanti chaturdashee,
brahma aṣhṭakaa-paurṇamaasyau tasmaat taaḥ pari-varjayet.
(amaavaasyaa) The no moon day (hanti) destroys (gurum) the teacher, (chaturdashee)
the fourteenth day of the moon (hanti) destroys (shiṣhyam) the disciple, (aṣhṭakaa) the 
eighth day and (paurṇamaasyau) the full moon day destroy (brahma) the Vedas 
themselves and (tasmaat) hence (taaḥ) these should (pari) always (varjayet) be left 
aside. 4:114

115. paansuvarṣhe dishaan daahe gomaayuvirute tathaa,
shvakharoṣhṭre cha ruvati paṅktau cha na paṭhed dvijaḥ. paansu-varṣhe dishaam daahe gomaayu-virute tathaa,
shva-khara-uṣhṭre cha ruvati paṅktau cha na paṭhet dvijaḥ.
(paansu)(varṣhe) When there are clouds of dust, (daahe) when fire is raging (dishaam)
in different directions, when (gomaayu) the jackals (virute) are howling, (tathaa) and
when (shva) the dog, (khara) the donkey (cha) and (uṣhṭre) the camel (ruvati) are crying 
(cha) or (paṅktau) have lined up together, then (dvijaḥ) the twice-born should (na) not 
(paṭhet) recite the Vedas. 4:115

116. naadheeyeeta shmashaanaante graamaante govraje’pi vaa,

The Vedas should (na) not (adheeyeeta) be studied (ante) close to (shmashaana) a 
funeral place, (ante) close to (graama) a village, (api) as well as, inside (go) a cow (vraje)
barn, (vaa) or (vasitvaa) while wearing (vaasaḥ) the clothes worn (maithunam) during a 
sexual intercourse, (cha) or immediately (prati)(gṛihya) after having accepted 
(shraaddhikam) the foods etc. from a shraaddha ceremony. 4:116

117. praaṇi vaa yadi vaa’praaṇi yatkiñchichchhraaddhikam bhavet,
tadaalabhyaapyanadhyaayaḥ paaṇyaasyo hi dvijaḥ smṛitaḥ. praaṇi vaa yadi vaa apraaṇi yat kiñchit shraaddhikam bhavet,
tat aalabhya api anadhyaayaḥ paaṇi aasyaḥ hi dvijaḥ smṛitaḥ.
Apart from the food, (yadi) if (yat)(kiñchit) anything else is accepted (shraaddhikam)
from a shraaddha ceremony, whether (praaṇi) living (vaa) or (apraaṇi) non-living, the 
braahmaṇa (bhavet) becomes (anadhyaayaḥ) ineligible of the Vedic studies (aalabhya)
after having taken (tat) those things (api) as well, (hi) because (paaṇi) the hand (dvijaḥ)
of the braahmaṇa (smṛitaḥ) is considered equivalent to his/her (aasyaḥ) mouth. 4:117

118. chaurairupaplute graame sambhrame chaagnikaarite,
aakaalikamanadhyaayam vidyaatsarvaadbhuteṣhu cha. chauraiḥ upaplute graame sambhrame cha agnikaarite,
aakaalikam anadhyaayam vidyaat sarva-adbhuteṣhu cha.
(sambhrame) During fearful circumstances, when (chauraiḥ) the thieves are (upaplute)
on a rampage (graame) in the village, (cha) or (agnikaarite) when something catches 
fire, (cha) and during (sarva) all kinds of (adbhuteṣhu) unusual occurrences, (vidyaat)
consider that time to be (anadhyaayam) unsuitable for studies (aakaalikam) until the 
same time next day. 4:118

119. upakarmaṇi chotsarge triraatraṅ kṣhapaṇan smṛitam,
aṣhṭakaasu tvahoraatramṛitvantaasu cha raatriṣhu. upakarmaṇi cha utsarge tri-raatram kṣhapaṇam smṛitam,
aṣhṭakaasu tu ahoraatram ṛitu-antaasu cha raatriṣhu.
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ४ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 4
371
(smṛitam) It is recommended (kṣhapaṇam) to leave aside, (tri) three (raatram) nights, 
(upakarmaṇi) at the ceremonial start of the study of the Vedas (cha) and (utsarge) at its 
closing ceremony, (tu) and also (aṣhṭakaasu) the eighth (ahoraatram) day and night of 
the moon during its waning phase, (cha) as well as, the last (raatriṣhu) night (antaasu)
at the end (ṛitu) of the season. 4:119

120. naadheeyeetaashvamaarooḍho na vṛikṣhan na cha hastinam,
na naavan na kharan noṣhṭran neriṇastho na yaanagaḥ. na adheeyeeta ashvam aarooḍhaḥ na vṛikṣham na cha hastinam,
na naavam na kharam na uṣhṭram na iriṇasthaḥ na yaanagaḥ.
One should (na) neither (adheeyeeta) study (aarooḍhaḥ) while sitting on (ashvam) a 
horse, (na) nor (vṛikṣham) a tree, (na) nor (hastinam) an elephant, (na) nor (naavam) a 
boat, (na) nor (kharam) a mule (na)(cha) nor (uṣhṭram) a camel, (na) nor (yaanagaḥ)
while traveling in a vehicle, (na) nor (iriṇasthaḥ) while one is on a barren land. 4:120

121. na vivaade na kalahe na senaayaan na saṅgare,
na bhuktamaatre naajeerṇe na vamitvaa na shuktake. na vivaade na kalahe na senaayaam na saṅgare,
na bhukta-maatre na ajeerṇe na vamitvaa na shuktake.
(na) Neither (vivaade) during a dispute, (na) nor (kalahe) during a verbal altercation or 
a physical fight, (na) nor (senaayaam) while serving in armed forces, (na) nor (saṅgare)
during a battle, (na) nor (bhukta)(maatre) immediately after eating, (na) nor (ajeerṇe)
during constipation, (na) nor (vamitvaa) after vomiting, (na) nor (shuktake) during an 
acid reflux. 4:121

122. atithiñ chaananujñaapya maarute vaati vaa bhṛisham, 
rudhire cha srute gaatraachchhastreṇa cha parikṣhate. atithim cha ananujñaapya maarute vaati vaa bhṛisham,
rudhire cha srute gaatraat shastreṇa cha parikṣhate. 
(ananujñaapya) Without the permission (atithim) of the guest, when (bhṛisham) strong 
(maarute) wind (vaati) is blowing, when (rudhire) blood (srute) is dripping (gaatraat)
from a bodily organ (cha) and when (parikṣhate) wounded (shastreṇa) by a weapon. 4:122

123. saamadhvanaavṛigyajuṣhee naadheeyeeta kadaachana, 
vedasyaadheetya vaa’pyantamaaraṇyakamadheetya cha. saama-dhvanau ṛig-yajuṣhee na adheeyeeta kadaachana,
vedasya adheetya vaa api antam aaraṇyakam adheetya cha. 
Where (saama) Saamaveda recitations (dhvanau) can be heard, do (na) not 
(kadaachana) ever (adheeyeeta) recite (ṛig) Ṛigveda or (yajuṣhee) Yajurveda there. (cha)
And (adheetya) after studying (vedasya) a veda (antam)till its end (vaa) or (aaraṇyakam)
a treatise on a veda (api) as well, do not study another Veda or another treatise on the 
same day. 4:123

124. ṛigvedo devadaivatyo yajurvedastu maanuṣhaḥ, 
saamavedaḥ smṛitaḥ pitryastasmaattasyaashuchirdhvaniḥ. ṛigvedaḥ deva-daivatyaḥ yajurvedaḥ tu maanuṣhaḥ, 
saamavedaḥ smṛitaḥ pitryaḥ tasmaat tasya ashuchiḥ dhvaniḥ. 
(daivatyaḥ) The divinities (smṛitaḥ) are considered to be (deva) the subject (ṛigvedaḥ) of 
the ṛigveda, (maanuṣhaḥ) the duties of the humans (yajurvedaḥ) of the Yajurveda (tu)
and (pitryaḥ) the rites for the ancestors (saamavedaḥ) of the Saamaveda and (tasmaat)
hence (dhvaniḥ) the sounds (tasya) of the later (ashuchiḥ) are impure. 4:124

125. etadvidanto vidvaansastrayeeniṣhkarṣhamanvaham,
kramataḥ poorvamabhyasya pashchaadvedamadheeyate. etat vidantaḥ vidvaansaḥ trayee-niṣhkarṣham anvaham,
kramataḥ poorvam abhyasya pashchaat vedam adheeyate.
(vidantaḥ) Knowing (etat) these (niṣhkarṣham) conclusions (trayee) about the three 
Vedas, (vidvaansaḥ) the scholars (anvaham) everyday study the Vedas (kramataḥ) in an
orderly fashion, (abhyasya) practicing (poorvam) the prior i.e. the ṛigveda and the 
Yajurveda first and then (pashchaat) later (adheeyate) study (vedam) the Saamaveda.

126. pashumaṇḍookamaarjaarashvasarpanakulaakhubhiḥ,
antaraagamane vidyaadanadhyaayamaharnisham. pashu-maṇḍooka-maarjaara-shva-sarpa-nakula-aakhubhiḥ,
antaḥ aagamane vidyaat anadhyaayam ahaḥ-nisham.
If during the class, (pashu) an animal including (maṇḍooka) a frog, (maarjaara) a cat, 
(shva) a dog, (sarpa) a snake, (nakula) a mongoose or (aakhubhiḥ) a rat (aagamane)
shows up (antaḥ) between the teacher and the disciple then (vidyaat) consider 
(anadhyaayam) stopping the study for that (ahaḥ) day and (nisham) night. 4:126

127. dvaaveva varjayennityamanadhyaayau prayatnataḥ,
svaadhyaayabhoomiñ chaashuddhamaatmaanañ chaashuchin dvijaḥ. dvau eva varjayet nityam anadhyaayau prayatnataḥ,
svaadhyaaya-bhoomim cha ashuddham aatmaanam cha ashuchim dvijaḥ.
(dvijaḥ) A twice-born should (nityam) always (prayatnataḥ) effortfully (varjayet) refrain 
from studying when (bhoomim)the place (svaadhyaaya) of study (ashuddham) is impure 
(cha) or he/she (aatmaanam) himself/herself (ashuchim) is impure because (dvau) both 
of these conditions are (eva) indeed (anadhyaayau) unsuitable for the study. 4:127
The 129th – 132nd shlokas present ideas that are unrelated to the resolves of a twice-born 
and are in contradiction with Maharṣhi Manu’s teachings.

129. na snaanamaachared bhuktavaa naaturo na mahaanishi, 
na vaasobhiḥ sahaajasran naavijñaate jalaashaye. na snaanam aacharet bhuktavaa na aaturaḥ na mahaa-nishi,
na vaasobhiḥ saha ajasram na avijñaate jalaashaye. 
A twice-born (aacharet) should take (snaanam) a bath, (na) neither immediately 
(bhuktavaa) after having eaten, (na) nor when one (aaturaḥ) is sick or hurt, (na) nor 
(mahaa)(nishi) during the middle of the night, (na) nor (saha) with (vaasobhiḥ) clothes 
(ajasram) on and (na) not (jalaashaye) in a water body (avijñaate) of unknown depth.
4:129

130. devataanaaṅ guro raajñaḥ snaatakaachaaryayostathaa,

A twice-born should (na) not (kaamataḥ) knowingly (aakraamet)step over (chhaayaam)
the shadow (devataanaam) of the divinites, (guroḥ) of the guru, (raajñaḥ) of the king,

(cha) and (deekṣhitasya) of someone trained in the performance of the yajña. 4:130

131. madhyandine’rdharaatre vaa shraaddham bhuktvaa cha saamiṣham, 
sandhyayorubhayoshchaiva na seveta chatuṣhpatham. madhyandine ardharaatre vaa shraaddham bhuktvaa cha saamiṣham,

(madhyan)(dine) At midday (vaa) or (ardha)(raatre) at midnight, (cha) and (bhuktvaa)
after having eaten (saamiṣham) a non-vegetarian meal (shraaddham) during a 
shraaddha ceremony, (cha)(eva) as well as, (ubhayoḥ) at both (sandhyayoḥ) of the times 
of transition between day and night, one should (na) not (seveta) pass through 
(chatuṣhpatham) a crossroad junction. 4:131

132. udvartanamasnaanam viṇmootre raktameva cha,
shleṣhmaniṣhṭhyootavaantaani naadhitiṣhṭhettu kaamataḥ. udvartanam asnaanam viṇ-mootre raktam eva cha,
shleṣhma-niṣhṭhyoota-vaantaani na adhi-tiṣhṭhet tu kaamataḥ.
(tu) And one should (na) not (kaamataḥ) knowingly (adhi)(tiṣhṭhet) stand/sit 
(udvartanam) on the scrapped off ointment, (asnaanam) on the water used for bath, 
(viṇ) on the feces or (mootre) the urine, (raktam) on the blood, (cha)(eva) as well as,
(shleṣhma) on the mucus, (niṣhṭhyoota) on the spit or (vaantaani) on the vomit. 4:132
The 135th – 136th shlokas advise against disrespecting some classes, which goes against 
Maharṣhi Manu’s doctrine of dignity and respect for everyone.

135. kṣhatriyañ chaiva sarpañ cha braahmaṇañ cha bahushrutam,
naavamanyeta vai bhooṣhṇuḥ kṛishaanapi kadaachana. kṣhatriyam cha eva sarpam cha braahmaṇam cha bahu-shrutam,
na avamanyeta vai bhooṣhṇuḥ kṛishaan api kadaachana.
(bhooṣhṇuḥ) One desirous of his/her well being should (na)(kadaachana) never 
(avamanyeta) disrespect (kṣhatriyam) a warrior, (sarpam) a snake, (cha)(eva) as well as,
(bahu)(shrutam) a wise and experienced (braahmaṇam) braahmaṇa, (vai) indeed, (api)
even if they are (kṛishaan) in a weaker position. 4:135

136. etattrayaṅ hi puruṣhan nirdahedavamaanitam,
tasmaadetattrayan nityan naavamanyeta buddhimaan. etat trayam hi puruṣham nirdahet avamaanitam,

tasmaat etat trayam nityam na avamanyeta buddhimaan. 
(hi) Because once (avamaanitam) disrespected, (etat) these (trayam) three (nirdahet)

(buddhimaan) a wise person would (na)(nityam) never (avamanyeta) disrespect (etat)

The 140th shloka is completely out of context and interrupts the flow. 
नाितकल्यंनाितसायंनाितमध्यिन्दनेिस्थते।
ना ातेन समंगच्छेन्नैको न व

षलैः सह ॥१४०॥
न। अितकल्यम्। न। अितसायम्। न। अितमध्यिन्दने। िस्थते॥
न। अ ातेन । समम्। गच्छेत्। न। एकः । न। वषलैः ृ । सह॥
140. naatikalyan naatisaayan naatimadhyandine sthite, 
naajñaatena samaṅ gachchhennaiko na vṛiṣhalaiḥ saha. na ati-kalyam na ati-saayam na ati-madhyandine sthite,
na ajñaatena samam gachchhet na ekaḥ na vṛiṣhalaiḥ saha. 
One (gachchhet) should travel (na) neither (ati) very early (kalyam) in the morning (na)
nor (ati) very late (saayam) in the night, (na) nor (ati)(sthite) exactly (madhyandine) at 
the noon time, (na) nor (samam) with (ajñaatena) an unknown person, (na) nor (ekaḥ)
by oneself and (na) nor (saha) with (vṛiṣhalaiḥ) a shoodra. 4:140
The 142nd – 144th shlokas are out of the current context of the resolves and propose some 
illogical and impractical ideas.

142. na spṛishetpaaṇinochchhiṣhṭo vipro gobraahmaṇaanalaan, 
na chaapi pashyedashuchiḥ sustho jyotirgaṇaandivi. na spṛishet paaṇinaa uchchhiṣhṭaḥ vipraḥ go-braahmaṇa-analaan,
na cha api pashyet ashuchiḥ susthaḥ jyotiḥ-gaṇaan divi. 
(vipraḥ) A twice-born should (na) not (spṛishet) touch (go) a cow, (braahmaṇa) a 
braahmaṇa and (analaan) the fire (paaṇinaa) with hands (uchchhiṣhṭaḥ) soiled with
food; (cha) and should (na) not (pashyet)see (jyotiḥ)(gaṇaan) the sun, the moon and the 
stars (divi) in the sky while one is (ashuchiḥ) impure (api) even if one is (susthaḥ) healthy.

143. spṛiṣhṭvaitaanashuchirnityamadbhiḥ praaṇaanupaspṛishet,

And in case, erroneously (spṛiṣhṭvaa) having touched (etaan) these when one is 
(ashuchiḥ) impure, (tu) then he/she should (nityam) regularly (upaspṛishet) sprinkle 
(adbhiḥ) water from his/her (paaṇi)(talena) palm (sarvaaṇi) on all of (praaṇaan) the 
sensory (cha) and (gaatraaṇi) bodily organs, (eva) as well as, (naabhim) on the navel.

144. anaaturaḥ svaani khaani na spṛishedanimittataḥ,

(anaaturaḥ) In a healthy state, one should (na) not (spṛishet) touch (svaani) his/her 
(khaani) sensory organs (animittataḥ) without any reason (cha) and (vivarjayet) should 
leave alone (sarvaaṇi) all of (romaaṇi) the hairs on (rahasyaani) the private parts of the 
body (eva) as well. 4:142

150. saavitraañchhaantihomaañshcha kuryaat parvasu nityashaḥ,

saavitraan shaanti-homaan cha kuryaat parvasu nityashaḥ,

(saavitraan) the chants of the Gaayatree mantra (cha) and (homaan) the yajña (shaanti)

(anu)(aṣhṭakaasu) on the following days i.e. the ninth days of the moon, one should 
(nityam) always (archet) pay respect (pitṛeen) to the ancestors. 4:150

151. dooraadaavasathaanmootran dooraat paadaavasechanam,
uchchhiṣhṭaannaniṣhekañ cha dooraadeva samaacharet. dooraat aavasathaat mootram dooraat paadau asechanam,

One should discharge the feces and (mootram) the urine (dooraat) at a distance 
(aavasathaat) from the residence, (asechanam) should wash one’s (paadau) feet 
(dooraat) at a distance, (cha) and (uchchhiṣhṭa) the leftover (anna) food (sam)(aacharet)
should be (niṣhekam) thrown (dooraat) at a distance (eva) as well. 4:151

152. maitram prasaadhanan snaanan dantadhaavanamañjanam,

(maitram) The discharge of the feces and the urine, (prasaadhanam) the adorning of the 
body, (snaanam) the bath, (dantadhaavanam) the brushing of the teeth, (añjanam) the 
applying of the eye liners, (cha) and (poojanam) the worship (devataanaam) of the 
divinities (kurveeta) should be done (poorvaahṇe) before the noon i.e. in the morning
(eva) itself. 4:152

(tu) And (parvasu) on the auspicious days, (artham) for one’s (rakṣhaa) protection, one

ruler (cha) and (guroon) the teachers (eva) as well. 4:153
The 165th – 169th shlokas point towards the punishments in hell, which is against the Vedic 
teachings. One’s lifeforms in the next lives is a cumulative result of all of the actions and 
not just one action as suggested in these shlokas.

165. braahmaṇaayaavagooryaiva dvijaatirvadhakaamyayaa, 
shatam varṣhaaṇi taamisre narake parivartate. braahmaṇaaya avagoorya eva dvijaatiḥ vadha-kaamyayaa,
shatam varṣhaaṇi taamisre narake parivartate. 
If (dvijaatiḥ) a twice-born (eva) even (avagoorya) raises a stick (braahmaṇaaya) towards 
a braahmaṇa (kaamyayaa) with the desire (vadha) of slaying him, he/she (parivartate)
shall wander (narake) in the hell named (taamisre) Taamisra (shatam) for one hundred 
(varṣhaaṇi) years. 4:165

(aajaateeḥ) life cycles. 4:166

167. ayudhyamaanasyotpaadya braahmaṇasyaasṛigaṅgataḥ,

168. shoṇitañ yaavataḥ paansoonsaṅgṛihṇaati maheetalaat,

(yaavataḥ) As many (paansoon) dust particles (maheetalaat) on the earth surface 
(saṅgṛihṇaati) are stained (shoṇitam) by the blood fallen from a braahmaṇa, (taavataḥ)

(shoṇita) the bleeding, (adyate) gets eaten (anyaiḥ) by other violent animals. 4:168

169. na kadaachid dvije tasmaad vidvaanavaguredapi,

(tasmaat) Hence, (vidvaan) a scholar should (na) not (kadaachit) ever (avaguret) raise a

181. etairvivaadaansantyajya sarvapaapaiḥ pramuchyate,
ebhirjitaishcha jayati sarvaan
̐llokaanimaangṛihee. etaiḥ vivaadaan santyajya sarva-paapaiḥ pramuchyate,

(santyajya) By relinquishing (vivaadaan) arguments (etaiḥ) with these individuals, 
(gṛihee) a householder (pramuchyate) is relieved (sarva) from all of his/her (paapaiḥ)
sins (cha) and (jitaiḥ) by conquering (ebhiḥ) their hearts, he/she (jayati) wins over 
(sarvaan) all of (imaan) these (lokaan) worlds. 4:181

182. aachaaryo brahmalokeshaḥ praajaapatye pitaa prabhuḥ,
atithistvindralokesho devalokasya chartvijaḥ. aachaaryaḥ brahma-loka-eeshaḥ praajaapatye pitaa prabhuḥ,

(aachaaryaḥ) The teacher (eeshaḥ) is the lord (brahma) of God's (loka) realm, (pitaa) the 
father (prabhuḥ) is the lord (praajaapatye) of the king’s realm, (atithiḥ) the guest 
(eeshaḥ) is the lord (indra) of the Indra’s (loka) realm, (cha)(tu) and (ṛitvijaḥ) the 
facilitator of the yajña is the lord (deva) of the divine (lokasya) realm. 4:182

183. jaamayo’psarasaan loke vaishvadevasya baandhavaaḥ,

(jaamayaḥ) The sisters are the lords (loke) of the realm (apsarasaam) of the nymphs, 
(baandhavaaḥ) the friends are the masters of the realm (devasya) of the divinities 
(vaishva) of the universe, (sambandhinaḥ) the relatives are (hi) indeed the masters (loke)

of the realm (apaam) of the waters and (maatṛi) the mother and (maatulau) the 
maternal uncle are the masters (pṛithivyaam) of the earthly realm. 4:183

184. aakaasheshaastu vijñeyaa baalavṛiddhakṛishaaturaaḥ,
bhraataa jyeṣhṭhaḥ samaḥ pitraa bhaaryaa putraḥ svakaa tanuḥ. aakaasha-eeshaaḥ tu vijñeyaaḥ baala-vṛiddha-kṛisha-aaturaaḥ,
bhraataa jyeṣhṭhaḥ samaḥ pitraa bhaaryaa putraḥ svakaa tanuḥ.
(vijñeyaaḥ) Know (baala) the children, (vṛiddha) the old, (kṛisha) the weak (tu) and 
(aaturaaḥ) the sick (eeshaaḥ) as the masters (aakaasha) of the sky, (jyeṣhṭhaḥ) the elder 
(bhraataa) brother (samaḥ) equivalent (pitraa) to the father, and (bhaaryaa) the wife 
and (putraḥ) the son (svakaa) as one’s own (tanuḥ) body. 4:184

185. chhaayaa svo daasavargashcha duhitaa kṛipaṇam param,
tasmaadetairadhikṣhiptaḥ sahetaasañjvaraḥ sadaa. chhaayaa svaḥ daasa-vargaḥ cha duhitaa kṛipaṇam param,
tasmaat etaiḥ adhikṣhiptaḥ saheta asañjvaraḥ sadaa.
(daasa)(vargaḥ) The servants are like (svaḥ) one’s (chhaayaa) shadow (cha) and 
(duhitaa)the daughter is eligible for (param) utmost (kṛipaṇam) love and care. (tasmaat)
Hence, even when one (adhikṣhiptaḥ) is disrespected (etaiḥ) by them, he/she should 
(sadaa) always (saheta) tolerate it (asañjvaraḥ) without resentment. 4:185
The 188th – 189th shlokas demonify the act of accepting donations, while as per the code 
of conduct, a braahmaṇa is expected to sustain on donations alone. Also by definition, an 
unscholarly person can not be classified as a braahmaṇa.
Braahmaṇa accepting donations
िहरण्यंभ

प्रितग नृ ्। अिवद्वान्। तु। भस्मीभवित । दा वत्॥

188. hiraṇyam bhoomimashvaṅ gaamannam vaasastilaan ghṛitam,
pratigṛihṇannavidvaanstu bhasmeebhavati daaruvat. hiraṇyam bhoomim ashvam gaam annam vaasaḥ tilaan ghṛitam,
prati-gṛihṇan avidvaan tu bhasmee-bhavati daaruvat.
(avidvaan) An unscholarly braahmaṇa, who (prati)(gṛihṇan) accepts the donations 
(hiraṇyam) of gold, (bhoomim) land, (ashvam) horses, (gaam) cows, (annam) grains, 
(vaasaḥ) clothes, (tilaan) sesame seeds (tu) and (ghṛitam) clarified butter, (bhavati) is 
reduced (bhasmee) to ashes (daaruvat) like a wood i.e. gets destroyed. 4:188

189. hiraṇyamaayurannañ cha bhoorgaushchaapyoṣhatastanum,
ashvashchakṣhustvacham vaaso dhṛitan tejastilaaḥ prajaaḥ. hiraṇyam aayuḥ annam cha bhooḥ gauḥ cha api oṣhataḥ tanum,
ashvaḥ chakṣhuḥ tvacham vaasaḥ dhṛitam tejaḥ tilaaḥ prajaaḥ.
Accepting donations (hiraṇyam) of the gold (cha) and (annam) the grains (oṣhataḥ)
incinerates i.e. destroys one’s (aayuḥ) longevity, that of (bhooḥ) the land (cha)(api) as 
well as (gauḥ) the cows destroys one’s (tanum) body i.e. one’s health, that of (ashvaḥ)
the horses destroys one’s (chakṣhuḥ) eyesight, that of (vaasaḥ) the clothes destroys 
one’s (tvacham) skin, that of (dhṛitam) the clarified butter destroys one’s (tejaḥ) aura
and energy and that of (tilaaḥ) the sesame seeds destroys one’s (prajaaḥ) offsprings.
4:189
The 191st shloka interrupts the flow and again talks about an unscholarly braahmaṇa.
तस्मादिवद्वािन्बिभयाद्यस्मा स्मात्प्रितग्रहात्
।

स्वल्पके न । अिप । अिवद्वान्। िह । पङ्के। गौःऽइव । सीदित ॥
191. tasmaadavidvaanbibhiyaadyasmaattasmaatpratigrahaat,
svalpakenaapyavidvaanhi paṅke gauriva seedati. tasmaat avidvaan bibhiyaat yasmaat tasmaat prati-grahaat,
svalpakena api avidvaan hi paṅke gauḥ iva seedati.
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ४ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 4
384
(tasmaat) Hence (avidvaan) an unscholarly braahmaṇa (bibhiyaat) should be afraid 
(prati)(grahaat) of accepting donations (yasmaat)(tasmaat) of anything, (hi) because by 
accepting (api) even (svalpakena) a small donations, (avidvaan) a unscholarly (seedati)
suffers (iva) like (gauḥ) a cow trapped (paṅke) in mud. 4:191
The 197th – 200th shlokas discuss hell, place the women in the same category as the 
shoodra, and declare someone being responsible for someone else’s sins. All of these 
ideas are in contradiction with Maharṣhi Manu’s teachings.
Conniving and deceitful
येबकव्रितनो िवप्रा येच माजार्रिलङ
्
िगनः ।

ये। बकव्रितनः । िवप्राः । ये। च । माजार्रिलङ्िगनः ॥ ते। पतिन्त । अन्धतािमस्रे। तेन ।पापेन । कमर्णा ॥
197. ye bakavratino vipraa ye cha maarjaaraliṅginaḥ, 
te patantyandhataamisre tena paapena karmaṇaa. ye baka-vratinaḥ vipraaḥ ye cha maarjaara-liṅginaḥ, 
te patanti andhataamisre tena paapena karmaṇaa. 
Those (vipraaḥ) braahmaṇa (ye) who are (baka)(vratinaḥ) deceitful (cha) and those (ye)
who (liṅginaḥ) show the signs of being (maarjaara) conniving, (tena) due to their 
(paapena)sinful (karmaṇaa) actions, (te) they (patanti) fall (andhataamisre) into the hell 
named Andhataamisra. 4:197

198. na dharmasyaapadeshena paapaṅ kṛitvaa vratañ charet, 
vratena paapam prachchhaadya kurvan streeshoodradambhanam. na dharmasya apadeshena paapam kṛitvaa vratam charet,
vratena paapam prachchhaadya kurvan stree-shoodra-dambhanam. 
(kṛitvaa) After having (paapam) sinned (apadeshena) in the garb (dharmasya) of 
righteousness, one should (na) not (charet) engage in the performance (vratam) of 
penances, just (prachchhaadya) for hiding one’s (paapam) sins (vratena) by the 
penances and (kurvan) trying (dambhanam) to deceive (stree) the women and (shoodra)
the shoodra by it. 4:198

199. pretyeha chedṛishaa vipraa garhyante brahmavaadibhiḥ, 
chhadmanaa’’charitañ yachcha vrataṇ rakṣhaansi gachchhati. pretya iha cha eedṛishaaḥ vipraaḥ garhyante brahma-vaadibhiḥ, 
chhadmanaa aacharitam yat cha vratam rakṣhaansi gachchhati. 
(vipraaḥ) The braahmaṇa (eedṛishaaḥ) like these (garhyante) are criticized (vaadibhiḥ)
by the preachers (brahma) of the Vedas (iha) in this World (cha) as well as (pretya) in 
the after life, (cha) and (yat) whatever (vratam) penances (aacharitam) are formed 
(chhadmanaa) deceitfully, they all (gachchhati) go (rakṣhaansi)towards the demons. 4:199

200. aliṅgee liṅgiveṣheṇa yo vṛittimupajeevati,

(aliṅgee) The unworthy (yaḥ) who (vṛittim)(upajeevati) earns a living, (veṣheṇa) by 
dressing up and wearing the symbols (liṅgi) of the worthy, (saḥ) he/she (harati) takes

lives (yonau) in the class of lowly insects and worms who (tiryak) can’t walk in a straight 
line. 4:200

202. yaanashayyaasanaanyasya koopodyaanagṛihaaṇi cha, 
adattaanyupabhuñjaana enasaḥ syaattureeyabhaak. 
yaana-shayyaa-aasanaani asya koopa-udyaana-gṛihaaṇi cha,
adattaani upabhuñjaanaḥ enasaḥ syaat tureeya-bhaak. 
(upabhuñjaanaḥ) By using (asya) someone’s (yaana) vehicle, (shayyaa) bed, (aasanaani)
seat, (koopa) water well, (udyaana) garden (cha) and (gṛihaaṇi) home, (adattaani)
without the owner’s explicit permission, one (syaat) is eligible for (tureeya)(bhaak) one 
fourth of the (enasaḥ) sins of the owner.
 4:202
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ४ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 4
386
The 205th – 225th shlokas are out of current context and interrupt the flow. The topic of 
what to consume and what not to, is discussed by Maharṣhi Manu in the next chapter. 
They also present ideas about different occupations that are in contradiction with 
Maharṣhi Manu’s doctrines.
Avoid foods given by these

ते। भञ्जीत ु । ब्रा णः । क्विचत्॥
205. naashrotriyatate yajñe graamayaajikṛite tathaa, 
striyaa kleebena cha hute bhuñjeeta braahmaṇaḥ kvachit. na ashrotriyatate yajñe graama-yaaji-kṛite tathaa,
striyaa kleebena cha hute bhuñjeeta braahmaṇaḥ kvachit. 
(braahmaṇaḥ) A braahmaṇa should (na) not (kvachit) ever (bhuñjeeta) consume food 
(yajñe) at a yajña that (ashrotriyatate) has been presided over by someone with no 
knowledge of the Vedas or by someone who (kṛite) performs (yaaji) yajña for (graama)
multiple people, (tathaa) and at a yajña in which (hute) offerings have been made 
(striyaa) by a woman (cha) or (kleebena) a eunuch. 4:205

206. ashleelametatsaadhoonaañ yatra juhvatyamee haviḥ, 
prateepametaddevaanaan tasmaattatparivarjayet. ashleelam etat saadhoonaam yatra juhvati amee haviḥ, 
prateepam etat devaanaam tasmaat tat parivarjayet. 
A yajña (yatra) where (amee) these i.e. a woman or a eunuch (juhvati) offers (haviḥ) the
offerings, (etat) that yajña becomes (ashleelam) obscene (saadhoonaam) for the 
benevolent and (prateepam) unpleasant (devaanaam) for the divinities, (tasmaat)
hence (tat) it should be (pari) completely (varjayet) avoided. 4:206

208. bhrooṇaghnaa’vekṣhitañ chaiva sanspṛiṣhṭañ chaapyudakyayaa, 
patatriṇaa’valeeḍhañ cha shunaa sanspṛiṣhṭameva cha. bhrooṇaghnaa avekṣhitam cha eva sanspṛiṣhṭam cha api udakyayaa,

(cha) Nor the food that (avekṣhitam) has been looked at (bhrooṇaghnaa) by an

(shunaa) by a dog (eva) as well. 4:208

209. gavaa chaannamupaaghraataṅ ghuṣhṭaannañ cha visheṣhataḥ, 
gaṇaannaṅ gaṇikaa’nnañ cha viduṣhaañ cha jugupsitam. gavaa cha annam upaaghraatam ghuṣhṭa-annam cha visheṣhataḥ,

(cha) Nor (annam) the food that (upaaghraatam) has been sniffed (gavaa) by a cow, 
(cha) nor (annam)the food that (ghuṣhṭa) has been declared to be reserved for someone 
(visheṣhataḥ) specifically, (cha) nor (gaṇa) the community (annam) food, nor (annam)

211. abhishastasya ṣhaṇḍhasya puñshchalyaa daambhikasya cha,

food that (avakṣhutam) has been sneezed upon. 4:213

220. pooyañ chikitsakasyaannam puñshchalyaastvannamindriyam,

(shastra) an arms (vikrayiṇaḥ) dealer is akin (malam) to feces. 4:220

221. ya ete’nye tvabhojyaannaaḥ kramashaḥ parikeerttitaaḥ,

(annaaḥ) The foods from (ete) these (anye) others (ye) who have been (kramashaḥ)
successively (parikeerttitaaḥ) declared as whose food is (abhojya) unworthy of 
consumption, (maneeṣhiṇaḥ) the wise (vadanti)say (teṣhaam) their (annam) foods to be 
equivalent to (tvak) skin, (asthi) bones (tu) and (romaaṇi) hairs. 4:221

222. bhuktvaa’to’nyatamasyaannamamatyaa kṣhapaṇan tryaham,

(ataḥ) Hence, after having (amatyaa) unknowingly (bhuktvaa) consumed (annam) the 
food (anyatamasya) from any of these, one should observe (kṣhapaṇam) a fast for (tri)
three (aham) days and after having (matyaa) knowingly (bhuktvaa) consumed these 
foods (cha) or having consumed (retaḥ) semen, (viṇ) feces or (mootram) urine, one 
(aacharet) should carry out (kṛichchhram) the seven day long penance called Kṛichchhra
(eva) as well. 4:222

223. naadyaachchhoodrasya pakvaannam vidvaanashraaddhino dvijaḥ,
aadadeetaamamevaasmaadavṛittaavekaraatrikam. na adyaat shoodrasya pakva-annam vidvaan ashraaddhinaḥ dvijaḥ,
aadadeeta aamam eva asmaat avṛittau eka-raatrikam.
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ४ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 4
393
(vidvaan) A scholarly (dvijaḥ) braahmaṇa should (na) not (adyaat) consume (annam) the 
food (pakva) cooked (shoodrasya) by a shoodra because they are (ashraaddhinaḥ)
unworthy of performing shraaddha. In case, (avṛittau) no other income is received, then 
he/she (aadadeeta) can take (aamam) raw grains (eva) just enough for (eka) one 
(raatrikam) evening meal, (asmaat) from this shoodra. 4:223

224. shrotriyasya kadaryasya vadaanyasya cha vaardhuṣheḥ, 
meemaansitvobhayan devaaḥ samamannamakalpayan. shrotriyasya kadaryasya vadaanyasya cha vaardhuṣheḥ, 
meemaansitvaa ubhayam devaaḥ samam annam akalpayan. 
(annam) The food (kadaryasya) from a miserly (shrotriyasya) scholar of the Vedas (cha)
and the food (vadaanyasya) from a philanthropic (vaardhuṣheḥ) moneylender, 
(meemaansitvaa) after careful consideration, (devaaḥ) the scholars (akalpayan) have 
deemed (ubhayam) both of them (samam) equivalent to each other. 4:224

shraddhaapootam vadaanyasya hatamashraddhayetarat. taan prajaapatiḥ aaha etya maa kṛidhvam viṣhamam samam,
shraddhaapootam vadaanyasya hatam ashraddhayaa itarat. 
However, God, (prajaapatiḥ) the lord of all masses, (etya) came close (taan) to them and 
(aaha) said “(maa) do not (kṛidhvam) decree (viṣhamam) what is not similar, (samam)
as similar. The food donated (vadaanyasya) by a philanthropist (pootam) is pious as it is 
given (shraddhaa) with devotion and (itarat) the other one i.e. from a miser (hatam) is 
inferior because of (ashraddhayaa) the lack of devotion.” 4:225
The 228th – 232nd shlokas present ideas that are exaggerated and fictional. Ideas like, one 
person causing the nirvaaṇa of another and attainment of the salvation just by donation 
of an item, contradict Maharṣhi Manu’s teachings.
Gains from the acts of donation
यित्कंिचदिप दातव्यंयािचतेनानस
ू
यया ।
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ४ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 4

उत्पत्स्यतेिह तत्पात्रंय ारयित सवर्तः ॥२२८॥

ू ॥उत्पत्स्यते। िह । तत्। पात्रम्। यत्। तारयित । सवर्तः ॥
228. yatkiñchidapi daatavyañ yaachitenaanasooyayaa, 
utpatsyate hi tatpaatrañ yattaarayati sarvataḥ. yat kiñchit api daatavyam yaachitena anasooyayaa,
utpatsyate hi tat paatram yat taarayati sarvataḥ. 
(yaachitena) When requested for donation, then (anasooyayaa) without any ill feeling, 
one (daatavyam)should donate (yat)(kiñchit) whatever possible, (api) even if it is a small 
amount, (hi) because amongst those donees (tat) someone (paatram) worthy 
(utpatsyate) will show up (yat) who shall (taarayati) relieve the donor (sarvataḥ) from 
all of the sins and sorrows. 4:228

229. vaaridastṛiptimaapnoti sukhamakṣhayyamannadaḥ, 
tilapradaḥ prajaamiṣhṭaan deepadashchakṣhuruttamam. vaaridaḥ tṛiptim aapnoti sukham akṣhayyam annadaḥ, 
tilapradaḥ prajaam iṣhṭaam deepadaḥ chakṣhuḥ uttamam. 
(vaaridaḥ) The donor of water (aapnoti) gains (tṛiptim) contentment, (annadaḥ) the 
donor of food gains (akṣhayyam) undiminished (sukham) happiness, (tilapradaḥ) the 
donor of sesame seeds gains (prajaam) children (iṣhṭaam) with desirable qualities, 
(deepadaḥ) and the donor of the lamps gets (uttamam) excellent (chakṣhuḥ) eyesight.

230. bhoomido bhoomimaapnoti deerghamaayurhiraṇyadaḥ, 
gṛihado’gryaaṇi veshmaani roopyado roopamuttamam. bhoomidaḥ bhoomim aapnoti deergham aayuḥ hiraṇyadaḥ, 
gṛihadaḥ agryaaṇi veshmaani roopyadaḥ roopam uttamam. 
(bhoomidaḥ) The donor of land (aapnoti) gets more (bhoomim) land, (hiraṇyadaḥ) the 
donor of gold attains (deergham) a long (aayuḥ) lifespan, (gṛihadaḥ) the donor of house 
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ४ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 4
395
gets (agryaaṇi) the best (veshmaani) houses, and (roopyadaḥ) the donor of silver gains 
(uttamam) excellent (roopam) beauty. 4:230
वासोद न्द्रसालोक्यमि सालोक्यम दः ।
अनड

वासोदः । चन्द्रसालोक्यम्। अि सालोक्यम्। अ दः ॥ अनडुद्दः । िश्रयम्।प ाम ु ्। गोदः । ब्रध्नस्य । िव पम्॥
231. vaasodashchandrasaalokyamashvisaalokyamashvadaḥ,
anaḍuddaḥ shriyam puṣhṭaaṅ godo bradhnasya viṣhṭapam. vaasodaḥ chandrasaa-lokyam ashvisaa-lokyam ashvadaḥ,
anaḍuddaḥ shriyam puṣhṭaam godaḥ bradhnasya viṣhṭapam.
(vaasodaḥ) The donor of clothes attains a home (lokyam) in the realm (chandrasaa) of 
the moon, (ashvadaḥ) the donor of a horse attains a home (lokyam) in the realm 
(ashvisaa) of the stars, (anaḍuddaḥ) the donor of an ox gains (puṣhṭaam) excessive 
(shriyam) wealth, and (godaḥ) the donor of a cow attains a place (viṣhṭapam) in the 
realm (bradhnasya) of the sun. 4:231
यानशय्याप्रदो भायार्मै यर्मभयप्रदः ।
धान्यदः शा तंसौख्यंब्र दो ब्र साि र्ताम्
॥२३२॥
यानशय्याप्रदः । भायार्म्। ऐ यर्म्। अभयप्रदः ॥ धान्यदः । शा तम्। सौख्यम्। ब्र दः । ब्र साि र्ताम्॥
232. yaanashayyaaprado bhaaryaamaishvaryamabhayapradaḥ,
dhaanyadaḥ shaashvatan saukhyam brahmado brahmasaarṣhṭitaam. yaana-shayyaa-pradaḥ bhaaryaam aishvaryam abhaya-pradaḥ,
dhaanyadaḥ shaashvatam saukhyam brahmadaḥ brahmasaarṣhṭitaam.
(pradaḥ) The donor (yaana) of a vehicle and (shayyaa) a bed gets (bhaaryaam) a wife, 
(pradaḥ) the giver (abhaya) of protection gains (aishvaryam) supremacy, (dhaanyadaḥ)
the donor of the grains gains (shaashvatam) eternal (saukhyam) happiness and 
(brahmadaḥ) the teacher of the Vedic wisdom (saarṣhṭitaam) becomes equivalent
(brahma) to God. 4:232
The 234th – 237th shlokas again talk about hell, limit the scope of forbidden actions like 
telling lies to only during and after the yajña, and try to exaggerate the impact of some 
acts of indiscretion as the complete destruction of the virtues from righteous actions. All 
of these concepts are in contradiction with Maharṣhi Manu’s doctrines.

234. yena yena tu bhaavena yadyaddaanam prayachchhati,
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ४ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 4
396
tattattenaiva bhaavena praapnoti pratipoojitaḥ. yena yena tu bhaavena yat yat daanam prayachchhati,
tat tat tena eva bhaavena praapnoti prati-poojitaḥ.
(yena)(yena) With whatever (bhaavena) feelings one (prayachchhati) gives (daanam) the 
donations (yat)(yat) of whatever things, he/she (eva) definitely (praapnoti) gets 
(tat)(tat) the same things (poojitaḥ) respectfully (prati) returned back to him/her later,
(tena) with similar (bhaavena) feelings. 4:234

235. yo’rchitam pratigṛihṇaati dadaatyarchitameva cha,
taavubhau gachchhataḥ svargan narakan tu viparyaye. yaḥ architam prati-gṛihṇaati dadaati architam eva cha,

The one (yaḥ) who (prati)(gṛihṇaati) receives (architam) respectfully (cha)(eva) as well 
as the one who (dadaati) gives (architam) respectfully, (ubhau) both of (tau) them 
(gachchhataḥ) go (svargam) to heaven (tu) and (viparyaye) the contrary (narakam) to 
hell. 4:235
Bragging about the righteous acts

236. na vismayeta tapasaa vadediṣhṭvaa cha naanṛitam,
naarto’pyapavadedvipraanna dattvaa parikeertayet. na vismayeta tapasaa vadet iṣhṭvaa cha na anṛitam,
na aartaḥ api apavadet vipraan na dattvaa pari-keertayet.
One should (na) not (vismayeta) be awestriken (tapasaa) after completing a resolve. 
One should (na) not (vadet) tell (anṛitam) a lie (iṣhṭvaa) after performing the yajña. One 
should (na) not (apavadet) criticize (vipraan) the braahmaṇa (api) even when (aartaḥ)
tormented by them. (cha) And one should (na) not (pari)(keertayet) brag (dattvaa) after 
donating. 4:236

237. yajño’nṛitena kṣhirati tapaḥ kṣhirati vismayaat, 
aayurvipraapavaadena daanañ cha parikeertanaat. yajñaḥ anṛitena kṣhirati tapaḥ kṣhirati vismayaat,
aayuḥ vipra-apavaadena daanam cha pari-keertanaat. 
The fruits (yajñaḥ) of yajña (kṣhirati) are destroyed (anṛitena) by telling lies, that of 
(tapaḥ) a penance (kṣhirati) are destroyed (vismayaat) by the feeling of awe, (aayuḥ) the 
longevity is destroyed (apavaadena) by the criticism (vipra) of braahmaṇa, (cha) and the 
fruits of (daanam) donating are destroyed (pari)(keertanaat) by bragging. 4:237
The 247th – 254th shlokas interrupt the flow. They also present ideas as being selective 
about the items that should be accepted including meat, not consuming the alms received 
by oneself, being selective about the caste of the donor and the shraaddha for the 
ancestors, all of which are contrary to Maharṣhi Manu’s teachings.

247. edhodakam moolaphalamannamabhyudyatañ cha yat,

(dakṣhiṇaam) The donations of (edha) the fuel, (udakam) the water, (moola) the 
vegetables, (phalam) the fruits, (yat) whaterver types (annam) of the grains, (madhu)
the honey (atha) and (abhaya) protection, when (abhyudyatam) received without

248. aahṛitaabhyudyataam bhikṣhaam purastaadaprachoditaam,

(mene) In the opinion of (prajaapatiḥ) God, (bhikṣhaam) a donation that (aahṛitaa) has 
been brought and (purastaat) kept in front of a braahmaṇa, (abhyudyataam) by the

249. naashnanti pitarastasya dasha varṣhaaṇi pañcha cha,
na cha havyam vahatyagniryastaamabhyavamanyate. na ashnanti pitaraḥ tasya dasha varṣhaaṇi pañcha cha,
na cha havyam vahati agniḥ yaḥ taam abhi-avamanyate.
The one (yaḥ) who (abhi)(avamanyate) disrespects (taam) this donation, (tasya) his/her 
(pitaraḥ) ancestors (na) do not (ashnanti) consume his/her offering for (dasha) ten (cha)
and (pañcha) five i.e. fifteen (varṣhaaṇi) years (cha) and (agniḥ) the fire (na) does not 
(vahati) carry his/her (havyam) offerings as well. 4:249

250. shayyaaṅ gṛihaankushaangandhaanapaḥ puṣhpam maṇeendadhi,
dhaanaa matsyaanpayo maansañ shaakañ chaiva na nirnudet. shayyaam gṛihaan kushaan gandhaan apaḥ puṣhpam maṇeen dadhi,

One should (na)(eva) never (nirnudet) refuse the donations (shayyaam) of the beds, 
(gṛihaan) the houses, (kushaan) the seats, (gandhaan) the perfumes, (apaḥ) the water, 
(puṣhpam) the flowers, (maṇeen) the gems, (dadhi) the yogurt, (dhaanaa) the rice, 
(matsyaan) the fishes, (payaḥ) the milk, (maansam) the meat (cha) and (shaakam) the 
vegetables. 4:250

251. guroonbhṛityaañshchojjiheerṣhannarchiṣhyandevataatitheen,

and (atitheen) the guests, one (prati)(gṛihṇeeyaat) should accept donations (sarvataḥ)
from everywhere, (tu) however, he/she should (na) not use (tataḥ) that donation for 
(svayam) self (tṛipyet) fulfillment. 4:251

252. guruṣhu tvabhyateeteṣhu vinaa vaa tairgṛihe vasan,
aatmano vṛittimanvichchhangṛihṇeeyaatsaadhutaḥ sadaa. guruṣhu tu abhyateeteṣhu vinaa vaa taiḥ gṛihe vasan,

(tu) And (abhyateeteṣhu) upon the death of (guruṣhu) the teachers and the elders (vaa)
or (vasan) when living (gṛihe) at home (vinaa) without (taiḥ) them, (anu)(ichchhan) for
the desire of one’s (aatmanaḥ) own (vṛittim) sustenance, he/she should (sadaa) always 
(gṛihṇeeyaat) accept donations (saadhutaḥ) from the benevolent. 4:252

ू
द्रेषु
भोज्यान्ना य ात्मानंिनवेदयेत्
॥२५३॥
आिधर्कः । कुलिमत्रम्। च । गोपालः । दासनािपतौ ॥एते। शद्रेषू ु। भोज्यान्नाः । यः । च । आत्मानम्। िनवेदयेत्॥
253. aardhikaḥ kulamitrañ cha gopaalo daasanaapitau,
ete shoodreṣhu bhojyaannaa yashchaatmaanan nivedayet. aardhikaḥ kulamitram cha gopaalaḥ daasa-naapitau,
ete shoodreṣhu bhojya-annaaḥ yaḥ cha aatmaanam nivedayet.
(aardhikaḥ) The one who farms on someone else’s land for a share of the produce, (kula)
a family (mitram) friend, (gopaalaḥ) a cow rearer, (daasa) a servant (cha) and (naapitau)
a barber, (annaaḥ) the food offerings of (ete) these (shoodreṣhu) shoodra (bhojya) are 
consumable (yaḥ) if (nivedayet) offered (aatmaanam) by themselves. 4:253
या शोऽस्य भवेदात्मा या शंच िचक िषर्तम
्
।
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ४ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 4
400
यथा चोपचरेदेनंतथाऽऽत्मानंिनवेदयेत्
॥२५४॥
या शः । अस्य । भवेत्। आत्मा । या शम्। च । िचक िषर्तम्॥
यथा । च । उपचरेत्। एनम्। तथा । आत्मानम्। िनवेदयेत्॥
254. yaadṛisho’sya bhavedaatmaa yaadṛishañ cha chikeerṣhitam,
yathaa chopacharedenan tathaa’’tmaanan nivedayet. yaadṛishaḥ asya bhavet aatmaa yaadṛisham cha chikeerṣhitam,
yathaa cha upacharet enam tathaa aatmaanam nivedayet.
(yaadṛishaḥ) Whatever (bhavet) happens to be (aatmaa) the tendencies, (yaadṛisham)
whatever are (chikeerṣhitam) the desires (asya) of this shoodra (cha) and (yathaa) in 
whatever way he/she (upacharet) is able to serve (enam) this braahmaṇa, he/she 
should (tathaa) accordingly (nivedayet) offer (aatmaanam) by himself/herself. 4:254
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ५ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 5
401
Extensions in Chapter 5
Cause of death
The 1st – 4th shlokas try to give the credit of this treatise to Bhṛigu and also bring forward 
the topic of death out of context.

ु

ृ

ु। महात्मानम्। अनलप्रभवम्। भगृ मु॥्
1. shrutvaitaanṛiṣhayo dharmaan snaatakasya yathoditaan,
idamoochurmahaatmaanamanalaprabhavam bhṛigum. shrutvaa etaan ṛiṣhayaḥ dharmaan snaatakasya yathaa uditaan,
idam oochuḥ mahaatmaanam anala-prabhavam bhṛigum.
(shrutvaa) After having listened (etaan) to these (dharmaan) duties (snaatakasya) of a 
graduate householder, (yathaa) as (uditaan)revealed, (ṛiṣhayaḥ) the sages (oochuḥ)said 
(idam) this (mahaatmaanam) to the great soul (bhṛigum) bhṛigu who (prabhavam) is 
radiant (anala) like fire. 5:1

2. evañ yathoktam vipraaṇaan svadharmamanutiṣhṭhaam,
katham mṛityuḥ prabhavati vedashaastravidaam prabho. evam yathaa uktam vipraaṇaam svadharmam anutiṣhṭhaam,
katham mṛityuḥ prabhavati veda-shaastra-vidaam prabho.
(prabho) O Illuminated! (katham) How can (mṛityuḥ) death (prabhavati) overpower 
(vipraaṇaam) the twice-borns who (vidaam) know (veda) the Vedas and (shaastra) the 
scriptures and (anutiṣhṭhaam) diligently adhere (svadharmam) to their individual duties 
(yathaa) as (uktam) explained (evam) in this treatise? 5:2

3. sa taanuvaacha dharmaatmaa maharṣheenmaanavo bhṛiguḥ,
shrooyataañ yena doṣheṇa mṛityurvipraañjighaansati. saḥ taan uvaacha dharmaatmaa maharṣheen maanavaḥ bhṛiguḥ,
shrooyataam yena doṣheṇa mṛityuḥ vipraan jighaansati.
(saḥ) He, (dharmaatmaa) the righteous soul (maanavaḥ) in Manu’s lineage, (bhṛiguḥ)
Bhṛigu (uvaacha) said (taan) to those (maharṣheen) sages, “(shrooyataam) Listen about
मनुस्मृित प्र ेपण अध्याय ५ । Manusmṛiti Extensions Chapter 5
402
(yena) those (doṣheṇa) vices that let (mṛityuḥ) death (jighaansati) kill those (vipraan)
twice-borns.” 5:3
अनभ्यासेन वेदानामाचारस्य च वजर्नात

ु। िवप्रान्। िजघां
सित ॥
4. anabhyaasena vedaanaamaachaarasya cha varjanaat,
aalasyaadannadoṣhaachcha mṛityurvipraañjighaansati. anabhyaasena vedaanaam aachaarasya cha varjanaat,
aalasyaat anna-doṣhaat cha mṛityuḥ vipraan jighaansati.
(anabhyaasena) Not practicing (vedaanaam) the study of the Vedas any longer, 
(aachaarasya) engaging (varjanaat) in forbidden behaviors, (aalasyaat) laziness (cha)
and consumption of (doṣhaat) improper (anna) foods, let (mṛityuḥ) death (jighaansati)
kill (vipraan) the twice-borns. 5:4
Unfit for consumption
The 6th – 7th shlokas mention animal sacrifice as well as, without any basis list some other 
things as forbidden.
लोिहतान्वृ
 िनयार्सान्वृ
 नप्रभवां
स्तथा । शेल
ुंगव्यंच पेय
ू
षंप्रयत्नेन िववजर्येत
्
॥६॥
लोिहतान्। व िनयार्सान ृ ्। व नप्रभवान ृ ्। तथा ॥ शेलमु्। गव्यम्। च ।पेयषमू ्। प्रयत्नेन । िववजर्येत्॥
6. lohitaanvṛikṣhaniryaasaanvṛishchanaprabhavaanstathaa,
sheluṅ gavyañ cha peyooṣham prayatnena vivarjayet. lohitaan vṛikṣha-niryaasaan vṛishchanaprabhavaan tathaa,
shelum gavyam cha peyooṣham prayatnena vivarjayet.
(lohitaan) The red (niryaasaan) sap (vṛikṣha) from the trees (tathaa) and sap 
(prabhavaan) produced (vṛishchana) when a tree is cut, (shelum) the indian cherry (cha)
and (gavyam) cow’s (peyooṣham) colostrum and transition milk, these should be 
(prayatnena) effortfully (vivarjayet) left aside. 5:6
